7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

CODE OF ORDINANCES CITY OF DUBLIN, TEXAS
CODE OF ORDINANCES
Chapter 1 - GENERAL PROVISIONS
Sec. 1-1. - Designation and citation of Code.
The ordinances embraced in this and the following chapters shall constitute and be designated the "Code
of Ordinances, City of Dublin, Texas" and may be cited as the "Dublin Code." This Code shall not be deemed to
repeal any preamble, recital or finding of fact contained in any ordinance included in this Code, but all such
matters shall be deemed incorporated in the sections in this Code derived from such respective ordinances.
State law reference—Authority of city to adopt a civil and criminal code of ordinances, V.T.C.A., Local
Government Code § 53.001 et seq.
Sec. 1-2. - De nitions and rules of construction.
(a)

De nitions. The following de nitions and rules of construction shall apply to this Code and all ordinances unless
the context requires otherwise:

City. The term "city" shall mean the City of Dublin, Texas.
City council, council. The terms "city council" and "council" shall mean the city council of the City of Dublin,
Texas.
State law reference—Governing body, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 312.011.

Code. The term "Code" shall mean this Code of Ordinances, City of Dublin, Texas.
Computation of time. In computing any period of time prescribed or allowed by this Code the day of the
act, event or default from which the designated period of time begins to run shall not be included. The last day
of the period so computed shall be included unless it is a Saturday, Sunday or legal holiday, in which event, the
period shall run until the end of the next day which is neither a Saturday, Sunday or legal holiday.
State law reference—Computation of time for state procedures, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 311.014.

Conjunctions. Unless the context clearly indicates the contrary, where a provision involving two or more
items, conditions, provisions or events are connected by the conjunction "and," "or" or "either…or," the
conjunction shall be interpreted as follows:
(1)
"And" indicates that all of the connected terms, conditions, provisions or events apply.
(2)
1/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

"Or" indicates that the connected terms, conditions, provisions or events apply singly or in any combination.
(3)
"Either…or" indicates that the connected terms, conditions, provisions or events apply singly, but not in
combination.

County. The term "county" shall mean Erath County, Texas.
Delegation of authority. A provision that authorizes or requires a city officer or city employee to perform
an act or make a decision authorizes such officer or employee to act or make a decision through subordinates.

ETJ. The term "ETJ" shall mean the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the city.
Gender. A word importing the masculine gender only shall extend and be applied to females, firms,
partnerships and corporations as well as to males.
State law reference—Gender, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.012, 312.003.

Herein. The term "herein" shall mean in this Code.
May. The term "may" shall be construed as being permissive and not mandatory.
State law reference—May, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 311.016.

Month. The term "month" shall mean a calendar month.
State law reference—Month, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 312.011.

Number. Terms in the singular include the plural, and terms in the plural include the singular.
State law reference—Number, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.012, 312.003.

Oath swear. A solemn affirmation is the equivalent to an oath, and a person shall be deemed to have
sworn if such person makes such an affirmation. In such cases, the terms "swear" and "sworn" shall be
equivalent to the terms "affirm" and "affirmed."
State law reference—Oath, swear, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.005, 312.011.

Officers, departments, boards or employees, etc. Whenever reference is made to officers, departments,
boards or employees, etc., such reference shall mean and refer to the officers, departments, boards or
employees, etc., of the City of Dublin, Texas.

Owner. The term "owner," as applied to property, includes any part owner, joint owner, tenant in
common, tenant in partnership, joint tenant or tenant by the entirety of the whole or part of such property.

Person. The term "person" shall mean any human being, governmental or political subdivision or public
agency, public or private corporation, partnership, firm, association or other organization, joint stock
company, joint adventure, receiver, executor, trustee, conservator, assignee, agent, or other legal
2/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

representative of any of the foregoing or any other legal entity.
State law reference—Person, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 311.005.

Personal property. The term "personal property" shall mean any property other than real property.
Property. The term "property" shall include real property and personal property.
State law reference—Property, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.005, 312.011.

Real property. The term "real property" shall include land, tenements and hereditaments.
Regulations. The term "regulations" shall mean the provisions of any applicable ordinance, rule, regulation
or policy.

Shall. The term "shall" is to be construed as being mandatory.
State law reference—Shall, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 311.016.

Sidewalk. The term "sidewalk" shall mean any portion of a street between the curbline or lateral line of the
roadway and the adjacent property line intended for pedestrian use.
State law reference—Sidewalk, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 316.001, 541.302.

Signature or subscription by mark. The term "signature" or "subscription by mark" shall include a mark
when the signer or subscriber cannot write. In such situations, such person's name shall be written near the
mark by a witness who writes his own name near such person's name.
State law reference—Signature, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.005, 312.011.

State. The term "state" shall mean the State of Texas.
Street. The term "street" shall mean the entire width of a way held by the city in fee or by easement or
dedication that has a part open for public use for vehicular travel. The term does not include a designated
state or federal highway or road or a designated county road.
State law reference—Street, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 316.001.

Tense. The present tense shall include the past and future tenses, and the future tense shall include the
present tense.
State law reference—Tense, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.012, 312.003.

Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. The abbreviation "Vernon's Ann. Civ. St." shall mean the latest edition or supplement
to Vernon's Annotated Civil Statutes.
State law reference—Statutory references, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 312.008.

3/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

V.T.C.A. The abbreviation "V.T.C.A." shall mean and refer to the latest edition or supplement of Vernon's
Texas Code Annotated.
State law reference—Statutory references, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 312.008.

Written or in writing. The term "written" or "in writing" shall be construed to include any representation of
words, letters or figures, whether by printing or otherwise.
State law reference—Written, in writing, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.005, 312.011.

Year. The term "year" shall mean a calendar year.
State law reference—Year, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.005, 312.011.
(b)

Interpretation of penal provisions. The provisions of V.T.C.A., Penal Code titles 1, 2 and 3 shall apply in the
interpretation of all penal provisions of this Code to the extent that such penal code mandates that they shall
apply.
State law reference—Application of titles 1, 2 and 3 of Texas Penal Code, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 1.03.
Sec. 1-3. - Catchlines of sections.
The catchlines of the sections of this Code, printed in boldface type, are intended as mere catchwords to
indicate the contents of the section and are not titles of such sections, or any part of the section, nor, unless
expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any such section, including the catchline, is amended or
reenacted.
State law reference—Headings of statutes, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 311.024.
Sec. 1-4. - History notes.
The history or source notes appearing in parentheses after sections in this Code have no legal effect, but
are merely intended to indicate the legislative history of that section.
Sec. 1-5. - References to chapters or sections.
All references to chapters or sections are to the chapters or sections of this Code, unless otherwise
specified.
Sec. 1-6. - References and editor's notes.
Editor's notes, cross references and state law references that appear in this Code after sections or
subsections are provided for the convenience of the user of the Code and have no legal effect.

4/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 1-7. - Continuation of existing ordinances.
The provisions of this Code, insofar as they are substantially the same legislation previously adopted by
the city relating to the same subject matter, shall be construed as restatements and continuations thereof,
and not as new enactments.
Sec. 1-8. - E ect of repeal of ordinances.
(a)
The repeal of an ordinance shall not revive any ordinances in force before or at the time the ordinance repealed
took e ect.
(b)
The repeal of an ordinance shall not a ect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took e ect,
nor any suit, prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the repeal for an o ense committed or cause of
action arising under the ordinance repealed.
State law reference—Effect of repeal of a repealing statute, V.T.C.A., Government Code §§ 311.030, 312.007.
Sec. 1-9. - Certain ordinances not a ected by Code.
(a)
Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code shall a ect the validity of any of the following:
(1)
Any o ense or act committed or done, or any penalty or forfeiture incurred before the e ective date of this
Code.
(2)
Any administrative ordinances of the city not in con ict or inconsistent with this Code.
(3)
Any ordinance promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the city or authorizing the issue of any
bonds of the city or any evidence of the city's indebtedness or any contract, right, agreement, lease, deed or
other instrument or obligation assumed by the city.
(4)
Any right or franchise granted by any ordinance.
(5)
Any ordinance adopting the budget or any appropriation ordinance.
(6)
Any ordinance levying or imposing taxes.
(7)
Any ordinance providing for local improvements and assessments for such improvements.
(8)
Any ordinance on investment and other nancial policies.
(9)
5/428

Any ordinance levying a fee, rate, deposit or charge.
(10)
Any ordinance calling an election.
(11)
Any ordinance establishing positions, classifying positions, establishing pension or employee bene ts, setting
salaries of city o cers and employees or any personnel regulations or indemni cation policies, or otherwise
related to employees.
(12)
Any ordinance relating to the acquisition of lands by the city by condemnation proceedings.
(13)
Any ordinance annexing territory, excluding territory or extending the boundaries of the city.
(14)
Any ordinance regarding plats or subdivisions.
(15)
Any ordinance adopting or amending the comprehensive plan.
(16)
Any land use, development, zoning or rezoning ordinance or amendment to the zoning map.
(17)
Any ordinance authorizing street maintenance agreements.
(18)
Any ordinance establishing and prescribing the street grades of any street.
(19)
Any ordinance dedicating, establishing, naming, locating, relocating, opening, paving, widening, repairing or
vacating any street or public way.
(20)
Any ordinance prescribing through streets, parking and tra c regulations, speed limits, one-way tra c,
limitations on loads of vehicles or loading zones.
(21)
Any ordinance adopted by reference by any section of this Code and not included herein.
(22)
Any temporary or special ordinance.
(b)
All such ordinances are recognized as continuing in full force and e ect to the same extent as if published at
length in this Code. All ordinances are on le in the city secretary's o ce.
Sec. 1-10. - Severability.
The city council declares that it is its intent to enact this Code and all provisions adopted by reference in
this Code without invalid or unconstitutional provisions. The sections, subsections, paragraphs, sentences,
clauses and phrases of this Code and all provisions adopted by reference in this Code are severable so that if
6/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

any section, subsection, paragraph, sentence, clause and phrase of this Code, or of any provision adopted by
reference in this Code, is declared unconstitutional or invalid by judgment of a court of competent jurisdiction,
such judgment shall not affect the validity of any other remaining section, subsection, paragraph, sentence,
clause and phrase of this Code, or of any provision adopted by reference in this Code.
State law reference—Intention in enactment of statutes, Government Code § 311.021; severability of statutes,
V.T.C.A., Government Code § 311.032.
Sec. 1-11. - Amendments to Code; e ect of new ordinances; amendatory language.
(a)
All ordinances adopted subsequent to this Code that amend, repeal or in any way a ect this Code may be
numbered in accordance with the numbering system of the Code and printed for inclusion in the Code. Portions
of this Code repealed by subsequent ordinances may be excluded from this Code by omission from a ected
reprinted pages. The subsequent ordinances as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be
prima facie evidence of such subsequent ordinances until such time that this Code of Ordinances and
subsequent ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a new code of ordinances by the city council.
(b)
Amendments to provisions of this Code may be made with the following language: "Section ;#rule; (chapter,
article, division or subdivision, as appropriate) of the Code of Ordinances, City of Dublin, Texas is amended to
read as follows:…" (set out the new provisions in full).
(c)
If a new section, subdivision, division, article or chapter is to be added to the Code, the following language may
be used: "Section ;#rule; (chapter, article, division or subdivision, as appropriate) of the Code of Ordinances, City
of Dublin, Texas is created to read as follows:…" (set out the new provisions in full).
(d)
All provisions desired to be repealed should be repealed speci cally by section, subdivision, division, article or
chapter number, as appropriate, or by setting out the repealed provisions in full in the repealing ordinance.
State law reference—Adoption of municipal ordinances, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 52.001 et seq.
Sec. 1-12. - Supplementation of Code.
(a)
Supplements to this Code shall be prepared and printed whenever authorized or directed by the city. A
supplement to this Code shall include all substantive permanent and general parts of ordinances passed by the
city council or adopted by initiative and referendum during the period covered by the supplement and all
changes made thereby in the Code. The pages of the supplement shall be numbered so that they will t
properly into the Code and will, where necessary, replace pages that have become obsolete or partially
obsolete. The new pages shall be prepared so that when they have been inserted, the Code will be current
through the date of the adoption of the latest ordinance included in the supplement.
(b)
7/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

In preparing a supplement to this Code, all portions of the Code that have been repealed shall be excluded from
the Code by the omission of such repealed portions from reprinted pages.
(c)
When preparing a supplement to this Code, the person authorized to prepare the supplement may make
formal, nonsubstantive changes in ordinances and parts of ordinances included in the supplement as necessary
to embody them into a uni ed code. For example, the person may:
(1)
Arrange the material into appropriate organizational units.
(2)
Provide appropriate catchlines, headings and titles for chapters, articles, divisions, subdivisions and sections to
be included in the Code and make changes in any catchlines, headings and titles already in the Code.
(3)
Assign appropriate numbers to chapters, articles, divisions, subdivisions and sections to be added to the Code.
(4)
Where necessary to accommodate new material, change existing numbers assigned to chapters, articles,
divisions, subdivisions or sections.
(5)
Change the term "this ordinance," or terms of the same meaning, to "this chapter," "this article," "this division,"
"this subdivision," "this section" or to "sections ;#rule; through ;#rule;." The inserted section numbers will
indicate the sections of the Code which embody the substantive sections of the ordinance incorporated in the
Code.
(6)
Make other nonsubstantive changes necessary to preserve the original meaning of the ordinances inserted in
the Code. In no case shall the codi er make any change in the meaning or e ect of ordinance provisions
included in the supplement or already embodied in the Code.
Sec. 1-13. - General penalty; continuing violations.
(a)
Whenever, in this Code or in any ordinance, rule or police regulation of the city, an act is prohibited or is made
or declared to be unlawful or an o ense or a misdemeanor, or the doing of any act is required, or the failure to
do any act is declared to be unlawful, where no speci c penalty is provided, the violation of any provision of this
Code or any ordinance, rule or police regulation shall be punished by a ne not exceeding $500.00, and the
violation of any provision of this Code or any ordinance, rule or police regulation that governs re safety, zoning
or public health and sanitation, including dumping of refuse, shall be punished by a ne not exceeding
$2,000.00; provided, however, that where the o ense is one for which a penalty is xed by state law, the penalty
for such o ense shall be the same as xed by state law. The penalty provided by this subsection, unless another
penalty is expressly provided, shall apply to the amendment of any Code section, whether or not such penalty is
reenacted in the amendatory ordinance.
(b)

8/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Except where otherwise provided in this Code, each day an o ense continues shall constitute a separate
o ense.
(c)
In addition to the penalty prescribed in this section, the city may pursue other remedies such as abatement of
nuisances, injunctive or other equitable relief, administrative adjudications and revocation of licenses or
permits.
State law reference—Penalty for ordinance violations, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 54.001; jurisdiction
of municipal court, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 29.003.
Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 2-1. - Change to type A general law municipality; o cial name.
(a)
The Town of Dublin changes to a type A general law municipality.
(b)
The o cial name of the town shall be known as the "City of Dublin", and its governing body shall be known as
the "city council".
(Ord. No. 2-8-94-1, §§ 1, 3, 2-8-1994)

State law reference—Type A general law city, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 5.001; general powers,
V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 51.001—51.018.
Secs. 2-2—2-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - CITY COUNCIL
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 2-31. - Wards; elections; polling place.
(a)
Pursuant to the provisions of V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 22.031, 22.034 and 22.040, the city is divided
into four wards, and the governing body of the city shall consist of a mayor who shall be elected by the quali ed
voters of the city for a two-year term, and two councilmen from each ward who shall be elected for a two-year
term by the quali ed voters of the ward. A map and legal description of the wards is on le in the o ce of the
city secretary.
(b)
At the annual election, one councilman shall be elected from each ward for the regular term of two years, and
the mayor shall be elected for a two-year term at the annual election in 1995.
9/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(c)
Except as modi ed by this Code, elections for the councilmen and mayor shall be held in the manner set forth
under applicable state law.
(d)
The polling place shall remain at Dublin City Hall, 213 East Blackjack, Dublin, Texas.
(Ord. No. 2-8-94-2, §§ 1, 3—5, 2-8-1994; Ord. No. 10-8-01-4, § 2, 10-8-2001)

State law reference—Term of office, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 22.035.
Sec. 2-32. - Single member district plan.
The single member district plan for the city is approved. The boundaries of each single member district is
hereby modified, amended and redrawn for the purposes of apportioning the population of the city and city
council wards as set forth in the district plan on file in the office of the city secretary.
(Ord. No. 7-8-02-1, § 2, 7-8-2002)

Secs. 2-33—2-50. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - MEETINGS
Sec. 2-51. - Citizen communications.
Citizens appearing before the city council may make a presentation at the beginning of the meeting under
the agenda item "Citizen Communications". A sign-in form will be provided for those wishing to address the
city council. In addition, upon being recognized by the mayor, citizens may make comments or statements
regarding specific agenda items when such items are first called by the mayor, prior to the beginning of
discussion and deliberation among the councilmembers. Once the period of public statements and comments
on an agenda item has concluded and city council discussion begins, citizens shall not interrupt the discussion
and deliberation of business by the city council. The mayor, or the city council by majority vote, may reopen
such agenda item for public comment and discussion.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-7, § 1, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 12-10-01-2, § 1, 12-10-2001; Ord. No. 10-20-03-1, § 2, 10-20-2003)

Sec. 2-52. - Time limitations.
Except as waived, or otherwise authorized by a vote of the city council, the following time limitations shall
apply to citizen communications:
(1)

General citizen communications. Citizens signing up to speak at the beginning of city council meetings under the
item "Citizen Communications" shall, upon being recognized by the mayor, have three minutes to address the
city council. No citizen shall have more than three minutes unless approved by majority vote of the city council.

10/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Citizens may also provide any additional comments or information in writing to the city council before, during or
after the city council meeting.
(2)

Citizen comments on speci c agenda items. Citizens shall, when recognized by the mayor, have two minutes to
address the city council regarding the subject of an agenda item then being considered by the city council.
Citizens may also provide any additional comments or information in writing to the city council before, during or
after the city council meeting.
(3)

Sponsor comments. A citizen or person who has made an application then being considered by the city council,
or who is the sponsor or speaker for a group that requested the agenda item, shall, upon being recognized by
the mayor, have ve minutes in which to speak on the agenda item.
(4)

Compliance required. Any person that, after notice and warning, refuses to comply with the applicable time
limits set forth above shall be deemed to be disrupting the meeting and may be removed as provided in this
division.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-7, §§ 1, 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 12-10-01-2, § 2, 12-10-2001; Ord. No. 10-20-03-1, § 3, 10-20-2003)

Sec. 2-53. - Rules of conduct for meetings.
The rules, regulations and provisions of this division are intended for the purpose of providing for the
efficient accomplishment of the public business. Except for a breach of the peace, it is the intent of this
division that no person shall be removed, prosecuted or fined for a violation of this division unless such
violation occurs after a warning is issued by the presiding officer or the city council. The rules of conduct,
order and decorum for city council meetings provided in this division shall include the following rules:
(1)

Conduct. Meetings of the city council shall be conducted in an orderly manner to ensure that the public has a
full opportunity to be heard and that the deliberate process of the city council is retained at all times. The
presiding o cer of the city council, who shall be the mayor or mayor pro tem, or in their absence any other
member so designated by the city council, shall be responsible for maintaining the order and decorum of
meetings.
(2)

Rules of conduct. While any meeting of the city council is in session, the following rules of conduct, order and
decorum shall be observed:
a.

Councilmembers. The members of the city council shall preserve order and decorum. A member of the city
council should not by conversation or other means delay or interrupt the city council proceedings when the
presiding o cer or another member of the city council has the oor.
b.

11/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

City sta members. Employees of the city shall observe the same rules of order and decorum as those which
apply to the members of the city council.
c.

Persons addressing the city council. Public communications at the city council meetings should not be a
substitute for any item that can be handled during the normal working hours of the municipal government. The
primary purpose of public communications is to allow citizens the opportunity to formally communicate with
the city council as a whole on an agenda item, or on citizen communications for matters that cannot be handled
during the regular working hours of the city government. Each person who addresses the city council shall do so
in an orderly manner and shall not made personal, impertinent, slanderous or profane remarks to any member
of the city council, sta or general public such as to disrupt the meeting. Any person who makes such remarks,
or who utters loud, threatening, personal or abusive language, or engages in any other disorderly conduct, that
disrupts, disturbs or otherwise impedes the orderly conduct of a city council meeting, may be warned and may
be removed from the city council meeting, and barred from further attendance of the city council meeting
during that meeting, as provided in this division.
d.

Members of the audience. No person in the audience at a city council meeting shall engage in disorderly or
boisterous conduct, including the utterance of loud, threatening or abusive language, whistling, stamping of feet
or other acts which disturb, disrupt or otherwise impede the orderly conduct of the city council meeting. Any
person who conducts himself in the aforementioned manner to disrupt the orderly conduct of the meeting
shall, at the discretion of the presiding o cer or a majority of the city council, be barred from further audience
before the city council during that meeting.
e.

Addressing the city council. A person wishing to address the city council regarding an item that is on the city
council meeting agenda shall submit a request on the form provided. Persons wishing to discuss a non-agenda
item on a subject of city business, or local or community interest over which the city council has or may assert
jurisdiction, shall submit a request for citizen communication on the form provided. No person shall address the
city council without rst being recognized by the presiding o cer.
(Ord. No. 10-20-03-1, § 4, 10-20-2003)

Sec. 2-54. - Procedures for addressing the city council.
The following procedures shall be observed by persons addressing the city council:
(1)
Each person addressing the city council shall step to the podium provided for the use of the public and shall
state his or her name and address, the organization if any which he or she represents, and, if during the citizen
communication portion of the meeting, the subject he or she wishes to discuss.
(2)
During the citizen communication portion, any subject which is applicable to an item on the agenda, is not a
matter regarding the business of the city, or is not a matter of local community concern over which the city
12/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

council has or may assert jurisdiction, may be deemed irrelevant by the presiding o cer or the city council and
upon such nding being made by the mayor or city council and notice being given to the speaker the remarks
shall be concluded.
(3)
Each person shall con ne his or her remarks to the city council agenda item or the stated citizen communication
subject being addressed.
(4)
Each person shall limit his or her remarks to the time permitted for such presentation as set forth in section 252, unless further time is granted by the city council.
(5)
All remarks shall be addressed to the presiding o cer and city council as a whole, and not to any single member
thereof, unless in response to a question from such member.
(Ord. No. 10-20-03-1, § 5, 10-20-2003)

Sec. 2-55. - Enforcement of decorum.
The rules of decorum and procedures for addressing the city council set forth above shall be enforced in
the following manner:
(1)

Warning. The presiding o cer shall request that a person who is breaching the rules of conduct, decorum or
procedures for addressing the city council be orderly and comply with the rules. If, after receiving a warning
from the presiding o cer, a person persists in disrupting the meeting, the presiding o cer shall order him or
her, to leave the city council meeting. If such person does not remove himself or herself, the presiding o cer
may order any law enforcement o cer who is on duty at the meeting as sergeant-at-arms of the city council, or
any other law enforcement o cer present, to remove that person from the city council chambers. Any
participant that physically threatens another participant by words or action may be warned and removed from
the meeting if not thereafter fully compliant with this division.
(2)

Removal. Any law enforcement o cer who is serving as sergeant-at-arms of the city council, or otherwise
present, shall carry out all orders and instructions given by the presiding o cer for the purpose of maintaining
order and decorum at the city council meeting. Upon instruction of the presiding o cer, it shall be the duty of
the sergeant-at-arms, or o cer, to remove from the city council meeting any person who is disrupting the
meeting and the proceedings of the city council.
(3)

Resisting removal. Any person who resists removal by the sergeant-at-arms, or o cer, shall be charged with a
violation of this section, unless such resistance rises to the point of being and becomes and is prosecuted as
resisting arrest.
(4)

13/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Penalty. Any person who commits a breach of the peace, or who, after notice and warning, violates this division
or who disrupts a city council meeting and is removed, will be referred to the chief of police for investigation and
the ling of charges as appropriate. Any person who commits a breach of the peace or who, after notice and
warning, violates this division shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished by a ne not to exceed
$500.00.
(5)

Motion to enforce. If the presiding o cer fails to enforce the rules set forth above, any member of the city
council may move to require him or her to do so, and an a rmative vote of a majority of the city council shall
require him or her to do so. If the presiding o cer fails to carry out the will of a majority of the city council, the
majority may designate another member of the city council to act as presiding o cer for the limited purpose of
enforcing any rule of this section which it wishes to enforce.
(6)

Breach of the peace. Notwithstanding any other term or provision of this division, any participant who shall by
their actions commit a breach of the peace, as de ned by the Texas Penal Code, may be arrested by any
certi ed law enforcement observing such action and may be led on and prosecuted therefor.
(Ord. No. 10-20-03-1, § 6, 10-20-2003)

ARTICLE III. - OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 2-81. - Personnel policies and procedures.
(a)

Adopted. The city shall adopt and, from time to time as necessary and advisable, amend, modify, review and
revise comprehensive personnel policies and procedures that shall be applicable to the o cers and employees
of the city. The city manager shall cause such policies and procedures, and any proposed modi cations or
amendments, to be drafted, prepared and recommended to the city council for review and action, as necessary,
to serve the best interests of the city and its employees and citizens.
(b)

City council approval. All personnel policies and procedures of the city, and all revisions, modi cations and
amendments thereto, shall be approved by the city council, in its discretion, by resolution, and no such policies,
procedures, revisions, modi cations or amendments shall be in e ect, except as approved by the city council
acting by resolution. Such policies, procedures, rules and regulations approved by resolution of the city council
shall be and remain in e ect until such policies, procedures, rules and regulations are repealed, modi ed or
amended by resolution, and all, or any part of, such policies, procedures, rules, regulations, revisions,
modi cations and amendments may be repealed, deleted, modi ed or amended at any time by the city council
acting in its discretion.
14/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(c)

Employment contracts. The personnel policies and procedures, rules and regulations of the city shall never be
construed or interpreted to create or result in any contract for employment, or to create, establish or result in
any o cer or employee of the city having or obtaining a property interest in any job, position, employment or
future bene t with the city. The city is an at-will employer, and it is the policy of the city that all o cers and
employees of the city shall be employees at-will, except for a written contract executed by and between the city
and an individual o cer or employee, if any, which is approved by a majority vote of the city council, acting at a
duly noticed public meeting, with the advice and counsel of the city attorney. No o cer or employee of the city
shall have and obtain, by implication or otherwise, any employment contract with the city.
(d)

Interpretation and construction. The personnel policies and procedures, rules and regulations of the city, as
approved by resolution from time to time, shall be interpreted and construed consistent with this section and in
a manner consistent with the city being and remaining an at-will employer.
(Ord. No. 8-9-99-1, §§ 1—4, 8-9-1999)

The city manager shall be appointed for an indefinite period and shall be subject to discharge at the will of
the city council. Both appointment and removal shall require a majority vote of the city council.

The annual salary and benefits of the city manager shall be set by the mayor and city council.
(Ord. No. 10-10-78-2, § 3, 10-10-1978; Ord. No. 3-14-05-4, § 4, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 2-104. - Temporary absence or disability.
During the prolonged absence or disability of the city manager, the city council shall designate some
properly qualified person to perform the duties of said office. The city manager shall make a reasonable effort
to notify the mayor and city secretary of any planned absence as soon as practicable before his or her
absence.

(Ord. No. 10-10-78-2, § 4, 10-10-1978; Ord. No. 3-14-05-4, § 5, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 2-105. - Powers and duties.
The duties and authority of the city manager shall be as follows:
(1)
To devote all working time and attention to the a airs of the city and to be responsible to the city council for the
e cient administration of the city's a airs.
(2)
To see that all provisions of federal, state, and local laws, ordinances, and resolutions are enforced.
(3)
To nominate, with the approval of the mayor and city council, all heads of departments. The city manager may
suspend department heads without pay pending approval of city council. A special city council meeting must be
called as soon as possible, in accordance with V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 551, with a majority of city council
present and voting to act.
(4)
To exercise supervision and control over all departments created by the city council.
(5)
To attend all meetings of the city council with a right to take part in the discussion—but having no vote—and to
be noti ed of all special meetings of the city council.
(6)
To see that all contracts with the city, including public utility franchises, are faithfully kept and performed and,
upon knowledge of any violation thereof, to call the same to the attention of the city council.
(7)
To assist the mayor in preparing and submitting to the city council, prior to the beginning of each scal year, a
budget of proposed income and expenditures for the ensuing year, as well as to invest all idle funds with the
assistance of the nance committee of the city council.
(8)
To instruct the city secretary to le the budget as required by state law after the budget has been approved by
the city council.
(9)
To keep the city council advised of the nancial condition and future needs of the city and to make such
recommendations for the welfare of the citizens of Dublin.
(10)
To report on nances and on administrative activities for the preceding year and to publish such reports as
required by law.
(11)
The limited administrative and personnel duties and responsibilities of the mayor, with respect to the day to day
operation of the city, which are by statute to be performed solely by the mayor, may be delegated by the mayor
to the city manager. The duties and responsibilities of the city manager shall be in addition to, and not in lieu of,
16/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

the day to day administrative and personnel duties of the mayor. To the fullest extent not in con ict with state
law, this division, or the express actions and directions by a majority vote of the city council, the city manager
shall have the responsibility, and the authority incident thereto, for the day to day supervision and management
of the city and the salaried o cers, employees and personnel of the city.
(Ord. No. 10-10-78-2, § 5(a—k), 10-10-1978; Ord. No. 3-14-05-4, § 6, 3-14-2005)

State law reference—Municipal budget, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 102.001 et seq.
Sec. 2-106. - Restrictions of city council.
(a)
The city council may consult and advise the city manager; make inquiries regarding appointment or removal of
personnel; and express their opinion regarding such appointments and removals.
(b)
In regard to the administrative and executive duties under the jurisdiction of the city manager, the city council
and its members shall deal solely through the city manager, and neither the city council nor any councilmember
shall give orders to any subordinate of the city manager, either privately or publicly.
(c)
Any willful violation of subsection (b) of this section by any member of the city council shall constitute o cial
misconduct.

DIVISION 4. - PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
Sec. 2-181. - Creation and purpose.
(a)

[Purpose.] A planning and zoning commission is created in order to accomplish the following purposes:
(1)
To identify community needs and to advise the city council of their short-range and long-range implications for
the total development of the city;
(2)
To recommend achievable community goals as a basis for long-range planning and development programs;
(3)
To recommend plans, programs and policies that will aid the entire community in achieving its de ned goals;
and
(4)
18/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

To interpret the adopted plans and programs to concerned citizens so that private activities and desires may be
accomplished in harmony with public needs and policies.
(b)

Membership and appointment. The planning and zoning commission shall be composed of ve persons with at
least three being quali ed electors of the city and two may be residents in the extraterritorial jurisdiction. The
city council will consider for appointment to the commission only those persons who have demonstrated their
civic interest, general knowledge of the community, independent judgment, interest in planning and zoning, and
availability to prepare for and attend meetings. It is the intent of the city council that members shall, by reason
of diversity of their individual occupations, constitute a commission, which is broadly representative of the
community.
(c)

Terms of o ce; lling of vacancies. The terms of three of the members shall expire on January 1 of each oddnumbered year and the terms of two of the members shall expire on January 1 of each even-numbered year.
The members of the commission shall be identi ed by place numbers one through ve. The odd-numbered
places shall expire in the odd-numbered years; the even-numbered places shall expire in the even-numbered
years. Commission members may be appointed to succeed themselves. Vacancies shall be lled for unexpired
terms, but no member shall be appointed for a term in excess of two years. Newly-appointed members shall be
installed at the rst regular commission meeting after their appointment.
(d)

Appointment of chairperson and vice chairperson. The chairperson and vice chairperson shall be appointed by
the mayor with approval of the council.
(e)

Organization; election of o cers; record of proceedings. The commission shall hold an organization meeting in
February of each year. The commission shall elect a secretary and such other o cers as its deems necessary
either from its membership or from sta representatives assigned by the mayor to work with the commission.
The commission shall meet regularly and shall designate the time and place of its meetings. The commission
shall keep a record of its proceedings consistent with the provisions of this Code and the requirements of law.
(f)

Duties and powers. The planning and zoning commission is charged with the duly and invested with the
authority to:
(1)
Inspect property and premises at reasonable hours when required to discharge its responsibilities under the
laws of the state and of the city.
(2)
Formulate and recommend to the city council for its adoption a comprehensive plan for the orderly growth and
development of the city and its environs, and from time to time recommend such changes in the plan as it nds
will facilitate the movement of people and goods, and the health, recreation, safety and general welfare of the
citizens of the city.
(3)
19/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Formulate a zoning plan as may be deemed best to carry out the goals of the comprehensive plan; hold public
hearings and make recommendations to the city council relating to the creation, amendment, and
implementation of zoning regulations and districts as provided by ordinance, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code,
as amended, authorizing cities to pass regulations.
(4)
Exercise all the powers of a commission as to approval of disapproval of plans, plats, or replats and vacations of
plans, plats or replats set out in the subdivision ordinance and V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 212
(Municipal Regulation of Subdivisions and Property Development).
(5)
Study and make recommendations on the location, extension, planning, vacating and closing of public rights-ofway, parks and other public places.
(6)
Study and make recommendations concerning the capital improvements program, including the construction of
public buildings, bridges, viaducts, street xtures and other structures and appurtenances. Study and make
recommendations on the design or alteration and on the location or relocation of works of art which are, or may
become, the property of the city.
(7)
Initiate, in the name of the city, for consideration at public hearings, all proposals: For the opening, vacating, or
closing of public rights-of-way, parks, or other public places; for the original zoning of annexed areas; and for
the change of zoning district boundaries on an area-wide basis. No fee shall be required for the ling of any
such proposal in the name of the city.
(8)
Formulate and recommend to the city council policies and regulations consistent with the adopted
comprehensive plan governing the location and/or operation of utilities, public facilities and services owned or
under the control of the city.
(9)
Review and make recommendations concerning annexation of land into the city.
(10)
Keep itself informed with references to the progress of city planning in the United States and other countries
and recommend improvements in the adopted plans of the city.
(11)
Submit a progress report to the city council every 180 days that summarizes its activities, major
accomplishments for the past year, and a proposed work program for the coming year. The report shall be
given to the city council in March and September and contain the attendance record of all members and the
identity of commission o cers for the year.
(g)

Meetings and quorum.
(1)
A motion may be made by any member other than the presiding o cer.
(2)
20/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

A motion to approve any matter before the commission or to recommend approval of any request requiring city
council action shall require a majority vote of the quorum of the members present. When fewer than all the
members are present for the voting and when all motions to recommend on a given application fail to carry by a
majority of the quorum of members present, consideration of the application shall be continued to the next
regular meeting upon motion carried by a majority of those present. However, a request or application shall not
be continued to the next regular meeting and shall be recorded in the minutes as a denial if all the members are
present for the vote and a motion fails to carry by a majority votes.
(h)

Disquali cation from voting.
(1)
A member shall disqualify themselves from voting whenever they nd that they have a personal or monetary
interest in the property under appeal, or that they will be directly a ected by the decision of the commission.
(2)
A member may disqualify himself or herself from voting whenever any applicant, or his or her agent, has sought
to in uence the vote of the member on the application, other than in the public hearing.
(i)

Rules of procedure.
(1)

Organization and o cers. In the absence of both the chairperson and vice chairperson, the commission shall
elect an acting chairperson.
(2)

Meetings.
a.

Quorum. A quorum shall consist of three members.
b.

Agenda. The city secretary shall prepare an agenda for each meeting of the commission, and shall attach to
each agenda a report of matters pending further action by the commission. The city secretary shall post a copy
of the agenda in the city hall as required by law for a period of three full calendar days, not counting the day of
posting, but which may count the day of the meeting.
c.

Regular meetings. Regular meetings shall be council chambers of the city hall, unless otherwise determined by
the commission.
d.

Special meetings. Special meetings for any purpose may be held: on the call of the chairperson, or on request of
two or more members and by giving written notice to all members deposited in the mail at least 72 hours
before the meeting, or as may be scheduled by a majority of the commission at any previous meeting. The time
and place of the special meeting shall be determined by the convening authority.
e.

Public meetings. Any party in interest may appear in his own behalf or be represented by council or agent.
(3)
21/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

O cial records.
a.

O cial records. The o cial records shall be the minutes of the commission, together with all ndings, decisions
and other o cial records of the commission.
b.

Recording of vote. The minutes of the commission's proceedings shall show the vote of each member, or
indicate a member's absence or failure to vote.
c.

Files; retention. All matters coming before the commission shall be led in the city's records. Original papers of
all requests and proposals shall be retained as a part of the permanent record.
d.

Public record. The o cial records and citizen requests led for commission action in regular or special meetings
shall be on le in the city hall and shall be open to public inspection during customary working hours.
(4)

Application procedures.
a.

Written request required. Every proposal submitted for commission action shall be made in writing. Where
appropriate, the city shall provide application forms. The proposal shall be led on city-provided forms, shall be
accompanied by all prescribed fees, and shall be complete in all respects before the city shall accept it for ling.
b.

Schedules and instructions. Every proposal or request for commission action or recommendation shall be led,
processed and considered in accordance with this section.
c.

Submission of supporting information. Information supporting a request or recommendation to approve or
disapprove any proposal before the commission shall be submitted through the secretary in writing or to the
commission in public meeting.
d.

Withdrawal of proposal. When any applicant desires to withdraw his or her proposal he or she may do so by
ling a written request with the secretary. Such request shall be e ective upon the date of its o cial receipt,
provided, however, that no such request shall be valid after notices have been mailed, except on action of the
commission. Withdrawal of a proposal at any stage of its processing shall terminate all consideration of it by the
city, and the case le shall be closed.
(Ord. No. 6-11-07-2, §§ 1—9, 6-11-2007)

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY

Secs. 2-191—2-210. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - INVESTMENT POLICY
Sec. 2-211. - Adoption.
This division amends, establishes and adopts the authorized and official Investment Policy of the City of
Dublin, Texas. Such investment policy shall be as set forth in sections 2-212—2-224 of this division and, for the
purposes of administrative efficiency and use, sections 2-212—2-224 may be excerpted and placed in any
manuals, reports or documents as the "City of Dublin, Texas Investment Policy".
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 1, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-212. - Investment policy.
The funds and financial resources of the City of Dublin shall be managed and invested in conformance
with the provisions and requirements of the PFIA; provided that, where the requirements of this policy are
more restrictive, the terms, provisions and requirements of this investment policy shall control.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-213. - Scope.
(a)
This investment policy applies to all nancial assets of the city and includes all funds listed as follows:
(1)
General fund.
(2)
Special revenue funds.
(3)
Debt service funds.
(4)
Enterprise funds.
(5)
Trust and agency funds.
(b)

Investment strategy. The city maintains portfolios which utilize speci c investment strategy considerations
designed to address the unique characteristics of the fund groups represented in the portfolios:
(1)

General, enterprise, and trust and agency funds: Investment strategies for these funds have as their primary
objective to assure that anticipated cash ows are matched with adequate investment liquidity. The secondary
23/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

objective is to create a portfolio structure that will experience minimal volatility during economic cycles. This
may be accomplished by purchasing high quality, short to medium-term securities which will complement each
other in a laddered or barbell maturity structure. The dollar-weighted average maturity of 365 days or less will
be calculated using the stated nal maturity date of each security. Funds shall be managed and invested with
the objectives of safety, liquidity and yield, in that order of priority.
(2)

Special revenue funds: Investment strategies for special revenue or special purpose fund portfolios have as their
primary objective to assure that anticipated cash ows are matched with adequate investment liquidity. These
portfolios should include at least ten percent in highly liquid investments to allow for exibility and
unanticipated project outlays. The stated nal maturity dates of securities held should not exceed the estimated
project completion date. Funds shall be managed and invested with the objectives of safety, liquidity and yield,
in that order of priority.
(3)

Debt service funds: Investment strategies for debt service funds shall have as the primary objective the
assurance of investment liquidity adequate to cover the debt service obligation on the required payment date.
Securities purchased shall not have a stated nal maturity date which exceeds the debt service payment date.
Funds shall be managed and invested with the objectives of safety, liquidity and yield, in that order of priority.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-214. - Statement of cash management philosophy.
The city shall maintain a comprehensive cash management program, to include the effective collection of
all accounts receivable, the prompt deposit of receipts to the city's bank accounts, the payment of obligations
so as to comply with state law and in accord with vendor invoices, and the prudent investment of idle funds in
accordance with this policy.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-215. - Objectives.
The city's investment program shall be conducted so as to accomplish the following objectives, listed in
priority order:
(1)
Safety of the principal invested;
(2)
Availability of su cient cash to pay obligations of the city when due;
(3)
Provide for diversi cation as appropriate given the total funds invested;
(4)

24/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Investment of idle cash to obtain a market rate of return throughout budgetary and economic cycles, consistent
with state and local laws and the objectives listed above.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-216. - Delegation of authority and training.
(a)
The city manager is responsible for overall management of the city's investment program and is designated as
the city's investment o cer. Accordingly, the city secretary is responsible for day-to-day administration of the
investment program and for the duties listed below:
Because the city secretary is responsible for duties that include the negotiation and execution of
investment transactions, the city secretary will also be designated as an investment officer.
(1)
Maintain current information as to available cash balances in city accounts, and as to the amount of idle cash
available for investment.
(2)
Make investments in accord with this policy.
(3)
Ensure that all investments are adequately secured.
(b)
The city manager shall accomplish such tasks and duties by supervising and directing the city secretary, or such
other designated o cer assigned such duties, regardless of the title thereof.
(c)
In order to ensure quali ed and capable investment management and in compliance with the PFIA, all
investment o cers shall attend at least one training session, from an independent training source approved by
the governing body, and containing at least ten hours of instruction relating to the o cer's responsibility under
the PFIA within 12 months after assuming duties. Thereafter, the investment o cer shall additionally attend at
least one training session, from an independent training source approved by the governing body, and
containing at least ten hours of instruction relating to the o cer's responsibility under the PFIA not less than
once in a two-year period.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-217. - Prudence.
(a)
Investments shall be made with judgment and care, under prevailing circumstances that a person of prudence,
discretion and intelligence would exercise in the management of the person's own a airs, not for speculation,
but for investment, considering the probable safety of capital and the probable income to be derived.
Investment of funds shall be governed by the following investment objectives, in order of priority:
25/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(1)
Preservation and safety of principal;
(2)
Liquidity; and
(3)
Yield.
(b)
In determining whether an investment o cer has exercised prudence with respect to an investment decision,
the determination shall be made taking into consideration:
(1)
The investment of all funds, or funds under the city's control, over which the o cer had responsibility rather
than a consideration as to the prudence of a single investment;, and
(2)
Whether the investment decision was consistent with the written investment policy.
(c)
The investment o cer, acting in accordance with written procedures and exercising due diligence, shall not be
held personally responsible for a speci c security's credit risk or market price changes, provided that these
deviations are reported immediately to the governing body and that appropriate action is taken to control
adverse developments.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 2256.006.
Sec. 2-218. - Investments.
(a)

Authorized investments. The funds available for investment in any fund of the city may be invested in the
following:
(1)
U.S. Treasury bills, notes or bonds, which are guaranteed as to principal and interest by the full faith and credit
of the United States of America;
(2)
Certi cates of deposit and other evidences of deposit at a nancial institution that; a) has its main o ce or a
branch o ce in Texas and is guaranteed or insured by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation or its
successor; b) is secured by obligations in a manner and amount provided by law for deposits of the city; or c) is
executed through a depository institution that has its main o ce or a branch o ce in Texas that participates in
the certi cate of deposit account registry service (CDARS) and meets the requirements of the Public Funds
Investment Act;
(3)
Direct obligations of the State of Texas or its agencies;
26/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(4)
Other obligations, which are unconditionally guaranteed or insured by the State of Texas or the United States of
America; and
(5)
Texas Local Government Investment Pools, which invest in instruments and follow practices allowed by law as
de ned in V.T.C.A., Texas Government Code § 2256.016, and have been authorized by the city council.
(b)

Not authorized investments. The following investment options are not authorized and are speci cally prohibited
by state law:
(1)
Obligations whose payment represents the coupon payments on the outstanding principal balance of the
underlying mortgage-backed security collateral and pays no principal;
(2)
Obligations whose payment represents the principal stream of cash ow from the underlying mortgage-backed
security and bears no interest;
(3)
Collateralized mortgage obligations that have a stated nal maturity date of greater than ten years;
(4)
Collateralized mortgage obligations, the interest rate of which is determined by an index that adjusts opposite
to the changes in a market index.
(c)

Selection of securities providers. A list will be maintained of "primary" dealers or regional dealers that qualify
under Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Rule 15C3-1 (Uniform Net Capital Rule). All nancial
institutions and broker/dealers who desire to become quali ed for investment transactions must supply the
following as appropriate:
The city council shall review, revise, and adopt a list of authorized broker/dealers at least
annually.
(1)
Audited nancial statements.
(2)
Proof of nancial industry regulatory authority (FINRA) certi cation.
(3)
Proof of state registration.
(4)
Completed broker/dealer questionnaire.
(5)
Certi cation of having read, understood, and agreed to comply with the investment policy in compliance with
the PFIA.
(d)
27/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

In order to create a competitive pricing environment for each investment transaction, the city shall solicit
quotations from multiple authorized broker/dealers.
(e)
All nancial institutions and broker/dealers who desire to become quali ed bidders for investment transactions
must provide an investment provider certi cate in compliance with the PFIA. No security shall be purchased
from any person who has not delivered the city an instrument in substantially the form required by V.T.C.A.,
Government Code § 2256.005(k).
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

State law reference—Authorized investments, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 2256.009 et seq.
Sec. 2-219. - Maximum maturity.
(a)
No individual investment will be made for longer than a 12-month period except with the prior approval of the
city council.
(b)
The maximum average dollar-weighted maturity allowed for pooled investments, based on the stated maturity
date for the portfolio, shall not exceed 180 days.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-220. - Qualifying institutions.
Investments may be made with or through the following institutions:
(1)
Federally insured banks located in the State of Texas.
(2)
Primary government security dealers reporting to the Market Reports Division of the Federal Reserve Bank of
New York.
(3)
Regional broker/dealers that have provided a certi cate in compliance with the PFIA and have been approved by
the city council.
(4)
Local Government Investment Pools established in compliance with the PFIA and have been approved by the
city council.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-221. - Collateralization and safekeeping.
(a)
28/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The city will accept as collateral for its certi cates of deposit and other evidence of deposit the following
securities:
(1)
FDIC coverage;
(2)
U.S. Treasury bills, notes or bonds;
(3)
State of Texas bonds;
(4)
Other obligations of the U.S. or its agencies and instrumentalities;
(5)
Letter of credit as issued by the Federal Home Loan Bank; and
(6)
Bonds issued by other Texas governmental entities (city, county, school, special districts), with a remaining
maturity of 20 years or less.
(b)
Securities pledged as collateral must be retained in an independent third party bank and the city shall be
provided the original safekeeping receipt on each pledged security. The investment o cer may approve release
of collateral, and any such release must be made in writing prior to its removal from the safekeeping account.
(c)
The nancial institution(s) with which the city invests and/or maintains other deposits shall provide quarterly,
and as requested by the city, a listing of the collateral pledged to the city marked to current market prices. The
listing shall include at a minimum, total pledged securities itemized by:
(1)
Name, type and description of the security.
(2)
Safekeeping receipt number.
(3)
CUSIP number.
(4)
Par value.
(5)
Current market value.
(6)
Maturity date.
(d)
Diversi cation. The city's investments shall be diversi ed to eliminate the risk of loss resulting from over
concentration of assets in a speci c maturity, a speci c issuer or a speci c class of securities. The following
general constraints shall apply:
(1)
29/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Maturities shall be staggered to avoid undue concentration of assets in a speci c maturity sector; and
(2)
Maturities selected shall provide for stability of income and reasonable liquidity.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-222. - Reports and review.
(a)
The city secretary shall prepare and submit to the city manager each calendar quarter, a summary report
showing a list of investments by city fund, the market value of each such investment, the total value of all
investments and cash on hand for each such fund, the annualized return for such fund for the previous
calendar quarter. The city manager shall review and approve such report and forward a copy thereof to each
member of the city council. The report shall contain a statement of compliance of the city's investment portfolio,
with state law and the investment strategy and policy approved by the city council and the statement must be
signed by all investment o cers.
(b)
In conjunction with the annual independent audit, the city manager and the city secretary shall cause a
compliance audit of management controls on the investments and adherence to this investment policy.
(c)
Performance standards. The investment portfolio will be managed in accordance with the parameters speci ed
within this policy. The portfolio should obtain a market average rate of return during a market/economic
environment of stable interest rates. A series of appropriate benchmarks shall be established against which
portfolio performance shall be compared. "Weighted average yield to maturity" shall be the portfolio
performance measurement standard.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

State law reference—Internal management reports, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 2256.023.
Sec. 2-223. - Continuing education and training.

Continuing education and training. The city manager and the city secretary shall become and remain
familiar with the requirements of the PFIA; and advise and consult with the officers and governing body of the
city for the purpose of assuring the city's compliance with this investment policy and the PFIA, and to assure
that the officers and council members of the city receive the training, if any, required by the PFIA.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-5, § 2, 12-13-1999; Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-908-4, §§ 1, 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-08-1, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)

Sec. 2-224. - Selection of depositories.
(a)

30/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Bidding process. Depositories shall be selected through the city's banking services procurement process, which
shall include a formal request for proposal (RFP) issued in compliance with applicable state law. This contract
can be extended as per the RFP speci cations. In selecting depositories, the credit worthiness of institutions
shall be considered, and the city manager shall conduct a comprehensive review of prospective depositories'
credit characteristics and nancial history.
(b)

Collateralized deposits. All depository deposits shall be insured or collateralized in compliance with applicable
state law. The city reserves the right, in its sole discretion, to accept or reject any form of insurance or
collateralization pledged towards depository deposits. Financial institutions serving as the city's depositories will
be required to sign a depository agreement with the city. The collateralized deposit portion of the agreement
shall de ne the city's rights to the collateral in case of default, bankruptcy or closing and shall establish a
perfected security interest in compliance with federal and state regulations, including:
(1)
The agreement must be in writing;
(2)
The agreement has to be executed by the depository and the city contemporaneously with the acquisition of the
asset;
(3)
The agreement must be approved by the board of directors or designated committee of the depository and a
copy of the meeting minutes must be delivered to the city; and
(4)
The agreement must be part of the depository's "o cial record" continuously since its execution.
(Ord. No. 9-12-05-4, §§ 1, 2, 9-12-2005; Ord. No. 09-18-06-2, §§ 1, 2, 9-18-2006; Ord. No. 6-9-08-4, § 2, 6-9-2008; Ord. No. 10-14-081, §§ 1, 2, 10-14-2008)
