ARTICLE VI. - CLAIMS AGAINST THE CITY
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Secs. 2-251—2-270. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - TORT CLAIMS
Sec. 2-271. - Notice required.
Before the city shall be liable in any suit, including suits for damages, injury or destruction to property of
any kind or nature or for damages, torts or injuries to persons of any kind or nature, in the event the injury
results in death or injuries to another, the person who may have a cause of action under the law by reason of

31/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

such death or injury shall, within 60 days or for good cause shown within six months from the date the
damage or injury was received, serve written notice upon the mayor and city council which includes all of the
following information:
(1)
The date and time when the injury or damage occurred and the location of the incident.
(2)
The nature of the damage or injury sustained.
(3)
The apparent extent of the damage or injury sustained.
(4)
A speci c and detailed statement of the facts of the incident and under what circumstances the damage or
injury occurred.
(5)
The amount for which each claimant will settle.
(6)
The actual place of residence of each claimant by street, number, city and state on the date the claim is
presented, and the actual residence of such claimant for the six months immediately preceding the incident.
(7)
In the case or personal injury, tort claims or death, the names and addresses of all persons who, according to
the knowledge or information of the claimant, witnessed the happening of the injury, or any part thereof, and
the names of the doctors, if any, to whose care the injured person is committed.
(8)
In the case of property damage, the location of the damaged property at the time the claim was submitted,
along with the names and addresses of all persons who witnessed the incident, or any part thereof, or who have
relevant information.
(Ord. No. 9-13-99-2, § 1, 9-13-1999)

State law reference—Notice of tort claim, V.T.C.A., Civil Practice and Remedies Code § 101.101.
Sec. 2-272. - Suits.
No suit of any nature whatsoever shall be instituted or maintained against the city unless the plaintiffs
therein shall ever prove that prior to the filing of the original petition the plaintiffs complied with the
notification requirements set forth herein and did thereby request from the city council the redress,
satisfaction, compensation or relief demanded in such suit, and that the same was, by vote of the city council,
refused.
(Ord. No. 9-13-99-2, § 2, 9-13-1999)

Sec. 2-273. - Service of notice.
32/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

All notices required herein must be served upon the mayor and the city council by certified mail or by
personally serving said persons. All such notices shall be effective only when actually received. The claimant
must prove that service upon the appropriate persons was perfected as herein required.
(Ord. No. 9-13-99-2, § 3, 9-13-1999)

Sec. 2-274. - Failure to notify.
Failure to notify the mayor and city council within the time and manner provided herein shall exonerate,
excuse and exempt the city from any liability whatsoever.
(Ord. No. 9-13-99-2, § 4, 9-13-1999)

Sec. 2-275. - Waiver.
No person may waive the notification requirements established herein. Actual knowledge of the incident
shall not constitute a waiver of the requirement of a written notification and service of such notice.
(Ord. No. 9-13-99-2, § 5, 9-13-1999)

Chapter 10 - ANIMALS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 10-1. - Pets in city hall complex.
(a)

De nitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a di erent meaning:

City hall complex means all city owned property contiguous and attached with city hall at 213 East
Blackjack, Dublin, Texas.

Exempt animals means law enforcement dogs or any animal used to aide a person with physical
disabilities.

Pet means a living, breathing animal.
(b)

Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to bring into, house, maintain or keep a pet animal inside the city
hall complex, with the exception of exempt animals as de ned in subsection (a) of this section.
(Ord. No. 7-9-01-6, § I, 7-9-2001)

Sec. 10-2. - Food, water, shelter and restraint of animals.

33/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Every person who owns, keeps or is in charge of an animal shall provide food, water and shelter, and shall
restrain the animal(s) at all times.
(Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. II, § 7, 1-13-2003)

Secs. 10-3—10-31. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - LIVESTOCK
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 10-32. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Large livestock shall mean horses, cows, bulls, cattle weighing 200 pounds or more, or any other large
animal.

Livestock shall be inclusive of horses, mules, cows, bulls, swine, sheep, goats, geese, chicken, ducks,
rabbits, fowl and any other large or small animal other than domesticated dogs or cats.

Slaughter shall mean to kill, eviscerate, disembowel, or behead.
Small livestock shall mean cattle weighing less than 200 pounds, swine, sheep, goats, geese, chickens,
ducks, rabbits, fowl or any other small animal other than domesticated dogs or cats.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 2, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 2, 2-9-2004)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
State law reference—Livestock defined, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code § 142.001.
Sec. 10-33. - Nuisance declared.
(a)
The keeping, or causing to be kept, of livestock within the city limits in violation of any of the provisions of this
article is declared to be a nuisance.
(b)
Any animal or fowl kept, maintained or harbored within the city which has erce, dangerous, or vicious
propensities or which has bitten scratched or otherwise attacked any person or any animal or fowl or which by
loud, unusual or prolonged barking or howling or other noise, shall cause the peace and quiet of any neighbor,
neighborhood or occupant of any adjacent premises to be disturbed, which has repeatedly destroyed or

34/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

damage any property, or is used for purposes determined illegal in this state, is hereby declared to be a
nuisance.
(c)
Except as otherwise provided in section 10-37, the slaughter of livestock within the city limits is hereby declared
to be a nuisance, and it shall be unlawful for any person to slaughter livestock within the city limits.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 1, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 1, 2-9-2004)

State law reference—Authority of city to define and prohibit nuisances, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §
217.002.
Sec. 10-34. - Health hazards.
Livestock must at all times be kept or maintained in a safe manner; must be kept in clean and sanitary
condition; and at all times must be con ned securely within a fenced area, so that the keeping of such livestock
will not constitute a danger to human life or property. Failure to securely con ne, or allow livestock to run free
shall be violation of this article.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 8, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 8, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-35. - Area requirements.
No person may keep large livestock at any location within the city limits which provides less than one-half
total acre for each animal defined as large livestock, or one-fourth acre total area for each animal defined as
small livestock, with the exception of fowl (ducks, geese or chickens) which will be 12 animals (six grown
chickens and six fryers, no more than ten weeks of age or four pounds) per one-fourth acre, or any
combination above. Where fowl are being kept on property that is less than one-fourth of an acre, they will be
kept penned to comply with other portions of this article.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 3, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 3, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-36. - Distance requirements.
No person, firm or corporation may keep any livestock within 150 feet of any structure or dwelling in
which people eat, sleep or dine; unless such person has secured a written, signed waiver from all owners, and
tenants of such structures or dwelling indicating no objections to the keeping of livestock in the subject
locations. Said waiver does not provide a permanent waiver, and may be revoked by any current or future
owners or tenants of such structures and dwellings.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 4, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 4, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-37. - Commercial purposes.
Under no circumstances are livestock permitted to be kept within the city limits if the primary purpose of
the keeping of such livestock is commercial in nature, unless the area is designated as agricultural.
Commercial purposes shall include, but are not limited to, the fattening of livestock for slaughter and sale
35/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(except for personal consumption), the breeding of livestock or any other similar activity.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 5, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 5, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-38. - Exceptions.
(a)
In accordance with state law, the provisions contained in section 10-34, section 10-35, section 10-36, and section
10-37, of this article do not apply to locations which have been in continuous agricultural operation since June 8,
1998, or before, and is listed on the tax rolls as agricultural exempt. This also applies to property that is within
the extraterritorial jurisdiction (ETJ). Con ned feeding operations are not allowed. Con ned feeding is hereby
de ned as penned or stable feeding with less than 100 square feet per animal per pen. This is in addition to the
area requirements for the total area and does not change the area requirements.
(b)
The prohibition against slaughtering livestock in the city limits contained in section 10-33 shall not apply to:
(1)
A licensed veterinarian who euthanizes livestock in the course of veterinary business.
(2)
A person who is trained in the humane destruction of animals and who euthanizes livestock in the course of
employment with a governmental entity responsible for animal control, a recognized animal shelter, or a
recognized humane society.
(3)
A person who slaughters livestock in the course of employment with a slaughterhouse, meat packing plant, or
other similar establishment that processes and prepares livestock products for eventual commercial sale.
(4)
The dressing or skinning of a deer that has been slaughtered outside of the city limits.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 19, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, art. III, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-39. - Running at large, herding.
(a)

Responsibility of owner. It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep or be in control of any animal which
runs at large within the city limits.
(b)

Herding. The driving of herds of animals along or upon any street, avenue or alley of the city is prohibited.
(c)

Applicability. This section shall not apply to or prohibit the herding of animals along or upon any street, avenue,
or alley of the city by:
(1)
Publicly or privately maintained circus, traveling show or rodeo which does not remain in Dublin longer than 30
days out of each year.
(2)
36/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Any o cer, agent or employee of the federal, state or local government or agencies thereof, if such herding is
done in the performance of its o cial duties.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 6(A)—(B), 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 6, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-40. - Keeping of swine prohibited.
(a)

Responsibility of owner. No person who is the owner of any swine, or any person who have any swine under his
management or control, shall keep the same or allow the same to remain in any pen or in any other place within
the city.
(b)

Applicability. This section shall not apply to or prohibit the keeping of swine by the following:
(1)
A publicly or privately owned zoo maintained or operated by a nonpro t organization or governmental entity;
(2)
A publicly or privately maintained circus, traveling show or rodeo which does not remain in the city longer than
30 days out of each year;
(3)
Slaughterhouses and livestock auctions; or
(4)
Hospitals, clinics or other premises operated by licensed veterinarians for the care and treatment of animals.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 7, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 7, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-41. - Violation; penalty.
Any person that violates any provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be punished as provided for in section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 19, 11-8-1999)

Secs. 10-42—10-60. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - IMPOUNDMENT AND FEES
Sec. 10-61. - Unrestrained livestock.
Any peace officer or agent of the city shall take up and impound any livestock animal found not restrained
by their owners as specified by this article or found to otherwise be in violation of this article.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 9, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 9, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-62. - Interference with city agents.

37/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

No person shall interfere with, hinder or molest any agent of the city in the performance of any duty of
the agent, or seek or release any animal in the custody of the city or its agents.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 19, 11-8-1999)

Sec. 10-63. - Temporary con nement of stray livestock.
If any stray livestock is found upon the premises of any residence, the owner or occupant of the premises
shall have the right to confine such animal temporarily until he can notify the city or the owner if known. When
notified, it shall be the duty of the city to retrieve and impound such animal as provided in this section in a
timely manner.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 17, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 17, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-64. - Sale of impounded livestock.
The city shall sell livestock impounded under the provisions of this division at a private sale for current
market value. All proceeds shall be paid to the city general fund after deducting all of the expenses of keeping
of the livestock, including housing, feeding and any other expenses that accrued prior to or during
impoundment of the livestock.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 10, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 10, 2-9-2004)

State law reference—Sale of impounded estrays, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code § 142.013; recovery of owner of
proceeds of sale, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code § 142.014.
Sec. 10-65. - Grace period.
(a)

Tagged livestock. Impounded tagged livestock shall be kept in the custody of the city for ve working days
before they will be sold or disposed of as provided in this division. Upon impoundment, the agents of the city
shall make a reasonable e ort to notify the owner that the livestock has been impounded and the conditions
whereby the owner may regain custody of such animal.
(b)

Nontagged livestock. Impounded livestock not wearing tags will be kept in the custody for three working days
before being sold or disposed of as provided in this division.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 11, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 11, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-66. - Disposition of impounded livestock.
If any livestock animal impounded is found to be infected with rabies, or if the animal is seriously injured,
or if the city has determined it is not saleable, or if it cannot be sold as provided in section 10-65, it shall
forthwith otherwise be destroyed or disposed of. All decisions as to the condition or saleability of the animal
shall be made by the agent of the city after seeking competent advice, if necessary.
38/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 12, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 12, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-67. - Redemption before sale.
The owner of any livestock not infected with a contagious disease and impounded under the provisions of
this division may redeem such animal before it is sold by paying the poundage fees as set out in section 10-68.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 13, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 13, 2-9-2004)

State law reference—Recovery of impounded estray by owner, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code § 142.010.
Sec. 10-68. - Poundage fees.
(a)
The following fees shall be charged for the impoundment of any livestock animal:
(1)
For taking up and impounding each animal, $20.00 per animal, or cost.
(2)
For taking care of each animal, $8.50 per day after the day of impoundment, or cost.
(b)
For computation purposes of the charges set forth in subsection (a) of this section, each day shall begin at 12:01
a.m. The full fee shall be charged when the animal is kept for any portion of any day.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 14, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 14, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-69. - Donated, unclaimed and impounded livestock.
Donated and impounded animals shall become the property of the city, which shall have the following
powers:
(1)

Authority to transfer title. The city may transfer title. In the event of such transfer of title, the person or agency
to whom title is transferred shall pay for such animal's food and care while in the animal shelter and shall
comply with the applicable vaccination provisions.
(2)

Right to destroy. The city may humanely destroy donated and impounded animals.
(3)

Custody by responsible and suitable person. The city may place any animal held at the animal shelter in the
custody of a person deemed to be a responsible and suitable owner, and who will agree to comply with the
provisions of this article.
(4)

Transfer of title to humane society. The city may transfer title of donated and impounded animals to any
legitimate humane society for purposes of adoption. There shall be no charge for expenses incurred for
previous care of animals, nor any charge for the transfer of title to said humane society.
39/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 15, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 15, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-70. - Records of impoundment.
The city shall keep a record for at least one year giving the description of all livestock impounded; the date
of impoundment; the date of sale; the amount realized for such animal; and the name and address of the
purchaser.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 16, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 16, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 10-71. - Citing to appear.
(a)
When an animal is found in violation of a provision of this division and its ownership is known to the agent of
the city, such animal need not be impounded by the agent. The agent may, if the owner agrees to sign a citation,
issue a citation which shall require the person to appear in court within ten days to answer a charge of a
violation of this division.
(b)
Signing the citation shall only be a promise of the owner to appear and is not an admission of guilt.
(c)
It shall be unlawful for any person upon being issued any citation to give the city employee a false name or
address.
(d)
It shall be unlawful to fail to appear in municipal court within ten days of the signing of the citation.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-2, § 18, 11-8-1999; Ord. No. 2-9-04-4, § 18, 2-9-2004)

Secs. 10-72—10-100. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - CONTROL OF DOMESTIC AND WILD ANIMALS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 10-101. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Animal: Any live, vertebrate creature domestic or wild.
At large: Any animal off the property of its owner and not under the control of a competent person.

40/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

City: Authorized agent of the city as deemed by the city manager.
Domestic animals: Domestic animals are those which are naturally tame and gentle, or which, by long
association with man, have become thoroughly domesticated and are now reduced to such a state of
subjection to his will that they no longer possess a disposition or inclination to escape.

Kennel: Any place where more than four dogs or four cats, or any combination of cats and dogs where the
total exceeds four animals over the age of ten weeks, and where such animals are raised, trained, boarded,
harbored or kept. Kennels are not allowed within the city limits, except pounds, clinics or hospitals.

Nuisance: Any animal or fowl kept, maintained or harbored within the city which has fierce, dangerous or
vicious propensities, or which has bitten, scratched or otherwise attacked any person or any animal or fowl, or
which, by loud, unusual or prolonged barking or howling shall cause the peace and quiet of any neighbor,
neighborhood or occupant of any adjacent premises to be disturbed, or which has repeatedly destroyed or
damaged any property, or is used for a purpose considered illegal in the state.

Restraint: An animal shall be deemed to be restrained when it is:
(1)
Con ned on the premises of the owner within a fence or closure;
(2)
Fastened or picketed by a lead, rope or chain so as to keep the animal on the premises;
(3)
Under the control of a person by a leash;
(4)
On or within a vehicle being driven or parked; or
(5)
At heel beside a competent person and obedient to that person's command.

Shelter: A structure made of adequate materials that protects animals from the elements of the weather.
Vaccination: One injection of rabies vaccine which has been approved by the United States Department of
Public Health.

Wild animals: Wild animals are those of wild nature or disposition so as to require to be reclaimed and
made tame by art, industry or education, or else must be kept in confinement to be brought within the
immediate control of the owner.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. I, § 1, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. I, § 1, 1-13-2003)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 10-102. - Exemption.

41/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Hospitals, clinics and other premises operated by licensed veterinarians for the care and treatment of
animals are exempt from the provisions of this article, except where such duties are expressly stated.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. II, § 4, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. II, § 4, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-103. - Restraint of animals.
Every person who owns, keeps or is in charge of an animal shall retrain the animal at all times.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. II, § 7, 7-10-2000)

Sec. 10-104. - Noise.
It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep or be in control of any animal which causes unreasonably
loud or unnecessary noise that causes material distress or discomfort to a person, or persons of ordinary
sensibilities in the immediate vicinity.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. II, § 3, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. II, § 3, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-105. - Wild animals.
(a)
It shall be unlawful to harbor, possess, maintain or sell any wild animal within the city limits.
(b)
This section shall not apply to or prohibit the keeping of wild animals by the following:
(1)
A publicly or privately owned zoo maintained or operated by a nonpro t organization or governmental entity.
(2)
A publicly or privately maintained circus, traveling show or rodeo which does not remain in the city for longer
than 30 days out of each year.
(3)
Hospitals, clinics and other premises operated by licensed veterinarians for the care and treatment of animals.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. II, § 2, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. II, § 2, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-106. - Permitted animals.
No person shall harbor or keep more than four dogs or four cats, or any combination of cats and dogs
when the total exceeds four animals, over the age of ten weeks, except in an animal pound, clinic or hospital.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. II, § 5, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. II, § 5, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-107. - Vaccination required.

42/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

No person shall own, keep or harbor a dog or cat over the age of four months within the city limits unless
the dog or cat has been vaccinated by a licensed veterinarian with an anti-rabies vaccine, and licensed by the
city. Said animal shall be vaccinated periodically at one-year intervals from the initial date of vaccination.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. II, § 6, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. II, § 6, 1-13-2003)

State law reference—Rabies vaccinations, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.021 et seq.
Sec. 10-108. - Violations; penalties.
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this article, except section 10-233, shall be deemed guilty
of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. IX, 7-10-2000)

The city manager shall appoint a quali ed person for a period to be terminated at the pleasure of the city

Sec. 10-133. - Records kept by the city.
It shall be the duty of the city to keep, or cause to be kept, accurate and detailed records of:
(1)

Impoundment and disposition. Impoundment and disposition of all animals coming into the custody of the city.
(2)

Bite cases. All bite cases reported to the city, and its investigation of such cases.
(3)

Monies received. Records shall be kept of all monies received under this chapter and shall be open to inspection
at reasonable times by persons responsible for similar records of the city, and shall be audited by the city
auditor in the same manner as other city records which are audited. All monies shall be deposited into the
general fund on the next working day.
(4)

Monthly reports. The agent of the city shall monthly, or at such times as may be required by the city manager,
account to the city council all monies received. The agent of the city shall at the time render to the city manager
a full statement of all animals or fowl received into the animal shelter during such month, showing the name of
the owner, if known, the date of sale, all of those animals or fowl destroyed, and all of the monies expended by
him during such month for the maintenance of said pound. He shall attach to such statement a receipt for all
such monies; the forms for such reports shall be furnished by the city.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. VII, § 33, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. VII, § 33, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-134. - Hearing on nuisance; notice.
(a)
Upon written complaint wherein any animal or fowl is alleged to be a nuisance as de ned in section 10-101, the
municipal court of the city shall have the authority to order and hold a hearing upon giving notice to the owner
of any such animal or fowl. A substantial copy of such order for a hearing, detailing the time, date, place and
purpose therefor, personally delivered or enclosed in a correctly addressed envelope to such owner, postage
prepaid, and deposited in the United States mail within not less than three days prior to the date of such
hearing, shall be deemed to be su cient and proper notice.
(b)
Any person violating any of the provisions of this section may be arrested upon written complaint. Such person
shall be taken immediately before the municipal court when such person refuses to give his written promise to
appear in court. Whenever any person so arrested is not immediately taken before the recorder of the
municipal court, the arresting o cer shall prepare, in duplicate, written notice to appear in such court. Such
notice shall contain the name and address of such person, the o ense charged and the time and place of the
44/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

o ense, and when and where such person shall appear in court. Such person must give his written promise to
appear in court, and may do so by signing a duplicate of the written notice prepared by the arresting o cer, and
such appearance shall be at least three days from the date of arrest, unless an earlier hearing is demanded. The
original of such notice shall be retained by the o cer and a copy thereof shall be delivered to such person, and
the o cer shall forthwith release such person.
(c)
Any person willfully violating any part of the written promise to appear in court, given as provided in this
section, is guilty of a misdemeanor, regardless of the disposition of the original charge.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. VI, § 34, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. VI, § 34, 1-13-2003)

No refunds shall be made on any license fee because of the death of the animal or its removal from the city

the agent, or seek or release any animal in the custody of the city or its agents.

Sec. 10-178. - Con nement of animal.
If any stray animal is found upon the premises of any resident, the owner or occupant of the premises
shall have the right to confine such animal temporarily until he can notify the city. When notified, it shall be the
duty of the city to retrieve and impound such animal as provided in this subdivision.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 16, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 16, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-179. - Removal without authority.
It shall be unlawful to remove, or attempt to remove, any impounded animal or fowl from the city animal
shelter, without the permission of the city.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. IV, § 26, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. IV, § 26, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-180. - Sale of impounded animals.
(a)
The city shall sell animals impounded under the provisions of this subdivision at private sale for $20.00, with
$5.00 being refunded when proof is made of the registration and vaccination by a licensed veterinarian. Failure
to comply and provide proof of registration and vaccination shall subject such person to a ne of not less than
$35.00 or more than $100.00.
(b)
All proceeds shall be paid to the city general fund after deducting all of the expenses of keeping of the animals,
including housing, feeding and any other expenses that accrued prior to or during impoundment of the animals.
(c)
Animals will not be sold for any research purposes.
47/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 9, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 9, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-181. - Grace period.
(a)

Tagged animals. Impounded tagged animals shall be kept in the custody of the city for ve working days before
they will be sold or disposed of as provided in this subdivision. Upon impoundment, the agents of the city shall
make a reasonable e ort to notify the owner that the animal has been impounded and the conditions whereby
the owner may regain custody of such animal.
(b)

Nontagged animals. Impounded animals not wearing tags will be kept in the custody of the city for three
working days before being sold or disposed of as provided in this subdivision.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 10, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 10, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-182. - Disposition of impounded animals.
If any impounded animal is found to be infected with rabies, or if the animal is seriously injured, or if the
city has determined such animal is not saleable, or if such animal cannot be sold as provided in section 10-181,
it shall forthwith otherwise be destroyed or disposed of. All decisions as to the condition or ability to sell the
animal shall be made by the agent of the city after seeking competent advice, if necessary.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 11, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 11, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-183. - Redemption before sale.
The owner of any animal not infected with a contagious disease and impounded under the provisions of
this subdivision may redeem such animal before it is sold by paying the poundage fees as set out in section
10-184. Fifty dollars will be added to the accumulated poundage fees and will be returned to the owner by
supplying proof of vaccination(s) by a licensed veterinarian. If the animal is not tagged and registered with the
city, is over four months of age and will reside within the city limits, it may not be redeemed until it has been
licensed and meets all requirements of the licensing, including, but not limited to, vaccinations.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 12, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 12, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-184. - Poundage fees.
(a)
The following fees shall be charged for the impoundment of any animal:
(1)
For taking up and impounding each animal, $20.00 per animal, or cost.
(2)
For taking care of each animal, $5.00 per day after the day of impoundment, or cost.
(b)

48/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

For computation purposes of the charges set forth in subsection (a) of this section, each day shall begin at 12:01
a.m. The full fee shall be charged when the animal is kept for any portion of any day.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 13, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 13, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-185. - Unclaimed and impounded animals.
Unclaimed and impounded animals shall become the property of the city, which shall have the following
powers:
(1)

Authority to transfer title. The city may transfer title. In the event of such transfer of title, the person or agency
to whom title is transferred shall pay for such animal's food and care while in the animal shelter and shall
comply with the applicable vaccination provisions.
(2)

Right to destroy. The city may humanely destroy unclaimed and impounded animals.
(3)

Custody by responsible and suitable person. The city may place any animal held at the animal shelter in the
custody of a person deemed to be a responsible and suitable owner, and who will agree to comply with the
provisions of this article.
(4)

Donated, sick or injured animals. If it is in the best interest of the city in the judgement of the agent of the city,
the city can accept an animal that is sick or injured. The city may destroy any animal by an humane method if it
has been donated to the shelter with the request that it be destroyed or if the animal is so sick or injured that its
cure is considered by the city to be impractical or if death is imminent, in either of such events, such destruction
may be done immediately, without notice of any waiting period.
(5)

Transfer of title to humane society. The city may transfer title of unclaimed and impounded animals to any
legitimate humane society for purposes of adoption. In the event of such transfer and subsequent placement of
the animal in the custody of a person deemed to be responsible and a suitable owner, the humane society shall
be required to give rabies shots to such animals over the age of four months which are transferred. There shall
be no charge for expenses incurred for previous care of animals, nor any charge for the transfer of title of
animals to the humane society.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 14, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 14, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-186. - Records of impoundment.
The city shall keep a record for at least one year giving the description of all animals impounded, the date
of impoundment, the date of sale, the amount realized for such animal, and the name and address of the
purchaser.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 15, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 15, 1-13-2003)

49/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 10-187. - Citing to appear.
(a)
When an animal is found in violation of a provision of this chapter and the owner of such animal is known to the
agent of the city, such animal need not be impounded by the agent. If the owner agrees to sign a citation, the
agent may issue a citation which shall require the person to appear in court within ten days to answer a charge
of a violation of this chapter.
(b)
Signing the citation shall only be a promise of the owner to appear and is not an admission of guilt.
(c)
It shall be unlawful for any person upon being issued any citation to give the city employee a false name or
address.
(d)
It shall be unlawful to fail to appear in municipal court within ten days of the signing of the citation.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. III, § 17, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. III, § 17, 1-13-2003)

Secs. 10-188—10-210. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - FIERCE, DANGEROUS OR VICIOUS ANIMALS
Sec. 10-211. - Special con nement requirements.
(a)
The owner of a erce, dangerous or vicious animal shall con ne such animal within a building or secure
enclosure. A erce, dangerous or vicious animal must be muzzled before leaving the secure enclosure.
(b)
The term "special con nement requirements" is not de ned, nor is the term "secure enclosure." If an animal is
able to climb, dig or otherwise escape from its enclosure, such enclosure is not secure.
(c)
The requirements for a secure enclosure are as follows:
(1)
The enclosure shall be constructed of chain-link fencing;
(2)
The height of the chain-link fence shall be six feet or higher;
(3)
The top of the enclosure must be chain-link fencing, or a material greater in strength than chain-link fencing,
and attached to the sides so that escape is impossible by climbing over the chain-link fence;
(4)
The chain-link fencing must be a minimum of one foot below ground level, or a concrete footing shall be poured
to secure the chain-link fence to prevent a dangerous animal from escaping by digging out or crawling under the
fence. The fence will be equal or greater in strength to the speci cations listed in this section.
50/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(5)
Gates on the enclosure must be kept locked.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. IV, § 27, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. IV, § 27, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-212. - Requirements for owners of dangerous animals.
(a)
No later than ten days after an animal is de ned as vicious, dangerous or erce, the owner shall:
(1)
Register the dangerous animal with the animal control authority for the area in which the animal is being kept.
(2)
Restrain the dangerous animal at all times on a leash, and in the immediate control of the person handling the
animal, and securely muzzled.
(3)
Obtain liability insurance coverage in the amount of $100,000.00 to cover damages resulting from an attack by
the dangerous animal causing bodily injury to a person, and provide proof of the required coverage to the
animal control authority.
(b)
The owner of a dangerous animal who does not comply with the requirements of this article shall deliver the
animal to the animal control authority not later than the tenth day after the owner learns that the animal is
dangerous.
(c)
If an application of any person or municipal court nds, after notice or hearing, that the owner of the vicious,
dangerous or erce animal has failed to comply with the provisions of this article, the court shall order the
animal control authority to seize the animal and shall issue a warrant authorizing the seizure. The animal control
authority shall seize the animal and provide for the impoundment of the animal in secure and humane
conditions.
(d)
The owner shall pay any cost or fee assessed by the city related to the seizure, impoundment, and destruction
of the animal.
(e)
The court shall order the animal control authority to humanely destroy the animal if the owner has not complied
with this article before the 11th day after the date on which the animal was seized or delivered to the animal
control authority.
(f)
The court shall order the animal control authority to return the animal to the owner if the owner complies with
this article before the 11th day after the date on which the animal was seized or delivered to the animal control
authority.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. IV, § 27, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. IV, § 27, 1-13-2003)

State law reference—Dangerous dog defined, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.041(2).
51/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 10-213. - Destruction of animals.
(a)
Any dog or other animal which has erce, dangerous or vicious propensities, or which has bitten, scratched or
otherwise attacked any person or animal and which is at large and is unable to be caught and impounded, and
which is or has displayed erce, dangerous or vicious propensities, may be destroyed by the agent or the city or
any police o cer without notice to the owner.
(b)
Any female dog or other animal at large within the city while in season is declared to be a public nuisance, and it
shall be the duty of the agent of the city or any police o cer to impound such dog or animal. If such dog or
animal is unable to be caught and impounded, and after reasonable inquiry, the owner thereof cannot be
determined or found, such animal may be destroyed by the agent of the city or any police o cer.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. IV, § 28, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. IV, § 28, 1-13-2003)

Secs. 10-214—10-230. - Reserved.
DIVISION 4. - QUARANTINE
Sec. 10-231. - Report by veterinarian.
It shall be the duty of every physician or other practitioner to report to the city the names and addresses
of persons treated for bites or scratches inflicted by animals, together with such other information as will be
helpful in rabies control.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. V, § 32, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. V, § 32, 1-13-2003)

Sec. 10-232. - Regulations.
(a)

City to quarantine; time period. Upon being presented a sworn a davit that an animal has bitten or scratched a
person, the city shall quarantine the identi ed animal for a period of ten days.
(b)

Places for quarantine. Quarantine shall be at the following places:
(1)
The animal shelter, at the owner's expense;
(2)
A licensed veterinary hospital, at the owner's expense;
(3)
Home quarantine—permissible when the city agrees that home quarantine is warranted and believes the
following requirements are satis ed:
Animals of unknown ownership will be quarantined at the animal shelter.

52/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

a.
The owner of the animal is a resident of the city and agrees to keep the animal con ned at his residence in the
city under the supervision of a licensed veterinarian;
b.
The animal was properly restrained at the time the bite occurred; and
c.
The animal was properly protected by a current rabies vaccination.
(c)

Surrender by owner. Upon demand made by the city, it shall be unlawful for the owner to fail to surrender any
animal for quarantine which has bitten or scratched a human or other animal, and which is suspected of having
been exposed to rabies, which expenses shall be borne by the owner.
(d)

Release to owner. The quarantined animal may be reclaimed by the owner if such animal is adjudged free of
rabies, and upon payment of the fees and compliance with the vaccine and registration provisions set forth in
this division.
(e)

Pathological examination. When an animal under quarantine, at any place approved by this division, diagnosed
by a licensed veterinarian as being rabid or suspected of being rabid, dies while under observation, the city shall
immediately send the head of such animal to the state health department for a pathological examination. The
city shall notify the proper health o cer of reports of human contacts and the diagnosis made of the suspected
animal after the pathological examination has been made.
(f)

Health o cials. When an animal bites or scratches a person so that the director of the health department
believes that the quarantine observation period cannot be observed because of the danger of developing
rabies, the health director shall order that the animal control o cer immediately forward the animal's head for
pathological examination.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. V, § 30, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. V, § 30, 1-13-2003)

State law reference—Quarantine of animals for rabies, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.041 et seq.
Sec. 10-233. - Citywide quarantine.
(a)

Conditions warranting. A citywide quarantine may be evoked for a period of 30 days by the city council upon
being noti ed by the state health department of a positive diagnosis of rabies of an animal, or after an
immediate threat of rabies.
(b)

Extending time. In the event there are additional positive cases of rabies occurring within the 30-day period of
the citywide quarantine, such period of quarantine shall be extended for additional reasonable periods of time.
(c)

53/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Animals bitten by rabid animals. During a period of citywide rabies quarantine, every unvaccinated animal bitten
by a rabid animal shall be destroyed. Any vaccinated animal will be con ned under quarantine regulations as
speci ed by this division.
(d)

Any animal in public. It shall be unlawful for any person to take or permit any animal in the streets or any other
public place during the period of citywide quarantine.
(e)

Exemption. Dogs used as seeing-eye dogs are exempt from the requirements of this section.
(f)

Exposed to rabies. The carcass of any dead animal suspected of having been exposed to rabies shall, upon
demand, be surrendered to the city.
(g)

Determined rabid. The city shall direct the disposition of any animal found to be infected with rabies.
(h)

Surrender after demand. No person shall fail or refuse to surrender any animal for quarantine, destruction or
disposal as required in this section when demand is made therefor by the city.
(i)
A penalty of not less than $100.00, and no more than $1,000.00 may be assessed by the municipal court for
failing to abide by any of the above quarantine regulations.
(Ord. No. 7-10-00-4, art. V, § 31, 7-10-2000; Ord. No. 1-13-03-1, art. V, § 31, 1-13-2003)

State law reference—Area rabies quarantine by the state, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.045.
Chapter 14 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 14-1. - Numbering of buildings.
(a)
Any building within the corporate city limits of Dublin, Texas which is used as a residence or business shall have
the correct street address numbers attached on the structure in a manner clearly visible from the nearest
street.
(b)
The street address numbers shall be a minimum of three inches in height each, and be placed on the street side
of the building. The numbers must be of a distinctly di erent color than the structure on which the numbers are
attached.
(c)
Street address numbers to all buildings within the corporate city limits of Dublin, Texas shall be assigned by the
city.
(d)
54/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

All requests for building street address numbers shall be made at the Dublin City Hall, Dublin, Texas.
(e)
All building street address numbers shall comply with the existing property restrictions, comprehensive
ordinances, and all other applicable governing ordinances and regulations.
(f)
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this ordinance, or shall fail to comply therewith, or with
any of the requirements thereof, within the city limits shall be deemed guilty of an o ense and shall be liable for
a ne not less than $200.00 and not to exceed the sum of $500.00. Each day the violation exists shall constitute
a separate o ense. Such penalty shall be in addition to all the other remedies provided herein.
(Ord. No. 1-10-00-3, §§ 1—5, 7, 1-10-2000; Ord. No. 06-13-05-1, §§ 1—6, 6-13-2005)

Sec. 14-2. - Violation; penalty.
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects or refuses to comply with, or who resists the
enforcement of, any of the provisions of this chapter shall be fined not more than $2,000.00 for all violations
involving zoning, fire safety or public health and sanitation, including dumping of refuse, and shall be fined not
more than $500.00 for all other violations of this chapter. Each day that a violation is permitted to exist shall
constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. No. 4-12-99-2, § 13, 4-12-1999)

Secs. 14-3—14-30. - Reserved.

ARTICLE IV. - DANGEROUS BUILDINGS
Sec. 14-91. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Building official means the city building inspector or a person employed, appointed or designated by the
city manager for purposes of making inspections, sending notices and otherwise enforcing the provisions of
this article.

56/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Dangerous building or unsafe building means any structure or building located within the incorporated
limits of the city that is within the definition of "dangerous building" or "unsafe building" as defined in the
Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings, 1997 edition, published by the International
Conference of Building Officials, on file in the city secretary's office, and that is:
(1)
In such a state or condition of repair or disrepair that all or any of the following conditions exist:
a.
The walls or other vertical structural members list, lean or buckle;
b.
Damage or deterioration exists to the extent that the building is unsafe;
c.
Loads on oors or roofs are improperly distributed, or the oors or roofs are of insu cient strength to be
reasonably safe for the purposes for which they are used;
d.
Damage by re, wind or other cause has rendered the building or structure dangerous to life, safety, morals or
the general health and welfare of the occupants or the people of the city;
e.
The building or structure is so dilapidated, substandard, decayed, unsafe, unsanitary or otherwise lacking in the
amenities essential to decent living or use that it is un t for human habitation or occupancy, or is likely to cause
sickness, disease or injury or otherwise constitutes a detriment to the health, morals, safety or general welfare
of the persons assembled, working or living in such building or structure or is a hazard to the public health,
safety and welfare;
f.
Light, air and sanitation facilities are inadequate to protect the health, morals, safety or general welfare of
persons who assemble, work or live in such building or structure;
g.
Stairways, re escapes and other facilities of egress are inadequate in case of re or panic;
h.
Parts or appendages of the building or structure are attached so that they are likely to fall and injure persons or
property;
(2)
Dilapidated, substandard or un t for human habitation and a hazard to the public health, safety and welfare of
the city's residents;
(3)
Regardless of its structural condition, unoccupied by its owners, lessees or other invitees and is unsecured from
unautho-rized entry to the extent that it could be entered or used by vagrants or other uninvited persons as a
place of harborage or could be entered or used by children; or
(4)
Boarded up, fenced or otherwise secured in any manner, if:
57/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

a.
The building constitutes a danger to the public even though it is secured from entry;
b.
The means used to secure the building are inadequate to prevent unauthorized entry or use of the building to
the extent it could be entered or used by vagrants or other uninvited persons as a place of harborage or could
be entered or used by children; or
c.
It is de ned as a dangerous or unsafe building by the Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings.

Responsible party means the owner, occupant or person in custody of a building or structure, and any
mortgagee or lienholder, as identified or listed on the current tax rolls of the tax appraisal district for the
property, together with any additional person or interest, if any, shown in the current records of the city
applicable to such property.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 2, 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 14-92. - Unsafe buildings declared a nuisance; enforcement of article.
(a)
It shall be unlawful for any person to maintain or permit the existence of any unsafe building in the city; and it
shall be unlawful for any person to permit any unsafe building to remain in such unsafe condition.
(b)
All unsafe buildings are declared to be public nuisances and shall be abated by repair, rehabilitation, demolition
or removal in accordance with the procedures provided in this article.
(c)
The building o cial shall enforce the provisions of this article.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 4, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-93. - Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings adopted.
The Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings, 1997 edition, published by the International
Conference of Building Officials, a copy of which has been exhibited to and approved by the city council, and
certified copies of which are on file in the offices of the city secretary, is adopted by reference and declared to
be the unsafe building abatement code of the city for the regulation, vacation, removal, repair or demolition of
unsafe buildings in a timely and legal manner in the city.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 3, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-94. - Local amendments to the Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings.

58/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Section 205 of the Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings, which deals with the board of
appeals, is amended to provide that the board of appeals shall be composed of five citizens of the city, and
preference shall be given to qualified architects, engineers and citizens knowledgeable in the construction
industry.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 3, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-95. - Duties of the building o cial.
The building official shall inspect, or cause to be inspected, every building, or portion thereof, reported to
be unsafe. If such building, or any portion thereof, is determined to be unsafe, the building official shall give
the responsible parties notice in accordance with the requirements set forth in the Uniform Code for the
Abatement of Dangerous Buildings and in compliance with sections 14-96 and 14-97. The building official shall
further:
(1)
Inspect, or cause to be inspected, when necessary, any building or structure within the incorporated limits of the
city, including public buildings, schools, halls, churches, theaters, hotels, tenements or apartments, multifamily
residences, single-family residences, garages, warehouses and other commercial and industrial structures of
any nature whatsoever for the purpose of determining whether any conditions exist which render such places a
dangerous building as de ned in section 14-91.
(2)
Inspect any building, wall or structure about which complaints have been led by any person to the e ect that a
building wall or structure is or may be existing in violation of this article.
(3)
Report any noncompliance with the minimum standards set forth in this article to the board of appeals. The
building o cial shall obtain from the secretary of the board of appeals a hearing date for a public hearing by the
board of appeals on any structure believed to be a dangerous building, and shall provide the secretary of the
board of appeals with copies of the written notice to persons with interests in the property as provided for in
section 14-97.
(4)
Appear at all hearings conducted by the board of appeals and testify as to the conditions of dangerous buildings
within the city.
(5)
Place a notice on all dangerous buildings which shall read as follows:
"This building has been found to be a dangerous building by the City of Dublin Building Official.
This notice is to remain on this building until it is repaired, vacated or demolished in accordance
with the notice which has been given to the owner(s), occupant(s) and person(s) with interests in
the property as shown by the records of the city secretary and the tax appraisal district. It is
unlawful to remove this notice until such notice is complied with."

59/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(6)
Perform the other requirements with respect to noti cation of public hearings as are set forth more speci cally
in this article.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 5, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-96. - Notice to repair.
If the building official should determine that any building or structure within the incorporated limits of the
city is a dangerous or unsafe building, he shall cause written notification to be sent, by certified mail, to the
owner and all other persons having an interest in the building after a diligent effort to discover each owner,
mortgagee and lienholder. Such notice shall contain a:
(1)
Description of the building or structure deemed unsafe, and its location;
(2)
Statement of the particulars which make the building or structure a dangerous building;
(3)
Notice of the date and time of a public hearing before the board of appeals to determine whether the building
complies with the standards set out in this article;
(4)
Statement that the owner, lienholder, mortgagee or persons with a legal interest in the building will be required
to submit at the hearing proof of the scope of any work that may be required to comply with this article and the
amount of time it will take to reasonably perform the work.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 6, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-97. - Su ciency of notice.
Notwithstanding any other term or provision of this article or the Uniform Code for the Abatement of
Dangerous Buildings, notice given pursuant to this article shall be sufficient and deemed properly served upon
the responsible parties if a copy of such notice is:
(1)
Personally served upon the responsible parties; or
(2)
Sent by registered or certi ed mail, return receipt requested, to the last known address of such responsible
parties as shown on the records of the city and the tax appraisal district; and
(3)
Posted in a conspicuous place in or about the building a ected by the notice.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 7, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-98. - Duties of the board of appeals.
60/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The board of appeals shall:
(1)
Schedule and hold a public hearing and hear testimony from the building o cial, the owner and other persons
having an interest in the dangerous building and any person desiring to present factual evidence relevant to the
unsafe building. Such testimony shall relate to the determination of the question of whether the building or
structure in question is a dangerous building; the scope of any work that may be required to comply with this
article; and the amount of time it will take to reasonably perform the work. The owner or a person having an
interest in the dangerous building shall have the burden of proof to demonstrate the scope of any work that
may be required to comply with this article and the time it will take to reasonably perform the work.
(2)
Upon conclusion of the hearing, the board of appeals shall determine by majority vote whether the building or
structure in question is a dangerous building. Upon a determination that the building or structure in question
constitutes a dangerous building, the board of appeals shall issue an order:
a.
Containing an identi cation of the building and the property on which the building is located;
b.
Making written ndings of the violations of the minimum standards that are present at the building;
c.
Requiring the owner and persons having an interest in the building to repair, vacate or demolish the building
within 30 days from the issuance of such order, unless the owner or a person with an interest in the building
establishes at the hearing that the work cannot reasonably be performed within 30 days, in which instance the
board of appeals shall specify a reasonable time for the completion of the work; and
d.
Containing a statement that the city will vacate, secure, remove or demolish the dangerous building and
relocate the occupants of the building if the ordered action is not taken within the time speci ed by the board of
appeals.
(3)
As soon as is practicable after the hearing, the board of appeals shall deliver a copy of the order by hand
delivery or certi ed mail to the owner and all persons having an interest in the property, as such persons appear
on the rolls of the tax appraisal district and in the o cial records of the city regarding such building, including all
identi able mortgagees and lienholders.
(4)
If the board of appeals allows the owner or a person with an interest in the dangerous building more than 30
days to repair, remove or demolish the building, in its written order, the board of appeals shall establish speci c
time schedules for the commencement and performance of the work and shall require the owner or person to
secure the property in a reasonable manner from unauthorized entry while the work is being performed. The
securing of the property shall be in a manner found to be acceptable by the city building o cial.
(5)

61/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The board of appeals may not allow the owner or person with an interest in the dangerous building more than
90 days to repair, remove or demolish the building or fully perform all work required to comply with the written
order of the board of appeals unless the owner or person:
a.
Submits a detailed plan and time schedule for the work at the hearing; and
b.
Establishes at the hearing that the work cannot reasonably be completed within 90 days because of the scope
and complexity of the work.
(6)
If the board of appeals allows the owner or person with an interest in the dangerous building more than 90 days
to complete any part of the work required to repair, remove or demolish the building, the board of appeals shall
require such owner or person to regularly submit progress reports to the board of appeals to demonstrate that
such owner or person has complied with the time schedules established for commencement and performance
of the work. The written order may require that the owner or person with an interest in the building appear
before the city building o cial to demonstrate compliance with the time schedules.
(7)
If the owner or a person with an interest in a dangerous building fails to comply with the order of the board of
appeals within the time speci ed in this section, absent appeal to the city council, the city may, at any time after
the expiration of 45 days from the date a copy of the nal decision of the board of appeals is mailed to each
known owner, lienholder or mortgagee, cause any occupants of the dangerous building to be relocated, and
may cause the dangerous building to be secured, removed or demolished at the city's expense. The city may
assess the expenses on and have a lien against the property on which the dangerous building was located,
unless it is a homestead as protected by the state constitution. The lien is extinguished if the property owner or
a person having an interest in the dangerous building reimburses the city for the expenses. The lien arises and
attaches to the property at the time the notice of the lien is recorded and indexed in the o ce of the county
clerk in the county in with the property is located. The notice of lien must contain the name and address of the
owner of the dangerous building if such information can be determined by a diligent e ort; a legal description
of the real property on which the building was located; the amount of expenses incurred by the city; and the
balance due. Such lien is a privileged lien, subordinate only to tax liens and all previously recorded bona de
mortgage liens attached to the real property.
(8)
In addition to the authority set forth in subsection (7) of this section, after the expiration of the time allotted in
the order for the repair, removal or demolition of a dangerous building, the city may repair the building at its
expense and assess the expenses on the land on which the building stands or to which it is attached. The
repairs contemplated by this section may only be accomplished to the extent necessary to bring the building
into compliance with the minimum standards established by this article, and to the extent such repairs do not
exceed minimum housing standards. This section shall be applicable only to residential buildings with ten or
less dwelling units. The city shall follow the procedures set forth in subsection (7) of this section for ling a lien
on the property on which the building is located.
62/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 8, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Homestead exemption, Texas Constitution art. 16, § 50.
Sec. 14-99. - Appeal to the city council.
Any responsible party that is aggrieved by the decision of the board of appeals under this article may
appeal such decision to the city council within ten days from the date of the decision appealed from. In such
event, the city council shall set a time and date for hearing such appeal and hold such hearing within 45 days
from the date of the appeal.
(1)
The purpose of the public hearing of the appeal shall be to determine whether or not the building is an unsafe
or dangerous building in accordance with the de nition and standards set forth in section 14-91, and to uphold,
reverse or modify the decision of the board of appeals.
(2)
The matter shall be set for public hearing before the city council at the earliest practicable date and notice of
such hearing shall be served on the responsible parties, each known mortgagee and lienholder, and the building
o cial not less than ten days prior to date of such hearing. All interested persons shall have the opportunity to
be heard and may introduce evidence to the city council for its consideration.
(3)
After the public hearing, the city council shall make such ndings and orders as it shall deem appropriate.
(4)
After the public hearing, if a building is found in violation of the standards set out in the de nition of "dangerous
building" or "unsafe building" as set forth in section 14-91, the city council may order that the decision of the
board of appeals be a rmed, reversed or modi ed and, in the latter instance, that the building be vacated,
secured, repaired, removed or demolished by the owner of such building within a reasonable time. The city
council also may order that the occupants of such building be relocated within a reasonable time. The city
secretary shall mail to each identi ed owner, mortgagee and lienholder a notice containing:
a.
The identi cation and address of the building and the property on which it is located;
b.
A description of the violation of this Code of Ordinances, if any, that is found by the city council to be present at
the building; and
c.
A statement that the city will vacate, secure, remove, repair or demolish the building or relocate the occupants
of the building if the ordered action is not taken within a reasonable time; or that the city will take no action.
(5)
As an alternative to the procedure prescribed by subsection (4) of this section, the city council shall make an
e ort to contact each mortgagee and lienholder before conducting the public hearing and shall give such
persons a notice of and an opportunity to comment at the hearing. If the city proceeds under this subsection,
63/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

the order issued by the city council shall specify a reasonable time for the building to be vacated, secured,
repaired, removed or demolished by the responsible party and an additional reasonable time for the ordered
action to be taken by any mortgagee or lienholder if the responsible party fails to comply with the order within
the time provided for action by the responsible party. Under this subsection, the city is not required to furnish
any notice to a mortgagee or lienholder other than a copy of the order if the responsible party fails to timely
take the ordered action.
(6)
If the building is not vacated, secured, repaired, removed or demolished, or the occupants are not relocated
within the allotted time, the city may vacate, secure, remove, repair or demolish the building or relocate the
occupants of such building at its own expense.
(7)
If the city incurs expenses under subsection (6) of this section, it may assess the expenses on and shall have a
lien against the property on which the building was or is located, unless it is a homestead as protected by the
state constitution. The lien is extinguished if the property owner or another person having an interest in the
legal title to the property reimburses the city for the expenses. The lien arises and attaches to the property at
the time the notice of the lien is recorded and indexed in the o ce of the county clerk. The notice must contain
the name and address of the owner, if such information can be determined by a reasonable e ort; a legal
description of the real property on which the building was located; the amount of expenses incurred by the city;
and the balance due.
(8)
If the notice is given and the opportunity to repair, remove or demolish the building is a orded to each
mortgagee and lienholder as provided in subsection (4) or (5) of this section, the lien is a privileged lien,
subordinate only to tax liens and all previously recorded bona de mortgage liens attached to the real property
to which the city's lien attaches.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 9, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-100. - Assessment of expenses and penalties.
(a)
If an appeal has been made to the city council by any interested party and the city council has held a hearing
pursuant to section 14-99, and the time allotted for the repair, removal or demolition of a building under section
14-99(4) or 14-99(5) has expired, then the city council may, in addition to the authority granted under V.T.C.A.,
Local Government Code ch. 214 and section 14-99:
(1)
Order the repair of the building at the city's expense and assess the expenses on the land on which the building
stands or to which it is attached; or
(2)
Assess a civil penalty against the responsible party for failure to repair, remove or demolish the building.

64/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The city building official shall invite at least two or more building contractors to make estimates
pertaining to the needed repair, removal or demolition of a building. The building official shall
cause an assessment of expenses or be made or a civil penalty based on such estimates. The
building official shall endeavor to minimize the expenses of any building repair, removal or
demolition order pursuant to this article.
(b)
The city may repair a building under subsection (a) of this section only to the extent necessary to bring the
building into compliance with the minimum standards of the city and only if the building is a residential building
with ten or less dwelling units. The repairs may not improve the building to the extent that the building exceeds
minimum standards prescribed by the city.
(c)
The city shall impose a lien against the land on which the building stands or stood to secure the payment of the
repair, removal or demolition expenses or the civil penalty, unless it is a homestead as protected by the state
constitution. Promptly after the imposition of the lien, the city shall le for record, in recordable form in the
o ce of the county clerk, a written notice of the imposition of the lien. The notice shall contain a legal
description of the land.
(d)
The city's lien to secure the payment of a civil penalty or the cost of repairs, removal or demolition is inferior to
any previously recorded bona de mortgage lien attached to the real property to which the city's lien attaches if
the mortgage lien was led for record in the o ce of the county clerk before the date the civil penalty is
assessed or the repair, removal or demolition is begun by the city. The city's lien is superior to all other
previously recorded judgment liens.
(e)
Any civil penalty or other assessment imposed under this section shall accrue interest at the rate of ten percent
per year from the date of the assessment until paid in full.
(f)
In any judicial proceeding regarding enforcement of the city's rights under this section, the prevailing party is
entitled to recover reasonable attorney's fees as otherwise provided by statute.
(g)
A lien acquired by the city under this section for repair expenses may not be foreclosed if the property on which
the repairs were made is occupied as a residential homestead by a person 65 years of age or older.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 10, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 14-101. - Violation; penalty.
(a)
The owner of any unsafe building or dangerous building who shall fail to comply with any notice or order given
by the authority of the board of appeals or city council to repair, vacate or demolish such building or structure
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
(b)
65/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

An occupant or lessee in possession of any unsafe building or dangerous building who fails to comply with any
notice or order to vacate such building and fails to repair such building in accordance with an order given by the
board of appeals shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
(c)
Any person removing the notice of a dangerous building as provided for in section 14-95(5) shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor.
(d)
The violation of any provision of this article shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor o ense punishable by a ne
of not less than $100.00 and not exceeding $2,000.00. Each day a violation of this article continues shall
constitute a separate o ense.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-4, § 11, 10-22-2001)
