Chapter 18 - BUSINESSES
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 18-1. - Occupation tax; deposit.
All persons engaging in a temporary business within the city, such as a carnival, skating rink or circus, and
not housed in a permanent building, shall be required to pay an occupation tax or two percent of the gross
receipts of such business, and shall deposit the sum of $20.00 with the city secretary before engaging in such
business, which deposit shall be forfeited if the person engaging in such temporary business leaves the city
without making a sworn affidavit as to the gross receipts during such business venture.
(Ord. No. 5-8-73, art. VII, 5-8-1973)
69/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Secs. 18-2—18-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - PEDDLERS AND ITINERANT VENDORS
Sec. 18-31. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

City means the municipal government for the City of Dublin, Erath County, Texas.
Itinerant vendor means all persons, as well as their agents and employees, who, from a location on private
property in the city, engage in the temporary or transient business of selling or offering for sale any goods,
wares, merchandise or service, including but not limited to plants, lumber, agricultural products, photographs,
produce, poultry, stock, fruit, or other foods or food products, clothing, jewelry, home improvements,
entertainment, novelties, toys and magazines.

Noncommercial purpose or cause means a purpose or cause not created, existing or espoused for the
generation of profit or the remuneration of individuals, including, but not limited to, the religious or charitable
solicitation of contributions, seeking political support or contributions, the promotion of civic causes, the
promotion of conservation of resources or animals, advocating a philosophy or religion, or minors conducting
fundraising activities, who represent an organization for the benefit of youths, including but not limited to Boy
Scouts, Girl Scouts, little league groups, and school groups.

Peddler means a person who goes from place to place, house to house, business to business, street to
street, or upon public property soliciting orders to sell, selling or offering for sale any goods, wares,
merchandise or service, including but not limited to food items, clothing, jewelry, home improvements,
entertainment, novelties, toys and magazines. Transfer of payment at the time of sale or later is immaterial.
The word "peddler" shall include the term "itinerant vendor." This term shall not include individuals connected
with noncommercial purposes or causes.

Temporary means any business transacted or conducted in the city for which premises have not been
purchased, hired or leased for at least 90 days, in, from or upon which the business is to be operated or
conducted.

Transient means any business of any itinerant vendor which may be operated or conducted by persons or
their agents or employees who reside away from the city or who have fixed places of business in places other
than the city, or who move stocks of the products listed under the definition of "itinerant vendor" in this article
or samples thereof into the city with the intention of selling the stock and returning to a place other than the
city, or who so move the products into the city with the purpose or intention of removing them or the unsold
portion thereof away from the city before the expiration of 90 days.
(Ord. No. 5-8-73, arts. I, IV, 5-8-1973; Ord. No. 4-11-05-4, art. I, 4-11-2005)
70/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 18-32. - Presumption.
The selling or offering for sale of any goods, wares, merchandise, service or item by any peddler or
itinerant vendor within the city shall raise a presumption that the goods, wares, merchandise, service or item
are subjects of intrastate commerce.
(Ord. No. 4-11-05-4, art. II, § 1, 4-11-2005)

Sec. 18-33. - Exemptions.
(a)
The term "itinerant vendor" or "peddler" shall not include anyone engaged in interstate commerce, or anyone
upon whom the provisions of this article would impose a direct and unlawful burden on interstate commerce,
provided however, any person claiming exemption under this section has the burden of providing
documentation to the city establishing such exemption before undertaking the selling, o ering for sale or
soliciting orders to sell any goods, wares, merchandise, service or item in the city.
(b)
The provisions of this article shall not apply to:
(1)
Commercial travelers or wholesale produce rms who sell or exhibit for sale goods, wares, merchandise or
services wholesale to retail merchants by invitation.
(2)
Rummage sales or other fund raising sales conducted by local churches, state sanctioned educational
institutions, and charitable organizations.
(3)
Newspapers.
(4)
City residents who have not attained 18 years of age.
(5)
Itinerant vendors associated with a community festival or event sanctioned by the city.
(6)
Peddlers or itinerant vendors who have a contractual relationship with the city.
(7)
Bona de residents of the state selling fruits, vegetables, dressed meats, fowl or farm products which were
produced on land within the state, owned or controlled by such vendor.
(8)
Noncommercial purposes or causes.
(Ord. No. 4-11-05-4, art. II, § 2, 4-11-2005)

Sec. 18-34. - Sale of certain products by transient vendor prohibited.

71/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

It shall be unlawful for any peddler or itinerant vendor to sell, offer for sale, exhibit for sale or exhibit for
the purpose of taking orders for sale thereof any of the following:
(1)
Live animal, reptile or fowl.
(2)
Other items that are otherwise unlawful to possess, sell, o er for sale, exhibit for sale or exhibit for the purpose
of taking orders for sale as provided by federal, state or local law or ordinance.
(Ord. No. 4-11-05-4, art. III, § 1, 4-11-2005)

Sec. 18-35. - Peddler's permit and itinerant vendor's license.
(a)

Required. It shall be unlawful for any peddler or itinerant vendor to sell, o er for sale, exhibit for sale or exhibit
for the purpose of taking orders for the sale thereof any goods, wares, merchandise, service or item in the city
without rst obtaining a peddler permit or itinerant vendor license, as appropriate. Peddler permits shall not be
issued in the name of a company but must be issued in the name of each person. Itinerant vendors to operate
from a xed location may have a single permit.
(b)

Application. Any person desiring a peddler permit or itinerant vendor license required in section 18-34(a) shall
apply for such permit or license to the city secretary. The application shall be in the form as the city requires and
shall include, but not necessarily be limited to, the following:
(1)
The applicant's full name, current address, driver's license number, or other identifying information acceptable
to the city secretary;
(2)
If the applicant is representing a business, the business name, address, telephone number, names and
addresses of the business o cers or partners;
(3)
A statement describing the kind and character of the goods, wares, merchandise, service or item to be sold,
o ered for sale or exhibited and the method of distribution to be used;
(4)
A Texas Sales Tax Certi cate issued by the Texas Comptroller of Public Accounts or a document from the Texas
Comptroller of Public Accounts certifying that the applicant is exempt from collecting and remitting sales tax;
(5)
Where food or food products are to be sold or o ered for sale, a health certi cate issued by a practicing
physician duly licensed by the state, showing the applicant to be in good health and free from all communicable
diseases;
(6)

72/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Where farm produce agriculture products are to be sold or o ered for sale, a signed statement from the county
agent certifying that the produce or agricultural product was grown or raised by the peddler or itinerant vendor
upon his land or land rented or leased by him;
(7)
Itinerant vendors must provide the physical location where conducting business and provide the property
owner's written permission for the itinerant vendor to conduct business on the property.
(c)

Fee. Before any peddler permit or itinerant vendor license shall be issued under the provisions of this article,
the applicant shall pay to the city a fee in the amount as the city council determines, which fee shall be for the
purpose of partially defraying the expenses of enforcing the provisions of this article.
(d)

Issuance. Upon the compliance by the applicant with all the provisions of this article, the city secretary shall
issue the license required by this article.
(e)

Duration. Peddler permits and itinerant vendor licenses required by the provisions of this article shall be valid
so long as the sale or exhibit authorized thereby is continuously held in the city, but in no event shall the permit
or license be valid for more than 90 days from the date of its issuance.
(f)

Transfer. Peddler permits and itinerant vendor licenses required by the provisions of this article shall not be
transferable and shall not give authority to more than one person to conduct a business as a peddler or
itinerant vendor, but any person having obtained a permit or license may have no more than three persons
assist in conducting the business.
(g)

Display. Every peddler or itinerant vendor conducting any business requiring a peddler permit or itinerant
vendor license under the provisions of this article such permit or license shall be in the peddler's or itinerant
vendor's possession and prominently displayed at all times.
(h)

Location. Separate permit or license shall be required for each location an itinerant vendor intends to locate.
Each separate location or conveyance used in any manner which shall cause the location or conveyance to come
under the provisions of this article shall be deemed a separate business and shall require a separate permit or
license though owned by the same person.
(i)

Times. Peddlers and itinerant vendors shall conduct business only during the daytime, but in no instance shall a
peddler or itinerant vendor conduct any business before 9:00 a.m. or after 7:00 p.m., and no business shall be
conducted on Sunday.
(j)

Noise prohibited. No peddler or itinerant vendor shall shout, below a horn, ring a bell or use any sound device
for the purpose of attracting attention to any goods, wares, merchandise, service, or item which such peddler or
itinerant vendor proposes to sell. A reasonable, non-amplifying sound device may be used if the device is
73/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

typically associated with the goods, wares, merchandise, service or item and the reasonable use of the device is
provided for on the peddler permit or itinerant vendor license at the time of issuance.
(k)

Calling at homes; request by citizen to leave premises. Peddlers making a call at the home of any citizen in the
city shall at the request of the citizen immediately leave the premises quietly.
(Ord. No. 5-8-73, art. II, 5-8-1973; Ord. No. 4-11-05-4, art. III, § 2, 4-11-2005)

Sec. 18-36. - Permit or license suspension or revocation.
(a)
If a representative designated by the city to enforce this article determines that a peddler or itinerant vendor
has violated any provision of this article or violated any federal, state or city law or ordinance or regulatory
agency rule, the city may suspend the peddler's permit or the itinerant vendor's license for a period not to
exceed three business days by personally serving the peddler or itinerant vendor with a written notice of the
suspension.
(b)
the written notice must provide the reason for suspension, the date the suspension begins, the duration of the
suspension, and a statement informing the peddler or itinerant vendor of his right to a public hearing before the
city manager. If the hearing cannot be immediately conducted, the city and the peddler or itinerant vendor shall
arrange the earliest reasonable date for the hearing. The results of the hearing shall be provided to the peddler
or itinerant vendor within ve business days of the hearing. If the peddler or itinerant vendor fails to make
arrangements for the hearing within three business days after requesting the hearing or if the peddler or
itinerant vendor chooses not to participate in the hearing, the city after proper notice, may revoke the peddler's
permit or the itinerant vendor's license.
(c)
If the peddler or itinerant vendor is dissatis ed with the results of the hearing before the city manager or if the
dispute is not thereby resolved, the city shall inform the peddler or itinerant vendor of their right to request a
hearing before the city council during the next regular city council meeting. The appeal must be tendered to the
city secretary within ten days of noti cation of the results of the hearing before the city manager.
(d)
The peddler or itinerant vendor shall forfeit the fee paid for the peddler permit or itinerant vendor license if the
city revokes such permit or license.
(Ord. No. 5-8-73, art. III, 5-8-1973; Ord. No. 4-11-05-4, art. III, § 3, 4-11-2005)

Sec. 18-37. - Penalty.
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article, or shall fail to comply therewith, or with
any of the requirements thereof, within the city limits shall be deemed guilty of an offense and shall be liable
for a fine not less than $200.00 and not to exceed the sum of $500.00. Each day the violation exists shall
constitute a separate offense. Such penalty shall be in addition to all the other remedies provided herein.
(Ord. No. 5-8-73, art. VIII, 5-8-1973; Ord. No. 4-11-05-4, art. IV, 4-11-2005)

Chapter 22 - CIVIL EMERGENCIES
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Secs. 22-1—22-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 22-31. - Liability of city.
This article is an exercise by the city of its governmental functions for the protection of the public peace,
health and safety, and neither the city, its agents and representatives, nor any individual, receiver, firm,
partnership, corporation, association or trustee, nor any of the agents thereof, in good faith carrying out,
complying with or attempting to comply with any order, rule or regulation promulgated pursuant to the
provisions of this article shall be liable for any damage sustained to persons as the result of such activity. Any
person owning or controlling real estate or other premises who voluntarily and without compensation grants
to the city a license or privilege, or otherwise permits the city to inspect, designate and use the whole or any
part of such real estate or premises for the purpose of sheltering persons during an actual, impending or
practice enemy attack or natural or manmade disaster shall, together with his successors in interest, if any,
not be civilly liable for the death of or injury to any person on or about such real estate or premises under
such license, privilege or other permission or for loss of or damage to the property of such person.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 6, 3-12-1991)

Sec. 22-32. - Overriding nature of regulations made pursuant to article.
At all times when the orders, rules and regulations made and promulgated pursuant to this article shall be
in effect, they shall supersede and override all existing ordinances, orders, rules and regulations insofar as the
existing ordinances, orders, rules and regulations may be inconsistent with the orders, rules and regulations
made and promulgated pursuant to this article.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 5, 3-12-1991)

Sec. 22-33. - Con ict.
This article shall not be construed so as to conflict with any state or federal statute or any military order,
rule or regulation.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 10, 3-12-1991)

Sec. 22-34. - O enses; penalties.
75/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(a)
It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully obstruct, hinder or delay any member of the emergency
management organization in the enforcement of any rule or regulation issued pursuant to this article.
(b)
It shall also be unlawful for any person to wear, carry or display any emblem, insignia or any other means of
identi cation as a member of the emergency management organization of the city, unless authority to do so has
been granted to such person by the proper o cials.
(c)
Any unauthorized person who shall operate a siren or other device so as to simulate a warning signal or the
termination of a warning shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this article and shall be subject to the penalties
imposed by this article.
(d)
Convictions for violations of the provisions of this article shall be punishable by a ne not to exceed $200.00.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 8, 3-12-1991)

State law reference—False alarms, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 42.06.
Secs. 22-35—22-60. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - ADMINISTRATION
Sec. 22-61. - Organization.
(a)

Director. There exists the o ce of emergency management director of the city, which shall be held by the mayor
in accordance with state law.
(b)

Coordinator. An emergency management coordinator may be appointed by and serve at the pleasure of the
emergency management director.
(c)

Responsibilities of director. The emergency management director shall be responsible for a program of
comprehensive emergency management within the city and for carrying out the duties and responsibilities set
forth in this division. He may delegate authority for execution of such duties to the coordinator, but ultimate
responsibility for such execution shall remain with the emergency management director.
(d)

Operational management organization. The operational emergency management organization of the city shall
consist of the o cers and employees of the city designated by the director in the emergency management plan,
as well as organized volunteer groups. The functions and duties of such organization shall be distributed among
such o cers and employees in accordance with the terms of the emergency management plan.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 1, 3-12-1991)

76/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 22-62. - Powers and duties of emergency management director.
The duties and responsibilities of the emergency management director shall include the following:
(1)
Conduct an ongoing survey of actual or potential hazards which threaten life and property within the city and an
ongoing program of identifying and requiring or recommending the implementation of measures which would
tend to prevent the occurrence or reduce the impact of such hazards if a disaster did occur.
(2)
Supervision of the development and approval of an emergency management plan for the city, and recommend
for adoption by the city council all mutual aid arrangements deemed necessary for the implementation of such
plan.
(3)
Authority to declare a local state of disaster. Such declaration may not be continued or renewed for a period in
excess of seven days, except by or with the consent of the city council. Any order or proclamation declaring,
continuing or terminating a local state of disaster shall be given prompt and general publicity and shall be led
promptly with the city secretary.
(4)
Issuance of necessary proclamations, regulations or directives which are necessary for carrying out the
purposes of this article. Such proclamations, regulations or directives shall be disseminated promptly by means
calculated to bring its contents to the attention of the general public and, unless circumstances attendant on the
disaster prevent or impede, promptly led with the city secretary.
(5)
Direction and control of the operations of the city emergency management organization, as well as the training
of emergency management personnel.
(6)
Determination of all questions of authority and responsibility that may arise within the emergency management
organization of the city.
(7)
Maintenance of liaison with other municipal, county, district, state, regional or federal emergency management
organizations.
(8)
Marshaling of all necessary personnel, equipment or supplies from any department of the city to aid in the
carrying out of the provisions of the emergency management plan.
(9)
Supervision of the drafting and execution of mutual aid agreements, in cooperation with the representatives of
the state and other local political subdivisions of the state, and the drafting and execution, if deemed desirable,
of an agreement with the county in which the city is located and with other municipalities within the county for
the countywide coordination of emergency management e orts.
(10)
77/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Supervision of and nal authorization for the procurement of all necessary supplies and equipment, including
acceptance of private contributions which may be o ered for the purpose of improving emergency
management within the city.
(11)
Authorizing of agreements, after approval by the city attorney, for use of private property for public shelter and
other purposes.
(12)
Survey of the availability of existing personnel, equipment, supplies and services which could be used during a
disaster, as provided for in this article.
(13)
Other requirements as speci ed in the Texas Disaster Act of 1975, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 418.001 et seq.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 2, 3-12-1991)

Sec. 22-63. - Commitment of funds.
No person shall have the right to expend any public funds of the city in carrying out any emergency
management activity authorized by this article without prior approval by the city council, nor shall any person
have any right to bind the city by contract, agreement or otherwise without prior and specific approval of the
city council, unless during a declared disaster. During a declared disaster, the mayor may expend and/or
commit public funds of the city when deemed prudent and necessary for the protection of health, life or
property.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 7, 3-12-1991)

Secs. 22-64—22-80. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - PLAN
Sec. 22-81. - Development and maintenance.
A comprehensive emergency management plan shall be developed and maintained in a current state. The
plan shall set forth the form of the organization; establish and designate divisions and functions; assign
responsibilities, tasks, duties and powers; and designate officers and employees to carry out the provisions of
this article. As provided by state law, the plan shall follow the standards and criteria established by the state
division of emergency management. Insofar as possible, the form of organization, titles and terminology shall
conform to the recommendations of the state division of emergency management. When approved, it shall be
the duty of all departments and agencies to perform the functions assigned by the plan and to maintain their
portion of the plan in a current state of readiness at all times. The emergency management plan shall be
considered supplementary to this article and have the effect of law during the time of a disaster.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 3, 3-12-1991)

78/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 22-82. - Interjurisdictional emergency management program.
The mayor is authorized to join with the county judge and the mayors of the other cities in the county in
the formation of an interjurisdictional emergency management program for the county and shall have the
authority to cooperate in the preparation of an interjurisdictional emergency management plan and the
appointment of a joint emergency management coordinator, as well as all powers necessary to participate in a
countywide program of emergency management insofar as the program may affect the city.
(Ord. No. 3-12-91-3, § 4, 3-12-1991)

Chapter 26 - COURTS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 26-1. - Copying charges for public records.
(a)
The service charge for copying governmental and public records shall be as follows:
(1)
For readily available information on standard size pages (up to 8½ inches by 14 inches) the copying charge shall
be $0.25 per page.
(2)
For information which is not readily available the copying charge shall be $0.15 per page, plus actual labor costs
incurred by the city in providing the requested information.
(b)
In addition, the city may also add any postal expenses which may be necessary to transmit the reproduced
documents to the requesting party.
(c)
The city secretary shall establish the copying or reproduction charge for nonstandard sized pages or documents
(maps, books, etc.).
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-1, § 7, 10-8-2001; Ord. No. 6-14-04-1, § 7, 6-14-2004)

State law reference—Charge for copy of public information provided by the municipal court clerk, V.T.C.A.,
Government Code § 552.266.
Sec. 26-2. - Con dential payment and communication records.
The municipal court clerk shall separately file from the records of any case in the municipal court any
documents collected, assembled or otherwise maintained containing a credit card, debit card charge card, or
other access device number. The municipal court clerk shall redact the e-mail address from any
communications received via e-mail or shall maintain such documents separately of the documents of the

79/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

case. The e-mail address of any individual communicating with the court shall not be disclosed to a member of
the public without express consent of the individual. Any requests for documents containing this information
shall be immediately referred to the city attorney's office.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-1, § 9, 10-8-2001; Ord. No. 6-14-04-1, § 9, 6-14-2004)

State law reference—Confidentiality of credit card numbers and certain e-mail addresses, V.T.C.A.,
Government Code §§ 552.136, 552.137.
Sec. 26-3. - Jury duty pay.
The city shall pay each person appearing in response to a duly noticed jury summons $6.00 for service in
municipal court for each day or fraction of each day they serve as a juror.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-1, § 8, 10-8-2001; Ord. No. 6-14-04-1, § 8, 6-14-2004)

Sec. 26-4. - Prima facie evidence.
(a)

Vehicles. In any prosecution charging a violation of this Code governing the stopping, standing or parking of a
vehicle, proof that the particular vehicle described in the complaint was parked in violation of this Code,
together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was, at the time of such parking, the registered
owner of such vehicle, shall constitute in evidence a prima facie presumption that the registered owner of such
vehicle was the person who parked or placed such vehicle at the point where, and for the time during which,
such violation occurred.
(b)

Properties. In any prosecution charging a violation regarding nuisances upon a property, the failure to comply
with any notice or order regarding a nuisance on a property or building in violation of an ordinance of the city,
including but not limited to failure to apply for a building permit or other permit or license required herein,
proof that the particular property described in the complaint was in violation of an ordinance regulating the
property, together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was, at the time of such notice,
violation or order or at the time when work was performed without a permit, the registered owner of such
property, shall constitute in evidence a prima facie presumption that the registered owner of such property was
the person who failed to comply with the notice or order or failed to apply for a permit for the time during which
such violation occurred in violation of the charged ordinance of the city.
(c)

Animals. In any prosecution charging a violation of an ordinance or statute regulating or governing the abuse,
neglect or ownership of an animal or failure to license an animal as required, proof that the particular property
described in the complaint was the premises upon which the animal resided, was harbored or maintained and a
violation of an ordinance or statute regulating or governing the animal alleged in the complaint together with
proof that the defendant named in the complaint was, at the time of such complaint or at the time when the
animal was in violation of said ordinance or statute, the registered owner of such animal or the person with
legal rights to reside on said property, shall constitute in evidence a prima facie presumption that the registered
80/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

owner of such property or the person with legal rights to reside on said property was the owner of the animal
and the person who failed to comply with or violated the ordinance or statute.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-1, § 10, 10-8-2001; Ord. No. 6-14-04-1, § 10, 6-14-2004)

Secs. 26-5—26-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - COLLECTION OF FINES, COSTS AND SPECIAL EXPENSES
Sec. 26-31. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Access device shall mean a card, plate, code, account number, personal identification number, electronic
serial number, mobile identification number, or other telecommunications service, equipment, or instrument
identifier or means of account access that alone or in conjunction with other access devices may be used to:
(1)
Obtain money, goods, services, or another thing of value; or
(2)
Initiate a transfer of funds other than a transfer originated solely by paper instrument.

Conviction or convicted shall mean any person be deemed to have been convicted for whom the
municipal court imposes any penalty or sentence, the person receives community service, supervision or
deferred adjudication, or the Court defers final disposition of the case.

Rules of the Road shall mean offenses committed under V.T.C.A., Transportation Code chs. 541—600.
School crossing zone shall mean a reduced-speed zone designated on a street by a local authority to
facilitate safe crossing of the street by children going to or leaving a public or private elementary or secondary
school during the time the reduce speed limit applies.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-1, § 2, 10-8-2001; Ord. No. 6-14-04-1, § 2, 6-14-2004)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 26-32. - Fees.
The fines imposed in the municipal court may be the same as are prescribed for like offenses by the penal
statutes of the state, but shall never be greater. Where any offense is covered solely and alone by ordinances
of the city, such ordinance shall control. The Municipal Court Clerk shall collect and report all court costs as
required.
(1)

State court costs.

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

a.
The municipal court clerk shall collect each and every court cost statutorily mandated to be collected for the
state. The municipal court clerk shall keep a record of each court cost collected for the bene t of the state and
report the collection to the director of nance or designee including forwarding the monies to be deposited with
the director of nance or designee as required by internal policy.
b.
The director of nance or designee may deposit the money in an interest bearing account. The director of

court costs collected for the bene t of the state to the comptroller of public accounts not later than the last day
of the month following the calendar quarter in which the court costs were collected.
c.
The director of nance or designee shall report the fees collected for a calendar quarter categorized according
to the class of o ense and shall report the court costs collected for the bene t of the state to the comptroller of
public accounts not later than the last day of the month following the calendar quarter in which the court costs
were collected.
State law reference—Fees remitted to state comptroller, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 133.055—

enforcement agencies other than state troopers and city police o cers executing a warrant must submit a

Failure to appear fees.
a.

Special expense. The Municipal Court Clerk shall collect a special expense of $25.00 for the issuance and service

to appear. The Municipal Court Clerk shall report each special expense collected to the Director of Finance or

Contract with state department of public safety. At all times that the city has a contract with the state
department of public safety to deny renewal of licenses for individuals failing to appear in court as directed, the

1.
The court enters judgment on the o ense for which the failure to appear was submitted;
2.
The case is dismissed; or
3.
Bond or other security is posted to reinstate the charge for which the warrant was issued.
4.
The defendant fails to pay or satisfy a judgment in the manner ordered by the court. Distribution of the funds
shall be as provided by agreement with the state department of public safety. The municipal court clerk shall
maintain a copy of the agreement and report each failure to appear fee collected as well as the distribution of
the fee to the director of nance or designee. Should a defendant fail to pay the $30.00 administrative fee as
required, the municipal court clerk shall report such failure to the state department of public safety and request
the department deny renewal of the defendant's license.

a.
Each defendant being permitted to make payments on any part of a ne, court cost or restitution on or after the

(5)

Arrest fees. The municipal court clerk shall collect a $5.00 arrest fee with each conviction. The arrest fee shall be

payable to the comptroller with the remaining $4.00 being reported as distributable to the city police
department. Any law enforcement agency other than the state trooper or a city police o cer submitting a
citation to the municipal court for which a conviction occurs, the municipal court shall hold the $5.00 arrest fee
for fteen working days. Should the law enforcement agency fail to claim the arrest fee in 15 working days after
the conviction, the municipal court clerk shall report the arrest fee as payable to the city police department. For
each citation that the city police department issues a citation and a conviction occurs, the full arrest fee shall be
reported as payable to the city police department.
State law reference—Court costs in certain counties, Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 102.009(a)(1).

Dishonored check fees. A service charge of $25.00 shall be assessed against any person who pays the city with a

to be paid by the defendant.

Sec. 26-33. - Funds.
In addition to the court costs mandated to be collected under state statute for the state and remitted to
the comptroller as court costs, and as set out in section 26-32, court costs shall be collected for each
conviction as follows:
(1)

Child safety fund.
a.

School crossing fee. Each defendant convicted of violating any provision of the Rules of the Road, V.T.C.A.,
Transportation Code tit. 7, subtit. C, within a school crossing zone or convicted for passing a school bus in
violation of V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.066, shall pay an additional $25.00, taxable as court costs.
b.

Failure to attend school fee. Each defendant convicted of violating the V.T.C.A., Education Code § 25.093,
Thwarting Compulsory Attendance, or V.T.C.A., Education Code § 25.094, Failure to Attend School, shall pay an
additional $20.00, taxable as court costs.
c.

Collection and deposit. The municipal court clerk shall collect such court costs, including the school crossing fee
and failure to attend school fee, and pay such court costs to the director of nance or designee for all o enses
governed by this subsection. For all nes collected pursuant to V.T.C.A., Education Code § 25.093, Thwarting
Compulsory Attendance, the municipal court clerk shall report 50 percent of the ne to be deposited to the
credit of the operating fund of the school district in which the child attends school or to the juvenile justice
alternative education program, if the child has been ordered to attend such a program. The remaining 50
percent of the ne collected under V.T.C.A., Education Code § 25.093 shall be reported as payable to the general
fund of the city. The director of nance or designee shall deposit the $25.00 school crossing fee and the $20.00
failure to attend school fee portion of such court costs into the child safety fund. The director of nance or
designee shall quarterly forward 50 percent of the ne collected under V.T.C.A., Education Code § 25.093,
payable to the school district which the convicted children attend or, if the children were sentenced to a juvenile
justice alternative education program, the city treasurer shall forward the 50 percent to such program. The
remaining 50 percent of the ne collected shall be deposited to the general fund of the city.
d.

7/12/2019

Seat belt fund. The municipal court clerk shall report each ne collected for violations committed after

interest bearing account and annually remit 50 percent of all nes collected from defendants for violations of
V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 545.412 and 545.413(b). The director of nance shall retain the entire ne for
violations of V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.413(a), which requires persons at least 15 years of age riding in
the front seat of a passenger vehicle to wear a safety belt, and deposit said ne with the city pursuant to this
article and applicable internal policy.

Sec. 26-34. - Waiver of nes, fees and costs of court.
The municipal court judge may hold a hearing to determine the economic capabilities of any defendant
filing a written motion seeking a finding of the court that the defendant is per se indigent and each alternative
method of discharging the fine or costs of court under Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art 43.09 would impose an undue
hardship on the defendant. The municipal court judge shall review the motion of the defendant, including any

89/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

another evidence deemed necessary, and on a finding that defendant is indigent as a matter of law and that
the alternative methods of discharge would work an undue hardship on the defendant the municipal court
judge may waive payment of any fines or costs for which the defendant has defaulted.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-1, § 5, 10-8-2001; Ord. No. 6-14-04-1, § 5, 6-14-2004)

Sec. 26-35. - Post-judgment collection of nes and court costs.
As provided in this Code and state statutes, the municipal court judge shall assess fines and court costs
against each defendant entering a plea of guilty or no contest or based upon the verdict of the court or jury
finding a defendant guilty. Defendants who have not timely appealed the judgment of the court and fail to
timely pay fines, fees, costs or restitutions as ordered shall be subject to permitted post-judgment collection
procedures.
(1)

Capias pro ne. The municipal court judge may order a capias pro ne to be issued for any defendant failing to
satisfy a judgment of the court according to the terms of the judgment. The municipal court clerk shall ensure
that each capias states the amount of the judgment and sentence, and commands a peace o cer to bring the
defendant before the court or place the defendant in jail until the defendant can be brought before the court.
State law reference—Capias pro fine, Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 45.045.
(2)

Commitment. Defendants failing to satisfy any judgment may be committed to satisfy the judgment as provided
in the Code of Criminal Procedure. Any defendant committed to jail, serving less than eight consecutive hours in
jail, shall not be given credit for time served. The court may specify a period of time that is not less than eight
hours or more than 24 hours as the period for which a defendant who fails to pay the nes and costs in the case
must remain in jail to satisfy $50.00 of the ne and costs. Defendants committing o enses prior to January 1,
2004, shall receive $100.00 credit for each time period served.
State law reference—Discharged from jail, Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 45.048.
(3)

Private collection contract. At all times that the city council has authorized a private collection contract with a
private attorney or a public or private vendor for collection services relating to nes, fees, restitutions or other
debts or costs, other than forfeited bonds, the municipal court is authorized to collect an additional 30 percent
on each such debt or account receivable that is more than 60 days past due and has been collected as a result
of the action of a duly authorized contractor. The municipal court clerk shall report the 30 percent as payable to
the contractor. Should the contractor collect less than the full sum due from defendant, the municipal court
clerk shall ensure that the payment is distributed rst in an amount su cient to fully compensate the contractor
and then in equal shares to the comptroller and the city until the comptroller is paid in full.
State law reference—Collection, Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 103.003.
(4)

90/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Civil assessment against property. The municipal court judge may review a judgment in which the defendant has
defaulted in payment, either in whole or part after sentencing, and may order the ne and costs be collected by
execution against the defaulting defendant's property in the same manner as a judgment in a civil suit.
State law reference—Collection of fines after judgment, Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 45.047.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-1, § 6, 10-8-2001; Ord. No. 6-14-04-1, § 6, 6-14-2004)

Chapter 30 - ENVIRONMENT
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Secs. 30-1—30-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - RUBBISH, BRUSH AND OTHER UNSANITARY MATTER
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 30-31. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Brush means large trees or shrub limbs, branches or trimmings which cannot be handled in standard city
garbage trucks.

City representative means the city's representative as appointed by the city council.
Rubbish means all waste material resulting from domestic or commercial operations and activities,
including, but not limited to, discarded large appliances, household and yard refuse, tires, automotive parts
and inoperable machinery.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-1), 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 30-32. - Duty of owner to maintain private property.
The owner of any lot, ground or premises within the city shall keep such lot, ground or premises free from
rubbish, brush and other unsanitary matter of any nature.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-2), 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Authority to prohibit unwholesome or unsanitary matter, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety
Code §§ 342.003, 342.004.

91/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 30-33. - Violation; penalty.
Any person violating any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be fined in an amount not less
than $100.00, and not exceeding $500.00, and such person shall be deemed guilty of a separate offense for
each and every day, or portion thereof, in which the violation is continued or permitted.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-9), 10-22-2001)

Secs. 30-34—30-50. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - ABATEMENT
Sec. 30-51. - Enforcement.
The city representative or any police officer shall enforce the provisions of this article, provided, that
where a fire hazard exists by virtue of a violation of this article, the provisions of this article may be enforced
by the fire marshal.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-3), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-52. - Notice to abate; service of notice.
Upon the failure of the owner of any lot, ground or premises within the city to keep such lot, ground or
premises free from rubbish, brush or any other objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter of any nature,
the city representative shall notify and instruct such owner to bring the lot, ground or premises into
compliance with section 30-32 within ten days. The notice shall be in writing and shall specify, with reasonable
particularity, the rubbish, brush or other objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter to be removed. The
notice may be served upon the owner by handing it to him in person, or by United States certified mail, return
receipt requested, addressed to the last known mailing address of the owner. If the owner cannot be
personally served or the certified letter is returned by the United States Postal Service, notice may be given by
publication two times within ten consecutive days in a newspaper of general circulation in the city.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-5), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-53. - Failure to comply with notice.
A person commits an offense if he is an owner of a lot, ground or premises within the city and fails to clear
such premises of rubbish, brush and any other objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter of any nature
within ten days after receiving a notice as required in section 30-52.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-4), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-54. - Appeal.

92/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

If, after notice and prior to a citation being issued, a property owner or occupant disagrees with the
property in question being in noncompliance with the requirements of section 30-53, he shall have the right of
appeal. The appeal board shall consist of the city manager, director of public works and a member of the city
council appointed to the appeal board by the city council. The request to meet with the appeal board must be
in writing and shall be submitted prior to the ten-day expiration of the original notice. Such appeal notice shall
be submitted to the city secretary and a receipt will be issued. An appeal will then be held within five working
days, and the person appealing shall be given the opportunity to meet with the appeal board. The appeal
board will give a decision and notify the person making such appeal in writing of their decision.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-6), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-55. - Removal of matter by the city; notice required.
(a)
In addition to any penalty imposed for a violation of section 30-53, upon the failure of the owner of any lot,
ground or premises within the city to keep such lot, ground or premises free from rubbish, brush or other
objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter, the city may remove such matter from the premises.
(b)
Before having any rubbish, brush or other objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter removed from the
premises, the city representative shall give the notice required in section 30-52 to the owner of such premises.
(c)
Notice given by the city representative in accordance with the provisions of section 30-52 in connection with a
violation of section 30-53 shall constitute notice in compliance with this section.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-7), 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Work or improvements by municipality, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.006.
Sec. 30-56. - Levy of charges; lien on property for failure to pay.
(a)
If the city removes rubbish, brush or other objectionable, unsightly or unsanitary matter from a premises upon
the failure of the owner of the premises to comply with the terms of the notice required under section 30-52,
charges in the amount of the total actual costs incurred by the city in performing such work shall be collected by
the city secretary. If the charges are not paid within 30 days after notice to the property owner that the charges
are due, the city secretary shall le with the county clerk a statement signed by the mayor or city secretary of
the total actual costs incurred by the city in cleaning and/or removing rubbish, brush or other objectionable,
unsightly or unsanitary matter from the premises.
(b)
Upon the ling of the statement under subsection (a) of this section, the city shall have a privileged lien against
the property, second only to tax liens and liens for street improvements, in the amount of the actual costs
incurred by the city, together with interest at the rate of ten percent per annum on such amount from the date
the costs were incurred.
93/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(c)
For any such expenditures and interest as set out in subsections (a) and (b) of this section, a suit may be
instituted and recovery and foreclosure had in the name of the city. The statement led under subsection (a) of
this section, or a certi ed copy thereof, shall be prima facie proof of the amount of actual costs incurred by the
city.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-8, § 1(I-8), 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Assessment of expenses, lien, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.007.
Secs. 30-57—30-90. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - WEEDS AND GRASS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 30-91. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

City representative means the city's authorized representative as appointed by the city council.
Person means any individual, firm, partnership, association, company, corporation or organization of any
kind.

Premises means any lot, plat or parcel of land, together with the front or side property between the
property line or sidewalk and curb or traveled way and the rear or side property between the property line
and centerline of an adjacent alley.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-9, § 1(I-1), 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 30-92. - Growth over 12 inches prohibited.
(a)

O ense. A person commits an o ense if he is an owner, occupant or person in control of an occupied or
unoccupied premises within the city limits and permits weeds, grass or vegetation located on the premises to
grow to a height greater than 12 inches.
(b)

Exceptions. It is an exception to the provisions of subsection (a) of this section that the property is being used
for the planting, cultivating, harvesting or storage of grains, hay, or plants commonly grown in the vicinity, and
the property in question is one or more acres in area. In such case, the 12 feet of property adjoining streets or
other property shall be cut to speci cations of this article.
94/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(c)

Defenses.
(1)
It is a defense to prosecution under subsection (a) of this section that the premises have been brought into
compliance within ten days from the date of issuance of a citation.
(2)
The defense to prosecution provided in subsection (b) of this section may not be asserted by a person who,
within the preceding one-year period, has been issued a citation for a violation of subsection (a) of this section
which resulted in:
a.
Dismissal of the complaint under the defense as set forth in subsection (c)(1) of this section;
b.
Dismissal of the complaint by deferred adjudication; or
c.
Conviction.
(d)

Culpable mental state. Allegation and proof of a culpable mental state is not required for the proof of an o ense
de ned by this section.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-9, § 1(I-2), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-93. - Violation; penalty.
Any person violating any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than $100.00 and
not exceeding $500.00, and such person shall be guilty of a separate offense for each and every day, or
portion thereof, in which the violation is continued or permitted.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-9, § 1(I-7), 10-22-2001)

costs incurred by the city in cutting and removing weeds or grass from the premises.
(b)
Upon the ling of the statement under subsection (a) of this section, the city shall have a privileged lien against
the property, second only to tax liens and liens for street improvements, in the amount of actual costs incurred,

ARTICLE IV. - LITTER
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 30-141. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

City representative means the city's authorized representative appointed by the city council.
Commercial handbill means any printed or written matter, sample or device, dodger, circular, leaflet,
pamphlet, paper, booklet or any other printed or otherwise reproduced original or copy of any matter of
literature which:
(1)
Advertises any merchandise, product, commodity or thing for sale;
(2)
Directs attention to any business or mercantile or commercial establishment, or other activity, for the purpose
of either, directly or indirectly, promoting the interest thereof by sales;
(3)
Directs attention to or advertises any meeting, theatrical performance, exhibition or event of any kind for which
an admission fee is charged for the purpose of private gain or pro t; or
(4)
While containing reading matter other than advertising matter, is predominantly and essentially an
advertisement, and is distributed or circulated for advertising purposes, or for the private bene t and gain of
any person so engaged as the advertiser or distributor.

Garbage means putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling, preparation,
cooking and consumption of food.

97/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Litter means "garbage," "refuse" and "rubbish", as such terms are defined in this section, and all other
waste material which, if thrown or deposited as prohibited in this article, tends to create a danger to public
health, safety and welfare.

Newspaper means any newspaper of general circulation as defined by general law; any newspaper duly
entered with the post office department of the United States in accordance with federal statute or regulation;
and any newspaper filed and recorded with any recording officer as provided by general law, and, in addition
thereto, means and includes any periodical or current magazine regularly published with not less than four
issues per year, and sold to the public.

Noncommercial handbill means any printed or written matter, sample or device, dodger, circular, leaflet,
pamphlet, newspaper, magazine, paper, booklet or any other printed or otherwise reproduced original or
copies of any matter of literature not included in the definition of a "commercial handbill" or "newspaper," as
such term is defined in this section.

Public place means any place to which the public or a substantial group of the public has access, including,
but not limited to, any and all streets, sidewalks, boulevards, alleys, rights-of-way or other public ways; any and
all public parks, squares, spaces, grounds and buildings; and the common areas of schools, hospitals,
apartment houses, office buildings, transport facilities and shops.

Refuse means all putrescible and nonputrescible solid wastes, including, but not limited to, garbage,
rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, dead animals, abandoned automobiles, and solid market and industrial
wastes.

Rubbish means nonputrescible solid wastes consisting of both combustible and noncombustible wastes,
including, but not limited to, paper and paper products, wrappings, cardboard and cardboard signs, tin,
aluminum and other metals, yard clippings, leaves, wood, glass, bedding, crockery and similar materials.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-1), 5-10-1988)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 30-142. - Throwing or depositing in public places prohibited; exception.
No person shall throw or deposit litter, in any manner whatsoever, in or upon any street, sidewalk or
other public place within the city, except in receptacles.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-2), 5-10-1988)

Cross reference—Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 78.
Sec. 30-143. - Throwing or depositing upon private property.
No person shall throw or deposit litter, in any manner whatsoever, in or upon any occupied, unoccupied
or vacant private property within the city, whether or not such property is owned by such person.
98/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-3), 5-10-1988)

Sec. 30-144. - Manner of placement in receptacles.
Persons placing litter in receptacles for litter shall do so in a manner so as to prevent such litter from
being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or private property.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-4), 5-10-1988)

Sec. 30-145. - Sweeping into gutters, streets or public places; responsibility for keeping sidewalks free from litter.
(a)
No person shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the city, the accumulation
of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway.
(b)
Persons owning or occupying property shall keep the sidewalk in front of their premises free from litter.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-5), 5-10-1988)

Cross reference—Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 78.
Sec. 30-146. - Throwing by persons in vehicles.
While a driver or passenger in a vehicle, no person shall throw or deposit, in any manner whatsoever, any
litter upon any street or other public place or private property within the city.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-6), 5-10-1988)

Cross reference—Traffic and vehicles, ch. 90.
Sec. 30-147. - Securing of load; surcharge.
(a)
No person shall drive or move any truck or other vehicle within the city unless such vehicle is constructed or
loaded so as to prevent any load, contents or litter from being blown or deposited upon any street, alley or
other public place as required by state law and subject to all exceptions recognized in state law.
(b)
A surcharge will be assessed against any load brought to any city disposal area which has not been secured as
required by state law.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-11), 5-10-1988)

State law reference—Transportation of loose materials, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code ch. 725.
Sec. 30-148. - Parks.

99/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

No person shall throw or deposit any litter in any park within the city, except in receptacles therefor, and
in such a manner that the litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any
part of the park or other public place. Where litter receptacles are not provided, all such litter shall be carried
away from the park by the person responsible for the presence of such litter and properly disposed of
elsewhere.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-7), 5-10-1988)

Cross reference—Parks and recreation, ch. 62.
Sec. 30-149. - Lakes.
No person shall throw or deposit litter in any fountain, pond, lake, stream or any other body of water in a
park or elsewhere in the city.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-8), 5-10-1988)

Sec. 30-150. - Handbills.
(a)

Throwing or depositing in public places. No person shall throw or deposit, in any manner whatsoever, any
commercial or noncommercial handbill in or upon any sidewalk, street or other public place within the city.
(b)

Depositing on uninhabited or vacant premises. No person shall place, throw or deposit, in any manner
whatsoever, any commercial or noncommercial handbill in or upon any private property or premises which is
temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-9, I-10), 5-10-1988)

Sec. 30-151. - Duty of owners and occupants to maintain private property free from litter.
It shall be unlawful for any owner, occupant or person in control of private property to place, throw,
deposit, permit to accumulate or permit or cause to be placed, thrown or deposited any litter on such private
property, or on any gutter adjacent to such private property, or in or on one-half of the portion of an alley
adjacent to such property, unless such litter has been deposited in receptacles for collection in compliance
with the requirements of section 30-144.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-12), 5-10-1988)

Sec. 30-152. - Violation; penalty.
Any person who violates any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be fined an amount not to
exceed $500.00, and such person shall be deemed guilty of a separate offense for each and every day, or
portion thereof, in which the violation is continued or permitted.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-16), 5-10-1988)

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Secs. 30-153—30-170. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - ABATEMENT
Sec. 30-171. - Enforcement.
The city representative or any police officer of the city shall have authority to enforce the provisions of this
article when violations of this article occur on private property. Any police officer of the city is authorized to
enforce the provisions of this article when a violation occurs in a public place as defined in section 30-141.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-17), 5-10-1988)

Sec. 30-172. - Clearing of litter from private property.
The city's representative shall notify the owner, occupant or person in control of private property,
including any gutter adjacent to such private property or one-half of the portion of an alley adjacent to such
private property, upon which litter has been thrown, deposited or permitted to accumulate, to remove such
litter within ten days and thereafter to maintain such private property free of litter. The notice shall be in
writing and may be served upon the owner, occupant or person in control of the private property by delivering
such notice to him in person or to an adult person at his residence or place of business, or by certified letter,
return receipt requested, addressed to such owner, occupant or person in control of the private property at
such person's last known mailing address. It shall be unlawful for any owner, occupant or person in control of
private property to fail, neglect or refuse to properly dispose of litter upon such private property within ten
days after the notice is provided as set forth in this section. A citation shall be issued if such litter has not been
removed within the ten-day period after the notice has been delivered.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-13), 5-10-1988)

Sec. 30-173. - Appeal.
If, after notice and prior to a citation being issued as provided in section 30-172, a property owner or
occupant disagrees with the property in question being in noncompliance with this article, he shall have the
right of appeal. The appeal board shall consist of the city manager, director of public works and a member of
the city council appointed to the appeal board by the city council. The request to meet with the appeal board
must be in writing and submitted prior to the ten-day expiration of the original notice. Such appeal notice shall
be submitted to the city secretary and a receipt will be issued. An appeal hearing will then be held within five
working days, and the person appealing shall be given the opportunity to meet with the appeal board. The
appeal board will give a decision on such appeal, and notify the person appealing in writing of their decision.
(Ord. No. 2-9-88-2, § 1(I-14), 5-10-1988)
