ARTICLE V. - ABANDONED AND JUNKED VEHICLES
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 30-201. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Abandoned motor vehicle means a vehicle that:
(1)
Is inoperative and over ve years old and is left unattended on public property for more than 48 hours;
(2)
Has illegally remained on public property for a period of more than 48 hours;
(3)
Has remained on private property without the consent of the owner or person in control of the property for
more than 48 hours; or
(4)

102/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Has been left unattended on the right-of-way of a designated county, state or federal highway for more that 48
hours.

Antique auto means a passenger car or truck that is at least 25 years old.
Collector means the owner of one or more antique or special interest vehicles, who collects, purchases,
acquires, trades or disposes of special interest or antique vehicles, or parts thereof, for personal use in order
to restore, preserve and maintain an antique or special interest vehicle for historic interest.

Demolisher means a person whose business is to convert a motor vehicle into processed scrap or scrap
metal, or to otherwise wreck or dismantle a motor vehicle.

Garage keeper means an owner or operator of a parking place or establishment or motor vehicle storage
facility or establishment for the servicing, repair or maintenance of a motor vehicle.

Junked vehicle means any vehicle that is designed to be self-propelled and is inoperable, and that:
(1)
Does not have lawfully a xed to it:
a.
An unexpired license plate; or
b.
A valid motor vehicle safety inspection certi cate.
(2)
Is wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled or discarded;
(3)
Remains inoperable for more that 30 consecutive days; or
(4)
Shows no signs of repair or restoration.

Motor vehicle means any motor vehicle subject to registration pursuant to the Certificate of Title Act,
V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 501.001 et seq.

Outboard motor means an outboard motor subject to registration under V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code
§ 31.001 et seq.

Police department means the City of Dublin Police Department and any other law enforcement agency as
defined in V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.001.

Special interest vehicle means a motor vehicle of any age that has not been altered or modified from the
original manufacturer's specifications and, because of its historic interest, is being preserved by hobbyists.

Storage facility means a garage, parking lot or any type of facility or establishment for the servicing,
repairing, storing or parking of motor vehicles.
103/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Watercraft means a vessel subject to registration under V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code § 31.001 et seq.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 2, 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 683.001, 683.002, 683.071.
Sec. 30-202. - Exceptions.
Vehicles which are under repair; awaiting parts or adjustments by an insurance company; at a licensed
salvage yard or commercial vehicle sales and/or repair facility are exempt from this article only where this
articles pertains to vehicles.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 15, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-203. - Violation; penalty.
Any person convicted of a violation any provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall
be punished as provided in section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 16, 10-22-2001)

Secs. 30-204—30-220. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
Sec. 30-221. - Responsibility.
The administration of this article shall be the responsibility of the chief of police or such department,
officer or employee of the city designated by the city council, provided, that the code enforcement officer is
authorized to administer and supervise the sections and provisions of this article applying to junk
vehicles.Whoever is so authorized may enter upon private property for the purposes specified in this article to
examine motor vehicles, or parts thereof, obtain information as to the identity of motor vehicles and to
remove, or cause the removal of, a motor vehicle, or parts thereof, declared to be a nuisance pursuant to this
article.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 3, 10-22-2001)

Secs. 30-222—30-240. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - PROCEDURE FOR ABATEMENT
Subdivision I. - In General

104/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Secs. 30-241—30-255. - Reserved.
Subdivision II. - Abandoned Motor Vehicles
Sec. 30-256. - Authority to take possession.
The police department is authorized to take into custody any abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft or
outboard motor found on public or private property.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 4, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.011.
Sec. 30-257. - Notice of impoundment to owner and lienholder.
The police department shall send notice of abandonment to each owner and lienholder of record
pursuant to the Certificate of Title Act, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 501.001 et seq. or, as applicable,
V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code § 31.001 et seq. Such notice shall be given within ten days after the date the
motor vehicle, watercraft or outboard motor is taken into custody, or the date the police department receives
a report of abandonment. The notice shall be sent by certified mail, return receipt requested, and shall specify
the year, make, model and identification number of the vehicle; set forth the location of the facility where the
vehicle is being held; and inform the owner and any lienholder of the right to reclaim the vehicle not later than
the 20th day after the date of the notice upon payment of all towing, preservation, storage and/or garage
keeper charges. The notice shall state that the failure of the owner or lienholder to exercise the right to
reclaim the vehicle within the time provided shall be deemed a waiver of all rights, title and interest in the
vehicle and their consent to the sale of the vehicle at a public auction. If the identity of the last registered
owner of the vehicle cannot be determined; the registration contains no address for the owner; or it is
impossible to determine with reasonable certainty the identity and addresses of all lienholders, notice by one
publication in a newspaper of general circulation in the city shall be made within ten days from the date the
vehicle was taken into custody or from the date the report of abandonment was received. The published
notice shall be sufficient if it contains the information otherwise required to be included in the notice by mail,
and a list of motor vehicles, watercraft or outboard motors may be included in the same publication.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 5, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.012.
Sec. 30-258. - Use by police department.
(a)
If an abandoned motor vehicle has not been reclaimed as provided in section 30-257, provided, that a garage
keeper's lien has not been attached to the vehicle, the police department may use such abandoned motor
vehicle for police department purposes if such use is cost e ective.
(b)
105/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

If the police department discontinues use of the abandoned motor vehicle, it shall auction such abandoned
motor vehicle as provided in section 30-259.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 6, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.016.
Sec. 30-259. - Auction sales; disposition of proceeds.
(a)
If an abandoned motor vehicle, watercraft or outboard motor has not been reclaimed within 20 days after the
date of notice and payment of all towing, preservation and storage charges resulting from the impoundment
thereof, the police department shall sell the motor vehicle, watercraft or outboard motor at a public auction.
Proper notice of the public auction shall be given and the garage keeper shall be noti ed of the time and place
of such auction if a vehicle is to be sold in satisfaction of a garage keeper's lien.
(b)
The police department shall furnish a sales receipt for each vehicle to the purchaser thereof at the public
auction. The proceeds from the auction shall be applied rst to reimburse the police department for the
expenses of the auction, costs of towing, preserving and storing the vehicle, and all notice and publication costs,
and any remainder from the proceeds of the sale shall be held for the owner of the vehicle or entitled lienholder
for 90 days, and then such amount shall be deposited in a special fund with the city treasurer, which amount
shall remain available for the payment of auction, towing, preserving, storage and all notice and publication
costs which result from placing other abandoned vehicles in custody, whenever the proceeds from a sale of
such other abandoned motor vehicles are insu cient to meet such expenses and costs. If the special fund on
deposit with the city treasurer accumulates to an excess of $1,000.00, the city council may transfer the balance
of such fund that exceeds $1,000.00 to the general fund for use by the police department as budgeted.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 7, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 683.014, 683.015.
Sec. 30-260. - Custody, reports and proceeds.
(a)
Upon receipt of a report from a garage keeper that a motor vehicle has been deemed abandoned pursuant to
V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.031, the police department shall follow the noti cation procedures set forth
in section 30-257 for the giving of notice to owners and lienholders of abandoned vehicles, except that custody
of the vehicle shall remain with the garage keeper until after the noti cation requirements have been satis ed.
(b)
A fee of $5.00 shall accompany the report of the garage keeper, and such fee shall be retained by the police
department receiving the report, and used to defray the cost of noti cation or other costs incurred in the
disposition of such vehicle, and such fee shall be deposited in the general fund of the city. Abandoned vehicles
left in storage facilities, which are not reclaimed after notice is given in accordance with this section, shall be
taken into custody by the police department and sold at auction, as in the case of other abandoned motor
106/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

vehicles. The proceeds of the sale shall rst be applied to the garage keeper's charges for servicing, storage and
repair of such vehicle; provided, however, that the police department shall retain an amount of two percent of
the gross proceeds of the sale for each vehicle auctioned, but in no event shall it retain less than $10.00, which
shall be used to defray expenses of custody and auction of the vehicle.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 8, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 683.031, 683.034.
Sec. 30-261. - Disposal to demolisher.
The police department is authorized to apply to the state department of transportation for authority to
sell, give away or dispose of any abandoned motor vehicle in its possession to a demolisher in accordance
with the provisions of V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.051.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 9, 10-22-2001)

Secs. 30-262—30-275. - Reserved.
Subdivision III. - Junked Vehicles
Sec. 30-276. - Public nuisance declared.
V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.072 declares that junked vehicles located in any place where they are
readily visible from a public place or public right-of-way are detrimental to the safety and welfare of the
general public; reduce the value of private property; invite vandalism; create fire hazards; constitute an
attractive nuisance creating a hazard to the health and safety of minors; produce urban blight adverse to the
maintenance and continuing development of the city; and are a public nuisance. The city council adopts such
findings and declarations, and declares that junked vehicles are a public nuisance.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 10, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-277. - Maintaining a public nuisance.
It shall be unlawful for any person to maintain a public nuisance within the city as defined in section 30276. Any person found guilty of maintaining a public nuisance as defined in section 30-276 shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and be subject to a fine not to exceed $200.00 for each offense and, upon the municipal court
finding any person guilty of maintaining a public nuisance as defined in section 30-276, the court shall order
removal and abatement of the public nuisance.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 11, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 30-278. - Procedures for abatement of public nuisance.
(a)

107/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The police department or code enforcement o cer, when desiring to remove and dispose of junked vehicles
from private property, public property or public rights-of-way, shall comply with the following procedures:
(1)
A written notice stating the nature of the public nuisance upon private property and that it must be removed
and abated within ten days, and further stating that any request for a hearing must be made before the
expiration of such ten-day period shall be mailed by certi ed mail, with a ve-day return receipt requested, to
the owner of the junked vehicle, any lienholder of record and the owner or the occupant of the private premises
upon which such public nuisance exists. If the notice is returned undelivered by the United States Post O ce,
o cial action to abate such nuisance shall be continued to a date not less earlier than the 11th day after the
date of such return.
(2)
The requirements of subsection (1) of this section shall also apply to the case of a public nuisance on public
property, and a similar notice shall be sent to the owner or the occupant of the public property and to the
owner or the occupant of the premises adjacent to the public property whereupon such public nuisance exists.
(3)
If the nuisance is not removed and abated and a hearing is not requested within the ten-day period provided, in
addition to any other procedure authorized by this article, a complaint may also be led in municipal court for
the violation of maintaining a public nuisance, provided, that such notice shall not be a requirement for any
such complaint being led in municipal court.
(4)
Once a vehicle has been removed under the provisions of this section, it shall not be reconstructed or made
operable.
(5)
Where the owner or occupant of the public or private premises upon which a public nuisance exists, or the
owner or occupant of the premises adjacent to the public right-of-way on which such nuisance vehicle is located
requests a public hearing within ten days after service of such notice to abate the nuisance, a public hearing
prior to the removal of the vehicle, or part thereof, as a public nuisance must be held before the building o cial.
Should the building o cial nd that such vehicle is a public nuisance as de ned in section 30-276, he shall enter
an order requiring the removal of the vehicle, or part thereof, from the public or private property or public rightof-way where it is situated, and such order shall include a description of the vehicle and the correct vehicle
identi cation number and license plate number of the vehicle, if available. Any aggrieved city o cer, owner or
lienholder may appeal any such decision of the building o cial to the city council.
(6)
The police department shall give notice to the state department of transportation within ve days after the date
of the removal of a junked vehicle by the police department, identifying the vehicle, or part thereof.
(b)
The procedures set out in this section shall not apply to a vehicle, or part thereof, which is completely enclosed
within a building in a lawful manner where it is not visible from the street or other public or private property;
which is stored or parked in a lawful manner on private property in connection with the business of a licensed
vehicle dealer or a junkyard; or an antique and special interest vehicle stored by a collector on his property,
108/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

provided, that the vehicle and outdoor storage areas are maintained in such a manner that they do not
constitute a health hazard and are screened from ordinary public view by means of a fence, rapidly growing
trees, shrubbery or other appropriate means.
(c)
The administration of the procedures of this section shall be carried out by regularly salaried, full-time
employees of the city, except that the removal of vehicles, or parts thereof, from property may be accomplished
by any other duly authorized person, including authorized wrecker service operators acting at the direction of
the city.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 12, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 683.074—683.076.
Sec. 30-279. - Disposal.
Junked vehicles, or parts thereof, may be disposed of by removal to a scrapyard, demolisher or any
suitable site operated by the city for processing as scrap or salvage.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 13, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.078.
Sec. 30-280. - Storage fees.
The police department shall be entitled to charge and collect reasonable storage fees for abandoned and
junked vehicles removed and stored pursuant to this article. Such fees shall be established by the city council
and, if the city council has not established such fees, the police department shall establish such fees. Such fees
may be charged beginning the day the vehicle is taken into custody for a period of up to ten days prior to the
date of the mailing of written notice pursuant to this article, and beginning on the day after written notice is
mailed, until the vehicle is reclaimed or disposed of pursuant to this article. If any such vehicle is stored with a
garage keeper, the police department shall not charge an additional fee for any day that the garage keeper
charges a fee.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-7, § 14, 10-22-2001)

Secs. 30-281—30-296. - Reserved.
ARTICLE VI. - PROPANE TANKS WITHIN THE CITY LIMITS
Sec. 30-297. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

109/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Inspector shall mean the code enforcement officer, the building inspector, or the person designated by
the city manager to enforce this ordinance.

LP-gas safety rules shall mean the rules adopted by the Railroad Commission in the Texas Administrative
Code, Title 16, Part 1, Chapter 9, including any National Fire Protection Association (NFPA) or other documents
adopted by reference, as amended from time to time.

Nuisance propane tank shall mean a propane tank that:
(1)
Has been determined by the inspector to be a danger to the public health, safety, or welfare, not maintained in
good working order or according to the LP-gas safety rules, or not utilized safely or according to the LP-gas
safety rules or manufacturer's instructions;
(2)
Notice has been given of said determination pursuant to section 30-301 herein, and
(3)
The propane tank has not been remedied pursuant to the terms of the notice within the time prescribed in
section 30-301.

Propane tank shall mean an external, above-ground tank that stores an alternate fuel source to natural
gas used primarily for in-home or commercial cooking or heating homes or businesses.
(Ord. No. 11-10-03-1, § 2, 11-10-2003)

Sec. 30-298. - Propane tanks prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for a person to use a propane tank or a nuisance propane tank within the city limits or
possess a propane tank or nuisance propane tank for the purpose of use within the city limits, except as
provided herein.
(Ord. No. 11-10-03-1, § 3, 11-10-2003)

Sec. 30-299. - Exceptions.
A person may use a propane tank within the city limits if:
(1)
The propane tank was in active use within the city limits as of the e ective date of the ordinance from which this
article is derived and remains on the property where the propane tank was located as of the e ective date of
the ordinance from which this article is derived; or
(2)
A waiver has been granted as provided in the ordinance from which this article is derived for use of the propane
tank on the property speci ed in the waiver, provided that the propane tank is located on the property speci ed
in the waiver and in active use.
110/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 11-10-03-1, § 4, 11-10-2003)

Sec. 30-300. - Registration; fee.
(a)
Any person possessing or using a propane tank within the city limits under one of the exceptions in section 30299 shall register the propane tank with the city.
(b)
A person who was actively using a propane tank within the city limits as of the e ective date of the ordinance
from which this article is derived shall register the propane tank within six-months of the e ective date of the
ordinance from which this article is derived and shall not be required to pay registration fee during the sixmonth period.
(c)
A person who has been granted a waiver shall register the propane tank within ten business days of the waiver
being granted.
(d)
A person who purchases a property upon which a propane tank is located and actively uses the propane tank
shall register as the new owner of the propane tank within one month of purchasing the property.
(e)
A person required to register under this section shall provide the city with the address where the propane tank
is located, the name of the person who owns or is leasing the propane tank, and the name, address, and
telephone number of the company, if any, leasing the propane tank.
(f)
The registration fee shall be $5.00. If a person does not register within the time prescribed herein, the person
shall incur a late fee of $5.00.
(Ord. No. 11-10-03-1, § 5, 11-10-2003)

Sec. 30-301. - Nuisance propane tanks.
(a)
A propane tank that constitutes a danger to the public health, safety, or welfare, is not being maintained in good
working order or according to the LP-gas safety rules, or is not being utilized safely or according to the LP-gas
safety rules or the manufacturer's instructions, is hereby declared to be a nuisance.
(b)
If the inspector determines that a propane tank is a nuisance, the inspector may issue written notice requiring
that the person who owns, possesses, keeps, or uses the propane tank meet certain remedial requirements to
correct the danger posed by the propane tank. The notice shall be given to the person who owns, possesses,
keeps, or uses the propane tank and to the company, if any, leasing the propane tank by personal service, by
posting notice at the property where the propane tank is located, or by certi ed mail, return receipt requested.
The person shall have seven days to comply with the notice. The person may le a written appeal to this notice
clearly stating the reasons for the appeal, to the city manager within seven days of service. The city manager or
111/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

designee shall conduct a hearing to determine the issues stated in the written appeal. At the hearing the formal
rules of evidence do not apply. The city manager or designee shall make his/her decision on the basis of
preponderance of the evidence presented. The decision of the city manager shall be rendered within 30 days
from receipt of the appeal. The decision of the city manager may be appealed to the city council within ten days
of the city manager's decision. A decision of the city manager that is not appealed within ten days is nal.
(c)
If the inspector determines that the propane tank constitutes an immediate danger to the public health, safety,
or welfare, the inspector shall take such action as is reasonable and necessary to protect the public health and
safety, including immediately declaring the propane tank to be a nuisance tank and/or seizing the propane tank.
(d)
If the person fails to comply with the notice or appeal the decision within seven days, the person shall deliver
the propane tank to the public works department located at 502 N. Norton, Dublin, Texas 76446. If the person
fails to deliver the propane tank to the public works department, the inspector may seize the propane tank.
(e)
Nothing herein precludes the city from seeking other remedies if a person fails to comply with the remedial
requirements stated or the decisions rendered in the appeal process.
(Ord. No. 11-10-03-1, § 6, 11-10-2003)

Sec. 30-302. - Waiver; fee.
(a)
A person who wishes to own, possess, keep, or use a propane tank within the city limits may apply for a waiver
from the city manager.
(b)
A waiver may be granted only if gas service is unavailable to the property for which the person is requesting the
waiver. For the purposes of this article, gas services shall be deemed unavailable if the nearest gas main is
located more than 200 feet from the nearest property line or boundary of the property for which the waiver is
being requested.
(c)
Any person who is denied a waiver may le a written appeal clearly stating the reasons for the appeal to the city
council within ten days of the denial of the waiver. The city council shall conduct a hearing to determine the
issues stated in the written appeal. At the hearing, the formal rules of evidence do not apply. The city council
shall make its decision on the basis of preponderance of the evidence presented. The decision of the city council
shall be rendered within 15 days from receipt of the appeal. A decision of the city manager that is not appealed
within ten days is nal.
(d)
A person who is granted a waiver from the city council shall maintain the propane tank in good working
condition or according to the LP-gas safety rules, utilize the propane tank safely or according to the LP-gas
safety rules of the manufacturer's instructions, and ensure that the propane tank is not a danger to the public
health, safety, or welfare.
112/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(e)
A nding by the inspector that the propane tank is a nuisance shall constitute revocation of the waiver upon
following the notice procedures of section 30-301.
(f)
The fee for applying for a waiver shall be $5.00.

A person granted a waiver shall be required to register the

propane tank pursuant to section 30-300.
(Ord. No. 11-10-03-1, § 7, 11-10-2003)

Sec. 30-303. - Location of propane tank.
Propane tanks installed after the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived shall not
be placed within 25 feet of any boundary or property line of the lot, tract or parcel of land on which the
propane tank is located. Propane tanks that are relocated within the boundaries of a lot, tract, or parcel of
land shall not be placed within 25 feet of any boundary or property line of the lot, tract or parcel of land on
which the propane tank is located.
(Ord. No. 11-10-03-1, § 8, 11-10-2003)

Secs. 30-304—30-325. - Reserved.
ARTICLE VII. - NOISE NUISANCES
Sec. 30-326. - Noises prohibited.
Any unreasonably loud, disturbing or unnecessary noise which causes material distress, discomfort or
injury to persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity thereof, or any noise of such character,
intensity and continued duration which substantially interferes with the comfortable enjoyment of private
homes by persons of ordinary sensibilities, is prohibited after the effective date hereof, and is hereby declared
to be a nuisance. The following acts, among others, are declared to come within the purview of this article and
to be nuisances within the meaning hereof, but said enumerations shall not be deemed to be exclusive, such
acts being as follows:
(1)
The playing of any radio, phonograph or other musical instrument in such manner or with such volume so as to
annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of persons of ordinary sensibilities in any dwelling, hotel or other
type residence;
(2)
The use of any stationary loudspeaker or ampli er to produce a noise or sound of such intensity that annoys or
disturbs persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity thereof; provided, however, that nothing
herein shall be constructed to prohibit the infrequent use of a loudspeaker or ampli er for periods of short
duration by a religious organization or association in the playing of music where the intensity of same does not
annoy or disturb such persons;
113/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(3)
The keeping of any animal or fowl which, by causing frequent or long continued noise, disturbs the comfort or
repose of persons of ordinary sensibilities in the immediate vicinity thereof;
(4)
The continued or frequent sounding of any horn or other signal device on any motor vehicle except as a danger
or warning signal, or the creation by means of any such signal device of any unreasonably loud or harsh noise
for any unnecessary purpose or unreasonable period of time;
(5)
The discharge into the open air of the exhaust of any xed and stationary steam engine, stationary internal
combustion engine, or motor vehicle or boat engine, except through an exhaust system in good working order
and in constant operation to prevent excessive or unusual noise; provided that this paragraph shall not apply to
trains and locomotives;
(6)
The creation of any excessive or unreasonable noise on any street or premises adjacent to any school, place of
religious worship, or other institution of learning while the same is in session, or any hospital, which
unreasonably interferes with the operation or use of any such institution;
(7)
The raucous shouting or crying of peddlers, hawkers or vendors which unreasonably disturbs the peace and
quiet of any neighborhood;
(8)
The use of any drum, loudspeaker or other instrument or device for the purpose of attracting attention by the
creation of noise to any performance, show or sale of merchandise;
(9)
The excavation or grading of land, or the erection, construction, demolition or alteration of any building or
structure, between the hours of 9:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m., within 600 feet of any occupied residential structure, or
that generates, produces or results in any noise or sound that may be heard at the property line of any occupied
residential structure; provided that this paragraph shall not apply to any such work, construction, repairs or
alterations that constitute an urgent necessity for the bene t and interest of the public safety, health or general
welfare, e.g. repairs and emergency installations by any public utility, or to any excavation, erection,
construction, demolition or alteration authorized by the city council to be undertaken between the hours of 9:00
p.m. and 7:00 a.m.; and
(10)
The playing of any stereo system located within a motor vehicle, the continued or frequent squealing of tires, or
the continued or frequent revving of any motor vehicle engine, in such a manner or with such volume as to
disturb persons within 50 feet of said motor vehicle or as to substantially impair the use or enjoyment of public
or private property.
(Ord. No. 1-12-04-3, § 2, 1-12-2004)

Sec. 30-327. - Exceptions.
114/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The prohibitions contained herein shall not apply to:
(1)
Any o cial of federal, state, or local government or to members of the armed forces of the United States or the
State of Texas engaged in the performance of o cial duties;
(2)
Persons engaged in the present performance or rendition of emergency medical services or services related to
the performance of lawful duties to protect the health, safety and welfare of the community;
(3)
Special events conducted in the municipal park or recreation areas pursuant to a special event permit
authorized by the director of parks and recreations;
(4)
Public parades duly permitted under this Code;
(5)
The use of outdoor sound ampli cation for outdoor public speeches, ceremonies, political assemblages or
paging purposes conducted at a xed outdoor location at least 100 feet from a residential district and the sound
was not audible beyond the property line of the premises on which it was located;
(6)
The use of sound ampli cation, intercom, or paging devices within the interior of a church, school, auditorium,
convention center, government building or similar public meeting place; or
(7)
Activities conducted on private or public school grounds including, but not limited to, school athletic and school
entertainment events which are approved, sponsored or sanctioned by the school, provided that the source of
the sound is on school property and does not create an unreasonable disturbance to any residential property
more than 500 feet from the school property.
(Ord. No. 1-12-04-3, § 3, 1-12-2004)

Sec. 30-328. - Person in control of property.
It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or fail to control the nuisances described in section 30-326(1)
or (2) that occur upon property which is under said person's control at the time the nuisance occurs.
(Ord. No. 1-12-04-3, § 4, 1-12-2004)

Sec. 30-329. - Enforcement.
(a)
This article may be enforced by a police o cer employed by the city or the city's code enforcement o cer.
(b)
If conduct that would otherwise violate this article consists of speech or other communication, of gathering with
others to hear or observe such speech or communication, or of gathering with others to picket or otherwise
115/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

express in a non-violent manner a position on social, economic, political or religious questions' the person or
persons must be ordered to move, disperse, or otherwise remedy the violation prior to arrest or citation.
(Ord. No. 1-12-04-3, § 5, 1-12-2004)

ARTICLE III. - BURNING; DAMAGED PROPERTY
Sec. 34-58. - Enforcement.
The civil and criminal provisions of this article shall be enforced by those persons or agencies designated
by municipal authority. It shall be a violation of this article to interfere with a fire fighter, police officer, or other
city employee in the performance of his or her duties. The code enforcement officer, a fire fighter, a police
officer or the fire chief is hereby authorized to enforce this article and the provisions of the Clean Air Act and
require any burn being conducted inconsistent with the Clean Air Act be extinguished immediately and may
issue a citation for the violations.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 7, 2-14-2000; Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 8, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 10, 7-12-2004)
116/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 34-59. - Inspection of premises.
Any premises emanating fire or smoke shall be subject to inspection by the fire chief, or authorized
representative, at any reasonable hour, or at any hour in cases of emergency.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 5, 2-14-2000; Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 6, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 7, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-60. - Duty to report re and smoke.
In the event of a fire or the discovery of a fire or unauthorized smoke discharge caused by a fire, burning
or smoldering combustibles on any property, the owner, occupant or person in control of the property or in
control of the fire from which the fire or smoke is emanating shall immediately report such condition to the
local fire department.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 2, 2-14-2000)

Sec. 34-61. - Burn ban and conditions.
During periods of time in which the County of Erath, Texas instates a burn ban for the county, the city
prohibits any burning, except as provided in 34-62(1) herein for the duration of the burn ban. Burning for
recreational or ceremonial purposes shall not be in violations of Title 30, Chapter 111, Texas Administrative
Codes as amended, including but not limited to the following:
(1)
Burning shall be commenced and conducted only when wind direction and other meteorological conditions are
such that smoke and other pollutants will not cause adverse a ects on any public road, landing strip, navigable
water, or o -site structure containing sensitive receptor(s).
(2)
If at any time the burning causes or may tend to cause smoke to blow onto or across a road or highway, it is the
responsibility of the person initiating the burn to post ag-persons on a ected roads.
(3)
Burning must be conducted to not create a nuisance, create smoke that is a nuisance or otherwise disturb the
peaceful use of the neighboring property owners shall be extinguished.
(4)
Burning shall be conducted in compliance with the following meteorological and timing considerations:
a.
The initiation of burning shall commence no earlier than one hour after sunrise. Burning shall be completed on
the same day not later than one hour before sunset, and shall be attended by a responsible party at all times
during the active burn phase when the re is progressing. In cases where residual res and/or smoldering
objects continue to emit smoke after this time, such areas shall be extinguished if the smoke from these areas
has the potential to create a nuisance or tra c hazard condition. In no case shall the extent of the burn area be
allowed to increase after this time.
117/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

b.
Burning shall not be commenced when surface wind speed is predicted to be less than six miles per hour (mph)
( ve knots) or greater than 23 mph (20 knots) during the burn period.
c.
Burning shall not be conducted during periods of actual or predicted persistent low-level atmospheric
temperature inversions.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 6, 2-14-2000; Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 7, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 8, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-62. - Open burning.
It shall be unlawful for any person within the city limits, in any way, to intentionally or carelessly burn or
cause to be burned any combustibles, including but not limited to trash, garbage, refuse, rubbish, litter, solid
waste, standing timber, lumber, building products, or together natural or synthetic materials on any street,
alley, lot or premises. Such prohibited fires shall include bonfires and fires used for ceremonial purposes not
in compliance herewith. The following exceptions to burning apply:
(1)
Burning may be conducted for the purposes of cooking or heating in a device designated for such a purpose by
the manufacturer.
(2)
A controlled burning for recreational purposes of grass, weeds, nonstanding timber, brush and/or leaves, per
section 34-63. No other trash, garbage, refuse, rubbish, litter or solid waste may be burned in a recreational
burn.
(3)
A controlled burning for ceremonial purposes of materials normally utilized in the type of ceremony performed
provided the materials is not prohibited per section 34-64 or state statute.
(4)
When approved by the code enforcement o cer, or his designee, or police supervisor on duty, or re chief or
assistant re chief, recreational res may be permitted in a manner approved by the code enforcement o cer.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 1, 2-14-2000; Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 1, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 1, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-63. - Permission required for recreational re.
A person wishing to burn any grass, weeds, nonstanding timber, leaves, brush or related material for
recreational purposes must receive verbal permission from the code enforcement officer, his designee, or
police supervisor on duty, or fire chief or assistant fire chief, prior to initiating the fire. No permission will be
given during burn bans enacted either by the city or county. Permission to burn is good only for the day that
permission is given. All permission to have a recreational fire shall not create responsibility or liability on the

118/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

part of the city to ensure the fire is properly contained, adequately supervised or otherwise safe. Individuals
initiating a recreational fire with permission of the city shall remain solely responsible for any civil or criminal
claims.
(Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 2, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 2, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-64. - Ceremonial res.
A person wishing to have a ceremonial fire shall be strictly responsible for compliance with state
regulations and the requirements of this article. No ceremonial fires shall consist of any electrical insulation,
treated lumber, plastics, non-wood construction/demolition materials, heavy oils, asphaltic materials,
potentially explosive materials, chemical wastes, and items containing natural or synthetic rubber. The code
enforcement officer, or his designee, or police supervisor on duty, or fire chief or assistant fire chief may
require a ceremonial fire be extinguished if the fire is, in the opinion of the officer, creating a health or safety
hazard or not in compliance with the Clean Air Act.
(Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 3, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-65. - Person responsible for recreational and ceremonial res.
A person 18 years of age or older shall be in attendance of any recreational or ceremonial fire with the
proper tools necessary to extinguish the fire. A recreational or ceremonial fire left unattended for any length
of time shall constitute a violation of this article.
(Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 3, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 4, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-66. - Smoke.
It shall be unlawful for any person within the city limits, in any way, to intentionally or carelessly burn or
cause to be burned any combustibles which causes noxious smoke or smoke of a significant quantity or
quality to be released so as to inhibit the use and enjoyment of neighboring properties and is hereby declared
a nuisance and is hereby prohibited.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 3, 2-14-2000; Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 4, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 5, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-67. - Repair and clean-up.
(a)
Any person, rm or corporation responsible for any re or unauthorized smoke discharge shall institute and
complete all actions necessary to remedy the e ects of such re and/or smoke, whether sudden or gradually, at
no cost to the city.
(b)
Whenever any building or other structure is partially burned, the owner thereof or the person in charge or
control thereof, within ten days after notice from the code enforcement o cer, shall remove from the premises
119/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

all refuse, debris, charred and partially burned lumber and material. If such building or other structure is burned
to the extent that it its rendered incapable of being repaired, the owner of the property upon which same is
located or the person in control thereof, within ten days after notice from the code enforcement o cer shall
remove from the premises all of the remaining portion of the building or structure.
(c)
All costs associated with such clean-up shall be borne by the owner, operator, person in control of the property
or other person responsible for the re or unauthorized discharge of smoke.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 4, 2-14-2000; Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 5, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 6, 7-12-2004)

Cross reference—Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14.
Sec. 34-68. - Penalty.
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article, or fail to comply therewith or any
requirements thereof, within the city limits shall be deemed guilty of an offense, and shall be liable for a fine
not less than $100.00 and not to exceed the sum of $2,000.00. Each day the violation exists shall constitute a
separate offense. Such penalty shall be in addition to all other remedies provided herein.
(Ord. No. 2-14-00-2, § 8, 2-14-2000; Ord. No. 11-12-02-2, § 9, 11-12-2002; Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 10, 7-12-2004)

Sec. 34-69. - Compliance with Clean Air Act.
All fires or burning outdoors shall be in strict compliance with the Clean Air Act, as amended. Verbal
authorization to burn shall not be an assurance that the burn is conducted in compliance with the Clean Air
Act. Permission shall be required for recreational fire to determine if a burn ban is in place. The obligation to
comply with the Clean Air Act shall rest solely upon the person conducting the burn.
(Ord. No. 7-12-04-2, § 9, 7-12-2004)

Secs. 34-70—34-100. - Reserved.
ARTICLE IV. - FIREWORKS
Sec. 34-101. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Fireworks means any contrivance made of paper, paste, board or other material, and containing
explosives of materials combined in various portions for the purpose of making a noise, creating an explosion
or producing a pyrotechnic display when ignited or lighted by hand or otherwise.
(Ord. No. 4-8-80-2, § II, 4-8-1980)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
120/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

State law reference—Fireworks defined, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.001.
Sec. 34-102. - Prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to have, keep, store, sell, offer for sale, give away, use, transport,
manufacture, discharge, ignite or in any manner aid another person in discharging or igniting any fireworks
within the corporate limits of the city.
(Ord. No. 4-8-80-2, § I, 4-8-1980)

Sec. 34-103. - Exceptions.
Nothing in this article shall be held to apply to the following:
(1)

Small arms ammunition. Possession or sale of normal stocks of small arms ammunition, unless such small arms
ammunition is being used or intended to be used for pyrotechnic display.
(2)

Photographic supplies. Possession, sale or use of normal amounts of ashlight composition by photographers
or dealers in photographic supplies.
(3)

Signaling devices. Possession or use of signaling devices for customary purposes by railroads, stopped motorists
or other persons requiring such signaling devices.
(Ord. No. 4-8-80-2, § V, 4-8-1980)

Sec. 34-104. - Possession constitutes prima facie evidence of intent to violate article.
Possession of any fireworks within the corporate limits of the city shall constitute prima facie evidence of
the intention to violate the provisions of this article and shall be deemed an offense.
(Ord. No. 4-8-80-2, § III, 4-8-1980)

Sec. 34-105. - Seizure and con scation of contraband without warrant; destruction.
Any fireworks found in the possession of any person which are being sold, offered for sale, used,
possessed, manufactured or stored in violation of this article are declared to be contraband. Such contraband
may be seized and confiscated by any police officer without a warrant and shall be destroyed under the
direction of the police chief or fire marshal.
(Ord. No. 4-8-80-2, § IV, 4-8-1980)

State law reference—Seizure of illegal fireworks, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.304.
Sec. 34-106. - Permit for public display.

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

A person who desires to conduct a commercial fireworks display must first apply for and obtain a permit
for such display from the city secretary. The city secretary shall not issue such a permit until the applicant has

(1)
Written authorization from the city council or a designated committee granting approval for such display, which
written authorization will certify that the city council believes that the applicant will take all necessary
precautions to protect the neighborhood from re, and that appropriate crowd and tra c control barriers will

Sec. 34-107. - Violation; penalty.
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and,
upon conviction, shall be fined in any amount not to exceed $200.00. Every violation of, and each day's failure
or refusal to comply with, the provisions of this article shall constitute a separate and distinct offense.
(Ord. No. 4-8-80-2, § VIII, 4-8-1980)

Chapter 38 - FLOODS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Secs. 38-1—38-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - FLOOD DAMAGE PREVENTION
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 38-31. - Statutory authorization.
The Legislature of the State of Texas has in V.T.C.A., Water Code § 16.311 et seq., delegated the
responsibility to local governmental units to adopt regulations designed to minimize flood losses. Therefore,
the city council of Dublin, Texas, does ordain the following regulations.
122/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. I, § A, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-32. - De nitions.
Unless specifically defined below, words or phrases used in this article shall be interpreted to give them
the meaning they have in common usage and to give this article its most reasonable application.

Appeal means a request for a review of the floodplain administrator's interpretation of any provision of
this article or a request for a variance.

Area of special flood hazard means the land in the floodplain within the city subject to a one percent or
greater chance of flooding in any given year. The area may be designated as zone A on the flood hazard
boundary map (FHBM). After detailed ratemaking has been completed in preparation for publication of the
flood insurance rate map (FIRM), zone A usually is refined into Zones A, AE, AH, AO, A1-99, VO, V1-30, VE or V.

Base flood means the flood having a one percent chance of being equaled or exceeded in any given year.
Critical feature means an integral and readily identifiable part of a flood protection system, without which
the flood protection provided by the entire system would be compromised.

Development means any manmade change to improved and unimproved real estate, including, but not
limited to, buildings or other structures, mining, dredging, filling, grading, paving, excavation or drilling
operations.

Elevated building means a nonbasement building:
(1)
Built, in the case of a building in zones A1-30, AE, A, A99, AO, AH, B, C, X and D, to have the top of the elevated
oor, or in the case of a building in zones V1-30, Ve or V, to have the bottom of the lowest horizontal structure
member of the elevated oor elevated above the ground level by means of pilings, columns (posts and piers) or
shear walls parallel to the oor of the water; and
(2)
Adequately anchored so as not to impair the structural integrity of the building during a ood of up to the
magnitude of the base ood.
In the case of zones A1-30, AE, A, A99, AO, AH, B, C, X and D, such term also includes a building
elevated by means of fill or solid foundation perimeter walls with openings sufficient to facilitate
the unimpeded movement of floodwaters. In the case of zones V1-30, VE or V, such term also
includes a building otherwise meeting the definition of "elevated building," even though the lower
area is enclosed by means of breakaway walls if the breakaway walls meet the standards of
Section 60.3(e)(5) of the National Flood Insurance Program regulations.

123/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Existing construction means, for the purposes of determining rates, structures for which the start of
construction commenced before the effective of the flood insurance rate map (FIRM) or before January 1, 1975
for FIRMs effective before that date. Such term may also be referred to as "existing structures."

Flood or flooding means a general and temporary condition of partial or complete inundation of normally
dry land areas from the:
(1)
Over ow of inland or tidal waters.
(2)
Unusual and rapid accumulation or runo of surface waters from any source.

Flood hazard boundary map (FHBM) means an official map of the city on which the Federal Emergency
Management Agency has delineated the boundaries of the flood, mudslide (i.e., mudflow) related erosion
areas having special hazards have been designated as zone A, M and/or E.

Flood protection system means the physical structural works for which funds have been authorized,
appropriated and expended, and which have been constructed specifically to modify flooding in order to
reduce the extent of the areas within the city subject to a special flood hazard and the extent of the depths of
associated flooding. Such a system typically includes hurricane tidal barriers, dams, reservoirs, levees or dikes.
Such specialized flood modifying works are those constructed in conformance with sound engineering
standards.

Floodplain or floodprone area means any land area susceptible to being inundated by water from any
source (see definition of Flood or flooding).

Levee means a manmade structure, usually an earthen embankment, designed and constructed in
accordance with sound engineering practices to contain, control or divert the flow of water so as to provide
protection from temporary flooding.

Levee system means a flood protection system which consists of a levee and associated structures, such
as closure and drainage devices, which are constructed and operated in accordance with sound engineering
practices.

Lowest floor means the lowest floor of the lowest enclosed area, including basement. An unfinished or
flood resistant enclosure, usable solely for parking of vehicles, building access or storage in an area other than
a basement area is not considered a building's lowest floor, provided, that such enclosure is not built so as to
render the structure in violation of the applicable nonelevation design requirement of Section 60.3 of the
National Flood Insurance Program regulations.

Manufactured home means a structure, transportable in one or more sections, which is built on a
permanent chassis and is designed for use with or without a permanent foundation when attached to the
required utilities. For floodplain management purposes, such term also includes park trailers, travel trailers
124/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

and other similar vehicles placed on a site for greater than 180 consecutive days. For insurance purposes, such
term does not include park trailers, travel trailers and other similar vehicles.
State law reference—Similar provisions, Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 5221f, § 3.

Mean sea level means, for purposes of the National Flood Insurance Program, the National Geodetic
Vertical Datum (NGVD) of 1929, or other datum, to which base flood elevations shown on the city's flood
insurance rate map are referenced.

New construction means, for floodplain management purposes, structures for which the start of
construction commenced on or after the effective date of the floodplain management regulation adopted by
the city.

Start of construction (for other than new construction or substantial improvements under the Coastal
Barrier Resources Act (Pub. L. 97-348)), includes substantial improvement and means the date the building
permit was issued, provided, the actual start of construction, repair, reconstruction, placement or other
improvement was within 180 days of the permit date. The actual start means either the first placement of
permanent construction of a structure on a site, such as the pouring of slabs or footings, the installation of
piles, the construction of columns, or any work beyond the stage of excavation; or the placement of a
manufactured home on a foundation. Permanent construction does not include land preparation, such as
clearing, grading and filling; nor does it include the installation of streets and/or walkways; nor does it include
excavation for a basement, footings, piers or foundations or the erection of temporary forms; nor does it
include the installation on the property of accessory buildings, such as garages or sheds not occupied as
dwelling units or not as part of the main structure.

Structure means a walled and roofed building, including a gas or liquid storage tank, that is principally
above the ground, as well as a manufactured home.

Substantial improvement means any repair, reconstruction or improvement of a structure, the cost of
which equals or exceeds 50 percent of the market value of the structure before the improvement or repair is
started, or if the structure has been damaged and is being restored, before the damage occurred. For the
purpose of this definition, "substantial improvement" is considered to occur when the first alteration of any
wall, ceiling, floor or other structural part of the building commences, whether or not such alteration affects
the external dimensions of the structure. Such term does not, however, include either:
(1)
Any project for improvement of a structure to comply with existing state or local health, sanitary or safety code
speci cations which are solely necessary to assure safe living conditions; or
(2)
Any alteration of a structure listed on the National Register of Historic Places or a state inventory of historic
places.

125/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Variance means a grant of relief to a person from the requirements of this article when specific
enforcement would result in unnecessary hardship. A variance, therefore, permits construction or
development in a manner otherwise prohibited by this article. (For full requirements see Section 60.6 of the
National Flood Insurance Program regulations.)

Violation means the failure of a structure or other development to be fully compliant with the city's
floodplain management regulations. A structure or other development without the elevation certificate, other
certifications or evidence of compliance required in Section 60.3(b)(5), (c)(4), (c)(10), (d)(3), (e)(2), (e)(4) or (e)(5)
of the National Flood Insurance Program regulations is presumed to be in violation until such time as that
documentation is provided.

Water surface elevation means the height, in relation to the National Geodetic Vertical Datum (NGVD) of
1929 (or other datum, where specified), of floods of various magnitudes and frequencies in the floodplains of
coastal or riverine areas.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 2, 8-11-1988)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 38-33. - Findings of fact.
(a)
The ood hazard areas of the city are subject to periodic inundation, which results in loss of life and property,
health and safety hazards, disruption of commerce and governmental services and extraordinary public
expenditures for ood protection and relief, all of which adversely a ect the public health, safety and general
welfare.
(b)
These ood losses are caused by the cumulative e ect of obstructions in oodplains which cause an increase in
ood heights and velocities, and by occupancy of ood hazards areas by uses vulnerable to oods and
hazardous to other lands because they are inadequately elevated, oodproofed or otherwise protected from
ood damage.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. I, § B, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-34. - Statement of purpose.
It is the purpose of this article to promote the public health, safety and general welfare and to minimize
public and private losses due to flood conditions in specific areas by provisions designed to:
(1)
Protect human life and health;
(2)
Minimize expenditure of public money for costly ood control projects;
(3)
126/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Minimize the need for rescue and relief e orts associated with ooding and generally undertaken at the
expense of the general public;
(4)
Minimize prolonged business interruptions;
(5)
Minimize damage to public facilities and utilities, such as water and gas mains, electric, telephone and sewer
lines, streets and bridges located in oodplains;
(6)
Help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the sound use and development of oodprone areas in such a
manner as to minimize future ood blight areas; and
(7)
Ensure that potential buyers are noti ed that property is in a ood area.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. I, § C, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-35. - Methods of reducing ood losses.
In order to accomplish its purposes, this article uses the following methods:
(1)
Restrict or prohibit uses which are dangerous to health, safety and property in times of ood, or which cause
excessive increases in ood heights or velocities;
(2)
Require that uses vulnerable to oods, including facilities which serve such uses, be protected against ood
damage at the time of initial construction;
(3)
Control the alteration of natural oodplains, stream channels and natural protective barriers, which are involved
in the accommodation of oodwaters;
(4)
Control lling, grading, dredging and other development which may increase ood damage; and
(5)
Prevent or regulate the construction of ood barriers which will unnaturally divert oodwaters or which may
increase ood hazards to other lands.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. I, § D, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-36. - Lands to which this article applies.
This article shall apply to all areas of special flood hazard within the jurisdiction of the city.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 3, § A, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-37. - Basis for establishing the areas of special ood hazard.
127/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The areas of special flood hazard identified by the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) in its
flood hazard boundary map (FHBM), Community No. 480219, dated August 8, 1978, and any revisions thereto,
are adopted by reference and declared to be a part of this article.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 3, § B, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-38. - Compliance.
No structure or land shall be located, altered or have its use changed without full compliance with the
terms of this article and other applicable regulations.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 3, § D, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-39. - Abrogation and greater restrictions.
This article is not intended to repeal, abrogate or impair any existing easements, covenants or deed
restrictions. However, where this article and other conflict or overlap, whichever imposes the more stringent
restrictions shall prevail.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 3, § E, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-40. - Interpretation.
In the interpretation and application of this article, all provisions shall be:
(1)
Considered as minimum requirements;
(2)
Liberally construed in favor of the city council; and
(3)
Deemed neither to limit nor repeal any other powers granted under state statutes.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 3, § F, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-41. - Warning and disclaimer of liability.
The degree of flood protection required by this article is considered reasonable for regulatory purposes
and is based on scientific and engineering considerations. On rare occasions greater floods can and will occur
and flood heights may be increased by manmade or natural causes. This article does not imply that land
outside the areas of special flood hazards or uses permitted within such areas will be free from flooding or
flood damages. This article shall not create liability on the part of the city, its officials or employees for any
flood damages that result from reliance on this article or any administrative decision lawfully made under this
article.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 3, § G, 8-11-1988)
128/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Secs. 38-42—38-60. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - ADMINISTRATION
Sec. 38-61. - Designation of oodplain administrator.
The city manager is appointed as the floodplain administrator to administer and implement the provisions
of this article and other appropriate sections of 44 CFR (National Flood Insurance Program regulations)
pertaining to floodplain management.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 4, § A, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-62. - Duties and responsibilities of the oodplain administrator.
The duties and responsibilities of the floodplain administrator shall include, but are not limited to, the
following:
(1)
Maintain and hold open for public inspection all records pertaining to the provisions of this article.
(2)
Review permit applications to determine whether proposed building sites will be reasonably safe from ooding.
(3)
Review, approve or deny all applications for development permits required by adoption of this article.
(4)
Review permits for proposed development to assure that all necessary permits have been obtained from the
federal, state or local governmental agencies (including Section 404 of the Federal Water Pollution Control Act
Amendments of 1972, 33 USC 1334) from which prior approval is required.
(5)
Make the necessary interpretation where interpretation is needed as to the exact location of the boundaries of
the areas of special ood hazards (for example, where there appears to be a con ict between a mapped
boundary and actual eld conditions).
(6)
In riverine situations, notify adjacent communities and the state coordinating agency, which is the Texas Natural
Resource Conservation Commission, prior to any alteration or relocation of a watercourse, and submit evidence
of such noti cation to the Federal Emergency Management Agency.
(7)
Assure that the ood-carrying capacity within the altered or relocated portion of any watercourse is maintained.
(8)
Obtain, review and reasonably utilize any base ood elevation data and oodway data available from a federal,
state or other source, in order to administer the provisions of division 4 of this article, when base ood elevation
data has not been provided in accordance with section 38-37.
129/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 4, § B, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-63. - Variances; appeals.
(a)
The appeal board, as established by the city, shall hear and render judgment on requests for variances from the
requirements of this article.
(b)
The appeal board shall hear and render judgment on an appeal only when it is alleged there is an error in any
requirement, decision or determination made by the oodplain administrator in the enforcement or
administration of this article.
(c)
Any person aggrieved by the decision of the appeal board may appeal such decision in the courts of competent
jurisdiction.
(d)
The oodplain administrator shall maintain a record of all actions involving an appeal, and shall report variances
to the Federal Emergency Management Agency, upon request.
(e)
Variances may be issued for the reconstruction, rehabilitation or restoration of structures listed on the National
Register of Historic Places or the state inventory of historic places without regard to the procedures set forth in
the remainder of this article.
(f)
Variances may be issued for new construction and substantial improvements to be erected on a lot of one-half
acre or less in size, contiguous to and surrounded by lots with existing structures constructed below the base
ood level, provided, the relevant factors in section 38-83 have been fully considered. As the lot size increases
beyond the one-half acre, the technical justi cation required for issuing the variance increases.
(g)
Upon consideration of the factors noted in subsection (f) of this section and the purposes of this article, the
appeal board may attach such conditions to the granting of variances as it deems necessary to further the
purposes of this article.
(h)
Variances shall not be issued without any designated oodway if any increase in ood levels during the base
ood discharge would result.
(i)
Prerequisites for granting variances shall be as follows:
(1)
Variances shall only be issued upon a determination that the variance is the minimum necessary, considering
the ood hazard, to a ord relief.
(2)
Variances shall only be issued upon:
130/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

a.
Showing a good and su cient cause;
b.
A determination that failure to grant the variance would result in exceptional hardship to the applicant; and
c.
A determination that the granting of a variance will not result in increased ood heights; additional threats to
public safety; extraordinary public expense; create nuisances; cause fraud on or victimization of the public; or
con ict with existing local laws or ordinances.
(3)
Any applicant to whom a variance is granted shall be given written notice that the structure will be permitted to
be built with a lowest oor elevation below the base ood elevation, and that the cost of ood insurance will be
commensurate with the increased risk resulting from the reduced lowest oor elevation.
(j)
Variances may be issued by the city for new construction and substantial improvements and for other
development necessary for the conduct of a functionally dependent use, provided, that the:
(1)
Criteria outlined in subsections (a)—(i) of this section are met; and
(2)
Structure or other development is protected by methods that minimize ood damages during the base ood
and create no additional threats to public safety.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 4, § D, 8-11-1988)

Secs. 38-64—38-80. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - PERMITS
Sec. 38-81. - Establishment of development permit.
A development permit shall be required to ensure conformance with the provisions of this article.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 3, § C, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-82. - Application.
An application for a development permit shall be presented to the floodplain administrator on forms
furnished by him, and may include, but not be limited to, plans, in duplicate, drawn to scale, showing the
location, dimensions and elevation of proposed landscape alterations, existing and proposed structures and
the location thereof in relation to areas of special flood hazard. Additionally, the following information shall be
required:
(1)

131/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Elevation, in relation to mean sea level, of the lowest oor, including basement, of all new and substantially
improved structures;
(2)
Elevation, in relation to mean sea level, to which any nonresidential structure shall be oodproofed;
(3)
A certi cate from a registered professional engineer or architect that the nonresidential oodproofed structure
shall meet the oodproo ng criteria of section 38-102(2);
(4)
Description of the extent to which any watercourse or natural drainage will be altered or relocated as a result of
proposed development;
(5)
Maintain a record of all such information in accordance with section 38-62(1).
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 4, § C(1), 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-83. - Approval; denial.
Approval or denial of a development permit by the floodplain administrator shall be based on all of the
provisions of this article and the following relevant factors:
(1)
The danger to life and property due to ooding or erosion damage;
(2)
The susceptibility of the proposed facility and its contents to ood damage and the e ect of such damage on
the individual owner;
(3)
The danger that materials may be swept onto other lands to the injury of others;
(4)
The compatibility of the proposed use with existing and anticipated development;
(5)
The safety of access to the property in times of ood for ordinary and emergency vehicles;
(6)
The costs of providing governmental services during and after ood conditions, including maintenance and
repair of streets and bridges, and public utilities and facilities, such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems;
(7)
The expected heights, velocity, duration, rate of rise and sediment transport of the oodwaters and the e ects
of wave action, if applicable, expected at the site;
(8)
The necessity to the facility of a waterfront location, where applicable;
(9)
The availability of alternative locations, not subject to ooding or erosion damage, for the proposed use;
132/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(10)
The relationship of the proposed use to the comprehensive plan for that area.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 4, § C(2), 8-11-1988)

Secs. 38-84—38-100. - Reserved.
DIVISION 4. - STANDARDS FOR FLOOD HAZARD REDUCTION
Sec. 38-101. - General standards.
The following standards are required in all areas of special flood hazards:
(1)
All new construction and substantial improvements shall be designed or modi ed and adequate anchored to
prevent otation, collapse or lateral movement of the structure resulting from hydrodynamic and hydrostatic
loads, including the e ects of buoyancy;
(2)
All new construction or substantial improvements shall be constructed by methods and practices that minimize
ood damage;
(3)
All new construction and substantial improvements shall be constructed with materials resistant to ood
damage;
(4)
All new construction or substantial improvements shall be constructed with electrical, heating, ventilation,
plumbing and air conditioning equipment and other service facilities that are designed and/or located so as to
prevent water from entering or accumulating within the components during conditions of ooding;
(5)
All new and replacement water supply systems shall be designed to minimize or eliminate in ltration of
oodwaters into the system;
(6)
New and replacement sanitary sewage systems shall be designed to minimize or eliminate in ltration of
oodwaters into the systems and discharge from the systems into oodwaters; and
(7)
On-site waste disposal systems shall be located to avoid impairment to them or contamination from them
during ooding.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 5, § A, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-102. - Speci c standards.
In all areas of special flood hazards where basic flood elevation data has been provided as set forth in
section 38-37, 38-62(8) or 38-103(c), the following standards are required:
133/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(1)

Residential construction. New construction and substantial improvement of any residential structure shall have
the lowest oor, including basement, elevated to or above the base ood elevation. A registered professional
engineer, architect or land surveyor shall submit a certi cation to the oodplain administrator that the standard
of this subsection as proposed in section 38-82(1) is satis ed.
(2)

Nonresidential construction. New construction and substantial improvement of any commercial, industrial or
other nonresidential structure shall either have the lowest oor, including basement, elevated to or above the
base ood level or, together with attendant utility and sanitary facilities, be designed so that, below the base
ood level, the structure is watertight with walls substantially impermeable to the passage of water and with
structural components having the capability of resisting hydrostatic and hydrodynamic loads and the e ects of
buoyancy. A registered professional engineer or architect shall develop and/or review structural design,
speci cations and plans for the construction, and shall certify that the design and methods of construction are
in accordance with accepted standards of practice as outlined in this subsection. A record of such certi cation,
which includes the speci c elevation, in relation to mean sea level, to which such structures are oodproofed
shall be maintained by the oodplain administrator.
(3)

Manufactured homes.
a.
Manufactured homes placed within zone A shall be required to be installed using methods and practices which
minimize ood damage. For the purpose of such requirement, manufactured homes must be elevated and
anchored to resist otation, collapse or lateral movement. Methods of anchoring may include, but are not
limited to, use of the over-the-top or frame ties to ground anchors. Such requirement is in addition to applicable
state and local anchoring requirements for resisting wind forces.
b.
All manufactured homes shall be in compliance with section 38-102(1).
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 5, § B, 8-11-1988)

Sec. 38-103. - Standards for subdivision proposals.
(a)
All subdivision proposals, including manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall be consistent with
sections 38-33, 38-34 and 38-35.
(b)
All proposals for the development of subdivisions, including manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall
meet development permit required set forth in section 38-81, section 38-82 and division 4 of this article.
(c)
Base ood elevation data shall be generated for subdivision proposals and other proposed development,
including manufactured home parks and subdivisions, which is greater than 50 lots or ve acres, whichever is
lesser, if not otherwise provided pursuant to section 38-37 or 38-62(8).
134/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(d)
All subdivision proposals, including manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall have adequate drainage
provided to reduce exposure to ood hazards.
(e)
All subdivision proposals, including manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall have public utilities and
facilities, such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems, located and constructed to minimize or eliminate
ood damage.
(Ord. No. 88-08-138, art. 5, § C, 8-11-1988)

Chapter 42 - HUMAN RELATIONS

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
