DIVISION 2. - FAIR HOUSING
Subdivision I. - In General
Sec. 42-51. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Discriminatory housing practice means an act that is unlawful under sections 42-91—41-93.
Dwelling means any building or structure, or portion thereof, which is occupied as a residence by one or
more families, or any vacant land which is offered for sale or lease for the construction of any such building or
structure, or portion thereof.

Family includes a single individual.
Person includes one or more individuals, corporations, partnerships, associations, labor organizations,
legal representatives, mutual companies, joint stock companies, trusts, unincorporated organizations,
trustees, fiduciaries and any other organization or entity of whatever character.

135/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

To rent includes to lease, sublease, let and otherwise to grant for a consideration the right to occupy a
premises not owned by the occupant.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 1, 9-11-1979)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 42-52. - Unlawful intimidation.
It shall be unlawful for any person to harass, threaten, harm, damage or otherwise penalize any individual,
group or business because that individual, group or business has complied with the provisions of this division.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 10, 9-11-1979)

Sec. 42-53. - Violation; penalty.
Any person who violates any provision of this division shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be fined a sum not to exceed $200.00 for each violation. Each day a violation continues after
the passage of 30 days from the date of the filing of the initial complaint with the fair housing administrator
shall constitute a separate and distinct offense.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 12, 9-11-1979)

Secs. 42-54—42-70. - Reserved.
Subdivision II. - Administration and Enforcement
Sec. 42-71. - Fair housing administrator.
The mayor shall appoint and the city council shall confirm a fair housing administrator (hereinafter
referred to as the "administrator"), who shall have the responsibility for implementing this division. The
administrator may delegate his authority to investigate and conciliate complaints to other city employees
under his direction.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 6, 9-11-1979)

Cross reference—Officers and employees, § 2-81 et seq.
Sec. 42-72. - Cooperation with the U.S. Secretary of Housing and Urban Development and the U.S. Attorney General.
The fair housing administrator and city attorney are authorized to cooperate with the U.S. Secretary of
Housing and Urban Development and the U.S. Attorney General pursuant to the provisions of Title VIII, Fair
Housing Act of 1968, PL 90-284, and may render such service to the secretary as they shall deem appropriate
to further the policies of this division.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 11, 9-11-1979)
136/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 42-73. - Complaints.
(a)
Only the person who claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing practice or who believes he will be
irrevocably injured by a discriminatory housing practice that has occurred may le a complaint with the fair
housing administrator. Such complaints shall be in writing and shall identify the person alleged to have
committed, or alleged to be committing, a discriminatory housing practice and shall state the facts upon which
the allegations of a discriminatory housing practice are based.
(b)
If, at any time the fair housing administrator shall receive or discover credible evidence and shall have probable
cause to believe that any person has committed, or are committing, a discriminatory housing practice as to
which no complaint has been led, the fair housing administrator may prepare and le a complaint upon his
own motion and in his own name and such complaint shall thereafter be treated in the same manner as a
complaint led by a person aggrieved.
(c)
The fair housing administrator shall receive and accept noti cation and referral complaints from the U.S.
Attorney General and the U.S. Secretary of Housing and Urban Development pursuant to the provisions of Title
VIII, Fair Housing Act of 1968, PL 90-284, and shall treat such complaints in the same manner as complaints led
pursuant to subsection (a) of this section.
(d)
All complaints shall be led within 60 days following the occurrence of an alleged discriminatory housing
practice. Upon the ling or referral of any complaint, the fair housing administrator shall provide notice of the
complaint by furnishing a copy of such complaint to the person named in the complaint who allegedly
committed, or were threatening to commit, an alleged discriminatory housing practice. The accused may le an
answer to the complaint within 15 days of receipt of the written complaint.
(e)
All complaints and answers shall be subscribed and sworn to before an o cer authorized to administer oaths.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 7, 9-11-1979)

Sec. 42-74. - Investigation; prosecution.
(a)
Upon the ling or referral of a complaint as provided in section 42-73, the fair housing administrator shall cause
a prompt and full investigation of the matter stated in the complaint to be made.
(b)
During or after the investigation, but subsequent to the mailing of the notice of complaint, the fair housing
administrator shall, if it appears that a discriminatory housing practice has occurred or is threatening to occur,
attempt by informal endeavors to e ect conciliation.
(c)
Upon completion of the investigation and informal endeavors at conciliation by the fair housing administrator,
but within 30 days of the ling of the complaint with the fair housing administrator, if the e orts of the fair
137/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

housing administrator to secure voluntary compliance have been unsuccessful, and if the fair housing
administrator has made a determination that a discriminatory housing practice has in fact occurred, the fair
housing administrator shall recommend to the city attorney that such violation be prosecuted in the municipal
court of the city. If the city attorney determines to prosecute, he shall institute a complaint and prosecute such
complaint to conclusion within 30 days after such determination, or as soon thereafter as practicable.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 8, 9-11-1979)

Sec. 42-75. - Cumulative legal e ect.
This division is cumulative in its legal effect and is not in lieu of any and all other legal remedies which the
person aggrieved may pursue.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 9, 9-11-1979)

Secs. 42-76—42-90. - Reserved.
Subdivision III. - Regulations
Sec. 42-91. - Discrimination prohibited in the sale or rental of housing.
It shall be unlawful for any person to:
(1)
Refuse to sell or rent, after the making of a bona de o er, or refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental of, or
otherwise make unavailable or deny, a dwelling to any person because of race, color, sex, religion or national
origin;
(2)
Discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling, or in the
provision of services or facilities in connection with the sale or rental of a dwelling, because of race, color, sex,
religion or national origin;
(3)
Make, print or publish, or cause to be made, printed or published, any notice, statement or advertisement
regarding the sale or rental of a dwelling that indicates any preference based on race, color, sex, religion or
national origin, or an intention to make any such preference, limitation or discrimination;
(4)
Represent to any person, because of race, color, sex, religion or national origin, that any dwelling is not available
for inspection, sale or rental when such dwelling is in fact so available;
(5)
For pro t or with the hope or expectation of pro t, to induce, or attempt to induce, any person to sell or rent
any dwelling by representations regarding the entry or prospective entry into the neighborhood of a person of a
particular race, color, sex, religion or national origin;
(6)
138/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

For pro t or with the hope or expectation of pro t, to in uence, or attempt to in uence, by any words, acts or
failure to act, any seller, purchaser, landlord or tenant of a dwelling so as to promote the maintenance of racially
segregated housing or so as to retard, obstruct or discourage racially integrated housing.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 2, 9-11-1979)

Sec. 42-92. - Discrimination prohibited in the nancing of housing.
It shall be unlawful for any bank, building and loan association, insurance company or other corporation,
association, firm or enterprise whose business consists, in whole or in part, of the making of commercial or
residential real estate loans, to deny a loan or other financial assistance to a person applying therefor for the
purpose of purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing or maintaining a dwelling because of the race, color,
sex, religion or national origin of such person or any person associated with him in connection with such loan
or other financial assistance.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 3, 9-11-1979)

Sec. 42-93. - Discrimination prohibited in the provision of brokerage services.
It shall be unlawful for any person to deny access to, or membership or participation in, any multiple
listing service, real estate brokers' organization or other service, organization or facility relating to the business
of selling or renting dwellings, due to race, color, sex, religion or national origin.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 4, 9-11-1979)

Sec. 42-94. - Exemptions and exclusions.
(a)
The following transactions shall be exempt from the application of sections 42-91—42-93:
(1)
The rental of units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied, or intended to be occupied, by no more than
four families living independently of each other if the owner actually maintains and occupies one of such units
as his residence;
(2)
The rental of a single room in a dwelling containing living quarters occupied, or intended to be occupied, by no
more than one family if the person o ering such room for rental actually maintains and occupies the remainder
of such dwelling as his residence and not more than four such rooms are o ered for rent.
(3)
The sale or rental of any single house by a private individual who owns such house, provided, that the:
a.
Sale or rental is made without the use of the sales or rental services of any real estate broker, agent or
salesman, or of such services of any person in the business of selling or renting dwellings.
b.
139/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sale is made without the publication, posting or mailing of any advertisement or written notice in violation of
section 42-91(3).
(b)
Nothing in this division shall prohibit a religious organization, association or society or any nonpro t institution
or organization operated, supervised or controlled by or in conjunction with a religious association or society
from limiting the sale, rental or occupancy of dwellings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial
purpose to persons of the same religion, or from giving preference to such persons, unless membership in such
religion is restricted on account of race, color, sex or national origin.
(c)
Nothing in this division shall prohibit a bona de private club, not in fact open to the public, which, as an
incident to its primary purpose, provides lodging, which it owns or operates for other than a commercial
purpose, from limiting the rental or occupancy of such lodgings to its members or from giving preference to its
members.
(d)
Nothing in this division shall bar any person from owning and operating a housing accommodation in which
rooms are leased, subleased or rented only to persons of the same sex, when such housing accommodation
contains common lavatory, kitchen or similar facilities available for the use of all persons occupying such
housing accommodation.
(Ord. No. 9-11-79-1, § 5, 9-11-1979)

Chapter 46 - LAW ENFORCEMENT
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Secs. 46-1—46-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - POLICE RESERVE FORCE
Sec. 46-31. - Established.
A police reserve force is established in the city.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-5, § 2, 10-8-2001)

State law reference—Authority of the city council to establish a police reserve force, V.T.C.A., Local
Government Code §§ 141.007, 341.012.
Sec. 46-32. - Quali cations, training.
At the time of appointment, each appointed reserve police officer shall be licensed by the Texas
Commission on Law Enforcement Standards and Education (TCLEOSE) as a permanent peace
officer/permanent reserve or as a provisional police officer/provisional reserve. Each appointed reserve officer
140/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

shall have satisfied all appointment conditions established by the chief of police, which may include, but are
not limited to, background and criminal history investigations; written and oral examinations; physical fitness
and agility examinations; psychological examinations; drug screening; and polygraph examination. It shall be
the individual responsibility of each reserve officer to maintain their standing as a licensed police officer or
reserve officer and to receive such training as is required to maintain such license. The reserve police officers
shall further maintain and complete not less than the continuing training as is required by the chief of police.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-5, § 3, 10-8-2001)

Sec. 46-33. - Number of authorized o cers.
The number of authorized reserve police officers is ten.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-5, § 4, 10-8-2001)

Sec. 46-34. - Supplementary to regular police force.
Reserve police officers may act only in a supplementary capacity to the regular police force and may not
assume full-time duties of regular police officers without complying with the department selection
requirements of full-time paid regular peace officers of the police department.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-5, § 7, 10-8-2001)

Sec. 46-35. - Compensation.
Reserve police officers will not receive direct monetary compensation from the city.
(Ord. No. 5-13-80-1, § 4, 5-13-1980)

Sec. 46-36. - Preparation and enforcement of policies, procedures, etc.
The chief of police will prepare and enforce department policies, procedures, regulation special orders
and requirements applicable to the qualifications, appointment, service, training, conduct, discipline and
dismissal of reserve police officers pursuant to this article.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-5, § 8, 10-8-2001)

Sec. 46-37. - Appointment of members; approval of city council required to carry weapon, act as o cer.
(a)
Subject to the rati cation and approval by the city council, the chief of police shall appoint the members of the
police reserve force, and the police reserve force shall serve at the discretion of the chief of police.
(b)
The appointment of members of the police reserve force shall not be in e ect, and a reserve police o cer shall
not carry a weapon or otherwise act as a peace o cer, until individual appointment is approved by majority
vote of the city council.
141/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 10-8-01-5, § 5, 10-8-2001)

Sec. 46-38. - Calling into service.
The chief of police may call the reserve police officers into service or schedule such reserve police officers
at any time he considers it necessary to have additional officers to preserve the peace and enforce the law.
Members of the reserve police force serve as peace officers during the actual discharge of official duties.
(Ord. No. 10-8-01-5, § 6, 10-8-2001)

Secs. 46-39—46-70. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - RACIAL PROFILING POLICY
Sec. 46-71. - Approval and adoption.
The city racial profiling policy (the "policy"), on file in the office of the city secretary and incorporated into
this section as if set forth fully in this section, is approved and adopted. The policy shall be and remain in full
force and effect until such time as such policy is repealed, modified or amended by resolution or ordinance of
the city council. Where the policy conflicts with the Code of Criminal Procedure or a specific department policy,
the more restrictive shall govern.
(Ord. No. 12-10-01-1, § 2, 12-10-2001)

Sec. 46-72. - City council approval.
The racial profiling policies and procedures of the city police department, and all revisions, modifications
and amendments to such policies and procedures, shall be approved by the city council, in its discretion, by
resolution, and no such policies, procedures, revisions, modifications or amendments shall be in effect, except
as approved by the city council acting by resolution. Such policies, procedures, rules and regulations as are
approved by resolution of the city council shall be and remain in effect until such policies, procedures, rules
and regulations are repealed, modified or amended by resolution, and all, or any part of, such policies,
procedures, rules, regulations, revisions, modifications and amendments may be repealed, deleted, modified
or amended, at any time, by the city council acting in its discretion.
(Ord. No. 12-10-01-1, § 4, 12-10-2001)

Sec. 46-73. - Orders of chief of police.
The chief of police is responsible for the day-to-day operation of the police department and he must
operate and manage the police department in a manner consistent with the policies and procedures of the
city, the laws of the state and federal government, the Code of Criminal Procedure and the public safety needs
of the citizens. The chief of police may from time to time issue orders or specific policy statements for the
police department that are consistent with the policy adopted in this article for the police department and that
142/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

are consistent with the personnel policies of the city as needed to guide officers and departmental practices
not specifically addressed in the policy or that vary the policies as needed to create policies that will comply
with changes in the law. The chief of police shall cause such policies and procedures, and any proposed
modifications or amendments to such policies and procedures, to be drafted, prepared and recommended to
the city council for review and action, as necessary, to serve the best interests of the city and the police
department employees and citizens.
(Ord. No. 12-10-01-1, § 3, 12-10-2001)

Sec. 46-74. - Interpretation and construction.
The policies and procedures, rules and regulations of the police department shall be interpreted and
construed consistent with the Code of Criminal Procedure. The general policies and procedures of the police
department shall not be interpreted or construed as creating third party rights. The policies and procedures,
rules and regulations of the police department shall be interpreted as a general guideline to be used by the
police department to promote professionalism and organizational development. Nothing in the policy, or its
amendments, shall be interpreted or construed as an obligation, mandate, requirement or agreement of the
city or the police department to function or operate in the manner or methods described in such policy.
(Ord. No. 12-10-01-1, § 6, 12-10-2001)

Sec. 46-75. - Governmental immunity.
Nothing in the policy adopted in this article shall be deemed to waive, modify or amend any legal defense
available at law or in equity to either the city, the police department or its employees, nor to create any legal
rights or claims on behalf of any third party. Neither the city, the police department nor its employees waives,
modifies or alters, to any extent whatsoever, the availability of the defense of governmental immunity under
the laws of the state.
(Ord. No. 12-10-01-1, § 7, 12-10-2001)

Sec. 46-76. - Audio and video equipment.
Immediately upon enactment of the policy adopted in this article, the chief of police shall commence
examination of the feasibility of installing video camera equipment and transmitter-activated equipment in
any city motor vehicle, now owned or acquired after passage of the policy adopted in this article, regularly
used to make traffic stops, and transmitter-activated equipment in each city motorcycle now owned or
acquired after the passage of the policy adopted in this article, regularly used to make traffic stops, and shall
report to the city council any such vehicles which are not equipped with adequate equipment. Such report
shall include funding options available to the city, including any funding available through the department of
public safety. If the findings of such examination supports the installation of additional equipment in any
motor vehicle required to be equipped, but not already equipped, the chief of police is authorized and
directed to apply for funding to secure the additional equipment, and if funds are available, the chief of police
143/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

shall take such actions, as necessary, to ensure installation of such additional equipment as expeditiously as
feasible. The chief of police is authorized and directed to certify to the department of public safety any need
for additional equipment for which funds are not available. Upon receipt of either sufficient funds or video
and audio equipment, the chief of police shall direct such actions, as necessary, to expeditiously install and
begin the operation of video and transmitter-activated equipment in each motor vehicle regularly used to
make traffic stops, and shall direct such actions, as necessary, to expeditiously install and begin the operation
of transmitter-activated equipment on each motorcycle regularly used to make traffic stops. The chief of police
is authorized and directed to certify to the department of public safety that such equipment has been installed
and is being used to record each traffic and pedestrian stop made by a peace officer employed by the city that
is capable of being recorded by video and/or audio equipment, as appropriate.
(Ord. No. 12-10-01-1, § 5, 12-10-2001)

Chapter 50 - MANUFACTURED HOMES AND TRAILERS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Secs. 50-1—50-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - MOBILE HOME PARKS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 50-31. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Building official means a person authorized by the city to perform the duties described in this article.
City mobile home committee means the code and ordinance committee as appointed by the city council to
perform the duties and functions described in this article.

Licensee means a person to whom a license for construction and/or operation and maintenance of a
mobile home park has been issued.

Mobile home means a structure that was constructed before June 15, 1976, transportable in one or more
sections, which, in the traveling mode, is eight body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length or,
when erected on-site, is 320 or more square feet, and which is built on a permanent chassis and designed to
be used as a dwelling with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the required utilities, and
includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical systems.

144/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Mobile home space means the ground area allocated for occupancy by one mobile home in the layout of a
mobile home park.

Non-park location means a mobile home placed in the city at a site other than a mobile home park.
Off-street parking space means an unobstructed area with minimum dimensions of nine feet by 18 feet,
allocated for parking a vehicle in the layout of a mobile home park.

Park means a plot of ground upon which two or more mobile homes, occupied as dwellings, are located.
Permit means when a non-park location use permit has been issued for the placement and use of a
mobile home within the city limits outside of a mobile home park.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § A, 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
State law reference—Similar definitions, Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 5221f, § 3.
Sec. 50-32. - Placement of mobile homes in non-park locations.
(a)

Permit required. No person shall locate a mobile home outside a mobile home park for use as a dwelling within
the city limits without obtaining a non-park location use permit as provided in this section.
(b)

Permit application. The application for a permit shall be reviewed by the building o cial and city re marshal to
determine compliance with the following requirements:
(1)
Design and construction of the mobile home shall conform with provisions of the United States Department of
Housing and Urban Development standards for mobile homes of 6-15-76, as may be amended or superseded
on the date of installation.
(2)
Conformity with all applicable provisions of section 50-37 or 50-34.
(3)
Conformity with section 50-36.
(c)

Permit issuance; fee. Upon approval of the building o cial and re marshal and payment of a permit fee of
$10.00, the city secretary shall issue a permit which shall be valid for as long as the mobile home shall be in
conformity with this article. No city utility service shall be provided to a mobile home in the non-park location
which does not have a valid permit.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § D, 10-22-2001)

State law reference—Authority to restrict mobile homes to a park, Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 5221f, § 4A.

145/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 50-33. - Regulation of placement of mobile homes; variances.
(a)
No mobile home shall be placed within eight feet from any side boundary line or 30 feet from any front or rear
boundary line of a lot located in the city, nor shall any mobile home be placed within ten feet from any existing
building.
(b)
A variance from the regulations set forth in subsection (a) of this section may be approved if a request is made
by such person to the city mobile home committee.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § L, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-34. - Subdivision of land within the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the city.
No person shall subdivide land within the extraterritorial jurisdiction of the city for the purpose of creating
a mobile home park until a plat of the park has been approved by the city mobile home committee. Such plat
shall be submitted to the city mobile home committee for approval, and shall be accompanied by the
information outlined in section 50-32(b)(1) and (2) and shall conform to the design requirements of division 3
of this article.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § K, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-35. - Mobile home tie-down, anchorage and foundation requirements.
(a)
Every person owning a mobile home located within the city shall provide adequate tie-downs to secure the
mobile home against any movement or overturning. Such tie-downs shall be equal to those required by the
Texas Department of License, Mobile Home Division, Standards and Requirements 063.55, as may be amended
or superceded on the date of installation of such mobile home.
(b)
All mobile homes within the city shall meet the tie-down requirements of this section and the skirting
requirements of section 50-98 within one month from the e ective date of the ordinance from which this
section is derived.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § C, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-36. - Age of mobile homes.
All mobile homes moved in or relocated within the city limits shall be ten years old or less from the date of
manufacture of the mobile home.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § B, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-37. - Violation; penalty.

146/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Any person who violates this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall
be punished as provided for in section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. II, 10-22-2001)

Secs. 50-38—50-60. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE
Sec. 50-61. - Required; application.
(a)
It shall be unlawful for any person to construct, maintain or operate a mobile home park within the city limits
without a license. No city utility service shall be provided to a park until the permit or license provided for in this
division shall have been issued. Written application for a license, signed by the applicant, shall be submitted to
the city secretary. Such application shall state the applicant's address and the legal description of the land
wherein construction of a park is proposed, and shall be accompanied by the following exhibits:
(1)
A plat showing the location and con guration of the proposed park, including the layout of the mobile home
spaces, streets, parking spaces, walkways and utility service lines;
(2)
Plans and speci cations for all buildings and service facilities.
(b)
Every person operating a park within the city limits on the e ective date of the ordinance from which this
section is derived (10-22-2001) shall submit a written application for a license within 60 days after such date,
accompanied by the exhibits as described in subsections (a)(1) and (2) of this section. The building o cial will
review each license application and make recommendations on such application to the city mobile home
committee. In considering the disposal of any such application, the city mobile home committee may take into
account the character of the neighborhood, with respect to present and anticipated land use and development,
wherein the park is proposed to be located or is in operation. The city will issue such license upon approval of
an application by the city mobile home committee.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § E, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-62. - Posting.
A mobile home park certificate shall at all times be conspicuously posted by the licensee in the office or on
the premises of the park.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § G, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-63. - Renewal or transfer.

147/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(a)
For validity, a mobile home park license shall be renewed each year. Renewal of such license will be e ected by
the city secretary upon payment by the licensee of an annual fee of $25.00.
(b)
To transfer a license or permit, a written request for such transfer shall be submitted to the city secretary. Upon
inspection of the park by the building o cial, and with his approval, the city secretary will issue a license
transfer, and the fee for such transfer shall be $25.00.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § F, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-64. - Revocation.
A mobile home park license may be revoked when the licensee is found guilty by a court of competent
jurisdiction of violating any provision of this article, and after holding a public hearing before the city mobile
home committee according to written notice given to the licensee at least ten days prior to such hearing. A
majority of the city mobile home committee shall vote to revoke such license.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § H, 10-22-2001)

Secs. 50-65—50-90. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - DESIGN AND CONSTRUCTION REQUIREMENTS OF PARKS
Sec. 50-91. - Size, spacing and clearance.
The minimum size of a mobile home park shall be one-half acre. A mobile home space shall be at least
three times larger than the mobile home to be placed on such space, but not less than 3,000 square feet in
area. Such spaces shall be clearly delineated on the ground in accordance with the layout plan submitted with
the license application. A minimum clearance of 30 feet between mobile homes shall be provided, and ten feet
between any mobile home and a park boundary that does not abut upon a public street. When a park
boundary abuts upon a public street, no mobile home shall be closer than 25 feet to such public street.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(1), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-92. - O -street parking spaces.
At least two parking spaces shall be provided for each mobile home space and one additional parking
space for each four mobile home spaces within a mobile home park. Construction shall be as prescribed in
section 50-93.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(2), 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Stopping, standing and parking of vehicles, § 90-31 et seq.
Sec. 50-93. - Access to and from public streets.
148/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Every mobile home park shall have direct access from a public street and each mobile home space shall
have direct access to a public street or internal street. Where an internal street provides access, the internal
street shall be dedicated to the public as an emergency access easement to allow for the rapid and safe
movement of vehicles used for the purpose of providing emergency health or public safety. Each emergency
access easement shall have a clear unobstructed width of at least 15 feet, and shall connect to a dedicated
public street at each end, or shall have a turnaround with a minimum diameter of 60 feet. Within parks with 20
or more mobile home spaces, the internal street shall be named, and mobile home spaces numbered to
conform with block numbers on adjacent public streets. Street signs shall be of a color and size contrasting
with street signs on public streets so that there is no confusion regarding which streets are private and which
are public. Such signs and numbers shall be of a standard size and placement to facilitate location by
emergency vehicles. Such internal streets shall be of all-weather construction. All parks shall provide walkways
of a minimum of 30 inches in width for pedestrian access to each mobile home from an internal or public
street.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(3), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-94. - Electrical service.
An electrical service connection shall be provided for each mobile home space within a mobile home park.
Design and construction of the park electrical system shall conform with the city's electrical code as may be
amended.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(4), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-95. - Water supply.
An adequate supply of potable water shall be supplied to each mobile home space within a mobile home
park through piping which conforms with the city's plumbing code as may be amended and, at least four
inches above the ground, an outdoor hydrant shall be installed at each mobile home space.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(5), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-96. - Sewage disposal.
Each mobile home space within a mobile home park shall be provided with a sewer riser pipe of a
minimum of four inches in diameter. The individual sewer connections and all other elements in the park
sewer system shall conform with the city's plumbing code as may be amended. Sewage disposal shall be into
the city's sewer system, unless an exception is granted by the city mobile home committee, permitting
disposal by other means that conform in design and construction with all applicable codes and regulations of
the city as may be amended.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § ((6), 10-22-2001)

149/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 50-97. - Drainage.
A mobile home park shall be located and graded so as to drain away all surface water in a safe and
efficient manner. Accumulations of stagnant water will not be permitted.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(7), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-98. - Fire protection.
Mobile home park service buildings, including, but not limited to, offices, laundry facilities and repair
shops, shall be provided with emergency fire extinguishing apparatus of such types and sizes as may be
prescribed by the city fire marshal. Fire resistant skirting, with the necessary vents, screens and/or openings,
shall be installed on each mobile home within ten days after the placement of such mobile home. To ensure
compliance by the mobile home owner with such requirement, the licensee shall make such compliance, and
confirmation thereof by the city fire marshal, a condition in the agreement for rental of a mobile home space.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(8), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-99. - Fuel supply.
Mobile home park gas piping systems shall be installed underground in accordance with the applicable
codes and regulations as may be amended. Gas outlets shall be capped when the mobile home spaces they
serve are vacant. Natural gas shall be supplied, except a liquefied petroleum gas system may be installed if the
nearest available natural gas supply is more than 1,000 feet from the park. Liquified gas propane systems shall
conform with applicable codes and regulations by the state railroad commission pertaining thereto and as
may be amended.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(9), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-100. - Extensions.
No structural extension shall be attached to a mobile home in violation of the spacing and clearance
requirements of section 50-91. An extension that does not violate such requirements may be installed only if it
meets the following requirements:
(1)
The addition/extension shall be metal, re resistant, double wall panels with mechanically connected joints, and
materials and construction shall conform with the minimum standards of the city building code.
(2)
The addition/extension length shall not be greater than that of the mobile home to which it is accessory.
(3)
The addition/extension shall be dismantled on removal of the mobile home to which it is accessory.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(10), 10-22-2001)

150/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 50-101. - Anchorage and foundations.
Anchorage and foundations for each mobile home shall conform to section 50-35.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § I(11), 10-22-2001)

Secs. 50-102—50-120. - Reserved.
DIVISION 4. - OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE OF PARKS
Sec. 50-121. - Register required.
A licensee under this article shall keep up to date and have available for inspection at the mobile home
park a register or park occupancy which shall contain the following information:
(1)
Name and legal address of park residents.
(2)
The registration date of each mobile home, including the make, length, width, year of manufacture and
identi cation number.
(3)
Location of each mobile home by space number or by street name and number in parks to which the street
naming requirements of section 50-93 apply.
(4)
A new register shall be initiated on January 1 of each year and the old register shall be retired, but retained on
the park premises for at least three years thereafter.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § J, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-122. - List of residents.
(a)
Within ten days after January 1 of each year, a licensee under this article shall furnish to the city tax assessorcollector a list of all mobile home residents in the park on January 1. The list shall contain each mobile home
owner's name and address; the make, length, width, year of manufacture and identi cation number of the
mobile homes; and the location description of such mobile homes within the park.
(b)
Within ten days after July 1 of each year, the licensee shall furnish to the city tax assessor-collector the same
data required in subsection (a) of this section for all residents who have moved into the park after January 1,
and information on all mobile homes that have moved out of the park after January 1, including the data
required in subsection (a) of this section, plus the date on which each mobile home left the park, and the
destination of the mobile home, if known or ascertained by licensee.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § J, 10-22-2001)
151/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 50-123. - Responsibility for maintenance.
A licensee under this article shall be responsible for keeping the mobile home park in a clean, safe and
sanitary condition, free of accumulations of rubbish and grass or weeds that might constitute a fire hazard or
give harborage to noxious insects or animals. Walks, streets and parking spaces shall be maintained in a
serviceable all-weather condition.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § J, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-124. - Fire prevention.
(a)

Open res. No open res shall be permitted in a mobile home park, except for outdoor cooking on camper type
stoves or charcoal grills.
(b)

Flammable liquids. No ammable liquids shall be stored beneath mobile homes or otherwise, except in
accordance with the city re regulations.
(c)

Skirting. The re resistant skirting speci ed in section 50-98 shall be maintained intact to prevent accumulations
of ammable materials beneath mobile homes.
(d)

Fire extinguishers. Emergency re extinguishing apparatus, if required, shall be inspected and tested at intervals
of time suggested by the manufacturer.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § J, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 50-125. - Garbage and refuse.
The storage, collection and disposal of refuse and garbage shall be conducted so as not to create health
hazards, rodent harborage, insect breeding grounds, fire hazards, litter or air pollution. Each mobile home
space shall be provided with rodentproof garbage receptacles of a sufficient number and size to properly
store all refuse and garbage between collections.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-6, art. I, § J, 10-22-2001)

Chapter 58 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 58-1. - Harvesting pecans on city property.
(a)
The general public is allowed to harvest all pecans on the ground only on city-owned lands; however, it is illegal
for any person to thrash any pecan trees on city-owned property. For the purposes of this section, the term
152/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

"thrash" means using poles, sticks, ropes, rocks or any other object to knock pecans from pecan trees, or
climbing pecan trees to shake pecans from their hulls.
(b)
A violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided for in section 1-13 of this
Code. Each act of thrashing shall be a separate o ense.
(Ord. No. 10-14-75, 10-14-1975)

Sec. 58-2. - Discharge of rearms prohibited; exceptions; penalty.
(a)
It shall be unlawful for any person to shoot o , re or discharge any gun, pistol, revolver or rearm of any
description within the corporate limits of the city, except in the protection of person or property.
(b)
This section shall not be construed to prohibit the discharge of rearms on premises owned or operated by any
branch of the armed services of the state or nation or any responsible organization existing for the purpose of
operating and maintaining a ri e or pistol ring range, provided, such discharge is in the course of the regular
functions of such organizations.
(c)
This section does not apply to any law enforcement o cer acting in the discharge of his duties.
(d)
Any person who violates the provisions of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be ned any sum not more than $200.00 for each and every o ense.
(Ord. No. 4-8-80-1, §§ 1—4, 4-8-1980)

State law reference—Authority to regulate discharge of a firearm, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 215.001;
weapons, V.T.C.A., Penal Code ch. 46; justification excluding criminal responsibility, V.T.C.A., Penal Code ch. 9.
Sec. 58-3. - Defacing or injuring public library property; overdue books.
(a)

Willful injury or defacement. It shall be unlawful to willfully injure or deface any book, newspaper, magazine,
pamphlet, manuscript or other property of the city public library by writing, marking, tearing, breaking,
mutilating or otherwise injuring or defacing such property.
(b)

Retention. It shall be unlawful to retain any book, newspaper, magazine, pamphlet, manuscript or other
property of the city public library for a period of 30 days after the giving of written notice to return such library
property, provided, such notice is given after the expiration of time for which such property was lent under the
rules of the city public library at that time. The written notice provided for in this subsection shall be deemed to
be given when such notice is deposited in the United States mail, postage prepaid, by registered or certi ed
mail, to the person to whom such property was lent. Such notice shall be given to the person at the address
re ected for such person on the most recent library card of such person according to the records of the city
public library at that time. The date for the return of such property according to the rules of the city public
153/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

library at that time may be proven upon trial of any o ense under this subsection by the submission into
evidence of the original booked card, or a true and correct copy thereof, as contained within the records of such
library. Upon the trial of any o ense under this subsection, proof of giving written notice as required in this
subsection may be proven by submission into evidence of the registered or certi ed mail return receipt
accompanying such notice as returned to the city public library by the United States Postal Service, or a true and
correct copy thereof, together with a copy of the form or notice then being given by such library. Failure of
delivery of such notice by the United States Post O ce shall not be deemed a defense to such o ense, provided,
notice was mailed to the address of the defendant as provided for in this subsection.
(c)

Penalty. Any person who violates any of the terms and provisions of this section shall be punished as provided
for in section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 11-09-82-1, §§ I—III, 11-9-1982)

State law reference—Municipal library, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 315.005.
Secs. 58-4—58-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - MINORS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Secs. 58-31—58-50. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - JUVENILE CURFEW
Sec. 58-51. - Short title.
This division shall be known and may be cited as the "Curfew Hours for Minors Ordinance."
(Ord. No. 2-12-01-2, § 1, 2-12-2001)

Sec. 58-52. - De nitions.
For the purposes of this chapter the following terms, phrases, words, and their derivations shall have the
meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words used in the present tense include the
future, words in the plural number include the singular number, and words in the singular number include the
plural number. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory.

Curfew hours means:
(1)
11:00 p.m. on any Sunday, Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday or Thursday, until 6:00 a.m. of the following day; and
(2)
154/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

12:01 a.m. until 6:00 a.m. on any Friday or Saturday.

Emergency means an unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting state that calls for
immediate action. The term includes, but is not limited to, a fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or
any situation requiring immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life.

Establishment means any privately-owned place of business operated for a profit to which the public is
invited, including, but not limited to, any place of amusement or entertainment.

Guardian means a:
(1)
Person who, under court order, is the guardian of a minor; or
(2)
Public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by a court.

Minor means any person under 17 years of age.
Operator means any individual, firm, association, partnership, or corporation, operating, managing, or
conducting any establishment. The term includes the members or partners of an association or partnership
and the officers of a corporation.

Parent means a person who is:
(1)
A natural parent, adoptive parent or stepparent of another person; or
(2)
At least 18 years of age and authorized by a parent or guardian in writing to have the care and custody of a
minor.

Public place means any place to which the public or a substantial group of the public has access and
includes, but is not limited to, streets, highways, and the common areas of schools, hospitals, apartment
houses, office buildings, transport facilities, and shops.

Remain means to:
(1)
Linger or stay; or
(2)
Fail to leave premises when requested to do so by a police o cer or the owner, operator or other person in
control of the premises.

Serious bodily injury means bodily injury that creates a substantial risk of death or that causes death,
serious permanent disfigurement, or protracted loss or impairment of the function of any bodily member or
organ.
155/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 2-12-01-2, § 2, 2-12-2001; Ord. No. 2-9-04-1, § 2, 2-9-2004)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 58-53. - Curfew-related o enses.
(a)
A minor commits an o ense if he or she remains in any public place or on the premises of any establishment
within the city during curfew hours.
(b)
A parent or guardian of a minor commits an o ense if he knowingly permits, or by insu cient control allows,
the minor to remain in any public place or on the premises of any establishment within the city during curfew
hours.
(c)
The owner, operator, or any employee of an establishment commits an o ense if he knowingly allows a minor
to remain upon the premises of the establishment during curfew hours.
(Ord. No. 2-12-01-2, § 3, 2-12-2001; Ord. No. 2-9-04-1, § 3, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 58-54. - Exceptions and defenses.
(a)
It is a defense to prosecution under section 58-53 that the minor was:
(1)
Accompanied by the minor's parent or guardian;
(2)
On a lawful errand, at the direction of the minor's parent or guardian, without any detour or stop;
(3)
In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
(4)
Engaged in an employment activity, or going to or returning home from an employment activity, without any
detour or stop;
(5)
Involved in an emergency;
(6)
On the sidewalk abutting the minor's residence of a next-door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the
police department about the minor's presence;
(7)
Attending an o cial school, religious, or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the
city, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor, or going to or returning
home from, without any detour or stop, an o cial school, religious, or other recreational activity supervised by
adults and sponsored by the city, a civic organization; or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the
minor;
156/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(8)
Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the United States Constitution, such as the free exercise of
religion, freedom of speech and the right of assembly; or
(9)
Married, or had been married, or had disabilities of minority removed in accordance with V.T.C.A., Family Code
ch. 31.
(b)
It is a defense to prosecution under section 58-53(c) that the owner, operator or employee of an establishment
promptly noti ed the police department that a minor was present on the premises of the establishment during
curfew hours and refused to leave.
(Ord. No. 2-12-01-2, § 4, 2-12-2001; Ord. No. 2-9-04-1, § 4, 2-9-2004)

State law reference—Removal of disabilities of minority, V.T.C.A., Family Code ch. 31.
Sec. 58-55. - Enforcement.
Before taking any enforcement action under this division, a police officer shall ask the apparent offender's
age and reason for being in the public place. The officer shall not issue a citation or make an arrest under this
division unless the officer reasonably believes that an offense has occurred and that, based on any response
and other circumstances, no defense set forth in section 58-54 is present.
(Ord. No. 2-12-01-2, § 5, 2-12-2001; Ord. No. 2-9-04-1, § 5, 2-9-2004)

Sec. 58-56. - Violations; penalties.
(a)
A person who violates a provision of this section is guilty of a separate o ense for each day or part of a day
during which the violation is committed, continued or permitted. Each o ense, upon conviction, is punishable by
a ne not less than $100.00 and not to exceed $500.00.
(b)
When required by V.T.C.A., Family Code § 51.08, as amended, the municipal court shall waive original jurisdiction
over a minor who violates section 58-53(a) and shall refer the minor to juvenile court.
(Ord. No. 2-12-01-2, § 6, 2-12-2001; Ord. No. 2-9-04-1, § 6, 2-9-2004)

State law reference—Class "C" misdemeanor, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 12.23; Juvenile Justice Code, V.T.C.A.,
Family Code chs. 51—60.
Chapter 62 - PARKS AND RECREATION
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 62-1. - De nitions.

157/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Alcoholic beverage means alcohol or any beverage containing more than one-half of one percent of
alcohol by volume, which is capable of use for beverage purposes, either alone or when diluted.

Bicycle means a device that a person may ride and that is propelled by human power and has two tandem
wheels, one of which is more than 14 inches in diameter.

City park means any land, park or recreation facility owned by the city, including the city park located on:
(1)
Highland Avenue in the city, being block 5, block 4, park of block 2, city addition, and block 28 and 29 of the
northside addition, and all adjoining lands; and
(2)
South Highway 377, being part of block 50, city addition, in the city.

Intoxicating beverages shall mean an "alcoholic beverage" as defined in V.T.C.A., Texas Alcoholic Beverage
Code § 1.04(1), as amended.

Person means any firm, corporation, partnership, individual human or other legal entity.
Roller blades, roller skates and skateboards mean any device with wheels attached to the bottom of the
shoe or board.

Tennis court means a facility located at a city park and used for playing tennis.
Tricycle means a vehicle with three tandem wheels, a steering handle, a saddle seat, and pedals by which
it is propelled.

Vehicle means a device that can be used to transport or draw persons or property on a highway. Such
term does not include:
(1)
A device used exclusively on stationary rails or tracks; or
(2)
Manufactured housing, as such term is de ned by the Texas Manufactured Housing Standards Act, Vernon's
Ann. Civ. St. art. 5221f.
(Ord. No. 8-11-92-1, § 1, 8-11-1992; Ord. No. 4-9-96-1, § I, 4-8-1996; Ord. No. 8-11-97-1, § I, 8-11-1997; Ord. No. 1-12-09-1, § 1, 112-2009)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
State law reference—Similar definitions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code §§ 541.201, 542.202.

158/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 62-2. - Park curfew.
(a)

Curfew hours. The Dublin City Park will be closed for public use every day from midnight to 6:00 a.m.
(b)

Exceptions. Persons participating in events in progress at the time of the park curfew will be allowed to remain
in the park as long as the event continues.
(c)

Penalty. Any person on Dublin City Park property during curfew hours, and who is not a participant in a
sanctioned activity, will be subject to a ne of $1.00—$200.00 if such person is found guilty of noncompliance
with the curfew by the city municipal court.
(Ord. No. 3-11-80-3, § VIII(A—C), 3-11-1980)

Sec. 62-3. - Use of roller blades, roller skates, skateboards, bicycles and tricycles on tennis courts.
It shall be unlawful for any person to use or operate roller blades, roller skates, skateboards, bicycles or
tricycles on the surface of the tennis courts in any city park.
(Ord. No. 4-9-96-1, § II, 4-8-1996)

Sec. 62-4. - Prohibited actions and defenses.
(a)
Subject to the following subsection (b), it shall be unlawful for any person to have in his or her possession any
intoxicating beverage at any time that person is in a city park within the City of Dublin, Erath County, Texas.
(b)
It shall be a defense to prosecution under subsection (a) if a person possesses an intoxicating beverage while
attending an "event" in a city park during the hours for which an event permit has been issued by the city
pursuant to the following subsection, if the person obtained the intoxicating beverage at the event, or if the
event permit authorized the person to transport the intoxicating beverage to the event, in a manner authorized
by the event permit.
(c)
It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his or her possession any intoxicating beverage at any event in a
city park within the City of Dublin, Erath County, Texas, except as authorized by the event permit. A person shall
not take or transport any intoxicating beverage to an event in a city park unless authorized to do so by the
terms and conditions of the event permit.
(Ord. No. 8-11-92-1, § 2, 8-11-1992; Ord. No. 1-12-09-1, § 2, 1-12-2009)

Sec. 62-5. - Speed limit established.
No person shall drive or operate any vehicle at a rate of speed greater than ten miles per hour in any city
park.
(Ord. No. 8-11-97-1, § 2, 8-11-1997)
159/428

7/12/2019

State law reference—Authority to regulate speed in parks, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.202(a)(6).
Sec. 62-6. - Drilling or mining prohibited.
The city council does prohibit drilling or mining in Dublin City Park.
(Res. No. 7-25-89-2, § 1, 7-25-1989)

Sec. 62-43. - Overnight camping permit.

160/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Persons wishing to camp overnight in the Dublin City Park must first obtain a permit from the city
secretary or his designated representative. The permit will specify the length of the stay, as well as the persons
camping. The cost of the permit is $1.00 per night. If the persons camping wish to use existing electrical
outlets, the permit will show the use and permit cost, which will be $3.00 per night.
(Ord. No. 3-11-80-3, § VIII(D), 3-11-1980)

Sec. 62-44. - Events and event permits.
(a)
The city administrator may issue a permit for the possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages in a city
park ("event permit") for a family reunion or picnic, an organized sporting or business event, a public meeting,
assembly, ceremony, speech or address, political meeting, exhibit, dramatic performance, play, motion picture,
trade fair, or similar event (individually and collectively an "event"). An event permit may not be issued for an
event in which a primary purpose will be the sale or consumption of intoxicating beverages.
(b)
An event permit may be issued for an event if:
(1)
A complete permit application is made and led with the city secretary not less than ten business days, nor
more than 365 calendar days prior to the date requested for the event;
(2)
No other activity has been scheduled for the city park during the hours for which the event permit is requested,
and, if another event is scheduled in the city park for the same day, su cient time exists both before and after
the requested times for the event for set-up and clean-up, as applicable;
(3)
The fee required for the issuance of an event permit is paid;
(4)
Security will be provided for the event by certi ed police o cers; and
(5)
The required security deposit for the event is paid.
(Ord. No. 1-12-09-1, § 3, 1-12-2009)

Sec. 62-45. - Permit applications.
(a)
A person seeking an event permit shall complete an application provided by the city in which the following
information is listed:
(1)
The name, address and telephone number of applicant;
(2)

161/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

If the event permit is for an organization, then the name, address and telephone number of a leader of the
organization;
(3)
If the event permit is for an individual other than the applicant, then the name, address and telephone number
of that individual;
(4)
The exact nature of the use or activity for which the event permit is sought;
(5)
The day and hours for which the permit is sought;
(6)
The city park or portion of the park desired to be used to carry out the proposed use or activity; and
(7)
An estimate of the anticipated attendance.
(b)
The applicant shall, in addition to the city secretary, le a copy of the application with the chief of police.
(c)
The chief of police, or his or her designee, shall evaluate the application:
(1)
Establish the number of police o cers required as security for the event;
(2)
Establish the dollar amount of the deposit required to secure payment of the police o cer(s) that will provide
security for the event;
(3)
The proposed activities for the event, the estimated attendance, the tra c, issues applicable to the hours
requested, the projected level of noise, the impact on neighboring residential areas and other related safety and
public welfare issues;
(4)
Establish the speci c criteria and authorization for the transport, possession and distribution of intoxicating
beverages at the event; including, speci cally, whether one or more licensed vendors will be authorized, if
attendees will be permitted to bring intoxicating beverages to the event for self consumption, and other
requirements applicable to the control of intoxicating beverages at the event; and
(5)
Forward his or her recommendation to the city administrator.
(Ord. No. 1-12-09-1, § 4, 1-12-2009)

Sec. 62-46. - Permit issuance.
(a)
The city administrator shall issue an event permit if he or she nds:
(1)
162/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The application is complete;
(2)
Complies fully with the ordinance from which this section derives;
(3)
Is accompanied by the application fee and the security deposit for the required security for the event; and
(4)
Approval of the application is recommended by the chief of police.
(b)
Notwithstanding the foregoing, an event permit shall not be issued if:
(1)
The proposed activity will unreasonably interfere with or detract from the general public use and enjoyment of
the city park;
(2)
The proposed activity will unreasonably interfere with or detract from the public health, safety or welfare;
(3)
The conduct of the proposed activity or use is reasonably likely to result in or create a clear and present danger
of violence resulting harm to the public or damage to property; or
(4)
The park or park facilities desired have already been reserved for another activity on the day and at the time
requested in the application.
(Ord. No. 1-12-09-1, § 5, 1-12-2009)

DIVISION 2. - REGULATIONS
Sec. 62-91. - Park buildings.
(a)

Cost. Organizations or person(s) that will be charging the general public a fee to attend such events as dances,
exhibitions, carnivals, etc. will be charged a set fee.
(1)
Organizations or person(s) that will be using the facilities for private use for such things that will not be charging
the general public will be charged a fee.
(2)
Organizations or person(s) renting the building(s) and/or facilities will be responsible for any damages incurred
that exceed the cost of the deposit.
(b)

Loud music. The recreational building in the Dublin City Park is close to a residential area. Due to this, we have
had many complaints concerning loud music at night. We have in turn instituted a policy in the policy
department whereby when a loud music call is reported, the o cer will verify the source and whoever is in
charge of the function will be requested immediately to turn down the music to an acceptable level. If the music
again becomes loud, the o cer will verify the call and at that time the o cer will shut down the function.
(c)

Dances. Any dance requires a minimum of two security guards to patrol the dance. The cost of the security
guards is on le in the city secretary's o ce. All dances start at 8:00 p.m. and end no later that 12:00 a.m. All
security guards will be there at 8:00 p.m. and will be paid in cash before the dance starts. It is the individual's
responsibility to contact the Dublin Police Department to make arrangements for the two security guards.
(d)

Cleaning supplies. Cleaning supplies, toilet paper, paper towels, brooms, mops and any other items will be
provided by the renter.
(e)

Cleanup area and time. The cleanup area will be inside of the recreational building (including the kitchen,
restrooms, front entrance and the stage areas) or any other recreational facility rented. This also includes any
other area outside the recreational facility used (parking lot, playground, etc.). Cleanup must be done no later
than 10:00 a.m. the following morning or the cleanup deposit will be FORFEITED, no exceptions.
(f)

Alcohol. Absolutely no alcohol on the premises at any time!! The city respectfully maintains an ordinance that
prohibits the use, consumption, or possession of alcohol in the Dublin City Park. Anyone with alcohol is subject
to eviction and/or a ne of $500.00. If the renter is aware that alcohol has been brought onto the premises the
function will be shut down and the renter is subject to a ne.
(g)
164/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Renters to comply with policy. Each renter agrees to comply with this policy and inform the participants of the
function.

Zip: ____________

)
