activities;
(4)
The area used must be cleaned within two calendar days of the last day of activity or the cleanup deposit will not
be refunded.
(b)

Outdoor carnivals. Sponsors of outdoor carnivals to be held at Dublin City Park must adhere to the following
guidelines:
169/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(1)
The sponsor must coordinate the dates of the carnival with the city to ensure there will be no con icts with
other scheduled activities;
(2)
A nonrefundable fee per day which is on le in the city secretary's o ce is due to the city prior to the rst day of
carnival activities;
(3)
A refundable cleanup deposit amount which is on le in the city secretary's o ce is due prior to the rst day of
activities;
(4)
The area used for the carnival site, and surrounding parking areas, must be cleaned within two calendar days
after the last day of carnival activities or the cleanup deposit will not be refunded.
(Ord. No. 3-11-80-3, § VI, 3-11-1980)

Chapter 70 - SIGNS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 70-1. - Findings of fact adopted.
The facts and recitations set out in the whereas clauses of the ordinance from which this chapter is
derived are found and declared to be true and correct and are incorporated in this section as findings of fact.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 1, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 70-2. - First Amendment rights.
This chapter shall not be construed, applied, interpreted nor enforced in a manner which violates the First
Amendment rights of any person, and the building official shall seek the advice and recommendation of the
city attorney prior to taking any action to enforce any provision of this chapter with respect to any sign or
speech by any person.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 2, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 70-3. - Violation; penalty.
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be punished as provided in section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 7, 10-22-2001)

Secs. 70-4—70-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - REGULATION
170/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 70-31. - Handbills and circulars.
Handbills and circulars are prohibited unless they are hand delivered to an individual.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 4(c), 10-22-2001)

Sec. 70-32. - Regulation of signs on rights-of-way.
No sign shall be erected or affixed within or project over any public right-of-way of any street or public
way within the city, or across the public right-of-way line extended across a railroad right-of-way. This section
shall not be construed to prohibit vehicular signs; nor to prohibit the carrying or display of signs by a person
as long as such sign is not connected or affixed to the real property comprising the public right-of-way, its
fixtures and appurtenances.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 3, 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 78.
Sec. 70-33. - Placing sign on right-of-way.
(a)
It shall be unlawful and a violation of this chapter for any person to place, deposit or install any sign upon or
projecting over any public right-of-way within the city, except as speci cally provided in this article.
(b)
No person shall attach any sign, paper or other material, or paint, stencil or write any name or number or
otherwise mark on any sidewalk, curb, gutter, street, tree or utility pole located on public property or within a
public right-of-way, public building, public fence or public structure. This section shall not prohibit the posting of
governmental signs or the painting or attachment of street address numbers to curbs.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 4(a), (b), 10-22-2001)

Cross reference—Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 78.
Sec. 70-34. - Exceptions.
The prohibitions set forth in this article shall not be applicable to the following signs:
(1)

Governmental signs. Signs erected or maintained pursuant to the discharge of any governmental function;
required by law, ordinance or governmental regulation; or located on property owned, leased or under control
of the federal or state government.
(2)

Railway signs. Signs within or on railway property and placed or maintained by the owner of the railway
property in reference to the operation of such railway.
(3)
171/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Utility signs. Signs marking utility or underground communication or transmission lines that are placed and
installed by the corresponding utility.
(4)

Signs or persons. Hand-held signs or signs, symbols or displays on persons or animals.
(5)

Plaques. Commemorative plaques of recognized historical societies and organizations.
(6)

Mailboxes and newspaper racks. Signs located on mailboxes, newspaper vending machines and curbside
residential newspaper holders which identify the owner and address of the premises or the name of the
newspaper sold or subscribed to, provided, that such devices are not placed so as to interfere with the safe
movement of pedestrians or vehicular tra c.
(7)

Garage sale signs. Any person may erect a sign on his own property, or property of another with the owner's
permission, for the purpose of advertising a garage or yard sale. Such person's name and address and the date
must be shown on the sign; however, such signs shall be removed within 24 hours of the sale.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 5, 10-22-2001)

Sec. 70-35. - Removal of signs.
(a)
The building o cial and any other city employee may immediately remove and discard any yard sale sign,
political sign, garage sale sign, placard and similar sign placed, deposited or installed on a city right-of-way.
(b)
If the building o cial shall nd that any business, commercial or political sign, other than the type referenced in
subsection (a) of this section, is located on the city right-of-way; is unsafe or insecure; is a menace to the public;
is abandoned; is maintained in a dilapidated condition; has been constructed or erected or is being maintained
in violation of this Code; or is not permitted as required in this article, he shall give the sign or property owner
written notice to repair, remove or obtain a permit for such sign, as applicable, within ten days after such notice.
If the property owner fails to remove, repair or obtain a permit for such sign so as to comply with all applicable
standards and regulations, the building o cial shall cause the sign to be removed or repaired, and such cost of
removal or repair shall be charged to and paid by the property owner. If such demolition or repair expenses are
not paid by the sign owner within 30 days of such billing, then such expenses shall constitute a valid lien and
claim against the property owner. If the owner of any sign located on the public right-of-way cannot be located
or identi ed after reasonable inquiry, the building o ce may remove such sign from the right-of-way. Notice to
any such owner shall provide the property owner with an opportunity to bring the sign into compliance or to
request a hearing before the city council to determine whether the sign should be repaired or removed. Such
appeal must be led in writing with the city secretary within ten days of the notice. After consideration of all
facts, the city council shall rule upon the appeal.
(c)

172/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The building o cial may cause any sign which is an immediate peril to persons or property to be removed
summarily and without notice.
(d)
Any sign that is located in a public right-of-way may be immediately removed by the building o cial without
notice to the owner of such sign if the sign obstructs the vision of the operators of motor vehicles operating on
nearby streets or alleys, or if such sign poses a clear threat to public safety because of its location, construction
or for any other reason.
(Ord. No. 10-22-01-5, § 6, 10-22-2001)

Chapter 74 - SOLID WASTE
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Secs. 74-1—74-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - DISPOSAL AND COLLECTION
Sec. 74-31. - De nitions.
For the purposes of this article, the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the
meaning ascribed to them in this section, provided, that unless specifically defined in this section, words or
phrases used in this chapter shall be interpreted so as to give them the same meaning as they have in
common usage, and to give this chapter its most reasonable application.

Bulky waste means stoves, refrigerators, water tanks, washing machines, furniture, used and discarded
mattresses and other waste materials other than construction debris, dead animals, hazardous waste or
stable matter with weights or volumes greater than those allowed for carts.

Bundle means tree, shrub and brush trimmings or newspaper and magazines securely tied together
forming an easily handled package not exceeding three feet in length and 35 pounds in weight.

Business unit shall mean any premises, locations or entities, public or private, including all industrial and
commercial entities, within the corporate limits of the city not a residential unit.

Cart means a plastic/metal trash can with lid designed to store residential refuse.
City shall mean the city of Dublin, Texas.
Commercial or industrial means and includes any establishment, public or private, rendering a service,
manufacturing a product, offering a product for sale or any other similar activity.

Construction debris means waste building materials resulting from construction, remodeling, repair or
demolition operations.
173/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Contractor means the person, corporation or partnership performing refuse collection and disposal under
contract with the city.

Customer means the person, firm or corporation receiving city water, wastewater or solid waste disposal
services for a residential or business unit, whether within the city or outside the city limits.

Dead animal means an animal or portion thereof that has expired from any cause.
Garbage means the accumulation of waste (animal, vegetable and/or other matter) that results from the
preparation, processing, consumption, dealing in, handling, packing, canning, storage, transportation, decay or
decomposition of meats, fish, fowl, bids, fruits, gains or other animal or vegetable matter (including, but not by
way of limitation, used tin cans and other food containers; and all putrescible or easily decomposable waste
animal or vegetable matter which is likely to attract flies or rodents); except (in all cases) any matter included
in the definition of bulky waste, construction debris, dead animals, hazardous waste, rubbish or stable matter.

Hazardous waste means waste, in any amount, which is defined, characterized or designated as
hazardous by the United States Environmental Protection Agency or appropriate state agency by or pursuant
to federal or state law, or waste, in any amount, which is regulated under federal or state law, including motor
oil, gasoline, paint and paint cans.

Person means and includes an individual human, partnership, co-partner ship firm, company, limited
liability partnership or other partnership or other such company, joint venture, joint stock company, trust,
estate, governmental entity, association or corporation or any other legal entity, or their legal representatives,
agents or assigns. The masculine gender shall include the feminine and the singular shall include the plural
where indicated by the context.

Producer means an occupant of a residential or business unit who generates refuse.
Refuse means residential refuse, bulky waste, construction debris and stable matter generated at a
residential unit, unless the context otherwise requires, and commercial and industrial refuse.

Residential refuse means all garbage and rubbish generated by a producer at a residential unit.
Residential unit means a dwelling within the corporate limits or service area of the city which is intended
for occupancy by a person or group of persons comprising not more than one family. A dwelling shall be
deemed to be occupied and shall be deemed by the city to be a separate residential unit for billing and
collection purposes when either water or electrical power services are being supplied thereto.

Rubbish means waste wood, wood products, tree trimmings, grass cuttings, dead plants, weeds, leaves,
dead trees or branches thereof, chips, shavings sawdust, printed matter, paper, pasteboard, rags, straw, used
and discarded clothing, used and discarded shoes and boots, combustible waste pulp and other products such
as are used for packaging or wrapping crockery and glass, ashes, cinders, floor sweepings, glass, mineral or
metallic substances, and any and all other waste materials not included in the definition of bulky waste,
construction debris, dead animals, garbage, hazardous waste or stable matter.
174/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Stable matter means manure and other waste matter normally accumulated in or about a stable, or any
animal, livestock or poultry enclosure, and resulting from the keeping of animals, poultry or livestock.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. I, § 4, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, §4, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, § 4, 12-15-2004; Ord. No. 3-14-05-6,
art. II, § 4, 3-14-2005)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 74-32. - Enforcement.
This article shall be enforced as provided for in chapter 94, article III, division 2, subdivision II of this Code.
Sec. 74-33. - Residential service.
The following rules, regulations and provisions shall, in addition to the other applicable provisions of this
article, govern the provision of solid waste services to residential units.
(1)

Mandatory participation by residential units. Every residential unit within the corporate limits of the city shall be
required to use garbage collection and disposal services provided under contract by the city when such
residential unit is occupied. A residential unit shall be deemed occupied when water, waste water, or electrical
power services are being supplied. Use of garbage collection and disposal services are presumed when any
utility service is provided to the service address, and the customer shall pay for the service as provided.
(2)

Curbside service. The contractor shall provide curbside collection service for the collection of no more than ten
bags, placed in a container, of residential refuse to each residential unit one time per week. Customers must not
place trash at curbside earlier than 5:00 p.m. the day before collection day.
(3)

Trash container placement at curb. Trash container for collection shall be placed at curbside for collection.
Curbside refers to that portion of the right-of-way adjacent to paved or traveled city roadways with placement
as close to the roadway as practicable without interfering with or endangering the movement of vehicles or
pedestrians. When construction work is being performed in the right-of-way, trash containers shall be placed as
close as practicable to an access point for the collection vehicle. The contractor may decline to collect any trash
not so placed.
(4)

Hours of operation. Collection of residential refuse and special collections scheduled by the city shall not start
before 7:00 a.m. or continue after 7:00 p.m. on the same day. Exceptions to collection shall be e ected only
upon the mutual agreement of the city and contractor, or when the contractor reasonably determines that an
exception is necessary to complete collection on an existing collection route due to unusual circumstances.
(5)

Holidays. In the event of suspension of regular collection service on a holiday, collection service shall be
provided on the next business day after the holiday.
175/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(6)

Complaints. All complaints shall be made directly to the contractor. In the case of veri ed missed scheduled
collections, the contractor shall arrange for the collection within 48 hours after the complaint is received. The
city shall notify customers of complaint procedures, and of the location and telephone number at which the
contractor can be reached between the hours from 8:00 a.m. to 4:30 p.m. on regular collection days.
(7)

Appeal. Any determination by the city, the contractor or the city's operator regarding the terms and provisions
of this article may be appealed to the city council, which shall conduct a hearing on the matter. The city, the
contractor or the city's operator, as applicable, shall, upon request, provide the customer with information
regarding appeals and hearing procedures.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. V, § 1, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VI, § 1, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-34. - Commercial and industrial units.
Commercial or industrial units shall arrange by individual agreement for collection and disposal of refuse
with the city or an independent company the city uses for residential services. Such operations shall comply
with all applicable laws. Vehicles and equipment used for such collections shall be kept in good repair,
appearance and sanitary condition, and all refuse shall be contained, tied or enclosed so as to prevent leaking,
spilling or blowing during hauling.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. V, § 2, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VI, § 2, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-35. - Violations notices.
(a)
If an o cer charged with the enforcement of this article shall determine that a person has violated any
provision of this article, such o cer may issue a citation.
(b)
If an o cer charged with the enforcement of this article shall determine that a situation exists which
immediately a ects or threatens the health, safety and well-being of the general public, and that immediate
action is necessary, such o cer may take such action as shall be necessary, including issuing citations for
violations of the terms and provisions hereof to the owner and/or occupant of the property upon which such
condition exists, as may be deemed appropriate and necessary.
(c)
If an o cer charged with enforcement of this article determines a situation constitutes an immediate threat to
the public health, safety and welfare, and the owner or occupant of the property is absent or fails to
immediately remedy the violation, the city manager or his designee may determine that an emergency exists
and order such action as may be required to protect the public health, safety and welfare.
(d)
If any owner or occupant shall fail or refuse to remedy any of the conditions prohibited by this article within a
reasonable period and after notice to do so, the city may terminate services or do such work or cause the same
176/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

to be done, and pay therefor, and charge the expenses in doing or having such work done or improvements
made to the owner(s) of the property, and such charge shall be a personal liability of such owner to the city.
(e)
Notices required pursuant to this article shall be in writing. Such notice may be served upon such owner and/or
occupant as follows: in person by an o cer or employee of the city; by letter addressed to such owner or
occupant at his/her post o ce address; or, if personal service may not be had, or the owner or occupant's
address be not known, then notice may be given by publishing a brief summary of such order in the o cial
newspaper of the city, two times in ten consecutive days, and by posting a notice on or near the front door of
each building on the property upon which the violation relates, or, if no building exists, by posting notice on a
placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the property to which the violation relates. Notice of
termination of services for non-payment shall be mailed regular rst class mail to the address designated on the
account for receipt or bill and shall be deemed served within three days of deposit in the regular mail. The
notice may state "Sanitary Improvements", "To Whom It May Concern" and a brief statement of the violation(s)
or delinquency. If the notice is for delinquency, the notice shall include a termination date and location for
payment for services. Service of the notice by any one of the above methods, or by a combination thereof, shall
be deemed su cient notice.
(f)
If an owner is mailed a notice in accordance with subsection (e) and the United States Postal Service returns the
notice as "refused" or "unclaimed" the validity of the notice is not a ected, and the notice is considered as
delivered.
(g)
Notice of nuisances provided by mail or by posting as set forth in subsection (e) may provide for year-round
abatement of the nuisance and inform the owner that should the owner commit any other violation of the same
kind that pose a danger to the public health and safety on or before the rst anniversary of the date of the
notice, the city without further notice may abate the violation at the owner's expense and assess the costs
against the property.
(h)
Persons in violation of this article or causing or creating a prohibited nuisance in the presence of a person
authorized to enforce this article may be cited or a complaint led for such violation without notice of the
violation, or warning, and such citation or complaint shall be led in the municipal court of the city.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VII, § 5, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 1, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-36. - Costs and appeals.
In addition to any other remedy provided in this article and cumulative thereto, the code enforcement
officer, after giving to the owner of the property ten days notice in writing, as provided in section 74-35 above,
may cause any of the work or improvements mentioned in this article to be done at the expense of the city,
and charge the owner or occupant of the property on which such work or improvements are done, or the
person to which the utility bills are addressed, and cause all of the actual cost to the city to be assessed on the
real estate or lot on which such expenses occurred; provided, that the owner of any such real estate may
177/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

appeal to the city council from the order of the code enforcement officer by filing a written statement with the
code enforcement officer within ten days after receipt of the notice provided for above, stating that such real
estate complied with the provision of this article before the expiration of a ten-day period. The city council
shall set a date, within 30 days from the date of the appeal, for hearing the appeal to determine whether the
real estate complied with the provisions of this article before the expiration of such ten-day period. The
authority of the code enforcement officer to proceed to cause such work to be done shall not be suspended
while an appeal from the order is pending. If it shall be determined by the city council that the premises
complied with the provisions of this article before the expiration of the ten-day period, then no personal
liability of the owner shall arise nor shall any lien be created against the premises upon which such work was
done.
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 2, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-37. - Cost of abatement constitutes lien.
Cumulative of the city's remedy by fine, as set forth herein, the city may do such work or cause the same
to be done to remedy such condition to remove such matter from such owner's premises at the city's expense
and charge the same to the utility bill of such property and assess the same against the real estate or lot or
lots upon which such expense is incurred as provided in state law.
(1)
Expenditures plus ten percent per annum interest on the expenditures from the date of such payment by the
city shall be added to the next billing cycle for utility bills for the real estate or lot or lots, if not already paid.
Payment shall be due and payable in full by the owner or occupant at the time of payment of such utility bill. If
the property is unoccupied, no utilities shall be furnished to the property where the work occurred until such
obligation, as herein set out, payable to the city for abatement of any nuisance described herein is paid in full.
(2)
Upon ling with the county clerk of Erath County, Texas, of a statement by the city secretary or designee of such
expenses, the city shall have a privileged lien upon said real estate or lot or lots, second only to tax liens and
liens for street improvements, to secure the expenditure so made and ten percent per annum interest, on the
amount from the date of such payment so made by the city.
(3)
The city may, additionally, institute suit and recover such expenses and foreclose such lien in any court of
competent jurisdiction, and the statement so led with the county clerk or a certi ed copy thereof shall be
prima facie proof of the amount expended in any such work or improvements to remedy such condition or
remove any such matter.
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 3, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-38. - Penalty.

178/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article, or shall fail to comply therewith, or with
any of the requirements thereof, within the city limits shall be deemed guilty of an offense and shall be liable
for a fine not less than $200.00 and not to exceed the sum of $2,000.00. Each day the violation exists shall
constitute a separate offense. Such penalty shall be in addition to all the other remedies provided herein.
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 5, 3-14-2005)

Secs. 74-39—74-60. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - RATES, BILLING AND TERMINATION OF SERVICES
Sec. 74-61. - Rates for solid waste services.
The following rates, fees and charges shall be charged and paid for solid waste services within the city.
(1)

Residential. The minimum monthly charge per residential unit shall be as the city council determines from time
to time. The city shall notify each residential customer in writing of the initial monthly rate and subsequent
changes in the monthly rate at least 30 days before the e ective date of such rate. The fee for the rst month of
service shall be collected on the rst billing cycle after application for service is made and payment of the
monthly rate shall be made each month thereafter.
(2)

Commercial or industrial. The rates for solid waste services for commercial and industrial customers shall be
determined by the city's agreement and contract based upon location, volume and frequency of service and/or
billed through an independent company.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. III, § 6, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. IV, § 6, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-62. - Billing and payment for services.
Bills for solid waste services shall be mailed on or about the last day of each month for the services
provided during the immediate preceding billing cycle.
(1)

Billing date. The billing date shall be the date of mailing and the failure of the customer to receive any such bill
shall in no way relieve the customer of the duty to pay for the services rendered on or before the due date.
(2)

Due date. All bills for solid waste collection services are due on or before the tenth day of each month or the
rst business day following the tenth if the tenth falls on a weekend or authorized city holiday (the "due date").
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. V, § 1, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-63. - Late charges.
179/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

If full payment of any bill is not made by the due date, or arrangements for payment are not made by the
due date, the bill is considered late, and the city shall promptly mail a second written notice that a late charge
equal to ten percent of the current bill for solid waste collection services is added to the billing. The bill shall
be considered delinquent if it is not paid in full, or arrangements for payment are not made, within ten days
after the date the second written notice is mailed (the "delinquent date").
(1)
The portion of a customer disputed bill is not considered late or delinquent until ten days after the completion
of the dispute determination if the customer disputes the bill or portion of the bill in good faith before the due
date.
(2)
Customers disputing any bill shall contact the city o ce prior to the bill's due date addressing the portion of the
bill which is disputed and the grounds for such dispute. Upon noti cation of the dispute and the grounds for
such dispute, whether by telephone, written communication, or in person at the city administrative o ce, the
city shall promptly make such investigation as the particular case shall require and report the results thereof to
the customer.
(3)
If the customer is dissatis ed with the results of the city's investigation or the dispute is not thereby resolved,
the customer shall be given an opportunity for a hearing before the city manager. If the hearing cannot be
immediately conducted, the city and the customer shall arrange the earliest reasonable date for the hearing.
The results of the hearing shall be provided to the customer within ve business days of the hearing. If the
customer fails to make arrangements for the hearing within three business days after requesting the hearing or
if the customer chooses not to participate in the hearing, the city after proper notice, may terminate service.
(4)
If the customer is dissatis ed with the results of the hearing before the city manager or if the dispute is not
thereby resolved, the city shall inform the customer of the customer's right to request a hearing before the city
council.
(5)
Pending the completion of the determination of the dispute, the customer shall not be required to pay the
disputed portion of the bill which exceeds the amount of the customer's average monthly usage at current
rates. Late fees and the service termination processing fee may be waived if the customer's dispute is made in
good faith. For purposes of this paragraph only, the customer's average monthly usage shall be the average of
the customer's gross service for the preceding six-month period. Where there is not any or insu cient previous
usage history existing, consumption for calculation of the average monthly usage shall be estimated on the
basis of usage levels of similar customers under similar circumstances.
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. V, § 2, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-64. - Termination of service and charges for service termination procedures.
(a)
180/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Termination for delinquency. The city shall have the right to and may terminate solid waste collection services to
any customer.
(b)

Service termination processing charges. A processing fee shall be assessed on a delinquent account after service
termination procedures have commenced as provided in section 74-64(a). Services shall not be restored until
the customer returns their delinquent account, including inactive accounts, to current status. An account is
considered current when all delinquent charges for services, applicable late fees, security fee or security fee
upgrade, and applicable service termination processing fees are paid in full or the customer makes payment
arrangements satisfactory to the city secretary.
(c)

Disconnect for vacation at customer's request. Customers may request temporary service disconnection for
vacation purposes for a current account. The customer shall notify the city and pay the required fee at least two
days prior to the e ective date of service disconnection.
(d)

Delinquent accounts. Any residence or property where collection services are requested to be provided, where a
de cient account is still outstanding from a previous customer, shall not be reconnected in a di erent name for
which the account was previously connected under, without paying the de ciencies on the account, unless the
person requesting collection services demonstrates that the person whose name on the account was previously
billed to, is no longer a resident of the property or in control of the property.
(1)
New owners of property or new leaseholders shall not be responsible for the delinquent accounts of a prior
owner or lessee who has vacated the premises.
(2)
No customer may establish a new account in his or her name who has an outstanding de ciency from any
previous utility account held by the city without paying all de ciencies in addition to the security fee for the new
utility account.
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. V, § 3, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-65. - Minors.
No account may be held in the name of a person who is under the age of 18 years unless, the minor
requesting services provides adequate evidence that the minor has been emancipated through marriage or
other legal means.
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. V, § 4, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 74-66. - Failure to pay for solid waste collection charges.
It shall be unlawful to receive solid waste collection service from the city and fail to pay the fees and
charges for such service. It shall be prima facie evidence that a delinquent customer is in violation of this
section, if the service fee or charges remain unpaid ten days after receiving written notice of such delinquency.
181/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Conviction of the offense of failure to pay a service fee or charge shall be a misdemeanor subject to a fine of
not less than $200.00 nor more than $2,000.00 dollars. Each day in violation shall be deemed a separate
offense and subject to the penalty herein provided.
(Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. V, § 5, 3-14-2005)

Chapter 78 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Secs. 78-1—78-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - STREET EXCAVATION
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 78-31. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Building official or official means the person, his staff or employees, or entity designated by the city to
perform the duties and responsibilities set forth in this article to be performed by the city, or, if no duties and
responsibilities have been designated, the city manager.

Construction activity or work includes, but is not limited to, the causing or carrying out of any manmade
change in any property or facility through building, erecting, installing, bulkheading, filling, mining, dredging,
clearing, paving, grading, excavating, boring, drilling or the addition, removal or alteration of any facility or any
improvement to property, including altering the size of any facilities, or other similar work or activity in, over,
under, through, along or across the rights-of-way or streets within the city limits.

Contractor means and includes, but is not limited to, the person possessing a permit, franchise or license
agreement as required under this article and all persons actually performing, directing, monitoring, managing
or overseeing any construction activity, work or other such similar activity in, over, under, through, along or
across any streets or rights-of-way within the city limits.

Excavation means any manmade formation of a cavity, hole or hollow by any means of digging, plowing,
quarrying, uncovering, blasting, scooping, drilling, dredging, bulldozing, relocating or making a cut, opening,
boring or other action or process to form a cavity, hole or hollow.

Facility or facilities means any plant, equipment and property, including, but not limited to, duct spaces,
manholes, poles, towers, utility pipes, pipes, conduits, lines, wires, transmission media, underground and
overhead passageways or other equipment, structures and appurtenances which are located in, over, under,
182/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

through, along or across the rights-of-way or streets.

Installation means the addition, removal, repair or alteration of any facility located in, over, under,
through, along or across the rights-of-way or streets.

Owner means any person having financial interests in property or facilities located in, over, under,
through, along or across streets and rights-of-way in the city, including the person directing the actions of any
contractor, paying a contractor or for whose benefit the actions of the contractor are undertaken.

Permanent structure means any facility located in, over, under, through, along or across the rights-of-way
or streets within the city limits that occupies, affixes or otherwise is to remain in the same location for a period
of more than 30 days.

Person means and includes an individual human, partnership, firm, company, limited liability partnership
or other partnership or such company, joint venture, joint stock company, association, legal entity or
corporation of any kind, including, but not limited to, any provider of any "utility service" or "public service," as
such terms are defined in this section.

Public service means any business or commercial activity which is not included in the definition of "utility
service," as such term is defined in this section, and that requires the use of the public streets or rights-of-way
for the location of any facility or equipment to provide services to persons or property situated within the city,
including, but not limited to, cable television service and services using a transmission media, but excluding
telephones, taxi service and solid waste collection.

Right-of-way means the surface of and the space above and below any and all present and future public
thoroughfares, public utility easements, public ways, public grounds, public waterways and, without limitation
thereof, any other public property within the corporate limits of the city.

Street means the surface of and the space above and below any and all present and future public streets,
avenues, highways, boulevards, drives, roads, bridges, alleys, lanes, viaducts and all other public roadways
within the city limits, and any highways, county roads or other public roadways for which the city has an
agreement or contract to control, regulate or maintain.

Transmission media means all cables, fibers, wires, tubes, pipes or other physical devices used to transmit
and/or receive communication signals, whether analog, digital or of other characteristics, and whether for
voice, video or data, or other purposes, which are physically located in the rights-of-way or streets.

Utility service has its common meaning and specifically includes, but is not limited to, electric, water,
wastewater, gas and telephone service.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 2, 2-21-2000)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 78-32. - Streets and rights-of-way.
183/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The city shall have exclusive dominion, control and jurisdiction in, over, under, through, along and across
the streets and rights-of-way, and may provide for the improvement thereof by paving, repaving, raising,
draining, realigning, closing or otherwise the use of such streets or rights-of-way. The provisions of law
providing for assessments against abutting property for street improvements are expressly adopted, without
limitation. Such exclusive dominion, control and jurisdiction in, over, under, through, along and across the
streets and rights-of-way of the city shall also include, but not be limited to, the power to regulate, locate,
remove or prohibit the location, installation, alteration or removal of any type of facility or other property in,
over, under, through, along or across any streets or rights-of-way. The location, alteration or removal,
including the route, of all facilities within the rights-of-way or streets shall be subject to the reasonable
direction of the city.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 3(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-33. - City rights reserved.
Nothing is this article grants permission for the occupation, obstruction, excavation, repair or alteration of
any street or right-of-way of the city, and any such use shall be subject to the consent of the city at its sole
discretion. Additionally, nothing in this article shall be construed as an assumption by the city, its officers and
employees of any responsibility to supervise construction activities, ensure adequate safety precautions by
contractors or to protect any owners or customers of any facilities located in, over, under, through, along or
across the rights-of-way or streets, or the owners of any property abutting, adjacent to or within the rights-ofway or streets from any damages caused to the facilities located in, or as the result of the construction
activities to, such rights-of-way or streets. Further, the city reserves the right to vacate any street or right-ofway at its sole discretion. If the city vacates or otherwise abandons a right-of-way or street, or any portion
thereof, the city, with or without notice to any permittee, may cancel any permits for such portion of a right-ofway or street without compensation or reimbursement to the permittee for any expenses associated with
moving any facilities located in such right-of-way or street, unless otherwise agreed in writing. The owner and,
as applicable, the contractor shall be solely liable and responsible for any and all injuries and/or damages
arising or resulting from any excavation, boring, trench, work or occupation of any street or right-of-way by or
on behalf of such owner or contractor.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 10, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-34. - City facilities and lands.
City facilities and lands shall not be altered, obstructed or occupied without the express written
permission of the city. Facilities not owned by the city shall not be located closer than ten feet laterally, and
shall not be located above or below any city-owned facility located underground, without express written
permission from the city. Additionally, no facilities may be located in, over, under, through, along or across any
parks, recreational land or other similar city-owned property, which is not a street or street right-of-way,
without the express written permission of the city.

184/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 6, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-35. - Permit and bond required for occupancy or construction activity on streets or rights-of-way.
It shall be unlawful for any owner or contractor, including his agents, servants, independent contractors or
employees, to occupy or obstruct any portion of the rights-of-way or streets, or to perform, or cause another
person to perform, any construction activity for any purpose in, over, under, through, along or across any
streets or rights-of-way without first having made all applications for permits and, when required, obtained all
permits for such occupancy or construction activity, together with a bond approved by the building official in
an amount determined as provided in this article, conditioned that the principal in such bond will discharge all
claim of every character arising from or occasioned by such occupancy or construction activity or by reason of
damages or injuries sustained by persons or property because of such occupancy, construction activity,
excavation or other such activity, and discharge all judgments obtained, together with all costs attached to
such judgments against the city by reason of any such claim, injury or damage sustained. During all such
activities, the contractor and owner carrying on any construction activity or excavation shall keep all streets
and rights-of-way adjacent to such construction activity or excavation in a clean, safe, orderly and
unobstructed condition, except as provided in this article, and shall restore all such streets, rights-of-way,
facilities and other structures damaged, altered or injured, in any way, to as good of a condition as they were
before the beginning of such activities. In lieu of providing a separate bond on each permit or construction
project, the owner or contractor may annually file a bond with the city providing the coverage to the city as
required in this section, which bond shall be and remain in effect for a term of one year, and shall be
applicable to all work performed by the owner or contractor within the city.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 3(B), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-36. - Franchise or license required for occupation of streets or rights-of-way for the providing of utility
service, etc.
It shall be unlawful for any person to use or occupy any street or right-of-way for the purpose of providing
abutting, adjoining or other property with any utility service, public service, data, voice or video transmission
service, cable television, taxi service or solid waste collection service without having first obtained a franchise
or license issued and approved by the city council, except as otherwise specifically provided by state law.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 3(C), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-37. - Work to cease immediately upon issuance of stop work order; commencing work.
(a)
Construction activity, excavation, obstruction or other work shall cease immediately upon the issuance of a stop
work order from the building o cial or any authorized law enforcement agent of the city.
(b)
It shall be unlawful to remove a stop work order placed upon a construction or work site until compliance with
this article has been accomplished. No work ordered to stop shall commence after issuance of the stop work
185/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

order until the violation has been corrected and the building o cial authorizes in writing the contractor to begin
work again.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 3(D), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-38. - Permit required for maintenance of an existing excavation.
It shall be unlawful and a violation of this article for any person, contractor or owner to maintain an
existing excavation within the city or work upon or assist in any way in the execution or operation of any such
excavation without an excavation permit having been issued by the city in accordance with this article.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 3(E), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-39. - Extension of building or facility over street or right-of-way.
It shall be unlawful for the owner of any building or property abutting on any street or right-of-way in the
city, or any tenant occupying such building or property, or any other person, to construct, build, operate or
maintain any building or facility, or part thereof, including a show window, which extends over any part of any
street or right-of-way.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 3(F), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-40. - Permit required to erect, install, remove, repair, build or alter utility posts, poles, towers or facilities.
It shall be unlawful to erect, remove, repair, install, build or alter, in any manner whatsoever, any posts,
poles, towers or other facilities that are erected for the purpose of bearing wires, cables or any other
transmission media, or to alter, in any manner, any existing posts, poles, towers or other facilities that are
used in connection with any telegraph, electric light, telephone, street railway, transmission media, radio or
similar purpose, and no posts, poles, towers or other facilities shall be erected, placed, kept or maintained
upon any streets or rights-of-way within the city, unless a written permit shall have first been obtained from
the building official to erect, install, remove, repair, build or alter, in any manner whatsoever, such posts,
poles, towers or other such facilities.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 3(G), 2-21-2000)

Cross reference—Utilities, ch. 94.
Sec. 78-41. - Violation; penalty.
Any person who shall violate any provision of this article, or shall fail to comply with any provision or
requirement of this article, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be liable for a fine not to
exceed $500.00. Each day the violation exists shall constitute a separate offense. Such penalty shall be in
addition to all other remedies provided in this article.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 12, 2-21-2000)
