h.
Any other pertinent data the building o cial may reasonably require.
(8)
Certi cate telecommunications provider. If the applicant for a permit purports to be a telecommunications
entity, in addition to the information required in subsections (1)—(7) of this section, the application shall include:
a.
Speci cations of the form of transmission media to be utilized;
b.
Design plans and speci cations concerning the transmission media;
c.
A copy of the certi cate of convenience and necessity, certi cate of operating authority or service provider
certi cate of operating authority from the public utilities commission authorizing local exchange telephone
service in the city;
d.
Veri cation of the current payment of all fees and right-of-way fees to the public utilities commission; and
e.
Other pertinent information as the building o cial may reasonably require.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(D), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-113. - Refusal of permit application.
The city council shall have the power and reserves the authority to refuse to issue a permit under this
subdivision, including a certificate of occupation, to any person, contractor or owner who has not complied
with this subdivision; has previously failed to comply with the terms, requirements or standards of any prior
permit issued for a similar project; or who has failed to provide insurance and a bond, as required.
Additionally, the city council shall have the power and reserves the authority to refuse any permit, or to modify
or amend any application for a permit, where the particular location, by reason of the nature of such particular
location, the character and value of the permanent improvements already erected on, or approximately
adjacent to, the particular location, and the use of which the land and surroundings, when in the building
official's opinion, or on appeal to the city council, in the city council's opinion, the excavating, operation of an
excavation or addition or alteration of any such proposed facility on such particular location or construction
activity would constitute a nuisance; be injurious to the public health; be a public hazard to the inhabitants as
a whole or to a substantial number of its inhabitants or travelers; be a disadvantage to the city in its planned
growth; or otherwise have a negative impact on the property values of property within the city.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(E), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-114. - Factors to be considered in review of permit application.

200/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

In considering and reviewing all plans submitted and applications for permits under this subdivision,
including a certificate of occupation, the building official shall be guided by the general purpose of orderly
municipal planning, avoiding conditions or the doing of any act constituting or creating a nuisance, health
hazard or endangering the public safety. As aids in accomplishing such purposes, the following points shall be
considered by the building official in reviewing permit applications; however, such aids shall not be exclusive
in the building official's consideration and ultimate recommendation:
(1)
The plan's compliance with all provisions of this article and other ordinances of the city;
(2)
The environmental impact of the development relating to the preservation of existing natural resources on the
site, and the impact on the natural resources of the surrounding properties and neighborhood;
(3)
The relationship of the development to adjacent uses in terms of harmonious use and design, maintenance of
property values and negative impacts;
(4)
The provision of a safe and e cient vehicular and pedestrian circulation system;
(5)
Surface water drainage and water drainage facilities of the excavation or installation, including soil and earth
erosion by water and wind;
(6)
Lateral supports of the excavation, including protection for existing buildings, facilities, streets and other
property to be a ected by such excavation;
(7)
Conditions in which the excavation, construction activity or installation are to be maintained, and safeguards to
be taken to prohibit the creation of a nuisance, health or safety hazard, attractiveness to children and features
provided to dispense with the endangering of lives and property of the public;
(8)
Proposed use or condition of land upon completion of the excavation process, construction activity or
installation;
(9)
Protection, access and encumbrance the installation, construction activity or excavation will have upon existing
facilities, and the location of the facilities in reference to the proposed excavation or installation, including the
size, quantity, location and permanent nature of the all facilities currently located, or proposed to be located, on
such site; and
(10)
Such other facts as may bear or relate to the coordinated, adjusted and harmonious physical development of
the city.

201/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

In arriving at the ultimate recommendation, the building official may attach such special
conditions to such permit as may be reasonably necessary to attain the overall purpose of this
article.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(F), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-115. - Appeals.
Appeals from the denial or granting of a permit under this subdivision, including a certificate of
occupation, shall be made to the city council.
(1)
If an application for a permit is refused, not later than ten days from the date of receiving notice of such refusal,
the applicant may appeal such permit refusal to the city council by directing a letter to the city council setting
forth the date of denial of the permit and the reasons the permit should be granted.
(2)
If the building o cial grants the permit, any citizen of the city who is, or may be, injured or damaged by the
granting of such permit may, within ten days of the recommendation to grant the permit, appeal the granting of
the permit to the city council by directing a letter to the city council, addressed to the o ce of the city secretary
at city hall, setting forth the date of the action by the building o cial and the reasons the person appealing
believes that he has been, or will be, injured by the action from which he is taking such appeal.
(3)
Upon the ling of such appeal, the right to operate under any such permit shall be suspended until nal
determination by the city council.
(4)
Upon receiving such notice of appeal, the city council shall direct the city secretary to place the appeal on the
city council's work agenda to be considered in the due order of city business. The city secretary shall then notify
the applicant and any other appellant as to the date and place where the city council will consider the appeal,
and shall publish a notice one time in the o cial newspaper at least ve days before the date when the city
council will consider the appeal.
(5)
Upon considering the appeal, the city council, by majority vote of all members in attendance and voting, shall
either grant or refuse to grant the permit. The decision of the city council shall be the nal decision and binding
on all parties.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(G), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-116. - Permit conditions.
All permits under this subdivision, including certificates of occupation, shall be issued based upon the
representations made within the permit application; information provided from the applicant; information
known to the building official and/or city council; and all plans and specifications submitted with the
202/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

application. Violations of any conditions of the permit or the general conditions listed in this section shall
constitute a forfeiture of all rights and privileges granted by the permit. The following general permit
conditions are in addition to the specific conditions identified in the specific permit:
(1)
Permit holders may not deviate from the plans and speci cations approved with the permit without prior
written permission from the building o cial and the amendment of such permit.
(2)
Permit holders must at all times comply with the requirements of this article and other applicable city
ordinances as well as state and federal laws.
(3)
No permit issued under the terms of this subdivision shall ever be transferred, sold, assigned or otherwise
disposed of in any manner to any other person without the written consent of the building o cial.
(4)
No permit shall be issued for less than the required permit fees.
(5)
Bonds must be maintained at all times as applicable to the permitted project.
(6)
All permit applications must contain complete and accurate information, plans and speci cations for the project.
(7)
No work shall be done under any permit issued under this subdivision, except as stated in the permit and in
compliance with state and federal laws, and the permittee shall ensure compliance at all times with such
requirements.
(8)
The building o cial shall at all times have authority to inspect the project site and stop all work not in
conformity with the permit, city ordinances or state or federal law. A copy of all permits shall be maintained at
the construction site and made available for inspection at all times when construction or installation work is
occurring. It shall be a violation of this article to interfere with a building o cial in the performance of his duties.
(9)
Any changes to the information provided in the application approved by the building o cial must be submitted
to the building o cial within 72 hours after the information has changed to amend the permit and, if such
changes are of a su cient degree to cause reconsideration, the building o cial shall have the same authority as
in an original application to approve or deny such amendments.
(10)
Approval of a permit does not constitute an agreement to undertake construction activities contrary to state,
federal or city requirements.
(11)
No permanent structure shall remain in the rights-of-way or streets without all proper permits and a current
occupation permit authorizing permanent occupation.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(H), 2-21-2000)
203/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 78-117. - Revocation of permit.
Any permit, including a certificate of occupation, issued under this subdivision may be cancelled if a notice
to cease operations or activities under such permit is issued and such notice is not immediately complied with.
Any such noncompliance shall constitute grounds for immediate revocation of any and all permits, or portions
thereof, for the project, when the following conditions exist:
(1)
A violation of any condition of the permit;
(2)
A violation of any provisions of this article or any other applicable ordinance or law relating to the speci cations
of the permit, excavation, construction or installation of the type of facility being installed, repaired, altered or
removed;
(3)
Failure to cease construction activities or correct such violations as directed by the building o cial; or
(4)
The existence of any condition, or the doing of any act, constituting or creating a nuisance or endangering the
lives or property of other persons.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(I), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-118. - Appeals from permit revocation or other action.
A permit holder, including a person having a certificate of occupation, pursuant to this article, who is
aggrieved by a revocation or any other action by the building official regarding such permit, may appeal to the
city council. The appeal shall be made by filing with the city secretary a written notice thereof within ten
calendar days from the date of the revocation of the permit or other action appealed from, including, but not
limited to, notices to repair and stop work orders. A fee of $100.00 shall be collected for processing the appeal.
The aggrieved person shall be given a hearing before the city council in due order of business, after which, the
city council may affirm, modify or overrule the building official's decision. Written notice of the time and place
of such hearing shall be served upon the permit holder at least five days prior to the date set for such hearing.
Notice of the hearing may be given by personal delivery to the permit holder or by deposit in the United States
mail in a sealed envelope with postage prepaid, addressed to such person at the address appearing in the
application or notice of appeal. All work shall be stopped at the construction site while the appeal is pending.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(J), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-119. - Franchise and license holders.
(a)
Utility service and public service providers having a current franchise or license agreement with the city shall be
governed by the terms of the franchise or license agreement and shall not be required to obtain an additional
204/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

certi cate of occupation or permit; post additional bond or insurance; and shall be exempt from paying any
permit fees when required by this subdivision to obtain a permit, but shall otherwise be subject to, bound and
governed by each and every term and provision of this article, except as explicitly exempted in the franchise or
license agreement.
(b)
Where the terms and conditions of the franchise or license agreement con ict with the provisions of this article,
the terms and conditions of the franchise or license agreement shall govern.
(c)
Unless otherwise exempted by a current franchise, license agreement or state law, the utility service or public
service provider shall:
(1)
Complete all applications for permits required in this subdivision, but shall not be required to pay the fees;
(2)
Provide the city with the information required in the application;
(3)
Coordinate with the city as directed by the building o cial based upon the size of the project and construction
activities;
(4)
Apply for all permits not less than ve working days prior to commencing any activity for which a permit must
be issued as required by this subdivision; and
(5)
Provide an estimation of the time for completion of each project.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 4(K), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-120. - Duties and responsibilities of permit holders, licensees and franchisees.
The contractor and owner, and any other person to whom a permit is issued under this subdivision, shall,
during the period for which the permit is issued and as provided in section 78-110, have all of the duties and
responsibilities identified in this section, other applicable city ordinances and as provided for in state and
federal law. The owner, his agents, assigns, contractors and subcontractors installing the facilities, shall
continually have the duties identified in this section for as long as facilities or property under the control of
any such owners, and any subsequent owners thereof, are located in the rights-of-way or streets, to perform
pursuant to the following terms:
(1)

Duty to barricade and protect. The owner, contractor and every person to whom a permit is issued under this
subdivision shall have a duty to ensure that each contractor, subcontractor, employee, agent or assignee:
a.
Prosecutes such work diligently and in a good and workmanlike manner; and
b.

205/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Safeguards and protects the public upon or using the streets, rights-of-way or other places where the work is
being performed, from accidents, injury or damage, by placing barriers, lights and other su cient safeguards,
including a watchman, if necessary, around all cuts, openings, excavations, installation sights and materials,
implements and tools used in connection with the construction activity, and shall conform to the provisions of
this article and all requirements of the building o cial during the prosecution and completion of such work. All
barricades and barriers shall be erected and maintained in compliance with accepted industry practices and
applicable safety standards. The owner and contractor shall be responsible for the costs and expenses of all
such barricades, barriers and watchmen.
(2)

Supervision of work. It shall be the duty of the owner, contractor and supervisor of the work site, who shall
cause any hole, cut, trench, excavation, mound, embankment, installation or other obstruction to be made in
any street or right-of-way, to carefully guard, or cause to be guarded, such hole, trench, excavation, mound,
embankment, installation or other obstruction while it may exist, and not to su er the hole, trench, excavation,
mound, embankment, installation or other obstruction to remain beyond a time reasonably su cient for the
completion of the construction or removal of the obstruction, and to repair the portion of such street, right-ofway or any facility or property a ected thereby so as to restore it to as good or better condition than existed just
previous to such activity.
(3)

Duty to promptly repair. It shall be the duty of the owner, contractor and supervisor of the work site, on whose
behalf the hole, trench, mound, excavation, construction activity, installation or other obstruction or intrusion
shall be made, or has been made, in the streets or rights-of-way of the city, to protect such hole, trench, mound,
excavation, construction activity, installation, obstruction or intrusion while such condition exists, and to
promptly repair it so as to leave the street or right-of-way in as good or better condition than existed before the
work. All facilities, streets, sidewalks or other structures or property damaged, altered or injured, in any fashion,
shall be restored with similar material and workmanship to that existing before it was damaged, altered or
injured through any actions of the owner, contractor or person employed in any fashion thereby. All work shall
be done to the satisfaction of the building o cial whose duty it shall be to inspect the work after it has been
done.
(4)

Removal and reconstruction where work is defective. All construction activities undertaken in the streets and
rights-of-way of the city are declared to be wholly subject to the exclusive control of the city, and in the opinion
of the building o cial, whenever any such work shall not have been duly completed within a reasonable time or
shall have been executed in a defective manner, whether because of bad workmanship or material or because
not true to lines, grades or speci cations required therefore, then upon written demand or notice from the
building o cial, such contractor or owner shall promptly remedy, complete or remove and reconstruct such
incomplete or defective construction, as the building o cial may require, and the provisions of this subsection
shall also comprehend and apply to all repairs, installations and maintenance activities. If the contractor or
owner shall fail or refuse to do remedy, complete or remove and reconstruct such incomplete or defective
construction within a reasonable time as speci ed in writing by the building o cial, then, if the building o cial
shall so order, such work may, at the expense of the owner and contractor, be completed, corrected or removed
206/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

and wholly or partially reconstructed by the city, or its instance, in such manner as, in the opinion of the building
o cial, may be necessary to make such work as good as originally required, and such work may be done by
contract or otherwise, under the provisions of this article and the direction of the building o cial.
(5)

Excavation. All excavations in the streets and rights-of-way are declared to be wholly subject to the rules,
regulations, directions and control of the city, and whenever, in the opinion of the building o cial, any such
work shall not be in compliance with this subsection, the permit and division 3 of this article, then, upon written
demand or notice from the building o cial, such owner and contractor shall promptly remedy, complete or ll
the excavation as the building o cial may require. All excavations made into any street, right-of-way or other
property shall be repaired to as good or better condition than such street, right-of-way or other property was in
prior to such excavation. Any excavation located in or over the rights-of-way or streets within the city shall and
does constitute a nuisance when such excavation is maintained or permitted to exist by any person in an
unwholesome or noxious condition; or in a manner by which stagnant water accumulates; or in a manner in
which water collects where it is possible and probable stagnant water accumulates; or in a manner in which
water collects where it is possible and probable mosquitoes will breed; or in a condition where rats could
harbor, or in a manner and condition constituting a breeding place for ies; or in a manner and condition where
lth, garbage, trash, debris or other discarded material accumulates and is deposited or is maintained or
permitted to exist in an unfenced, open condition, accessible to children or other members of the public; or is
maintained and worked in such a manner as to disturb, e ect or destroy the lateral support of or block or
otherwise impede tra c on any street, alley, road or right-of-way; or is maintained or permitted to exist in any
condition which constitutes a possible and probable medium of transmission of disease to or between human
beings; or to maintain or permit to exist any one or more of the conditions enumerated in this subsection.
(6)

Relocation of facilities. All persons placing facilities in the rights-of-way or streets, or owning, operating or
maintaining facilities in, over, under, through, along and across the rights-of-way or streets of the city, shall be
responsible for the relocation and costs of relocation of such facilities when the public health, safety or public
purpose requires relocation, or when such facilities are located in such rights-of-way or streets without a
permanent occupation permit, license or franchise as appropriate for the occupation.
a.

Permanent relocation. Upon 30 days' written notice by the city, the owner of a facility shall, at the owner's
expense, begin relocation of its facilities that are within a right-of-way or street, when deemed necessary by the
city for the public health or safety, or any public purpose, or to permit the widening, straightening or
improvement of a street, drainage, water or sewer project, or any other public works project. The notice by the
city may specify the new location for the owner's facilities along the rights-of-way or streets. The city shall have
the right to move any facilities within the rights-of-way or streets to cure or otherwise address a public health or
safety concern; to accomplish a public purpose; or to widen, straighten or improve a street, water or sewer
project or other public works project, or when no permit for occupation has been granted and the owner
refuses to move the facilities. The owner shall pay the costs and expenses of moving the facilities.
b.
207/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Temporary relocation. Upon 30 days' written notice by the city, the owner of a facility shall temporarily relocate
any portion of such facility within the rights-of-way or streets, at the owner's own expense, when deemed
essential by the city for the public's health and safety; or to permit construction activities of the city; water or
sewer projects; or any other public works project. The notice by the city shall specify the a ected areas where
the facilities are located and the area for temporary relocation of the owner's facilities along the rights-of-way or
streets. The city shall have the right to move any facilities within the rights-of-way or streets to cure or otherwise
address a public health or safety concern; to widen or straighten streets, water or sewer projects; or other
public works projects or construction activities where the owner refuses to move the facilities. The city shall
assess the reasonable costs and expenses of moving the facilities against the owner.
c.

Temporary removal of aerial wires. Upon the request of any person, the owner of aerial wires shall temporarily
remove, raise or lower aerial wires within the city to permit the moving of houses or other bulky structures. The
expense of such temporary removal, raising or lowering of wires shall be paid by the bene ted parties, and the
owner of the wires may require such payment in advance. The owner shall be given not less than ve business
days advance notice to arrange for such temporary wire changes.
(7)

Tra c interference. The owner and contractor shall endeavor to minimize disruptions to the e cient use of the
rights-of-way and streets by pedestrians and vehicular tra c, and the rights-of-way and streets shall not be
blocked for a longer period than shall be reasonably necessary to execute all construction, maintenance and/or
repair work. Prior to blocking any street or right-of-way the owner and/or contractor shall obtain a permit as
required in this subdivision.
(8)

Maintenance of facilities. The owner of any facility and a person holding a certi cate of occupancy, license or
franchise shall be responsible for ensuring the continued maintenance, repair, removal of any nuisance and
other such upgrades or repairs to maintain such facility in a safe and good workmanlike condition. Any
vegetative growth interfering with such facilities that is determined by the building o cial to be a nuisance shall
be removed, cut or cleared at the sole cost and expense of the owner of the facility or holder of the certi cate of
occupancy, license or franchise. Circumstances and conditions that impose a threat to the public health, safety
or welfare shall be promptly remedied by the owner, and a known emergency condition that exists and is
determined to require immediate attention so as not to reasonably allow for notice under this section may be
immediately abated by the city, and notice of the abatement and costs for the expenses incurred therefor will
be forwarded to the owner or holder of the certi cate of occupancy, franchise or license for reimbursement to
the city as required in section 78-67.
(9)

Tree trimming. The owner of facilities located within the rights-of-way or streets shall not trim any trees upon or
overhanging the rights-of-way without rst obtaining a permit as provided in this subdivision. All activities and
costs necessary to protect and preserve the facilities from damage due to trees shall be the responsibility of the
owner of such facilities.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, § 7(A—J), 2-21-2000)
208/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Secs. 78-121—78-140. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - SPECIAL PROVISIONS FOR CONSTRUCTION IN STREETS AND RIGHTS-OF-WAY
Sec. 78-141. - Permit.
The person in charge of construction in streets and rights-of-way shall have a copy of the permit for such
work, and its attachments, on the job at all times. Deviations to the approved permit must have prior approval
of the city. Utilities having a franchise with the city shall not be required to obtain permits for street cuts, but
shall coordinate with the city, as advisable, based on the size of the utility project and work.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(1), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-142. - Liabilities.
The city assumes no responsibility for conflict with existing utility lines, pipelines, highway appurtenances
or natural obstacles. Permittees, contractors and owners shall be responsible for the workmanship and any
damages by a contractor or subcontractor.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(14), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-143. - Existing utilities.
The exact location of any utilities or facilities that may conflict with a proposed installation should be field
verified by the installer during construction. The contractor will be responsible for verifying the horizontal and
vertical location of all affected facilities, whether by pot holing or hand digging, prior to any excavation or
boring.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(2), 2-21-2000)

Cross reference—Utilities, ch. 94.
Sec. 78-144. - Notice.
The permittee, contractor or subcontractor shall notify the building official not more than 24 hours after
any damage to other utilities, facilities or other appurtenances or property, whether public or private. Once a
permit has been issued, the permittee must notify the building official at least 48 hours prior to commencing
any work or construction activity permitted in such permit.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(13), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-145. - Weekends, nights and holidays.

209/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Construction work which is to be accomplished on weekends, nights or holidays will proceed at the
discretion of the building official, provided, that emergency work required to be undertaken on weekends,
nights, holidays and outside of normal business hours shall be undertaken and completed in compliance with
this article, and the contractor shall obtain a permit for such work on the first business day following the date
of such work.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(12), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-146. - Warning and protective devices; parking of employees' vehicles; storage of construction equipment
and materials.
(a)
Warning and protective devices, including agmen and watchmen, as necessary, shall be used to prevent
creation of a tra c hazard and to ensure the safety of the public as advisable and prudent considering the
scope of the work. When provided, such devices, agmen and watchmen shall be in accordance with the Manual
of Uniform Tra c Control Devices.
(b)
Parking of employees' cars and trucks on both sides of the pavement will be prohibited, and all such vehicles
shall be parked on one side of the road and, in no instance, closer than a minimum of eight feet from the edge
of the pavement.
(c)
All construction equipment and materials stored on city rights-of-way shall be limited to work in progress, and
stored in a manner and at such locations (a minimum of 30 feet from the nearest tra c lane) so as not to
interfere with the safe passage of tra c.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(3), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-147. - Method of construction.
Trench width shall be held to a minimum and backfilled to a density approximating that of the adjacent
soil in a manner satisfactory to the city. The fill material shall be installed in six-inch layers, and each layer shall
be compacted to 95 percent density. A six-inch concrete slab shall be placed over the trench and shall extend
12 inches on each side of the trench. The top of the slab shall be two inches below the top of the paving.
Alternatively, a six-inch layer of asphalt may be substituted and compacted to the finished grade of adjacent
pavement.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(4), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-148. - Concrete slab design.
Concrete slabs shall be reinforced with a six-inch by six-inch No. 6 wire mesh. The wire mesh shall be
properly supported throughout its placement to maintain its position approximately equidistant from the top
and bottom surface of the slab. Type III Portland cement (high early), making 2,500 psi concrete at three days,
210/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

or as directed by the city, shall be used. The slab shall be cured and closed to traffic as per state specifications.
(This section shall not apply if six inches of asphalt is substituted for the concrete.)
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(5), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-149. - Asphalt.
If asphalt is not substituted for concrete, as set forth in section 78-148, the concrete shall be thoroughly
cleaned and a tack coat of asphalt shall be applied, and then hot mix asphaltic concrete (type D), as specified
in item 340 of the Texas Transportation Commission Manual, shall be applied and compacted. If six inches of
asphalt is substituted for the concrete, the asphalt shall meet the specifications set forth in this section.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(6), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-150. - Access.
Ingress and egress at all private and public streets and drives will be provided at all times.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(7), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-151. - Right-of-way and street restorations.
All excess excavations, materials, supplies, etc. shall be removed from the right-of-way after installation is
complete, and the right-of-way shall be reshaped to its original section, including fertilizing, seeding and/or
sodding as may be required when existing grass has been disturbed.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(8), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-152. - Right-of-way and street damage.
The owner, contractor and permittee will be responsible for any damage to the rights-of-way or streets,
including, but not limited to, the pavement structure caused by settlement due to pavement cuts. Contractors
are responsible for obtaining exact facility locations from all utilities prior to excavation. Such liability shall
extend for a period of one year from the date the repair of such pavement cut is completed.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(9), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-153. - Excavation.
(a)
Prior to beginning any excavation, trenching or digging which may damage a pipeline, cable, wire or any other
such apparatus or facilities located in, over or under the streets or rights-of-way of the city, the owner or
contractor shall rst obtain a permit before excavation and contact all of the owners of the pipeline, cable, wire
or other facility, and determine if the proposed excavation will cause damage to such pipeline, cable, wire or
other facility.
(b)
211/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

If physical contact is made with, or damage or injury is suspected to, any pipeline, cable, wire or other such
apparatus or facility during any excavation, trenching, digging or other construction activity, the person or
contractor making the physical contact with, or suspecting the damage or injury to, the pipeline, cable, wire or
other apparatus or facility shall immediately contact the building o cial and the owner of the pipeline, cable,
wire or other apparatus or facility for any necessary inspections and repairs.
(c)
During any excavation, trenching or digging, if the person or contractor performing such excavating, trenching
or digging notices or suspects damage or injury to any lateral support to streets or other facilities in the rightsof-way, streets or adjacent property, such person shall immediately contact the city and, if applicable, the owner
of the property, for any necessary inspections and repairs.
(d)
All persons to whom permits may be granted to excavate the streets or rights-of-way shall, at their own cost and
expense, deliver to such place, as may be designated by the building o cial for such purpose, all such surplus
earth, dirt, stone, gravel or other material coming out of such excavation as shall be necessary for the purpose
of re lling the excavation.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(10), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 78-154. - Erosion.
Erosion control measures (i.e., silt fences) and advance warning signs, markers, cones and barricades
must be in place before any work begins. The permittee shall be responsible for stormwater management
erosion control that complies with city, state and federal guidelines. Requirements shall include, but not be
limited to, silt fencing around any excavation that will be left overnight; silt fencing in erosion areas until
reasonable vegetation is established; barricade fencing around open holes; and wire-backed silt fencing
around high erosion areas.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-6, exh. A(11), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 78-155—78-180. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - OBSTRUCTIONS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Secs. 78-181—78-205. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - IN CENTRAL BUSINESS DISTRICT
Sec. 78-206. - De nitions.
As used in this division, the following words and phrases have the meaning provided in this section.

212/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Commercial or business building means a building that was originally constructed and occupied for a
commercial, retail, or business use, or is currently used and occupied for commercial, retail, or business
use, or a building that has been rewired and modified to comply with the building code for commercial
occupancy and uses.

Goods and Merchandise means tangible personal property for sale. Motor vehicles for sale on a lot,
tract or parcel shall not be considered goods and merchandise.

Person shall mean and include an individual human, partnership, co-partnership firm, company,
limited liability partnership or other partnership or other such company, joint venture, joint stock
company, trust, estate, governmental entity, association or corporation or any other legal entity, or their
legal representatives, agents or assigns. The masculine gender shall include the feminine, the singular
shall include the plural where indicated by the context.

Right-of-way orROW means a strip of land publicly owned, that is used, set aside, dedicated, reserved
or platted as public street, highway, roadway, or sidewalk, and which shall include the surface of, and the
space above and below any and all present and future public thoroughfares, public utility easements,
public ways, public grounds, public waterways and without limitation by the foregoing, any other public
property within the corporate limits of the city. The usage of the term "right-of-way" or "ROW" shall mean
every right-of-way within the city that is shown on an official map of the city, Erath County, or the state, to
be separate and distinct from the lots or parcels adjoining such right-of-way and not included within the
dimensions or areas of such lots or parcels.
(Ord. No. 4-12-04-2, § 2, 4-12-2004)

Sec. 78-207. - Display or storage of good and merchandise regulated.
It shall be unlawful for any owner, occupant, or employee of a commercial or business building to store or
display any goods or merchandise upon any portion of a sidewalk or public right-of-way, or to otherwise allow
any goods or merchandise to occupy any portion of a sidewalk or public right-of-way, when the commercial or
business building is not open for business and accepting customers, in the areas of the city zoned as central
business district.
(Ord. No. 4-12-04-2, § 3, 4-12-2004)

Sec. 78-208. - Exceptions and exemptions.
(a)
The provisions of section 78-207 shall not apply to or a ect the following persons or sales:
(1)
Persons selling goods pursuant to an order or process of a court of competent jurisdiction;
(2)
Persons acting in accordance with their powers, authority and duty as a public employee or o cial;
213/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(3)
Persons selling goods and merchandise in connection with a religious organization or other non-pro t
organization, such as the Girl Scouts, Boy Scouts, or Eagle Scouts;
(4)
Persons and businesses participating in a special program or festival that is sponsored or permitted by the city
during the term of the special program or festival, for the purpose of promoting the local economy or
community.
(b)
The prohibitions in this article shall not apply to the movement of goods or merchandise over or across
sidewalks or public rights-of-way when such movement is made or accomplished for the purpose of transferring
such goods or merchandise from one point to another for a lawful purpose.
(c)
The prohibitions in this article shall not be construed to apply to merchandise dispensing units, e.g. soft drink
machines, newspaper racks, pay telephones, ATMs, etc., benches, dining tables, seating, ower boxes, planters,
or other objects that are not for sale, placed on the sidewalk, where at least four feet of sidewalk or other area
between the display and the travel lanes of any street or highway remains unobstructed for pedestrian use.
(Ord. No. 4-12-04-2, § 4, 4-12-2004)

Sec. 78-209. - Obstructing pedestrian tra c prohibited.
In no instance shall any person completely obstruct, block, or impede or allow to be obstructed, blocked,
or impeded, pedestrian traffic on a sidewalk or public right-of-way in the areas of the city zoned as central
business district, unless specifically permitted by the city.
(Ord. No. 4-12-04-2, § 5, 4-12-2004)

Sec. 78-210. - Compliance with city ordinances.
Any sales or displays or other occupancy of sidewalks or public rights-of-way permitted under section 78208(a) shall be conducted in compliance with all applicable fire, building, and other ordinances regulating
public health and safety.
(Ord. No. 4-12-04-2, § 6, 4-12-2004)

Sec. 78-211. - Penalty.
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article, or shall fail to comply therewith, or with
any of the requirements thereof, within the city limits shall be deemed guilty of an offense and shall be liable
for a fine not less than $100.00 and not to exceed the sum of $500.00. Each day the violation exists shall
constitute a separate offense. Such penalty shall be in addition to all the other remedies provided herein.
(Ord. No. 4-12-04-2, § 7, 4-12-2004)

Sec. 78-212. - Culpable mental state not required.
214/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Unless otherwise specifically required, allegations and evidence of culpable mental state are not required
for proof of an offense under this article.
(Ord. No. 4-12-04-2, § 8, 4-12-2004)

Chapter 82 - SUBDIVISIONS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 82-1. - De nitions.
For the purpose of this chapter, certain terms and words are defined in this section. Definitions not
expressly prescribed in this section are to be construed in accordance with their customary usage in municipal
planning and engineering practices. Any office referred to in this chapter by title means the person employed
or appointed by the city in that position or his duly authorized representative.

Alley means a minor public right-of-way which is used primarily for vehicular service access to the back or
the side of properties otherwise abutting on a street.

Building line means a line beyond which buildings must be set back from the street or road right-of-way
line on which the property fronts.

City means the City of Dublin, Texas, together with all of its governing and operating bodies.
City council or council means the duly elected governing body of the city.
City manager means the highest administrative official of the city or his designated representative.
City secretary means the person holding the position of city secretary, as appointed by the city council.
Commission means the planning and zoning commission.
Comprehensive plan means the official plan of the city and adjoining areas, adopted by the city council,
including all of its revisions. The comprehensive plan indicates the general locations recommended for various
land uses, transportation routes, public and private buildings, streets, parks and other public and private
developments and improvements.

Cul-de-sac means a street having only one outlet to another street and terminated on the opposite end by
a vehicular turnaround.

Dead-end street means a street, other than a cul-de-sac, with only one outlet.
Engineer means a person duly authorized under the provisions of the Texas Engineering Registration Act,
as amended, to practice the profession of engineering and is a registered professional engineer.

215/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Final plat means any plat of a lot, tract or parcel of land requested to be recorded of record in the county
deeds records.

Flood means a temporary rise in stream level that results in inundation of areas not ordinarily covered by
water.

Floodway means the channel of a watercourse and portions of the adjoining floodplain which are
reasonably required to carry and discharge the regulatory flood.

Lot means an undivided tract or parcel of land having frontage on a public street, and which is, or in the
future may be, offered for sale, conveyance, transfer or improvement as a building site, which is designated as
a distinct and separate tract.

Planning and zoning commission means the commission appointed by the city council to review and/or
recommend actions or policies relating to land use, zoning, building construction and codes.

Preliminary plat means any plat of a lot, tract or parcel of land that is not to be recorded of record, but is
only a proposed division of land for review and study by the city.

Replatting means the resubdivision of any part or all of any block of a previously platted subdivision,
addition, lot or tract.

Street means a public right-of-way, however designated, which provides vehicular access to adjacent land.
(1)

Collector street or secondary street means a street which is continuous throughout several residential districts
and is intended as a connecting street between residential districts and business districts or major streets.
(2)

Major street means the principal tra c thoroughfares continuous across the city, which are intended to connect
remote parts of the city, or areas adjacent thereto.
(3)

Residential street or minor street means a street which is primarily intended to serve tra c within a
neighborhood or limited residential district, and which is not necessarily continuous throughout several
residential districts.
(4)

Street width means the shortest distance between the lines which delineate the rights-of-way of a street, or
where curbs exist, from the back of curb to back of curb.

Subdivider means any person or his agent dividing, or proposing to divide, land so as to constitute a
"subdivision," as such term is defined in this section. The term "subdivider" shall be restricted to include only
the owner or equitable owner, or authorized agent of such owner or equitable owner, of land sought to be
subdivided.

216/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Subdivision or addition means any division of a lot, tract or parcel of land into two or more lots or sites for
the purpose, whether immediate or future, of sale or building development. Such term also includes
resubdivision or replatting of land, lots or tracts. Division of land in parcels of five acres or more for
agricultural purposes shall not be included within such definition, unless any such division of five acres or
more includes the planning or development of a new street or access easement.

Surveyor means a licensed state land surveyor or registered public surveyor as authorized by state
statutes to practice the profession of surveying.

Utility easement means an interest in land granted to the city, the public generally and/or a private utility
corporation for installing or maintaining utilities across, over or under private land, together with the right to
enter on such land with machinery and vehicles necessary for the maintenance of such utilities.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 2, 11-8-1999)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 82-2. - Interpretation and application.
In the interpretation and application of the provisions of this chapter, it is the intention of the city council
that the principles, standards and requirements provided for in this chapter shall be the minimum
requirements for the platting and developing of subdivisions in the city and its extraterritorial jurisdiction, and
where other ordinances of the city are more restrictive in their requirements, such other ordinances shall
control.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 1(1.100), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-3. - Intent.
The procedures and standards for the development, layout and design of subdivisions of land within the
corporate limits and extraterritorial jurisdiction of the city, as authorized by Local Government Code ch. 212,
are intended to:
(1)
Promote and develop the utilization of land in a manner so as to assure the best possible community
environment in accordance with the comprehensive plan of the city.
(2)
Guide and assist developers in the correct procedures to be followed, and inform them of the standards which
shall be required.
(3)
Protect the public interest by supervising the location, design, class and type of streets, sidewalks, utilities and
essential areas and services required.
(4)
Protect and promote the public health, safety and general welfare.
217/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 1(1.200—1.204), 11-8-1999)

State law reference—Municipal regulation of subdivisions and property development, V.T.C.A., Local
Government Code ch. 212.
Sec. 82-4. - Purpose and jurisdiction.
The city council adopts the regulations set forth in this chapter to control the subdivision of land within
the corporate limits and extraterritorial jurisdiction of the city in order to provide for the safe, orderly and
healthful development of the city and to secure adequate provisions for traffic, light, air, recreation,
transportation, water, drainage, wastewater and other public facilities.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 3, 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-5. - Violations; penalties; injunction.
(a)
In behalf of the city, when directed by the city council, the city attorney shall institute appropriate action in a
court of competent jurisdiction to enforce the provisions of this chapter or the standards referred to in this
chapter with respect to any violation of this chapter which occurs within any area subject to all, or a part of, the
provisions of this chapter.
(b)
In addition, any abutting owner or lessee or other person prejudicially a ected by the violation of the terms of
this chapter may resort to any court of competent jurisdiction for any writ, or to obtain such relief, either in law
or equity, as may be deemed advisable in these premises.
(c)
If any subdivision exists for which a nal plat has not been approved or in which the standards contained or
referred to in this chapter have not been complied with in full, the city council shall pass a resolution reciting the
facts of such noncompliance and failure to secure nal plat approval. When directed by the city council, the city
secretary or his designee shall cause a certi ed copy of such resolution under the corporate seal of the city to be
led in the deed records of the county. If full compliance and nal plat approval are secured after the ling of
such resolution, the city manager or his designee shall forthwith le an instrument in the deed records of the
county stating such compliance and approval.
(d)
Any person who shall violate or cause or permit any person to violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall
be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be ned an amount not to exceed $2,000.00 for each
o ense relating to re safety or public health and sanitation, and shall be ned not more than $500.00 for all
other o enses. Each day that such a violation shall exist is declared to be a distinct and separate o ense and
shall be punishable as such.
(e)
The city shall have and retain the right of injunctive relief against any person who is in the process of or about to
violate any section, paragraph or part of this chapter. Such right for injunctive relief shall exist independent of
218/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

any other penalty provisions of this chapter and not in lieu of such provisions. The right for injunctive relief is
essential to the city that it maintain an orderly, properly planned and properly engineered control over
subdivisions, thereby protecting the health, morals, safety and well being of the citizens and halting any attempt
by any person to in ict temporary or permanent injury on the general public by a failure to comply with the
terms of this chapter.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 12(12.100—12.500), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-6—82-40. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION
Sec. 82-41. - Filing fees.
Appropriate fees shall be paid upon submission of plats for consideration to the city. All fees shall be paid
prior to application deadlines, and shall not be refundable regardless of action taken by the city approving
authorities. The city council shall determine and revise the fee schedule, as needed.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 11, 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-42. - Variances.
A variance may be granted when a subdivider can show that a provision of this chapter would cause
unnecessary hardship if strictly adhered to. The city council may authorize a variance when, in the opinion of
the city council, a departure may be made from the requirements of this chapter without destroying the intent
of this chapter. A written request for such a variance should accompany preliminary and final plat submission.
The planning and zoning commission will review each variance request and make recommendations on such
request to the city council.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 9, 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-43. - Reservations.
(a)

Permitted purposes. No land contained in a proposed subdivision shall be reserved for any use other than a use
permitted by the city council in its approval of the subdivision, if approval is granted.
(b)

Parks and playgrounds. The subdivider shall be required to dedicate park sites for public use to the city on the
basis of eight percent of the acreage to be divided. The required dedication may be met by a payment of money
in lieu of land, when permitted or required by the city council, at a rate of $400.00 per acre to be divided.
(c)

Park land dedication fund.
(1)

219/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

There is established a special fund for the deposit of all sums paid in lieu of land dedication under this
subsection (c) or any preceding ordinance, which fund shall be known as the "park land dedication fund."
(2)
The city shall account for all sums paid in lieu of land dedication under this subsection (c) with reference to the
individual plats involved. Any funds paid for such purposes must be expended by the city within ten years from
the date such sums are received by the city for acquisition or development of a neighborhood park.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 8(8.100—8.202), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-44—82-70. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - PLATS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Secs. 82-71—82-90. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - PRELIMINARY PLATS
Sec. 82-91. - Preapplication conference.
(a)
Prior to the preparation of a preliminary plat, the subdivider should meet with the city manager to become
familiarized with the city's comprehensive plan, utility policies, street policies, other ordinances, development
policies and fees, and any other pertinent factors, such as, but not limited to, sidewalks, curbs and gutters,
drainage study, park dedication and alleys relating to the proposed subdivision plans.
(b)
If the property to be platted extends into the city's extraterritorial jurisdiction, the subdivider shall be informed
that he should consult also with the county judge or his designated appointee on county subdivision
regulations.
(c)
The subdivider may be represented by his land planner, engineer or surveyor.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 4(4.100—4.103), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-92. - Administrative function.
(a)
In accordance with an understanding of the preapplication conference as provided for in section 82-91, the
subdivider shall submit a preliminary plat of the entire area being subdivided to the city secretary's o ce not
less than 20 days prior to the planning and zoning commission meeting.
(b)
The city manager will certify that all required information for platting procedures are submitted. Incomplete
submittals will be returned to the subdivider prior to further processing by the city.
220/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(c)
The city secretary shall mail a notice, by registered or certi ed mail, to each property owner within 200 feet of
the property to be subdivided, stating that a subdivision proposal is pending before the planning and zoning
commission. The notice shall state the date, place and time of the meeting at which the subdivision or
resubdivision proposal will be considered.
(d)
The city manager shall review the preliminary plat in accordance with ordinance requirements and prepare a
report for the planning and zoning commission meeting to assist in their understanding of the plat proposal.
When necessary, in the opinion of the city manager, a request will be made of the city's engineer, public works
director, subdivider's engineer, telephone company, electrical company or any other profession to obtain
information concerning the preliminary plat for the planning and zoning commission meeting.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 4(4.200—4.214), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-93. - Function of city council.
(a)
After receiving the recommendation of the planning and zoning commission on a preliminary plat, the city
council shall review the preliminary plat, and take action on the preliminary plat within 30 days of the planning
and zoning commission meeting. The preliminary plat may either be approved as submitted, conditionally
approved with modi cations or disapproved.
(b)
Action on the preliminary plat by the city council shall be put in writing, certi ed to by the mayor and attached to
three copies of the preliminary plat. One copy of the preliminary plat shall be returned to the subdivider, and
two copies shall be retained in the city secretary's o cial les.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 4(4.220—4.222), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-94. - Subdivider's understanding of action taken.
(a)
Approval or conditional approval with modi cation of the preliminary plat does not constitute acceptance of the
subdivision, but provides authority to proceed with the preparation of the nal plat. Any work done on the
subdivision before the nal plat is accepted by the city and authorization given to start construction is done at
the risk of the subdivider.
(b)
Approval or conditional approval with modi cations of the preliminary plat expires at the end of six months,
unless a nal plat has been submitted to the city for processing. If a written request from the subdivider is
received prior to the end of the six-month period, the city council may grant an extension for up to 180
additional days; however, only one such extension shall be granted.
(c)
The subdivider will have to resubmit a preliminary plat to be processed through the planning and zoning
commission if the rst preliminary plat was disapproved or the time to submit a nal plat has expired.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 4(4.230—4.233), 11-8-1999)
221/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 82-95. - Preparation requirements.
(a)
The preliminary plat shall be submitted by the subdivision to the city at least 20 days before the meeting of the
planning and zoning commission, and shall contain the following:
(1)
A reproducible tracing and six copies of the preliminary plat;
(2)
Any existing or proposed deed restrictions;
(3)
A letter requesting the city to process the preliminary plat;
(4)
A listing of adjacent property owners and other property owners within 200 feet of the property to be
subdivided, with the addresses of such persons as recorded by the county clerk;
(5)
A check in the amount of the ling fee.
(b)
The preliminary plat shall be drawn to a scale of one inch to 200 feet or larger on sheets of a maximum size of
24 inches by 36 inches, regardless of the size subdivision, and shall show or be accompanied by the following
information:
(1)
The name of the subdivision, which shall not duplicate an existing or pending subdivision.
(2)
A complete legal description, by metes and bounds, of the land being subdivided.
(3)
The total acreage and total number of lots and blocks within the subdivision.
(4)
The name of the owner and his address, unless such address is given in the letter of transmittal. If the owner is
a partnership, corporation or other legal entity other than an individual, the name of the responsible individual,
such as the president or vice-president, must be given.
(5)
The name of the registered engineer, registered public surveyor or land planner responsible for preparing the
preliminary plat.
(6)
North point, and north is to be at the top of the sheet, if possible.
(7)
Date, and each revision shall bear a new date.
(8)

222/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Boundaries of the subdivision which shall be drawn in very heavy lines and shall include overall dimensions and
bearings.
(9)
Adjacent right-of-way lines of the proposed subdivision shall be drawn with dashed lines.
(10)
A tie to an original corner of the original survey of which such land is a part.
(11)
Name and location of adjacent subdivisions, streets, easements, pipelines, watercourses, etc., and the property
lines and name of adjoining property owners in unsubdivided tracts.
(12)
Existing and proposed topographic and plain metric features within the subdivision, including water sources and
ravines, high banks, width or existing or proposed easements, contour lines at two-foot intervals, and any other
physical features pertinent to the subdivision.
(13)
Existing transportation features within the subdivision, including the location and width of rights-of-way, streets,
alleys and easements.
(14)
Proposed features, including the location, width, surfacing and name of streets, approximate width and depth of
all lots, alleys and easements, and schematic plans and outline speci cations for drainage, sanitary facilities and
utilities.
(15)
Designation of any sites for special uses, including churches, wastewater disposal plants, water plants, business
industries or other special land uses. If the proposed use is unknown, it shall be designated as unrestricted.
Where a proposed site in the area taken in by a proposed addition or subdivision is planned for a school, park
or public building, such site shall be reserved on the preliminary plat for the proposed facility.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 4(4.240—4.242), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-96. - Combination preliminary and nal plat.
At his option, the subdivider may elect to combine the preliminary plat and final plat when the land
proposed to be subdivided or resubdivided meets the following conditions and requirements:
(1)
Such land abuts upon a street of adequate width and is situated so that no additional streets, alleys, easements
or other public property are required in order to meet the requirements of this chapter.
(2)
The perimeter of the tract being subdivided has been surveyed and marked on the ground and a plat thereof
prepared and led with the city council and the nearest corner of each lot or parcel of such proposed
subdivision is within 200 feet of a known corner which is adequately marked by a concrete monument or iron
stake.
(3)
223/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The topography of the tract and surrounding land is such that no regard need be given in such subdivision to
drainage, or, where drainage facilities are required arrangements have been made for the construction of such
facilities.
(4)
The utilities, has required in this chapter, are in place to serve each parcel or lot of such subdivision or
resubdivision, or arrangements to provide such utilities have been made.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 4(4.500—5.401), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-97—82-120. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - FINAL PLATS
Sec. 82-121. - Administrative action upon receiving submittal.
(a)
Upon approval or conditional approval of a preliminary plat, the subdivider shall provide one reproducible
tracing and six legible white print copies of a nal plat to the city secretary's o ce that incorporates all changes,
directions and additions imposed by the city. The submittal shall not be less that 20 days prior to the planning
and zoning commission meeting, but within the time period established by the preliminary plat approval.
(b)
The city manager or his designated representative will certify that all required information for the platting
procedure is submitted. Incomplete submittals will be returned to the subdivider prior to further processing by
the city.
(c)
The city secretary shall mail a notice, by registered or certi ed mail, to each property owner within 200 feet of
the property to be subdivided, stating that a subdivision proposal is pending before the planning and zoning
commission. The notice shall state the date, place and time of the meeting at which the subdivision or
resubdivision proposal will be considered.
(d)
The city manager shall review the nal plat in accordance with ordinance requirements and prepare a report for
the planning and zoning commission meeting to assist in their understanding of the plat proposal. When
necessary, in the opinion of the city manager, a request will be made of the city's planner, engineer, public
works director, subdivider's engineer, telephone company, electrical company or any other profession to obtain
information concerning the nal plat for the planning and zoning commission meetings.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 5(5.100—5.104), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-122. - Function of city council.
(a)
Upon receipt of a recommendation from the planning and zoning commission, the city council shall review the
nal plat and, within 30 days following the planning and zoning commission meeting, shall take action on the
224/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

nal plat as submitted or modi ed by recommending one of the following:
(1)
Final plat approval;
(2)
Final plat approval with conditions;
(3)
Disapproval of the nal plat.
(b)
Action on a nal plat by the city council shall be put in writing, certi ed to by the mayor and shall be attached to
the three copies of the nal plat. One copy shall be returned to the subdivider and two copies shall be retained
in the city secretary's o cial les.
(c)
In the event of disapproval of the nal plat, the city may withhold all city improvements of any nature, including
the furnishing of wastewater and water facilities and services, from all additions which have not been approved
as provided by law, and further permits may not be issued by the building o cial on any piece of property other
than an original or a resubdivided lot in a duly approved and recorded subdivision.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 5(5.200—5.203), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-123. - Processing approved nal plats.
(a)
The subdivider shall direct his engineer to design, stake and supervise the construction of facilities in
accordance with approved plans and speci cations and the regulations set forth in this chapter. The city will
inspect the construction to be undertaken.
(b)
The subdivider shall direct his contractors to construct all improvements as identi ed in the approved
engineering plans and to provide the city with a one-year maintenance bond in the amount of ten percent of the
construction contact price, along with three white print sets and one sepia set of as-built plans to the city council
for acceptance of the title, use and maintenance of the improvements.
(c)
Upon completion of such improvements and compliance with the regulations set forth in this chapter, the city
manager shall present as-built plans to the city council for acceptance of the title, use and maintenance of the
improvements.
(d)
No nal plat shall be led with the county clerk unless and until all requirements of the subdivision regulations
set forth in this chapter have been complied with and such stipulations as may be set by the city council have
been met.
(e)
Final plat approval will expire six months after approval by the city council unless the plat has been led for
record. The subdivider may apply in writing for an extension of such time period prior to the end of such six225/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

month period. At the discretion of the city council, such period may be extended for six months, but not beyond
a total of one year.
(f)
Within 30 days after the city council's approval of a nal plat the city secretary shall review such nal plat for the
proper signature and the ful llment of all stipulations established by the city council. If every item is in order
and complied with, the city secretary shall record the nal plat at the county clerk's o ce.
(g)
For nal plats that are outside the corporate limits of the city, but within its extraterritorial jurisdiction, the city
secretary shall forward a copy of the nal plat to the county judge for action and approval by the
commissioner's court prior to recording a plat with the county clerk.
(h)
The city secretary shall retain one copy of the nal plat recorded in the county records for the city les.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 5(5.300—5.308), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-124. - Preparation requirements.
(a)
The nal plat shall be drawn in India ink on tracing cloth, mylar or comparable substitute, on sheets of 24 inches
by 36 inches, or multiple thereof, and to a scale of one inch to 100 feet. Where more than one sheet is required,
an index sheet of a maximum size of 24 inches by 36 inches shall be led, showing the entire subdivision at a
reduced scale.
(b)
A title, including the name of the subdivision; the name of the land owners; the name of the registered engineer
or registered public surveyor responsible for the preparation of the nal plat; the scale and location of the
subdivision with reference to an original corner of the original survey of which such land is a part; the date,
north point and total acres in the subdivision shall be included on the nal plat.
(c)
The certi cate of the registered engineer or licensed surveyor who surveyed, mapped and monumented the
land shall be placed on the face of the nal plat, as follows:

THE STATE OF TEXAS:
KNOW ALL MEN BY THESE PRESENTCE:
COUNTY OF ERATH

That I, ____________
, do certify that I prepared this plat from an actual and accurate on-the-ground survey of the land and that the
corner monuments shown thereon were properly placed under my personal supervision, in accordance with
the subdivision regulations of the City of Dublin, Texas.

Signature and Seal of Registered Professional Engineer or
Surveyor

(d)
A certi cate of ownership and dedication to the public of all streets, easements, alleys, parks, playgrounds or
other dedicated public uses, signed and acknowledged before a notary public by the owners and any holders of
liens against the land, shall be submitted with the nal plat.
(e)
An accurate on-the-ground boundary survey of the property, with bearings and distances, and showing the lines
of all adjacent streets, easements and alleys with their names and widths shall be submitted with the nal plat.
Streets, alleys and lot lines in adjacent subdivisions shall be shown dashed. All necessary data to reproduce the

railroads, width of streets, alleys and easements to be retained and other physical features deemed pertinent to

engineering data:
(1)
Streets. Complete curve data (delta, length of curve, point of curvature, point of reverse curvature, point of
tangency) shown on the centerline or on each side of the street; length and bearing of all tangents; dimensions
from all angle points of the curve to an adjacent lot line.
(2)
Watercourses and easements. The distance to be provided along the side lot lines from the front lot line or the
high bank of a stream; the traverse line to be provided along the edge of all large watercourses, in a convenient
location, preferably along a utility easement if paralleling the drainage easement or stream.

Lot and block lines and numbers of all proposed lots and blocks, with complete dimensions, for front, rear and
side lot lines shall be provided on the nal plat.
(i)
Building setback lines shall be shown on all lots on the nal plat.
(j)
Two sets of plans and speci cations, certi ed to by a registered professional engineer, shall be provided for the
installation of water, wastewater, paving and drainage, and such plans and speci cations must be approved by
the city building o cial prior to the beginning of any construction of the subdivision.
(k)
227/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

A receipt showing that all taxes have been paid shall be submitted with the nal plat.
(l)
The city council shall be satis ed that the subdivider will be in a nancial position to install, or cause to be
installed, at his own cost, risk and expense, all of the improvements required in this chapter. The city council
may require such security as, in its sole absolute discretion, it may deem best in order to inure the orderly
development within any subdivision, speci cally including, but not limited to, a performance bond equal to the
estimated cost of the improvements. It is expressly understood that, as a condition to the approval of such
subdivision, no sales will be completed until all utilities are installed and all other improvements required by this
chapter are made within the block in which such lot is contained.
(m)
The city council shall review the nal plat, and when it is satis ed that all conditions and requirements have
been met, the city council shall approve such plat using the following format:
"City of Dublin
