ARTICLE IV. - STANDARDS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 82-161. - Engineer.
The subdivider shall retain the services of an engineer registered in the state, whose seal shall be placed
on each sheet of the subdivision drawing, and who shall be responsible for the design and inspection as set
forth in this article. Performance bonds and maintenance bonds shall be submitted for 100 percent of the cost
of all work and for the performance of all materials and equipment for a period of two years after acceptance
of the subdivision by the city.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.100), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-162. - Easements.

228/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Where necessary to adequately serve the subdivision with public utilities, easements shall be retained by
the subdivider for poles, wires, conduits, storm sewers, wastewater lines, water lines, open drains, gas lines or
other utilities. Such easements may be required across part of lots (including side lines) other than along
boundary lines if, in the opinion of the city council, such easements are needed.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.800—6.801), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-163. - Utility placement.
All utilities shall be placed underground. The placement of overhead electrical and telephone utilities will
be considered on a case-by-case basis.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.960), 11-8-1999)

Cross reference—Utilities, ch. 94.
Sec. 82-164. - Survey requirements.
(a)
Monuments consisting of one-half-inch iron pipe or one-half-inch reinforced steel or larger, 24 inches in length,
encased in six-inch concrete, shall be placed at all corners of the block lines and at the point of intersection of
curves and tangents of the subdivision.
(b)
At least one benchmark for each subdivision shall be permanently installed in an approved manner, with the
location and the elevation as shown on the plat. Permanent benchmarks shall be ve-foot long concrete posts,
six inches in diameter, with the top at least 12 inches below nished grade.
(c)
Lot markers shall be metal, at least 24 inches in length, placed at each corner of all lots, ush with the average
ground elevation, or they may be countersunk, if necessary, to avoid being disturbed.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 7(7.100—7.300), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-165. - As-built drawings.
The engineer representing the subdivider shall present to the city council, reproducible complete as-built
plans for all paving, drainage structures, water lines and sewer lines, within 30 days after completion of each
contract.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 10, 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-166—82-190. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - STREETS AND ALLEYS
Sec. 82-191. - In general.
229/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The subdivider shall be responsible for constructing paved streets within the subdivision, subject to the
conditions contained in this division. When required by the city council, curbs and gutters shall be subject to
the conditions contained in this division.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.200), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-192. - Arrangement.
Unless otherwise approved by the city council, provision shall be made for the extension of major streets
through any new subdivision. Collector streets shall be provided as required by the city council for the
circulation of traffic through the subdivision and the connection thereof to the major streets. Adequate minor
streets shall be provided to accommodate the subdivision. Off-center street intersections with streets in
adjacent subdivisions should be avoided. All major and collector streets shall be continuous or in alignment
with existing streets unless variations are deemed advisable by the city council due to topography and
requirements of traffic circulation.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.201), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-193. - Plans and speci cations.
Plans and specifications for required street improvements shall be submitted to and approved by the city
building official prior to the time the work on such improvements is commenced. Any improvement made
shall be subject to the approval and acceptance of the city building official. The subdivider shall pay the entire
cost of street improvements. Curbs and gutters shall conform to class A concrete in accordance with Texas
Highway Department Standard Specifications. All streets shall be surfaced with one of the following surface
types:
(1)
Six inches of compacted depth of exible base to 96—100 percent maximum density in accordance with the
AASHO T99 and 1½ inches of compacted asphaltic concrete in accordance with Texas Highway Department
Standard Speci cations for Road and Bridge Construction, January 2, 1972, hereinafter referred to as the "THD
speci cations."
(2)
Five inches of compacted reinforced Portland cement concrete (class A) in accordance with THD speci cations.
(3)
Six inches of compacted asphaltic concrete in accordance with THD speci cations.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.202), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-194. - Testing of materials.

230/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The subdivider shall have all material for street improvements tested by an independent commercial
testing agency to determine that each street in the subdivision meets the requirements and specifications set
forth in this division. The results of such tests are to be presented to the city council prior to the final approval
of any subdivision. The costs of securing the tests and subsequent results are to be borne wholly by the
subdivider.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.203), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-195. - Width.
Major streets in a subdivision shall have a minimum right-of-way of 80 feet and a minimum paving width
of 42 feet. Collector streets shall have a minimum dedicated right-of-way of 60 feet and a minimum paving
width of 38 feet. Minor or residential streets shall have a minimum dedicated right-of-way of 50 feet and a
minimum paving width of 30 feet. Major streets having a right-of-way width of less than 100 feet shall be
increased to a 100-foot right-of-way for a distance of 150 feet on either side of any intersection with another
major street. The right-of-way shall be gradually and uniformly increased from the regular right-of-way width
to a 100-foot width within an additional 150 feet.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.204), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-196. - Curves.
Complete curve data (delta, length of curve, radius, point of curvature, point of reverse curvature, point of
tangency) shown on the centerline or on each side of the street, length and bearings of all tangents and
dimensions from all angle points of curve to an adjacent side lot line shall be provided.
(1)

Major streets. Curves in major streets are to have a centerline radius of 2,000 feet or more. Exceptions to such
standard may be granted only by the city council.
(2)

Collector streets. Curves in secondary or collector streets are to have a centerline radius of 800 feet or more.
Exceptions to such standard may be granted by the city council.
(3)

Minor or residential streets. Curves in minor or residential streets are to have a minimum centerline radius of
150 feet.
(4)

Reverse curves. Reverse curves are to be separated by a minimum tangent of 100 feet, unless they are
connected by spirals.
(5)

Street jogs and street intersections. Street jogs and street intersections shall not be closer than 125 feet.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.205), 11-8-1999)

231/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 82-197. - Intersections.
(a)
All major, secondary or minor streets shall intersect at a 90-degree angle. Variations to such standard must be
approved by the city council.
(b)
Curbs at acute angle intersections approved by the city council shall have a minimum 25-foot radii at acute
corners.
(c)
Each new street intersection with, or extending to meet, an existing street, shall be tied to the existing street on
the centerline.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.206), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-198. - Culs-de-sac.
(a)
Dead-end streets may be platted where the city council deems it advisable and where the land being subdivided
adjoins property not being subdivided, in which case, the streets shall be carried to the boundaries thereof.
Streets designed to be permanently dead-end streets shall not be longer than 600 feet and shall be provided at
the closed end with a paved cul-de-sac at least 80 feet in diameter on a street right-of-way of at least 100 feet in
diameter.
(b)
Temporary turnarounds are to be used at the end of a street more than 400 feet long that will be extended in
the future, and the following should be placed on the plat:
"Cross-hatched area is temporary easement for turnaround until street is extended (direction) in
a recorded plat."
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.207), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-199. - Partial or half streets.
Partial or half streets may be provided where the city council feels that a street should be located on a
property line.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.208), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-200. - Private streets.
Private streets are prohibited.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.201), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-201. - Street names.

232/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

New streets shall be named so as to provide continuity of name with existing streets and so as to prevent
conflict with identical or similar names in other parts of the city.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.209), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-202. - Street lighting.
Street lighting shall be provided by the subdivision developer and shall conform to the most current
edition of the Illuminating Engineering Society Handbook. Lighting levels shall be as recommended for very
light traffic in residential areas, medium traffic on feeder streets and heavy traffic on thoroughfares.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.930), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-203. - Street signs and water meter boxes.
All street signs and water meter boxes shall be provided and installed by the subdivision developer, and
must meet the specifications set forth by the city.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.940), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-204. - Alleys.
(a)

Pavement type. All alleys shall be paved with materials conforming to street paving requirements.
(b)

Width. A minimum paved width of ten feet and a minimum right-of-way of 20 feet shall be required for all alleys.
(c)

Drainage. Adequate drainage shall be provided within the paved section or by swells to drain all lots to streets
without drainage easements through lots, where possible. The depth of swell shall be as required for drainage
with a minimum longitudinal slope of one-half of one percent toward a street or drainage easement.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.300—6.303), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-205—82-230. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - SIDEWALKS
Sec. 82-231. - When required.
In the opinion of the city council, when pedestrian traffic constitutes a safety issue, sidewalks will be
required.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.401), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-232. - Requirements.
233/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The following requirements shall be applicable where sidewalks are provided:
(1)
Sidewalks shall be located on the subdivision side of all thoroughfares and collector streets adjacent to a
subdivision.
(2)
Sidewalks shall be located on both sides of all internal thoroughfare, collector and local streets of a subdivision.
(3)
Such additional sidewalks shall be provided as the subdivider may desire.
(4)
Sidewalks shall be placed in the right-of-way and shall be a minimum of four feet in width. Sidewalks serving
commercial areas may be placed at the back of the curb if they are designed to be ve feet in width.
(5)
Sidewalks shall be constructed with a minimum pavement thickness of four inches of reinforced concrete.
Sidewalks shall have a minimum cross slope of one-fourth inch per foot for drainage.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.400), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-233—82-250. - Reserved.
DIVISION 4. - LOTS, BLOCKS AND BUILDING LINES
Sec. 82-251. - Lot standards.
Standards applicable to residential lots in a subdivision shall be as follows:
(1)

Size. Minimum lot sizes shall be provided in the city's zoning ordinance, as set forth in chapter 102 of this Code.
(2)

Facing.
a.

Street frontage. Each lot shall be provided with the minimum frontage on an existing or proposed public street
required by the zoning ordinance, as set forth in chapter 102 of this Code.
b.

Double front. Double front lots are prohibited, except where backing on major thoroughfares.
c.

Front facing. Wherever feasible, each lot should face the front of a similar lot across the street. In general, an
arrangement placing adjacent lots at right angles to each other should be avoided.
(3)

Numbering. All lots shall be numbered consecutively within each block. Lot numbering may be cumulative
throughout the subdivision if the numbering continues from block to block in a uniform manner that has been
234/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

approved on an overall preliminary plat.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.500—6.503), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-252. - Block standards.
Standards applicable to blocks in subdivisions shall be as follows:
(1)

Length.
a.
Residential blocks shall not be longer than 1,200 feet when measured along the center of the block, and not
shorter than 600 feet.
b.
Maximum block length along a major street shall be 1,600 feet, except under special conditions and upon
approval of the city council.
(2)

Width. Blocks shall be wide enough to allow two tiers of lots of at least minimum depth, except under special
conditions and upon approval of the city council.
(3)

Numbering. Blocks shall be numbered consecutively within the subdivision and/or sections of an overall plat as
recorded.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.600—6.603), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-253. - Building line standards.
Subdivision building lines shall be as provided in the city's zoning ordinance as set forth in chapter 102 of
this Code.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.700), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-254—82-270. - Reserved.
DIVISION 5. - WATER AND SEWER
Subdivision I. - In General
Sec. 82-271. - Flood regulations.
The city shall review each proposed subdivision to assure:
(1)
All such proposals are consistent with the need to minimize ood damage.
235/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(2)
All public utilities and facilities, such as wastewater, gas, electrical and water systems, are located, elevated and
constructed to minimize or eliminate ood damage.
(3)
Adequate drainage is provided so as to reduce exposure to ood hazards.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.950), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-272—82-285. - Reserved.
Subdivision II. - Drainage and Storm Sewers
Sec. 82-286. - Proof of adequate drainage required.
Any land which, in its natural state, is subject to a 100-year flood or which cannot be properly drained shall
not be subdivided, resubdivided or developed until it is demonstrated to the satisfaction of the city council
that the construction of specific improvements proposed by the developer can be expected to yield a usable
building site. Adequate drainage shall be provided within the limits of the subdivision. The protection of
adjoining property shall be considered in the review of submitted plans.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.900), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-287. - Size.
Sizing of inlets, storm sewers, outfalls, culverts and drainage ditches shall be based on the following:
(1)

Design storm. The design storm shall be based on rainfall intensity-frequency data as published in the most
recent publication by the department of agriculture. The interior drainage system shall be designed for a storm
with a frequency of occurrence of one in ve years.
(2)

Runo computations. Runo computations shall be by standard engineering procedures.
(3)

Sewers. Sewers shall be sized to carry the discharge derived from the formula as set forth in subsection (2) of
this section. Capacity of storm sewers shall be determined by the use of Mannings Formula, on the basis of
hydraulic gradients rather than physical of the pipe. The minimum size of a storm sewer shall be 18 inches.
Storm sewers will be required where subsurface conditions indicate a potential for seepage or underground
ow as determined by the public works director.
(4)

Inlets. Where storm sewers are required, inlets shall be spaced so that the maximum travel distance of water in
a gutter will not exceed 600 feet. Inlets will be sized using an allowable capacity of one cubic foot per second,
per foot of opening for a throat height of ve inches.
(5)
236/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Ditches. Ditches shall be sized to carry the runo (Q) derived from the formula as set forth in subsection (2) of
this section.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.901), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-288. - Design.
Design of storm sewers, outfalls, culverts and drainage ditches shall conform to the following
requirements:
(1)

Manholes. Manholes (inlets or junction boxes) shall be provided at all changes in grade or alignment, sewer
intersections and at a maximum of 1,000 feet on straight lines. If monolithic, reinforced concreted sewer lines
are used, a manhole shall not be required where leads from inlets intersect the main sewer. The design of
manholes shall conform to the standard speci cations as approved by the city council.
(2)

Inlets. The design of inlets shall conform to standard speci cations as approved by the city council.
(3)

Pipe. All pipe for storm drains shall be reinforced concrete pipe (RCP), ASTM C76, class 3 with a minimum
diameter of 18 inches. Where, in the opinion of the building o cial, added strength of pipe is needed for tra c
loads over minimum cover or for excessive height of back ll, concrete pipe shall be ASTM C14 extra-strength or
ASTM C76, class IV or class V. Pipe shall have a minimum cover of not less than one foot over the top of pipe.
Monolithic, reinforced concrete sewers may be used for storm sewers 36 inches and larger.
(4)

Ditches. Where approved by the city council, drainage ditches may be used for outfalls to natural or major
drainage channels. Ditches shall have a minimum grade of not less than one-tenth percent and side slopes not
steeper than a ratio of two to one.
(5)

Outfalls. Outfalls from sewers and ditches into natural drainageways shall enter at the grade of the natural
drainage channel. If necessary, drop type outfall structures shall be used to prevent erosion.
(6)

Major drainageways and structures. The design of major drainageways through a subdivision and major
structures, such as box culverts or bridges, across a major drainage channel shall be coordinated with the Texas
Transportation Commission standards.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.902), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-289—82-305. - Reserved.
Subdivision III. - Water System
Sec. 82-306. - Provision of water lines and mains; design certi cate required.
237/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(a)
The subdivider shall provide all water lines necessary to properly serve each lot of the subdivision and ensure
that existing and/or new water facilities can supply the required demand for domestic use and re protection at
the desired pressure. The subdivider shall install all mains, and shall extend service to all lots terminating
thereon with a curbstop.
(b)
The subdivider shall submit a certi cate to the city building o cial certifying that the water system has been
designed in accordance with the requirements of the state health department and rules and regulations of the
state re insurance commission. Approval of the design of the water system is required from the public works
director.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.910), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-307. - Water lines.
Piping for water mains and connections shall conform to the recommendations of the city's director of
public works or his designated engineer in the design and layout of the water distribution system. The design
shall be acceptable, without penalty, to the state fire insurance commission.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.911), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-308. - Fire hydrant outlet threading.
Threading on fire hydrant outlets shall be suitable for use by the city's fire protection equipment.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.912), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-309. - Valves.
At intersections of water distribution lines, the number of valves shall be one less than the number of
radiating lines (two valves for two connections and three valves for cross connection).
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.913), 11-8-1999)

Secs. 82-310—82-325. - Reserved.
Subdivision IV. - Wastewater Sewer System
Sec. 82-326. - Required.
All subdivisions shall be provided with a wastewater disposal system approved by the state health
department.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.920), 11-8-1999)

238/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 82-327. - Connection required.
Connection with the wastewater system shall be required.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.921), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-328. - Installation of mains and lines.
The subdivider shall install all wastewater mains and lines to each lot within the subdivision. If the public
system is not within 1,200 feet of the subdivision, those portions of the system which lie under paved streets
shall be installed and capped off and temporary waste treatment will be provided by the subdivider in
accordance with the requirement of state and county health officials.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.922), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-329. - Location.
Where the location of the wastewater line is not clearly defined by dimensions on the drawing, the sewer
shall not be closer than ten feet horizontally or six feet vertically to a water supply main or service line. Gravity
wastewater lines passing over water lines shall be constructed for a distance of ten feet each side of the
crossing encased in accordance with regulations of the state department of health.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.923), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-330. - Materials and sizes.
Materials for wastewater lines and the sizes of such lines shall conform to the city's standards and
recommendations of the city's director of public works or his designated engineer in the design and layout of
the wastewater system.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.924), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-331. - Minimum piping size.
Six-inch diameter pipe shall be the minimum acceptable for wastewater mains and lines.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.925), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-332. - Manholes.
Manholes shall be spaced not more than 500 feet apart, and shall be constructed in accordance with the
specifications of the director of public works, as approved by the city council.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(6.926), 11-8-1999)

Sec. 82-333. - Force mains.

239/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Force mains shall be cast iron pipe and fittings, pressure class. Pipes shall have mechanical joints
approved by the director of public works.
(Ord. No. 11-8-99-3, § 6(.927), 11-8-1999)

It is ordained by the city council that the one percent city sales tax on residential use of gas and electricity
is retained as provided by the 65th legislature, at the first called session of the state.
(Ord. No. 12-12-1978, § I, 12-12-1978)

The city adopts the provisions of V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 33.07 so that an additional penalty of 15 percent of

January 1, 1984.
(Ord. No. 5-8-84-1, 5-8-1984)

ARTICLE IV. - HOTEL OCCUPANCY TAX
Sec. 86-91. - De nitions.

240/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. The term "herein" means
in this article.

Hotel means a building in which members of the public obtain sleeping accommodations for a
consideration. Such term includes a hotel, motel, tourist home, tourist house, tourist court, lodging house, inn,
roominghouse or bed and breakfast. Such term does not include a hospital, sanitarium, nursing home or a
dormitory as defined in V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.001.

Person means any human being or legal entity, and includes a corporation, partnership and an
incorporated or unincorporated association.

Quarter or quarterly period means a quarter of a calendar year. The first quarter is composed of the
months of January, February and March; the second quarter is composed of the months of April, May and
June; the third quarter is composed of the months of July, August and September; and the fourth quarter is
composed of the months of October, November and December.

Regulation means the provisions of any applicable ordinance, rule, regulation or policy.
Tourism means the guidance or management of tourists.
Used or occupied, as applied to any room or building, means and includes the terms "intended, arranged
or agreed to be used or occupied."

Visitor information center means a building, or a portion of a building, used to distribute or disseminate
information to tourists.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 1, 4-10-2000)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
State law reference—Similar provisions, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.001.
Sec. 86-92. - Levied.
There is levied a tax upon the cost of occupancy of sleeping rooms in hotels, located within the city or its
extraterritorial jurisdiction (ETJ) for which the occupancy cost of the room is $2.00 or more per day. Such
occupancy tax shall be seven percent of the consideration paid for such sleeping room. The tax shall not apply
to a person who is a permanent resident of the sleeping room or who is otherwise exempt from paying the tax
pursuant to V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.001 et seq.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 2, 4-10-2000)

State law reference—Tax authorized, V.T.C.A., Tax Code §§ 351.002, 351.0025; rate, V.T.C.A., Tax Code §
351.003.
241/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 86-93. - Collection.
Every person owning, operating, managing or controlling any hotel within the city or its ETJ shall collect the
tax imposed and provided in this article.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 3, 4-10-2000)

Sec. 86-94. - Reporting of receipts for sleeping rooms.
On or before the last day of the month following each quarter, every person required to collect the tax
imposed by this article shall file a report with the city secretary showing the consideration paid for all sleeping
rooms during the preceding quarter and the amount of tax collected on such occupancies and sleeping rooms.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 4, 4-10-2000)

Sec. 86-95. - Payment; records of exemptions.
On or before the last day of the month following each quarter, every person required to collect the tax
imposed by this article shall pay the tax due to the city for the preceding quarterly period. If the occupancy of
any sleeping room is exempt by state law from the tax established pursuant to section 86-92, it shall be the
responsibility of the person required to collect the tax to document and provide records establishing the
exemption.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 5, 4-10-2000)

Sec. 86-96. - Penalty for late report or payment.
Any person who shall fail to file a report as required in this article or pay the tax as imposed in this article
when such report or payment is due, shall forfeit five percent of the amount due as a penalty. If any past due
tax is not paid within 30 days after the due date, such person shall forfeit an additional five percent of such tax
as an additional penalty.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 6, 4-10-2000)

Sec. 86-97. - Interest on taxes due and unpaid.
Taxes imposed in this article which remain due and unpaid from and after the last day of the calendar
month following the quarter for which such taxes are due and payable shall draw interest at the rate of one
percent per calendar month beginning 60 days from the last day of the quarterly period for which such taxes
are payable.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 7, 4-10-2000)

Sec. 86-98. - Attorney fees and costs.

242/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

If the matter of a report not being filed or taxes not being paid when due as required in this article is
forwarded to the city attorney for action, an amount equal to 15 percent of the taxes, penalties and interest
finally determined to be owing and payable shall be added to such amount as attorney fees and costs of
collection. If any action is required to be filed in any state court to obtain the required report or collect
delinquent taxes, the person responsible for collecting the taxes and filing the report shall be liable to the city
for its reasonable attorney fees and costs, provided, that such attorney fees shall in no event be less than 15
percent of the total amount of taxes, penalties and interest due and payable.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 8, 4-10-2000)

State law reference—Tax collection, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.004.
Sec. 86-99. - Noti cation and collection of delinquent taxes.
The city manager is authorized and directed to notify the city attorney of any hotel occupancy tax for
which a report is not timely filed or the tax is not timely paid as required by this article. Upon the city manager
referring the delinquent report or tax to the city attorney, an additional amount equal to 15 percent of the
taxes, penalties and interest due shall be added to the amount due and payable. Upon the receipt of such
notification from the city manager, the city attorney is:
(1)
Directed to promptly give written notice to the person owning, operating, managing or controlling the hotel for
which such report has not been received or for which the taxes have not been paid, demanding that the report
be promptly led and the taxes be promptly paid, as applicable;
(2)
Directed to pursue the demand for performance and compliance with this article, including the payment and
collection of all applicable penalties, interest, late charges, attorney fees and charges; and
(3)
Authorized and directed to le suit, if the report is not led or, as applicable, all amounts due and payable are
not paid within 30 days after the date of the demand by the city attorney, to obtain:
a.
The ling of any report required by this article;
b.
The payment of all taxes, penalties, interest and fees due and payable pursuant to this article;
c.
An injunction prohibiting the continued operation of the hotel for which the report has not been led or the
taxes have not been paid; and
d.
Such other and further relief that may be available at law or in equity.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 9, 4-10-2000)

243/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 86-100. - Escrow account.
Subject to the legislative discretion of the city council, 50 percent of all hotel occupancy taxes received by
the city shall be deposited into an escrow account to be held, maintained and appropriated by the city. The
funds and balances of the escrow account shall be managed and invested in compliance with the city's
investment policy, and all earnings of such escrow account shall be deposited and remain in such account
subject to appropriation by the city council. The escrow account shall be reserved, held and increased for any
purpose allowed by V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.101 et seq., as amended.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 10, 4-10-2000)

State law reference—Use and allocation of revenue, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.101 et seq.
Sec. 86-101. - Records of receipts and expenditures.
The city shall maintain a record that accurately identifies the receipt and expenditure of all revenue
derived from the tax imposed by this article.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 11, 4-10-2000)

Sec. 86-102. - Tourism.
Subject to future appropriations and actions by the city council, 50 percent of the hotel occupancy tax
receipts are set aside and appropriated for the advertisement of the city and the promotion of tourism within
the city. Such funds are currently appropriated annually for the promotion of tourism and the operation of a
visitor information center pursuant to a contract between the city and the chamber of commerce.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 12, 4-10-2000)

Sec. 86-103. - Criminal penalty.
A person required by this article to collect the tax imposed in section 86-92, or to make reports as
required in this article, who fails to collect the tax, file the report or pay the tax, shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $500.00 for each offense. The
failure to collect the tax, file the required report and pay the tax collected prior to such payment becoming
past due shall each constitute and be a separate offense and shall be punishable by a fine.
(Ord. No. 4-10-00-1, § 13, 4-10-2000)

State law reference—Misdemeanor penalty authorized, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.004(c).
Chapter 90 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL

244/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 90-1. - Tra c control signs and devices.
(a)

Rati cation and con rmation of existing tra c control signs and devices. The installation, placement, erection
and enforcement of the tra c control signs and devices as set forth in exhibit A, on le in the o ce of the city
secretary, are authorized, con rmed and rati ed by the city council. Each stop sign listed in such exhibit shall
require tra c traveling on the rst street listed to stop and yield the right-of-way to any tra c or motor vehicle
on any other street listed in column two for that line in compliance with the transportation code. Each yield sign
listed in such exhibit shall require tra c traveling on the street listed to yield the right-of-way to any tra c or
motor vehicle on any other street listed in column two for that line in compliance with the transportation code.
The nal column, to such exhibit, in some instances, denotes four-way stops or additional signs for that line of
streets.
(b)

Violation; penalty. Any person who tampers with, alters, removes, destroys, covers or hinders the visibility of any
tra c control device of the city in a manner which is inconsistent with its use as a tra c control device violates
this section. Any person who violates this section, or any part thereof, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and,
upon conviction, shall be punished by a ne not to exceed $200.00. Each day and each incident of violation of
this section shall constitute a separate o ense.
(Ord. No. 12-10-01-3, §§ 2, 4, 12-10-2001)

State law reference—Traffic control signals, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.007 et seq.
Sec. 90-2. - U-turns prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person driving any type of automobile or gasoline propelled vehicle to execute
a U-turn on any street or at any intersection of any street within the city limits, unless there is a street sign at
such point of turn authorizing the execution of a U-turn.
(Ord. No. 10-12-71, art. I, 10-12-1971)

Sec. 90-3. - Unlawful to block alleys.
It shall be unlawful to park an automobile, pickup or truck in any alley in the city in such a manner so as to
block the normal flow of traffic. For the purpose of this section, the term "normal flow of traffic" means free
passage of motor vehicles in any direction in an alley.
(Ord. No. 7-11-72, art. I, 7-11-1972)

Cross reference—Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 78.
Secs. 90-4—90-30. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING OF VEHICLES

245/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 90-31. - Vehicles in excess of 12,000 pounds prohibited from entering designated city parking lot.
(a)

Unlawful act. It shall be unlawful for any person to operate, drive, park, leave standing or in any other manner
cause the entry, parking or leaving of any vehicle rated in excess of 12,000 gross pounds, according to the
manufacturer's classi cation, upon any portion of the city's parking lot located south of West Live Oak and East
of North Park Street.
(b)

Posting of notice. The city manager is directed to take such actions as are reasonably necessary to ensure signs
are su ciently posted at the major points of vehicular ingress re ecting the unlawful entry as provided in
subsection (a) of this section in order to notify reasonably prudent and observant drivers, and to ensure that all
departments of the city requiring notice of the requirements under this section, are duly noti ed of such
unlawful entry and are provided the necessary information to e ectuate the change.
(c)

Enforcement. The chief of police and members of the police department, both regular and reserve o cers, are
empowered to enforce this section.
(d)

Towing and removal. Any vehicle which shall be or remain standing or parked upon any portion of the parking
lot described in subsection (a) of this section is in violation of this section. The owner or driver of a vehicle
parked in violation of this section who has been given previous notice or citation for parking such vehicle in
violation of this section may be removed by or upon an order by a police o cer. The owner of such vehicle shall
be responsible for the payment of any fees incurred for the towing and/or storage of such vehicle.
(e)

Prima facie evidence. In any prosecution charging a violation of this section governing the stopping, standing or
parking of a vehicle, proof that the particular vehicle described in the complaint was parked in violation of this
section, together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was, at the time of such parking, the
registered owner of such vehicle, shall constitute in evidence a prima facie presumption that the registered
owner of such vehicle was the person who parked or placed such vehicle at the point where, and for the time
during which, such violation occurred.
(f)

Penalties. Any person convicted of violating any provision of this section shall be punished as provided for in
section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 11-12-01-1, §§ 2—7, 11-12-2001)

Sec. 90-32. - Parking restrictions in residential areas; noise; penalty.
(a)

De nitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a di erent meaning:

Zoned as residential means any area of the city as defined by the zoning ordinance, chapter 102 of this
Code, except those areas zoned C commercial district, CBD central business district and I industrial district.
246/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Words used in this section shall have the meaning, if any, given in the V.T.C.A., Transportation
Code.
(b)

Commercial motor vehicles. It shall be unlawful for any person or owner to leave, park or stand any truck
tractor, road tractor, semitrailer or any other commercial motor vehicle with a manufacturer's gross vehicle
weight of 12,000 pounds or more within or adjacent to any area zoned as a residential district. This subsection
shall not prevent the parking or standing of the such vehicles in residentially zoned areas for the purpose of
loading and unloading passengers, freight or merchandise, as long as the normal ow of tra c is not impeded
or does not obstruct the view of tra c or any tra c control device, and is not otherwise a health and safety
hazard.
(c)

Exception. An exception to the requirement of subsection (b) of this section shall be that a truck tractor and
truck trailer may be allowed to parked on private property with the permission of the property owner as long as
the vehicle is not:
(1)
In the street;
(2)
Impeding tra c;
(3)
Obstructing the ow of tra c;
(4)
Obstructing the view of tra c;
(5)
Obstructing the view of a tra c control device; and
(6)
Otherwise a health and safety hazard.
(d)

Trailers. It shall be unlawful for any person or owner to leave, park or stand any mobile home, boat trailer, stock
trailer, utility trailer or any other type of trailer upon any public street or alley within any area zoned as a
residential district, except that a recreational vehicle owned by an out-of-town guest of a residential property
owner may be parked on the street in front of the property owned by such host for a period of time not to
exceed 24 hours. This subsection shall not prevent the parking or standing of such vehicles in residentially
zoned areas for the purpose of loading and unloading passengers, freight or merchandise, as long as the
normal ow of tra c is not impeded or the view of tra c or any tra c control device is not obstructed, and is
not otherwise a health and safety hazard.
(e)

Public service company vehicles exempt. This section shall not apply to street construction, maintenance and
repair equipment used by public service companies engaged in repairing or extending public service utilities,
and motor buses when taking on or discharging passengers.
247/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(f)

Authority to tow; responsibility for expense. The city police department and code enforcement o cer shall have
the authority to tow away any vehicle or trailer deemed to be impeding the regular ow of tra c, or determined
to be a tra c hazard, or obstructing the view of tra c or any tra c control device. The expense of such towing
and storage shall be borne by the owner of the towed vehicle or trailer.
(g)

Prolonged and/or unreasonable noise. Nothing in this section shall allow a person or owner to cause or
generate a prolonged and/or unreasonable noise that shall cause the peace and quiet of any person on any
adjacent premises to be disturbed.
(h)

Violation; penalty. Any person convicted of violating any provision of this section shall be punished as provided
for in section 1-13 of this Code.
(Ord. No. 02-12-01-1, §§ 1—5, 2-12-2001)

ARTICLE IV. - TRUCKS
DIVISION 1. - RESTRICTIONS
Sec. 90-76. - Truck use of engine brakes prohibited.
The city council hereby restricts the use of any engine brake within the city in an attempt to reduce noise,
prevent destruction of pavement at intersections and facilitate lower speeds within the downtown traffic
corridors.
(Ord. No. 12-9-02-5, § 1, 12-9-2002)

Sec. 90-77. - Enforcement.
This division shall be strictly enforced by the city police department.
(Ord. No. 12-9-02-5, § 2, 12-9-2002)

Sec. 90-78. - Violation and penalties.

252/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Any person violating this division may be cited and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished by a fine of
not less than $50.00, nor more than $200.00 for each offense.
(Ord. No. 12-9-02-5, § 3, 12-9-2002)

Secs. 90-79—90-99. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - DESIGNATED TRUCK ROUTES
Sec. 90-100. - Purpose.
The operator of any truck in excess of 26,000 GVW or gross cargo weight rating of 26,000 pounds or
greater, shall not drive or operate such truck on any public street or roadway, except upon such streets that
are designated in section 90-103 as truck routes. Whenever any street designated as a truck route is being
repaired or is otherwise temporarily out of use, the city manager or their designee, is authorized to designate
alternate truck routes for such periods as may be necessary.
(Ord. No. 8-11-08-2, § 3, 8-11-2008)

Sec. 90-101. - De nitions.

Authorized emergency vehicle means a vehicle of: A fire department; police or sheriff's department; public
or private ambulance service; a volunteer fire department or emergency medical services department; the city
or any utility providing public utility service.

Truck means every motor vehicle designed, used or maintained primarily for the transportation of
property or drawing other vehicles or trailers that carry property with an overall gross weight, including truck
and/or trailer(s), of 26,000 pounds or greater (GVW), or with a gross cargo weight rating of 26,000 pounds or
greater.

Vehicle means every motor-driven device, in, upon, or which any person or property is or may be
transported or drawn upon a roadway.
(Ord. No. 1-14-08-1, § 2, 1-14-2008; Ord. No. 8-11-08-2, § 2, 8-11-2008)

Sec. 90-102. - Exceptions.
(a)
The following vehicles are exempt from the terms of this division while engaged in the listed activity:
(1)
Authorized emergency vehicles responding to or from, or at the scene of, an emergency call;
(2)
Vehicles being used to provide any municipal service such as the installation, repair or maintenance of any
public street, asset or property, collection of garbage, grounds keeping, public transport, etc.;
253/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(3)
Vehicles used or operated by the city or the city's franchisee, conducting approved franchisee related activities
being used to install, repair or maintain any public service or utility such as telephone, electricity, cable
television, gas, water or sewer line; and
(4)
Recreational vehicles and personal trailers. As used in this division, recreational vehicles shall mean a vehicular
portable structure designed for a temporary or short-term occupancy for travel, recreational or vacation usage.
Personal trailers shall mean a wheeled device made to be hauled by a motor vehicle upon a road or highway,
including, but not limited to; a horse trailer or similar device used to transport animals, car or motorcycle trailer,
boat trailer, lawn equipment trailer, gooseneck trailer, or any other trailer designed to carry large items and
designed to be drawn by a motor vehicle.
(b)
Trucks restricted to the streets and roadways designated as truck routes under this division may depart from
such truck routes where it is necessary to load or unload merchandise at locations situated o designated truck
routes. Provided however, such trucks shall not leave a designated truck route until they have reached a
turning-o point that can be described as the shortest distance practical to the ultimate destination of the
vehicle which is consistent with the reasonable operation of the vehicle. It shall be a defense to a charge under
this section that the person so charged show by competent evidence that the truck was making a delivery or
pickup that necessitated deviation from the designated truck route and that the shortest distance to the
destination was taken.
(Ord. No. 1-14-08-1, § 3, 1-14-2008; Ord. No. 8-11-08-2, § 4, 8-11-2008)

The roadway is designated as a truck route under this division; or
(2)
The operation of the truck at the time and place is exempt under this division.

The city shall, erect or cause to be erected, signs marking the designated truck routes and prohibiting
truck traffic within the city except on the designated and marked truck routes.
(Ord. No. 1-14-08-1, § 5, 1-14-2008; Ord. No. 8-11-08-2, § 6, 8-11-2008)

The chief of police and members of the police department, both regular and reserve officers, are
empowered to enforce this division.
255/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 1-14-08-1, § 6, 1-14-2008; Ord. No. 8-11-08-2, § 7, 8-11-2008)

Sec. 90-106. - Penalties.
Any person convicted of violating any provision of this division shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall
be subject to a fine in an amount not to exceed $200.00. Each day the violation exists shall constitute a
separate offense. Such penalty shall be in addition to all the other remedies provided herein.
(Ord. No. 1-14-08-1, § 7, 1-14-2008; Ord. No. 8-11-08-2, § 8, 8-11-2008)

Sec. 90-107. - Damage to public property.
It shall be illegal for any person to knowingly or intentionally damage public streets, roadways or any sign
posted by the city for the regulation of traffic. Any person who knowingly, intentionally or recklessly causes
damage to public streets, roadways or any sign posted thereon for the regulation of traffic shall be responsible
for the costs of repair.
(Ord. No. 1-14-08-1, § 8, 1-14-2008)

Sec. 90-108. - Parking prohibited.
Except as permitted in section 90-102 of this division or for emergency purposes, the parking of trucks
along streets, roadways and rights-of-way within the city is prohibited.
(Ord. No. 1-14-08-1, § 9, 1-14-2008)

Sec. 90-109. - Prima facie evidence.
In any prosecution charging a violation of this division governing the use of designated truck routes, proof
that the particular truck described in the complaint was in violation of this division, together with proof that
the defendant named in the complaint was, at the time of such violation, the operator of such truck, shall
constitute in evidence a prima facie presumption that the operator of such truck was the person who failed to
confine their travel within designated truck routes while within the city and for the time during which, such
violation occurred.
(Ord. No. 8-11-08-2, § 9, 8-11-2008)

ARTICLE II. - WATER

256/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Secs. 94-19—94-39. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - CONSERVATION
Sec. 94-40. - Water conservation plan/drought contingency plan.
(a)

Approval. The city council approves and adopts as the city's water conservation plan/drought contingency plan
on le in the o ce of the city secretary and included in full as a part of this section as if recited verbatim in this
section. The city commits to implement the program according to procedures set forth in the adopted plan.
(b)

Annual report. The city shall report to the Texas Water Development Board annually on the implementation and
e ectiveness of the plan in accordance with the outline set forth in the plan.
(c)

Responsibility for implementation and enforcement. In regards to the implementation and enforcement of the
conservation and drought contingency plan, the city manager is designated as the o cial responsible for
implementation and enforcement.
(d)

Noncompliance; penalty. Users of city water, except for the city, that do not comply with this section shall be
subject to a penalty and ne of not less than $25.00 per day and no more than $200.00 per day for each day of
noncompliance and/or disconnection or discontinuance of water service to such users by the city.
(e)

Applicability of speci c state law regarding water supplies. The city hereby acknowledges that V.T.C.A., Water
Code § 11.039 authorizes water suppliers to distribute available water supplies on a pro rata basis during times
of water shortage and the city agrees to adopt this method.
(f)

Viable water sources. The city recognizes that there is no viable alternative water source available to the city
should the city lose the Upper Leon River Municipal Water District supply. Potable water would have to be
imported by tanker truck.
(g)

Applicability of speci c state law regarding contracts between city and water wholesales. The city acknowledges
the language in V.T.C.A., Water Code § 11.039, that any future contract entered into between the city and a
water wholesaler contain a provision requiring the wholesaler to develop and implement a water conservation
plan or water conservation measure themselves. The city agrees to include this language in any future contracts.
(Ord. No. 8-14-00-1, §§ I—IV, 8-14-2000; Ord. No. 7-8-02-2, §§ 1—3, 7-8-2002)

Sec. 94-41. - Responsibility of city manager regarding drought conditions.

257/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The city manager shall take the necessary steps to ensure that he is aware of any and all drought
conditions which may exist from time to time, and that he informs the city council immediately of any
condition that might indicate the onset of a drought as outlined in the water conservation plan for the city. In
addition, the city manager shall apprise the city council as the severity of the conditions change.
(Ord. No. 10-14-96-4, § 1, 10-14-1996)

Sec. 94-42. - Determination of severity of drought conditions; actions.
When the city council is notified by the city manager that certain conditions have been met which indicate
the onset of any drought condition, that the city council will declare a mild, moderate or severe drought
condition, as is appropriate. Further, the city council will instruct the city manager to take the appropriate
action as indicated in the water conservation plan for the city for the conditions then existing.
(Ord. No. 10-14-96-4, § 2, 10-14-1996)

Secs. 94-43—94-72. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - WATER WELLS
Subdivision I. - In General
Sec. 94-73. - Private wells.
No person shall drill a well within the city limits. Drilling for minerals, including water, shall strictly be prohibited.
The city as part of the operation of public services is exempt from this section.
(Ord. No. 11-8-71, arts. I, II, X, 11-8-1971; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. II, § 5, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. II, § 5, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. III, § 5, 3-14-2005)

Secs. 94-74—94-104. - Reserved.
Subdivision II. - Administration and Enforcement
Sec. 94-105. - Water works board.
The mayor shall appoint three citizens to serve as a water works board, one to serve one year, one to
serve two years, and one to serve three years or until their successor has been duly qualified, to make or have
made examinations of all wells within the city; privately owned or otherwise; to make or have made at any
time the necessary analysis or tests of water therefrom; to go upon the land and property of the owner of a
well for that purpose; and to supervise the construction, repair, abandonment and plugging of wells and the
operation of such wells.
(Ord. No. 11-8-71, art. XI, 11-8-1971)

258/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Cross reference—Boards, commissions and authorities, § 2-141 et seq.
Secs. 94-106—94-123. - Reserved.
Subdivision III. - Regulations
Sec. 94-124. - Drilling through septic tank drain eld.
It shall be unlawful to drill, or have drilled, a new water well through a sub-irrigated septic tank drainfield.
(Ord. No. 11-8-71, art. IV, 11-8-1971)

Sec. 94-125. - Slush pits required.
It shall hereafter be unlawful for any person to drill a new water well or rework an existing well in the city
without providing and using portable slush pits or tanks in which to contain and subsequently dispose of any
slush or other waste, water, material or matter created by and involved in the drilling, reworking or deepening
of such well. It shall be unlawful to permit any such slush or other waste material or matter to run or drain
into the city streets and alleys or on other public or private places or property without the express consent of
the owner thereof, and it shall further be unlawful to divert or drain or permit any such slush or other waste
material or matter to empty into the city sanitary sewer or underground storm sewer system.
(Ord. No. 11-8-71, art. III, 11-8-1971)

Sec. 94-126. - Casing required.
It shall be unlawful for any person to drill, or have drilled, a water well in the city unless the same is cased
from a point at least one foot above the surface of the ground to a point at least 30 feet below the surface of
the ground and the entire length of the casing cemented so that all of the void space between the outside of
the casing and the sides of the drilled hole is filled with cement, provided, that this provision regarding casing
shall not apply to existing wells or the reworking or deepening thereof, and, providing further, that the
preceding requirement of bringing or extending the casing one foot above the surface of the ground may be
waived by the health officer or city administration in favor of any alternate surface completion method that
will effectively seal off the well from the flow or drainage of surface water back into the well, in which event,
the permit may be issued.
(Ord. No. 11-8-71, art. V, 11-8-1971)

Secs. 94-127—94-150. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - WATER AND WASTEWATER SERVICE
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
259/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Secs. 94-151—94-168. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - CONNECTIONS
Subdivision I. - In General
Sec. 94-169. - De nitions.
For the purposes of this division, the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the
meaning ascribed to them in this section, provided, that unless specifically defined below, words or phrases
used in this division shall be interpreted so as to give them the same meaning as they have in common usage,
and so as to give this division its most reasonable application.

Business unit means any premises, locations or entities, public or private, including all industrial and
commercial entities, within the corporate limits of the city not a residential unit.

City means the City of Dublin, Erath County, Texas.
City's operator means the person, firm, corporation, municipal corporation or political subdivision which
the city has designated to operate and maintain the city's water system.

Commercial or industrial means and includes any establishment, public or private, rendering a service,
manufacturing a product, offering a product for sale or any other similar activity.

Connection means the initial or first connection ("tap") or any subsequent additional connection of a
residential or business unit to the city's water system.

Customer means any person, firm or corporation receiving city water or wastewater services for a
residential or business unit, whether within the city or outside the city limits.

Master meter means the separate connection through which one metering facility serves other
establishments or entities occupying the same building, location or adjoining property.

New connection means public or private, commercial or residential structures that are built on site.
Person means and includes an individual human, partnership, co-partner ship firm, company, limited
liability partnership or other partnership or other such company, joint venture, joint stock company, trust,
estate, governmental entity, association or corporation or any other legal entity, or their legal representatives,
agents or assigns. The masculine gender shall include the feminine, the singular shall include the plural where
indicated by the context.

Residential unit means a dwelling within the corporate limits or service area of the city intended for
occupancy by a person or group of persons comprising not more than one family. A dwelling shall be deemed
occupied and shall be deemed by the city to be a separate Residential Unit for billing and collection purposes
260/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

when either water or electrical power services are being supplied thereto.

Separate connection means the individual metering facilities for each residential or business unit for
which city services have been requested or provided, whether occupied or not.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. I, § 4, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. II, § 1, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. II, § 1, 12-15-2004; Ord.
No. 3-14-05-6, art. II, § 4, 3-14-2005)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 94-170. - Authority.
This article is adopted pursuant to the police powers and authority given general law cities by the
constitution, codes and general laws of the State of Texas, including but not limited to V.T.C.A., Local
Government Code chs. 51 and 402.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. I, § 1, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. I, § 1, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. I, § 1, 12-15-2004; Ord.
No. 3-14-05-6, art. II, § 1, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-171. - Purpose.
The purpose of this division is to provide for public health and general welfare, the efficient and effective
provision of city services and the protection of the environment and natural resources of the community.
From and after the passage of this article all residential, business, commercial and industrial occupancies and
uses within the city and its service area shall conform to the following rules and regulations.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. I, § 2, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. I, § 2, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. I, § 2, 12-15-2004; Ord.
No. 3-14-05-6, art. II, § 2, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-172. - Mandatory connection to city system.
(a)
Except as provided otherwise in this division, no building, tract of land or structure in an area of the city for
which water service is available shall be occupied for residential, commercial, industrial or other such purposes
unless such buildings or structures are connected by a separate connection to the city water system. Property
that abuts a street, road or other public way in which a public water supply is located and is within two hundred
feet of such water line is deemed to have access to the city water system. No tract of land shall be required to
be connected to the city water system that requests connection to the city water system in writing and is denied
connection; provided that the city may subsequently require connection to the city water system when city
water service is made available in a public right-of-way abutting the property.
(b)
Each residential unit and business unit within the city shall be connected by separate connection to the city
water system as soon as city water service is available to such unit, unless speci cally exempted herein.
(c)

261/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Any unoccupied residential unit or business unit within the city for which water service has been provided
previously by the city water system or its predecessor shall be connected to the city water system by a separate
connection prior to occupancy.
(d)
Any two or more residential units that are found to be obtaining water service through a single meter shall be
required to connect each such unit by a separate connection to the city water system within 30 days.
(e)
Each business unit within the city shall be connected by a separate connection to the city water system as soon
as city water service is available to such unit, unless speci cally exempted.
(f)
Any commercial or industrial establishments or entities located within a single building and served by a master
meter on the e ective date of the ordinance from which this division is derived may elect to continue to receive
water service through such master meter.
(g)
From the e ective date of the ordinance from which this division is derived, no person or commercial or
industrial establishment shall be permitted to obtain service through a master meter or otherwise provide
water service to another person or entity, except as provided otherwise in this chapter.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. II, § 1, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. II, § 1, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. II, § 1, 12-15-2004; Ord.
No. 3-14-05-6, art. III, § 1, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-173. - Application for water connections.
Each person desiring water service shall be required to complete an application for such service and pay
such fees as are established by the ordinance from which this division is derived. No service shall be rendered
until such fees are paid.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. II, § 2, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. II, § 2, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. II, § 2, 12-15-2004; Ord.
No. 3-14-05-6, art. III, § 2, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-174. - Connections and taps to water and wastewater system.
(a)

Certi cation. Connections shall not be made to either the city water or the wastewater system until the city's
operator or other party designated by the city council has certi ed that the respective system or applicable
portion thereof is adequate and operational. Water service shall not be provided to any residential or business
unit not in compliance with rules and regulations promulgated by the Texas Department of Health, the Texas
Commission on Environmental Quality (TCEQ) or other appropriate regulatory agency as set out in the Texas
Water Code or as otherwise required by statute or regulation.
(b)

Service access. Upon application for connection to the water system the applicant shall grant an easement of
ingress and egress to and from the meter or point of service for such installation, maintenance and repair as the
city, in its judgment, may deem necessary. Taps and connections will not be made when, in the opinion of the
262/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

city's operator, the work area is obstructed by building materials and debris or the work area is not completed
to nished grade. When sidewalks, driveways or other improvements have been constructed prior to application
for service, such application shall be construed and accepted as a waiver of a claim for damages to such
improvements resulting from the reasonable actions of the city's operator in installation of the customer's
connection.
(c)

City property. All meters, ttings, boxes, valves and appurtenances installed by city personnel or agent shall
remain the property of the city. City maintenance of the water service ends at the customer side of the
connection to the water meter itself. City maintenance of the wastewater service ends at the property line.
(d)

Connections. All connections to the city water system and/or wastewater system shall be made by the city's
operator unless speci ed otherwise by the city council. No person, other than the properly authorized agents of
the city, shall be permitted to tap or make any connections with the mains, distribution or collection lines of the
city's water system, or wastewater system, except for emergency re ghting purposes, or make any repairs or
additions to or alterations in any meter box, tap, pipe, cock or other xture connected with the water service
except by the written permission of the city council. No new dual or multiple connections (being more than one
user on a single meter) shall be permitted.
(e)

Plan approval required. Each applicant for a connection shall within ten days prior to payment of tap fees
submit to the city operator the following information:
(1)
On all new commercial, residential or duplex constructions, one set of drawings showing details of building
plumbing, site plumbing and the location, size and number of proposed connections to the city's water system
and/or wastewater system;
(2)
A general description of the type of proposed establishment; and
(3)
The city's operator or other party designated by the city council shall review the information presented and may
approve or reject the application, or request that further information be submitted prior to approval of the
application. The applicant shall be noti ed in writing as to the basis for rejection. Failure to construct the
facilities in accordance with approved drawings shall constitute a basis for denial of city water services. Payment
of tap fees to the city prior to the approval of plans shall not constitute approval of said plans or approval for
service as set forth herein; any unauthorized connection or connections may be removed at the expense of the
person or rm causing such connection or connections to be made.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. II, § 3, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. II, § 3, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. II, § 3, 12-15-2004; Ord.
No. 3-14-05-6, art. III, § 3, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-175. - Damage or injury to waterworks system.

263/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

It shall be unlawful for any person, in any way, to intentionally or carelessly break, deface or in any
manner damage, injure or destroy any hydrant, standpipe, lock box or other property belonging to the city or
belonging to others, and used in connection with the waterworks system of the city. No person other than a
duly authorized agent of the city shall remove, repair, or tamper with or in any way interfere with the city's
meter boxes, meters, lock boxes, water service lines, sewer service lines, or other water or sewer system
appurtenances. The city reserves the right to immediately and without notice remove the meter or disconnect
water service to any customer whose meter has been tampered with and to assess actual repair charges to
the customer plus a damage fee.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VI, § 1, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. VI, § 1, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. VI, § 1, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VII, § 1, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-176. - Repair of damages to waterworks system.
All meters, fittings, boxes, valves and appurtenances installed by the city shall remain the property of the
city. The city reserves the right on 24-hour notice and no appeal being filed, to remove the meter or disconnect
water service to any customer whose meter or lock box has been tampered with and to assess actual repair
charges to the customer plus a damage fee. As necessary or advisable to protect the public health or the
operation and function of the city's water or sewer system, the city further reserves the right and authority to
proceed immediately and without notice to disconnect, or to repair when and as necessary and appropriate,
any meter, pipe, line or other appurtenance connected to the city water or sewer system, and if such repair is
made to any such line, pipe or appurtenance owned by any private property owner to assess the actual repair
charges to the customer who owns, rents, or controls such property. Failure to repair or failure to pay for
repairs performed by the city shall constitute cause for the city to terminate services to the customer charged
with the repairs. The city requires each customer to "CALL BEFORE YOU DIG" in order for the city water
department to locate lines for the customer. Repair charges will be assessed to the customer if NO attempt is
made to contact the city water department before digging and damage occurs. Repair charges are due within
ten days from the date of invoice and are as follows:
(1)

Labor charges. Regular time for repairs needed during normal business hours; after 5:00 p.m. and weekends,
actual cost for labor at the prevailing rate.
(2)

Equipment rental; actual cost to city. If not paid within ten days from the date of invoice, the city reserves the
right to immediately and without notice remove the meter or disconnect water service until all repair charges
are paid in full.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VI, § 2, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. VI, § 2, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. VI, § 2, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VII, § 2, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-177. - Disconnection for failure to comply.

264/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

It shall be the duty of the city to disconnect the city service from any place where the provisions of this
article are violated, whether inside or outside of the city.
(Ord. No. 11-8-71, art. IX, 11-8-1971)

Sec. 94-178. - Violation; penalty.
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this division, or shall fail to comply therewith, or with
any of the requirements thereof, within the city limits shall be deemed guilty of an offense and shall be liable
for a fine not less than $200.00 and not to exceed the sum of $2,000.00. Each day the violation exists shall
constitute a separate offense. Such penalty shall be in addition to all the other remedies provided herein.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VII, § 5, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. VII, § 5, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. VII, § 5, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 5, 3-14-2005)

Secs. 94-179—94-209. - Reserved.
Subdivision II. - Enforcement
Sec. 94-210. - Enforcement.
The civil and criminal provisions of this chapter shall be enforced by the persons or agencies designated
by the city, including, but not limited to, the city police department, the building official, and the code
enforcement officer. It shall be a violation of this chapter to interfere with a code enforcement officer, or other
person authorized to enforce this chapter, in the performance of his or her duties.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VII, § 4, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. VII, § 4, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. VII, § 4, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 4, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-211. - Violations and notices.
(a)
If an o cer charged with the enforcement of this division shall determine that a person has violated any
provision of this division, such o cer may issue a citation.
(b)
If an o cer charged with the enforcement of this division shall determine that a situation exists which
immediately a ects or threatens the health, safety and well-being of the general public, and that immediate
action is necessary, such o cer may take such action as shall be necessary, including issuing citations for
violations of the terms and provisions hereof to the owner and/or occupant of the property upon which such
condition exists, as may be deemed appropriate and necessary.
(c)
If an o cer charged with the enforcement of this division determines a situation constitutes an immediate
threat to the public health, safety and welfare, and the owner or occupant of the property is absent or fails to
265/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

immediately remedy the violation, the city manager, or his designee, may, determine that an emergency exists
and order such action as may be required to protect the public health, safety and welfare.
(d)
If any owner or occupant shall fail or refuse to remedy any of the conditions prohibited by this division within
seven days after notice to do so, the city may terminate services or do such work, or cause the same to be done,
and pay therefor, and charge the expenses in doing or having such work done or improvements made to the
owner of the property, and such charge shall be a personal liability of such owner to the city.
(e)
Notices required pursuant to this division shall be in writing. Such notice may be served upon such owner
and/or occupant as follows: in person by an o cer or employee of the city; by letter addressed to such owner or
occupant at his/her post o ce address; or, if personal service may not be had, or the owner or occupant's
address be not known, then notice may be given by publishing a brief summary of such order in the o cial
newspaper of the city, two times in ten consecutive days, and by posting a notice on or near the front door of
each building on the property upon which the violation relates, or, if no building exists, by posting notice on a
placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the property to which the violation relates. Notice of
termination of services for non-payment shall be mailed regular rst class mail to the address designated on the
account for receipt or bill and shall be deemed served within three days of deposit in the regular mail. The
notice may state "Sanitary Improvements," "To Whom It May Concern" and a brief statement of the violation(s)
or delinquency. If the notice is for delinquency, the notice shall include a termination date and location for
payment for services. Service of the notice by any one of the above methods, or by a combination thereof, shall
be deemed su cient notice.
(f)
If an owner is mailed a notice in accordance with subsection (e) of this section and the United States Postal
Service returns the notice as "refused" or "unclaimed," the validity of the notice is not a ected, and the notice is
considered as delivered.
(g)
Notice of nuisances provided by mail or by posting as set forth in subsection (e) may provide for year-round
abatement of the nuisance and inform the owner that should the owner commit any other violation of the same
kind that pose a danger to the public health and safety on or before the rst anniversary of the date of the
notice, the city without further notice may abate the violation at the owner's expense and assess the costs
against the property.
(h)
Persons in violation of this division, or causing or creating a prohibited nuisance in the presence of a person
authorized to enforce this division, may be cited or a complaint led for such violation without notice of the
violation, or warning, and such citation or complaint shall be led in the municipal court of the city.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VII, § 1, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. VII, § 1, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. VII, § 1, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 1, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-212. - Costs and appeals.

266/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

In addition to any other remedy provided in this division and cumulative thereto, the code enforcement
officer, after giving to the owner of the property ten days notice in writing, as provided in section 94-211(e),
may cause any of the work or improvements mentioned in this division to be done at the expense of the city,
and charge the owner or occupant of the property on which such work or improvements are done, or the
person to which the utility bills are addressed, and cause all of the actual cost to the city to be assessed on the
real estate or lot on which such expenses occurred; provided, that the owner of any such real estate may
appeal to the city council from the order of the code enforcement officer by filing a written statement with the
code enforcement officer within ten days after receipt of the notice provided for above, stating that such real
estate complied with the provision of this division before the expiration of a ten-day period. The city council
shall set a date, within 30 days from the date of the appeal, for hearing the appeal to determine whether the
real estate complied with the provisions of this division before the expiration of such ten-day period. The
authority of the code enforcement officer to proceed to cause such work to be done shall not be suspended
while an appeal from the order is pending. If it shall be determined by the city council that the premises
complied with the provisions of this division before the expiration of the ten-day period, then no personal
liability of the owner shall arise nor shall any lien be created against the premises upon which such work was
done.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VII, § 2, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. VII, § 2, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. VII, § 2, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 2, 3-14-2005)

Sec. 94-213. - Cost of abatement constitutes lien.
Cumulative of the city's remedy by fine, as set forth herein, the city may do such work or cause the same
to be done to remedy such condition to remove such matter from such owner's premises at the city's expense
and charge the same to the utility bill of such property and assess the same against the real estate or lot or
lots upon which such expense is incurred as provided in state law.
(1)
Expenditures plus ten percent per annum interest on the expenditures from the date of such payment by the
city shall be added to the next billing cycle for utility bills for the real estate or lot or lots, if not already paid.
Payment shall be due and payable in full by the owner or occupant at the time of payment of such utility bill. If
the property is unoccupied, no utilities shall be furnished to the property where the work occurred until such
obligation, as herein set out, payable to the city for abatement of any nuisance described herein is paid in full.
(2)
Upon ling with the county clerk of Erath County, Texas, of a statement by the city secretary or designee of such
expenses, the city shall have a privileged lien upon said real estate or lot or lots, second only to tax liens and
liens for street improvements, to secure the expenditure so made and ten percent per annum interest, on the
amount from the date of such payment so made by the city.
(3)
The city may, additionally, institute suit and recover such expenses and foreclose such lien in any court of
competent jurisdiction, and the statement so led with the county clerk or a certi ed copy thereof shall be
267/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

prima facie proof of the amount expended in any such work or improvements to remedy such condition or
remove any such matter.
(Ord. No. 5-8-00-1, art. VII, § 3, 5-8-2000; Ord. No. 12-9-02-4, art. VII, § 3, 12-9-2002; Ord. No. 12-15-04-1, art. VII, § 3, 12-15-2004;
Ord. No. 3-14-05-6, art. VIII, § 3, 3-14-2005)
