Portable storage building means any accessory structure of 120 square feet or less designed to be
transported from one location on a specific site to another location either on the same lot or on a separate lot.

Premises means land, together with any buildings or structures occupying such land.
Private club means an association of persons meeting regularly for their mutual benefit or for the
promotion of a common purpose, supported jointly through payment of membership dues, all members
having the right to vote on policies and business.

Private drive (street or place) means an open, unoccupied space, other than a street or alley, permanently
established, reserved or dedicated in private ownership as the principal means of vehicular access to property
abutting thereon.

Recreational equipment, major, means and includes boats, trailers and boat trailers, travel trailers, pickup
campers or coaches (designed to be mounted on automotive vehicles), motorized dwellings, tent trailers,
horse trailers, utility trailers, etc., and cases or boxes used for transporting recreational equipment, whether
occupied by such equipment or not.

Recreational vehicle means a vehicle towed or self-propelled on its own chassis or attached to the chassis
of another vehicle and designed or used for a temporary dwelling, recreational or sporting purposes. Such
term shall include, but shall not be limited to, travel trailers, pickup campers, camping trailers and boats and
boat trailers.

Recreational vehicle camping area means any development, site, parcel or tract of land designed,
maintained or intended to be used for the purpose of providing shortterm (14 days or less) occupancy of
camper vehicles, recreational vehicles, tents or trailers.

Residence. See the definition of "Dwelling". When used with the term "district", the term "residence"
means an area of residential regulations.

Reversed frontage means a lot abutting two or more streets at their intersection. A reversed frontage lot
shall be deemed to front on that street at which it has its greatest frontage, unless otherwise specified by the
city manager.

Room means a building, or portion thereof, which is arranged, occupied or intended to be occupied as
living or sleeping quarters, but not including toilet or cooking facilities.

Roominghouse means a building, other than a hotel, where lodging for three, but not more than 12,
persons is provided for definite periods for compensation pursuant to previous arrangements.

Screening device means a fence, wall, hedge or other device which is solid, made of durable material and
without holes, penetrations or other openings other than those required for passage, and which is designed to
prevent persons from seeing through. A screening device shall be at least six feet, but not more than eight

303/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

feet, in height, unless otherwise specifically permitted by the provisions of this chapter or approved as a
variance by the zoning board of adjustment.

Seasonal color means landscape areas used for annual and perennial flowers intended to maintain yearround color accents.

Semi-nude means a state of dress in which clothing fails to completely and opaquely cover a human
buttock, anus, male genitals, female genitals, or any part of the female breast or breasts that is situated below
a point immediately above the top of the areola.

Setback means the distance from the property line to the nearest part of the building, structure or sign,
measured perpendicularly to the property line. See also "Building line". The nearest part of the building shall
include building projections such as eaves, awnings, window boxes, roof, and porch overhangs that extend
from the building or structure.

Sexual encounter center means a business or commercial enterprise that, as one of its primary business
purposes, offers any of the following for consideration:
(1)
Physical contact in the form of wrestling or tumbling between persons of the opposite sex; or
(2)
Activities between male and female persons and/or persons of the same sex when one or more of the persons
is in a state of nudity or semi-nude.

Sexually oriented business means an adult arcade, adult bookstore or adult video store, adult cabaret,
adult motel, adult motion picture theater, adult theater, escort agency, nude model studio or sexual encounter
center.

Showroom warehouse means a sales and office facility for a product that, by nature of the bulk
dimensions of the product, requires a larger than normal ratio of storage area to sales and office area to
maintain a normal operating product inventory. A showroom warehouse is specifically not intended to be a
wholesale distribution center.

Shrubs mean plants which grow vertically in a multibranched growth pattern.
Sign means a presentation of letters, numbers, figures, pictures, emblems, insignias, lines or colors, or any
combination thereof, displayed for the purpose of information, direction or identification, or to advertise or
promote a business, service, activity, interest or product.

Sign, abandoned, means any sign:
(1)
Which, for at least six continuous months, does not identify or advertise a bona de business, lessor, service,
owner, product or activity;
304/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(2)
For which no legal owner can be found; or
(3)
Which pertains to a time, event or purpose which no longer applies.

Sign, animated, means any sign having a conspicuous and intermittent variation in illumination, message
or physical position of any or all of its parts, or that uses movement or change of lighting to depict action or
create a special effect or scene.

Sign area means the area of the smallest individual rectangle, triangle or circle, or combination of not
more than two contiguous rectangles, triangles or circles, which will encompass all elements of the sign, which
form an integral part of the display, including background, borders and structural trim. The area of a doubleface sign shall be construed to be the area of the largest single face of the sign, provided, that the interior
angle formed by the two faces does not exceed 30 degrees.

Sign, building, means any sign attached to, applied on or supported by any part of a building, such as a
wall, roof, window, canopy, awning, arcade or marquee, that encloses or covers usable space, as contrasted to
a freestanding sign.

Sign, canopy, means any sign that is a part of or attached to an awning, canopy or other fabric, plastic or
structural protective cover over a door, entrance, window or outdoor service area. A marquee is not a canopy.

Sign, changeable copy, means a sign, or portion thereof, with characters, letters or illustrations that can be
changed or rearranged without altering the face or surface of the sign. A sign on which the message changes
more than eight times per day shall be considered an animated sign and not a changeable copy sign for the
purposes of this chapter. A sign on which the only copy that changes is an electronic or mechanical indication
of time and temperature shall be considered a time and temperature portion of a sign and not a changeable
copy sign for the purposes of this chapter.

Sign, detached, means any sign which is not attached, inclusive of signs on movable objects, except signs
on vehicles which are moving or are parked only temporarily, incidental to their principal use for
transportation.

Sign, dilapidated or deteriorated, means any sign:
(1)
Where any portion of the nished material, surface or message portion of the sign is visibly faded so as to no
longer be clearly read, aked, broken o , missing, cracked, splintered, defective or otherwise visibly deteriorated
or in a state of disrepair so as not to substantially appear as it was intended or designed to appear when
originally constructed; or
(2)
Whose elements or structural support or frame members are visibly bent, broken, dented, or torn, twisted,
leaning or at angles other than those at which it was originally erected, such as may result from being blown or
305/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

by the failure of a structural member.

Sign, directional, means an off-premises sign whose content is limited exclusively to the identification (for
commercial purposes) of a specific premises or occupancy located elsewhere, and which tells the location of or
route to such premises or occupancy.

Sign, freestanding, means any sign supported by structures or supports that are placed on or anchored in
the ground and that are independent from any building or other structure. Pole signs and monument signs
are examples of freestanding signs.

Sign height means the distance from the base of the sign at normal grade to the top of the highest
attached component of the sign. Normal grade shall be construed to be the lower of the existing grade prior to
construction, or the newly established grade after construction, exclusive of any filling, berming, mounding or
excavating solely for the purpose of locating the sign. In cases in which the normal grade cannot be reasonably
determined, sign height shall be computed on the assumption that the elevation of the normal grade at the
base of the sign is equal to the elevation of the nearest point of the crown of a public street or the grade of the
land at the principal entrance to the main building on the lot, whichever is lower.

Sign, incidental, means a sign, generally informational, that has a purpose secondary to the use of the lot
on which it is located, such as "no parking", "entrance", "loading only", "telephone" and other similar directives.
No sign with a commercial message greater that one square foot shall be considered as an incidental sign.

Sign, integral roof, means any sign erected or constructed as an integral, or essentially integral, part of a
normal roof structure of any design, such that no part of the sign extends vertically above the highest portion
of the roof and no part of the sign is separated from the rest of the roof by a space of more than six inches.

Sign, marquee, means any sign attached to, in any manner, or made a part of a marquee.
Sign, monument, means a freestanding sign having a low profile and made of stone, concrete, metal,
routed wood planks or beams, brick or similar materials, including individual lettering, which repeats or
harmonizes with the architecture of the establishment it serves. Monument signs must be built on a
monument base as opposed to a pole base. A monument sign may contain the name, logo, address, product
or service of the establishment, and a changeable copy panel.

Sign, nonconforming, means any sign that was lawfully constructed and maintained prior to the effective
date of the ordinance from which this section is derived and which does not conform to the requirements of
this chapter.

Sign, pole, means any sign which is mounted on a pole or structural support in such a manner that the
sign itself is not contiguous with the ground or mounted upon a building.

Sign, portable, means any sign not permanently attached to the ground or other permanent structure, or
a sign designed to be transported, including, but not limited to, signs designed to be transported by means of
wheels; signs converted to A-frame or T-frame; menu or sandwich board signs and umbrellas used for
306/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

advertising.

Sign, projecting, means any sign affixed to a building or wall in such a manner that its leading edge
extends more than six inches beyond the surface of such building or wall.

Sign, residential, means any temporary sign located in a district zoned for residential use, that may include
political matter; notice of sale or rent of the property upon which it is located; advertisement for home
contractors; or other messages not otherwise prohibited.

Sign, roof, means any sign erected and constructed wholly on and over the roof of a building; supported
by the roof structure; and extending vertically above the highest portion of the roof.

Sign, suspended, means a sign that is suspended from the underside of a horizontal plane surface and is
supported by such a surface.

Sign, temporary, means any sign that is used or only temporarily and is not permanently mounted.
Sign, vehicle, means any sign attached to or painted on vehicles parked and visible from the public rightof-way.

Sign, wall, means any sign attached parallel to, but within six inches of a wall, or is painted on the wall
surface, or erected and confined within the limits of an outside wall of any building or structure which is
supported by such a wall or building, and which displays only one sign surface.

Sign, window, means any sign, picture or symbol, or any combination thereof, designed to communicate
information about an activity, business, commodity, event, sale or service, that is placed inside a window or
upon the windowpanes or glass and is visible from the exterior of the window.

Special exception means a use that would not be appropriate generally or without restriction throughout
the zoning district, but which, if controlled as to number, area, location or relation to the neighborhood, would
be wholly compatible with conditions affecting the public health, safety, welfare, morals, order, comfort,
convenience, appearance, prosperity or general welfare. Such uses may be permitted in such zoning district as
special exceptions if approved by the zoning board of adjustment (see article III, division 3 of this chapter).

Special interest vehicle means a motor vehicle of any age that has not changed from the original
manufacturer's specifications, and because of its historic interest, is being preserved by a hobbyist.

Specified anatomical areas means:
(1)
Any of the following, or any combination of the following, when less than completely and opaquely covered:

Any human genitals, pubic region or pubic hair;

Any buttock; or

Specified sexual activities means and includes any of the following:
(1)
The fondling or other erotic touching of human genitals, pubic region, buttocks, anus or female breasts;

Sex acts, normal or perverted, actual or stimulated, including intercourse, oral copulation or sodomy;

Stable or barn, commercial, means a structure or building used for the boarding and quartering of horses,
cows or other domestic livestock on a fee or other remuneration basis.

Stable or barn, private, means a structure or building used for quartering horses, cows or other domestic
livestock of the property owner.

Story means the part of a building included between the surface of one floor and the surface of the floor
next above, or if there is no floor above, that part of the building which is above the surface of the highest
floor thereof. A top story attic is a half story when the main line of the eaves is not above the middle of the
interior height of such story. The first story is the middle of the interior height of such story. The first story is
the highest story having its interior floor surface not more than four feet above the curb level, established or
mean street grade or average ground level.

Street means a public way between two right-of-way lines, other than an alley or private drive, which has
been dedicated or deeded to the public and accepted by the city for public use and affords a principal means
of access (vehicular or otherwise) to property abutting thereon, as well as for utilities and sidewalks.

Street frontage means the distance for which a lot line of a lot adjoins a public street, from one lot line
intersecting such street to the furthest distant lot line intersecting the same street.

Street line means the right-of-way of a street.
Structural alteration means any change in the supporting members of a building, such as bearing walls,
columns, beams or girders, or any substantial change in the roof or exterior walls, except such repair or
replacement as may be required for the safety of the building, but not including openings in bearing walls as
permitted by the city building code.

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Structure means anything constructed or erected with a fixed location on the ground, or attached to
something having a fixed location on the ground. Such term includes, but is not limited to, buildings, mobile
homes, billboards and poster panels.

Subdivision ordinance means the latest approved ordinance providing for the division or redivision of land
into two or more lots, tracts, sites or parcels for the purpose of development (chapter 82 of this Code).

Substantial enlargement of a sexually oriented business means the increase in floor area occupied by the
business by more than 25 percent, as the floor area existed on the effective date of the ordinance from which
this section derives, or under a certificate of occupancy therefor.

Thoroughfare has the meaning as defined in the city's latest approved subdivision ordinance (chapter 82
of this Code).

Tourist home or dude ranch means a dwelling in which accommodations are provided or offered for
transient or temporary guests for compensation.

Tower means any structure that is designed and constructed primarily for the purpose of supporting one
or more antennae, including self-supporting lattice towers, guyed towers or monopole towers. Such term
includes radio and television transmission towers, microwave towers, common carrier towers, personal
telecommunications towers and similar structures.

Townhouse means a single-family dwelling facility constructed in a series, or group of units having
common walls, each on a separate lot of record.

Transfer of ownership or control of a sexually oriented business means and includes any of the following:
(1)
The sale, lease or sublease of the business;
(2)
The transfer of securities which constitute a controlling interest in the business, whether by sale, exchange or
similar means; or
(3)
The establishment of a trust, gift or other similar legal device which transfers the ownership or control of the
business, except for transfer by bequest or other operation of law upon the death of the person possessing the
ownership or control.

Travel trailer means a mobile vehicle built on a chassis and designed and used as a temporary place of
dwelling, and of such size and design as to be subject to licensing for towing on the highway by a passenger
motor vehicle or other prime mover and not requiring a special permit for moving on the highway as
contrasted to a mobile home.

309/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Understory/accent tree means a small evergreen or deciduous perennial woody plant which would grow
below the top layer of the forest and typically has unique branching and textural or seasonal color
characteristics.

Used or occupied includes the term "intended", "designed" or "arranged to be used or occupied".
Utility facility means any water supply, water treatment, water pumping, water storage or other water
facility; any sewerage treatment or pumping facility; any electrical generating facility, electrical transmission,
switching facility or electrical substation; any telephone exchange or other similar telephone communication
facility; any natural gas pumping or storage facility; or any cable television receiving or transmission facility,
when owned and operated by the city, or any utility or communications concern operating under a franchise
approved by the city council.

Variance means a relaxation of the terms of this chapter where such variance will not be contrary to the
public interest and where, owing to conditions peculiar to the property and not the result of the actions of the
applicant, a literal enforcement of this chapter would result in unnecessary and undue hardship. Except as
specifically authorized in article III, division 3 and article IV of this chapter, a variance is authorized only for
height, area and size of structures or size of yards and open spaces. The establishment or expansion of a use
otherwise prohibited shall not be allowed by a variance, except as provided in article III, division 3 and article
IV of this chapter, nor shall a variance be granted because of the presence of nonconformities in the zoning
district or uses in an adjoining zoning district.

Yard means a required open space, other than a court unoccupied and unobstructed by any structure, or
portion of a structure, from 30 inches above the general ground level of the graded lot upward; provided,
however, that fences, walls, poles, posts and other customary yard accessories, ornaments, furniture and roof
overhangs not exceeding 30 inches may be permitted in any yard subject to height limitations and
requirements limiting obstruction of visibility.

Yard, front: A yard extending between side lot lines across the front of a lot adjoining a public street. (See
Figure 3.)
(1)
In the case of through lots, unless the prevailing front yard pattern on adjoining lots indicates otherwise, front
yards shall be provided on all frontages. Where one of the front yards that would normally be required on a
through lot is not in keeping with the prevailing yard pattern, the city manager may waive the requirement for
the normal front yard and substitute therefore a special yard requirement which shall not exceed the average of
the yards provided on adjacent lots.
(2)
In the case of reversed frontage corner lots, a front yard of the required depth shall be provided on either
frontage, and a second front yard of the depths required for second front yards in the district shall be provided
on the other frontage.
(3)
310/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

In the case of corner lots with more than two frontages, the city manager shall determine the front yard
requirements, subject to the following limitations:
a.
At least one front yard shall be provided having the full depth required generally in the district;
b.
No other front yard on such lot shall have less than the minimum required second front yard for corner lots.
(4)
Depth of required front yards shall be measured from the front lot line to the nearest part of the building,
structure or sign, measured perpendicularly to the front lot line. See also "Building line". The nearest part of the
building shall include building projections such as eaves, awnings, window boxes, roof, and porch overhangs
that extend from the building or structure.

Yard, rear, A yard extending across the rear of the lot between lot lines. In the case of through lots there
will be no rear yards, but only front and side yards. All other lots will have a rear yard. (See Figure 3.)
(1)
Depth of a required rear yard shall be measured in such a manner that the yard established is a strip of the
minimum depth required by district regulations with its inner edge parallel with the rear lot line. The minimum
depth required by district regulations shall be measured from the rear lot line to the nearest part of the
building, structure or sign, measured perpendicularly to the rear lot line. See also "Building line". The nearest
part of the building shall include building projections such as eaves, awnings, window boxes, roof, and porch
overhangs that extend from the building or structure.
(2)
In cases where a rear lot line is not evident, or if evident but not parallel to the front building line, the minimum
rear yard requirement shall be the distance from the rear-most point of the lot along a line from that point
drawn perpendicular to a line drawn from the foremost points of the two side lots, providing that the rear yard
is parallel to at least one lot line along the rear of the lot.

Yard, side: A yard extending from the rear line of the required front yard to the front of the required rear
yard, or in absence of any clearly defined rear lot line to the point on the lot farthest from the intersection of
the lot line involved with the public street. In the case of through lots, side yards shall extend from the rear
lines of front yards required. (See Figure 3.)
(1)
Width of a required side yard shall be measured in such a manner that the yard established is a strip of the
minimum width required by district regulations with its inner edge parallel with the side lot line.
(2)
The minimum width required by district regulations shall be measured from from the side lot line to the nearest
part of the building, structure or sign, measured perpendicularly to the side lot line. See also "Building line". The
nearest part of the building shall include building projections such as eaves, awnings, window boxes, roof, and
porch overhangs that extend from the building or structure.
311/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Yard, special, means a yard behind any required yard adjacent to a public street, required to perform the
same functions as a side or rear yard, but adjacent to a lot line placed or oriented so that neither the term
"side yard" or "rear yard" clearly applies. In such cases, the administrative official shall require a yard with
minimum dimensions as generally required for a side yard or rear yard in the district in which such lot is
located, determining which shall apply by the relation of the portion of the lot on which the yard is to be
located to the adjoining lots, with due regard to the orientation and location of structures and buildable areas
thereon.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 4, 2-21-2000; Ord. No. 2-19-04-2, § 2, 2-19-2004; Ord. No. 06-13-05-3, § 4, 6-13-2005)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.

Sec. 102-3. - Interpretation and purposes.
In their interpretation and application, the provisions of this chapter shall be held to be the minimum
requirements adopted for the promotion of the public health, safety and welfare. The zoning regulations and
districts established in this chapter have been made in accordance with a comprehensive plan for the purpose
of promoting the health, safety, morals and general welfare of the city; lessen, among other things, congestion
in the streets; secure safety from fire, panic and other dangers; provide adequate light and pure air; avoid
undue concentration of population; and facilitate adequate provisions for transportation, water, sewerage,
schools, parking areas and other public requirements.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 2, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-4. - Scope.
It is not intended by this chapter to repeal, abrogate, annul or in any way impair or interfere with existing
provisions of other laws or ordinances (except as they may be specifically repealed by the terms of this
chapter), or with private restrictions placed upon property by covenant, deed, easement or other private
agreement. Where this chapter imposes a greater restriction upon land, buildings or structures than is
imposed or required by other laws, ordinances, deeds, covenants or agreements, the provisions of this
chapter shall govern.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 3, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-5. - Saving clause.
All rights or remedies of the city are expressly saved as to any and all violations of this chapter or any
zoning ordinance or amendments thereto of the city that have accrued at the time of the effective date of the
ordinance from which this section is derived; and as to such accrued violations, the court shall have all of the
powers that existed prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this section is derived; and all
existing violations of previous zoning or building ordinances which would otherwise become nonconforming
312/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

uses under this chapter shall not become legal nonconforming uses under this chapter, but shall be
considered as violations of this chapter in the same manner that they were violations of prior zoning
ordinances of the city.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 32, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-6. - Violations; penalties.
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects or refuses to comply with, or who resists the
enforcement of, any of the provisions of this chapter shall be fined not less than $5.00, nor more than
$2,000.00 for each offense. Each day that a violation of this chapter exists shall constitute a separate offense.
The penalty set forth in this section should not be construed as exclusive, and the city is provided that any
other remedy available to it, in law or in equity, is not intended to be, and is not foreclosed by the provision of
such penalty.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 7, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-7. - Injunction; civil penalties.
The city shall have and retain the right to seek injunctive relief and/or civil penalties against any person
who is in the process of violating, or about to violate, any section, paragraph or part of this chapter. Such right
for injunctive relief and/or civil penalties shall exist independent of the other penalty provisions of this
chapter, and not in lieu thereof.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 29, 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-8—102-40. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - ZONING CODE
Sec. 102-41. - Uniform Zoning Code adopted.
There is adopted by reference, as if set out fully in this section, the publication known as the Uniform
Zoning Code, 1997 edition, as published by the International Conference of Building Officials. The Uniform
Zoning Code shall be maintained as a public record in the office of the building official and is available for
public inspection and copying during regular business hours.
Secs. 102-42—102-70. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY

313/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 102-71. - Fees, charges and expenses.
The city council shall establish a schedule of fees, charges and expenses and a collection procedure for
building permits, certificates of zoning compliance, appeals, applications for amendments and other matters
pertaining to this chapter. No action shall be taken on any application or appeal until all applicable fees,
charges and expenses have been paid in full.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 30, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-72. - Limitation of reapplication for zoning classi cation.
When the city council has denied a proposal with prejudice, or when the applicant has withdrawn his
proposal after notice has been made of the planning and zoning commission's meeting on such proposal, no
reapplication requesting the same zoning classification shall be accepted by the city or scheduled for hearing
by the planning and zoning commission within a period of 12 months from the city council's denial with
prejudice or the applicant's withdrawal; provided, however, upon receipt of a request stating how conditions
have changed substantially within the city since the prior denial with prejudice or withdrawal, the planning and
zoning commission may waive the mandatory delay period and authorize the acceptance of a new application.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 33, 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-73—102-90. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
Sec. 102-91. - Established.
There is established a planning and zoning commission for the city. The power and authority of the
planning and zoning commission shall be advisory only.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-8, 12-13-1999)

Sec. 102-92. - Appointment of members; terms; vacancy.
The planning and zoning commission shall consist of five members to be duly appointed by the city
council. Councilmembers of each ward shall propose one nominee per ward. The nominee need not be a
resident of the ward of the councilmember who nominates him, but must be a resident of the city or its
extraterritorial jurisdiction (ETJ). The fifth member of the planning and zoning commission shall be appointed
by the mayor. Members of the planning and zoning commission shall serve for a period of two years, except
for the initial appointments, of which two appointees shall serve for a period of one year and shall be the
appointees from the odd-numbered wards. Vacancies shall be filled by appointment of the city council for the
unexpired term.
(Ord. No. 12-13-99-8, § 1, 12-13-1999)
314/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 102-93. - Ex o cio members.
The city planner or the official acting in such capacity shall be an ex officio member of the planning and
zoning commission.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 2, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-94. - O cers; minutes; meetings.
The planning and zoning commission shall elect from its members a chairman, vice-chairman and such
other officers as may be deemed necessary, for a period of one year. The planning and zoning commission
shall adopt rules for the practical and efficient transaction of its business; and its findings, determinations and
other actions shall be recorded in its minutes, which record shall be a public record. At least one meeting per
month shall be held and additional meetings may be held from time to time upon the call of the chairman. If a
member should fail to attend three consecutive regular monthly commission of the planning and zoning
commission, such member shall be automatically dropped from the planning and zoning commission and a
vacancy thereon shall be declared.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 2, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-95. - Duties.
(a)
The planning and zoning commission shall respond to requests and directives of the city council, and shall have
the power to promote public interest in and understanding of the comprehensive plan and planning, and
consult and advise with public o cials and agencies, public utilities, civic education professionals and other
organizations and citizens in relation to the protection and carrying out of the comprehensive plan or special
planning projects or reports.
(b)
Through the city manager, all public o cials shall furnish to the planning and zoning commission, within a
reasonable time, such available information as it may reasonably require for its work.
(c)
It shall be a function and duty of the planning and zoning commission to review and recommend to the city
council any updates, changes or additions to the comprehensive plan of the city (1990) for the physical
development of the city and any land outside the city limits but within its extraterritorial jurisdiction (ETJ) which,
in the opinion of the planning and zoning commission, bears a relation to the city. Such recommendations for
development shall include, but not be limited to, the development of streets, bridges, parks, waterways and
other public ways, grounds, places and spaces; the general location and extent of public utilities, whether
publicly-owned or privately-owned, for water, light, sanitation, transportation, communication, power, heat, fuel
and other purposes; and the removal, relocation, widening, extension, narrowing, vacating, abandonment or
change of use of such existing or future public ways, grounds, places, spaces, buildings, property or utilities.
(d)
315/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

For continuity, communication and good management, actions taken or recommended as a result of this
chapter, shall be recommended to the city council and coordinated through the o ce of the city manager, who
in turn will provide liaison to the planning and zoning commission.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 3, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-96. - Recommendations.
The planning and zoning commission shall make recommendations for a zoning ordinance zoning and
subdivision ordinance, and shall review requests for variances from such ordinances and make
recommendations to the city council regarding such variance requests.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 4, 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-97—102-120. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - ZONING BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT
Sec. 102-121. - Purpose.
It is the declared purpose of this chapter that nonconforming uses be eliminated and be required to
conform to the regulations prescribed in this chapter, having due regard for the property rights of the persons
affected when considered in light of the public welfare and the character of the area surrounding the
designated nonconforming use and the conservation and preservation of property. The city council shall, from
time to time, on its own motion or upon cause presented by interested property owners, inquire into the
existence, continuation or maintenance of any nonconforming use within the city.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 21(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-122. - Organization.
(a)
A zoning board of adjustment shall be established and have all of the powers and authority in accordance with
V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 211.008, as amended. The board shall consist of ve voting members
appointed by the city council. Members of the board shall serve two-year terms, with places 1, 3 and 5
appointed in odd-numbered years and places 2 and 4 appointed in even-numbered years. In addition, the city
council may appoint up to four alternates to serve in the absence of any board member. The board shall elect a
chairman from its members. Any member or alternate of the board may be removed for just cause by the city
council. For the purposes of this subsection, the term "just cause" includes three unexcused absences from
regular or special meetings of the board. Vacancies shall be lled by appointment by the city council of a
suitable person to serve out the unexpired term of any person whose place on the board, either as a member or
alternate, has become vacant for any cause.
(b)

316/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The board may adopt rules to govern its proceedings; provided, however, that such rules are not inconsistent
with the terms of this chapter. Meetings of the board shall be held at the call of the chairman, who may
administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses. All meetings of the board shall be open to the public.
The board shall keep minutes of its proceedings, showing the vote of each member upon each question, or, if
absent or failing to vote, indicating such fact, and shall keep records of its examinations and other o cial
actions, all of which shall be led in the o ces of the board and kept as a public record.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 21(B), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-123. - Jurisdiction.
The zoning board of adjustment shall have all powers granted, and be organized and controlled, by the
provisions of V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 211.009. The board is vested with power and authority, and in
appropriate cases and subject to appropriate conditions and safeguards, to make such exemptions and
exceptions to the terms of this chapter in harmony with its general purposes and intent in accordance with
general or special rules contained in this chapter for the purpose of rendering full justice and equity to the
general public.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 21(C), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-124. - Power.
The zoning board of adjustment shall have the following powers:
(1)

Variances. The board may authorize a variance from the regulations set forth in this chapter when, in its
opinion, undue hardship will result from requiring strict compliance with such regulations. In granting a
variance, the board shall prescribe only conditions that it deems necessary or desirable to protect the public
interest. In making its ndings as required in this section, the board shall take into account the nature of the
proposed use of the land involved; existing uses of land in the vicinity; and the probable e ect such variance will
have upon tra c conditions and the public health, safety, convenience and welfare in the vicinity. No variance
shall be granted unless the board nds that:
Such findings of the board, together with the specific facts upon which such findings are based,
shall be incorporated into the official minutes of the meeting of the board at which such variance
is granted. Variances may be granted only when in harmony with the general purpose and intent
of this chapter so that the public health, safety and welfare may be secured and substantial
justice done. Pecuniary hardship to the applicant, standing alone, shall not be deemed to
constitute an undue hardship.
a.
There were special circumstances or conditions a ecting the land involved such that the strict application of the
provisions of this chapter deprive the applicant of reasonable use of his land;
b.
317/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The variance is necessary for the preservation and enjoyment of a substantial property right of the applicant;
c.
The granting of the variance will not be detrimental to the public health, safety or welfare, or injurious to other
property in the area; and
d.
The granting of a variance will not have the e ect of preventing the orderly development of other land in the
area in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
(2)

Special exceptions. The board may permit a special exception when such use or development is speci cally
authorized under subsection (1) of this section. In reaching its decision, the board shall determine that the
requested exception will establish only the uses permitted under this chapter; that the location of the proposed
activities and improvements are clearly de ned on the site plan led by the applicant; and that the exception
will be wholly compatible with the use and permitted development of adjacent properties either as led or
subject to such requirements as the board nds to be necessary to protect and maintain the stability of adjacent
properties.
(3)

Appeals of decisions of administrative o cers.
a.
The board may hear and decide appeals where it is alleged that there is an error in any order, requirement,
decision or determination made by the administrative o cer in the enforcement of this chapter.
b.
In exercising its power, the board may, in conformity with the provisions of V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch.
211, revise or reform, wholly or partly, or may modify the order, requirement, decision or determination as
sought to be made, and shall have all of the powers of the o cer from whom the appeal is taken, and may
require such conditions and safeguards as the board nds necessary to preserve the spirit and intent of this
chapter.
(4)

Nonconforming uses.
a.
The board may permit the reconstruction, extension or enlargement of a building occupied by a preexisting
nonconforming use on the lot occupied by such building, provided, such reconstruction does not prevent the
return of such property to a conforming use.
b.
The board may require the discontinuance of nonconforming uses under any plan whereby the full value of the
structure or use can be amortized within a de nite period of time, taking into consideration the general
character of the neighborhood and the necessity for all property to conform to the regulations of this chapter.
c.
The board may determine whether an existing nonconforming animal lot, barn or stable may continue, with
additional restrictions, or be discontinued if petitioned under the provisions of article IV of this chapter. In
318/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

making its determination, the board shall consider public health, animal welfare and nuisance conditions, as
well as the general character of the neighborhood.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 21(F), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-126. - Concurring vote.
The concurring vote of four members of the zoning board of adjustment shall be necessary to reverse any
order, requirement, decision or determination of the administrative officer, or to decide in favor of the
application on any matter upon which it is required to pass under this chapter or to affect any variance in this
chapter.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 21(G), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-127. - Appeals; stay of proceedings.
319/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(a)
Appeals to the zoning board of adjustment can be taken by any person aggrieved by any o cer, department or
board of the city or a ected by any decision of the administrative o cer. Such appeal shall be taken within 15
days after the decision has been rendered by the administrative o cer, by ling a notice with the o cer from
whom the appeal is taken and the board specifying the grounds of such appeal. The o cer from whom the
appeal is taken shall forthwith transmit to the board all of the papers constituting the record upon which the
action appealed from was taken.
(b)
An appeal shall stay all proceedings of the action appealed from, unless the o cer from whom the appeal is
taken certi es to the board, after the notice of appeal shall have been led with him, that, by reason of facts
stated in the certi cate, a stay would, in his opinion, cause imminent peril to life or property. In such a case,
proceedings shall not be stayed, other than by a restraining order which may be granted by the board or a court
of record on application, after notice to the o cer from whom the appeal is taken on due case shown.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 21(D), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-128. - Hearings.
(a)
The zoning board of adjustment shall x a reasonable time for the hearing of any appeal, variance, special
exception or other matter which the board is authorized to review under this division, give public notice thereof,
as well as due notice to the parties and interests, and decide the matter within a reasonable time. Upon the
hearing, any party may appear in person or by attorney or agent. The notice provided in this section shall be
given by publication in the o cial city publication, stating the time and place of such hearing, which shall not be
earlier than ten days from the day of such publication, and in addition, the board shall mail notices of such
hearing to the petitioner and the owners of property lying within 200 feet of any point of the lot, or portion
thereof, on which an appeal, variance, exception or other action is proposed, and to all persons deemed by the
board to be a ected. Such property owners and persons shall be determined according to the current tax rolls
of the city and substantial compliance therewith shall be deemed su cient; provided, however, that the
depositing of such written notice in the mail by the board shall be deemed su cient compliance with the
purpose of this subsection.
(b)
Any special exceptions authorized by the board, either under the provisions of this chapter or under the
authority granted to the board under state statutes, shall authorize the issuance of a building permit for a
period of 90 days from the date of the favorable action on the part of the board, unless the board, in its
minutes, shall, at the same time, grant a longer period. If a building permit shall not have been issued within
such 90-day period or as the board may speci cally grant, the special exceptions shall be deemed to be waived,
and all rights under such special exceptions shall be terminated. Such termination and waiver shall be without
prejudice to a subsequent appeal to the board in accordance with the rules and regulations regarding appeals.
(c)

320/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The same appeal to the board shall not be allowed on the same piece of property prior to the expiration of one
year from a ruling of the board on any appeal to the board, unless other property in the same zoned areas shall
have, within such one-year period, been altered or changed by ruling of the board, in which case, such change of
circumstance shall permit the allowance of an appeal, but shall in no way have force in law to compel the board,
after a hearing to grant such subsequent appeal, but such appeal shall be considered on its merits, as in all
other cases.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 21(E), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-129. - Grievances.
Any persons, jointly or separately, aggrieved by any decision of the zoning board of adjustment or any
taxpayer or officer, department or board of the city may present to a court of record a petition, duly verified,
setting forth that such decision is illegal, in whole or in part, and specifying the grounds of such illegality. Such
petition shall be presented to the court within ten days of the questioned decision of the board, and not after
such ten-day period, and shall comply in all respects with the requirements set forth in V.T.C.A., Local
Government Code § 211.011.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 2(H), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-130—102-150. - Reserved.
DIVISION 4. - PERMITS AND CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY
Sec. 102-151. - Building permits.
All applications for building permits shall be accompanied by a drawing or plat, in triplicate, showing the
lot plan; the location of the building on the lot; accurate dimensions of the building and lot; and such other
information as may be necessary to provide for the enforcement of the regulations set forth in this chapter.
The plat shall be prepared after the lot has been staked by a licensed surveyor. A careful record of the original
copy of such application and plat shall be kept in the office of the building official and a duplicate copy shall be
at the building site at all times during construction.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 24, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-152. - Conditional uses.
(a)

Purpose. The purpose of the conditional use procedure is to allow for review of uses which would not be
appropriate generally or without certain restriction throughout a zoning district, but which, if controlled as to
the number, area, location or relation to the neighborhood would promote the health, safety, and welfare of the
community. The procedure is intended to allow board public review and evaluation of the proposed
development and to ensure adequate mitigation of potentially unfavorable impacts.
(b)
321/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Conditional use permits.
(1)

Permit Required. No conditional use shall be established, operated, or maintained except as authorized by a
conditional use permit issued in accordance with the requirements of this section.
(2)

Conditional use permit issued by city council. A conditional use permit may be issued only for the conditional
uses permitted by the city's zoning ordinances, and for substantially similar uses, and only for the district where
the conditional use is authorized. A conditional use permit may be issued by the city council acting after a public
hearing and a recommendation on the proposed use from the planning and zoning commission (the
"Commission").
(3)

Application. An application for a conditional use permit shall be made in writing in a form prescribed by the city
secretary and shall be accompanied by such information as may be requested (including a site plan, if required)
in order to properly review the proposed use. Such information may include, but is not limited to, site and
building plans, drawings and elevations, and operational data.
(4)

Report by the city inspector or city manager. Either the city inspector or the city manager shall visit the site of
the proposed conditional use and the surrounding area and shall prepare ndings to be delivered to the
planning and zoning commission and to the city council.
(5)

Notice—public hearing by planning and zoning commission.
a.
The commission shall hold a public hearing on each application for a conditional use permit.
b.
Written notice of such hearing shall be given to the owners of all real property located within 200 feet in all
directions of the property that is the subject of the hearing. Notice shall be given not less than ten days prior to
the date of the hearing either by personal service or by depositing a copy of the notice in the mail addressed to
each owner at his address shown on the last approved city tax roll, with postage paid.
c.
Such notice shall state the purpose, date, time, and place of the hearing and shall contain a brief description of
the proposed development, including its nature, scope, and location. The notice shall also describe any
variances the applicant has requested and shall state the location and times at which the applications and
supporting documents are available for public inspection. The time and place of the public hearing to be held
before the city council shall also be included if known at the time the notice is given and, if it is not known at
such time, a telephone number shall be provided where information on the hearing before the city council will
be available at a later date.
(6)

Review and recommendation by the planning and zoning commission.
a.
322/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The commission shall review the application for a conditional use permit to determine whether the proposed
conditional use complies with each of the general criteria in subsection (c) of this section and with each of the
speci c criteria in subsection (d) of this section applicable to the proposed use, and shall make a separate
nding thereon for each criterion.
b.
The commission shall not recommend approval of an application unless it nds that the proposed conditional
use as presented or as modi ed by the commission, complies with each of the general and applicable speci c
criteria.
c.
A recommendation of approval may be conditioned on the applicant's adoption of speci ed changes, additions,
limitations, safeguards, or e ective time periods designed to assure compliance with the criteria.
(7)

Hearing before city council. The city council shall review an application for a conditional use permit at a public
hearing after receiving ndings and a recommendation from the planning and zoning commission.
(8)

Review and action by city council.
a.
The city council shall determine whether the proposed conditional use complies with each of the general criteria
in subsection (c) of this section and with each of the special criteria in subsection (d) of this section applicable to
the proposed use and shall make separate ndings thereon or adopt the ndings made by the commission.
b.
The city council may condition its approval of an application on the applicant's adoption of speci ed changes,
additions, limitations, safeguards, or e ective time periods designed to assure compliance with the criteria.
c.
The city council shall not grant a conditional use permit unless it nds that the proposed conditional use, as
presented or as modi ed by the council, complies with each of the applicable general and speci c criteria;
otherwise it shall deny the application.
(c)

General criteria applicable to all conditional uses. A proposed conditional use permit must comply with all the
following criteria:
(1)
The appearance, size, density and operating characteristics of the proposed conditional use are compatible with
the surrounding neighborhood and uses;
(2)
Any construction, remodel, improvement or alteration of any structure shall comply with the height and area
regulations for the particular district in which the structure is located and shall be compatible with the
appearance and operating characteristics of the surrounding neighborhood;
(3)
The proposed use will not have an adverse e ect on the value of surrounding properties nor impede their
proper development;
323/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(4)
The proposed use will not create a nuisance factor nor otherwise interfere with a neighbor's enjoyment of his
property or operation of his business;
(5)
The tra c that the proposed use can reasonably be expected to generate on existing streets will not create nor
add signi cantly to congestion, a safety hazard, or a parking problem in the area, nor will it disturb the peace
and quiet of the neighborhood;
(6)
Parking requirements applicable to a property shall be determined by the use of the property as provided in art.
VII, div. 2 of this Code entitled "Parking and Vehicular Circulation Regulations"; upon expiration, lapse, or
revocation of a conditional use permit, the current existing permitted use of the property shall determine the
parking regulations applicable to the property until such time that another conditional use permit may be
granted or the use otherwise changes; and
(7)
The proposed use complies with all other applicable ordinances and regulations.
(d)

Criteria applicable to individual conditional uses. The "B-1" Neighborhood Business Uses permitted as
conditional uses in the Single Family district, the Duplex Residential District, the "MH-1" Manufactured Home
District-1, and the "MH-2" Manufactured Home District-2 must comply with all the following speci c criteria as
well as the foregoing general criteria:
Signage. A freestanding sign or building sign pertaining to the identification of a building,
business, product(s), or service(s) manufactured, sold or offered on the premises where the sign
is located may be erected and maintained upon any premise where a "B-1" Neighborhood
Business Use is permitted; provided that not more than one sign shall be erected or maintained
upon any premise. The sign shall not exceed six square feet. No portable sign or animated sign
shall be erected or maintained on a premise. Signs shall be maintained in good, safe condition
and shall not be allowed to become dilapidated or deteriorated. Applicants wishing to erect and
maintain a sign shall submit a site development plan showing the proposed location of the sign in
relation to existing structures on the property. Location of the sign shall be approved prior to
erection of the sign as part of the conditional use permit procedure.
(e)

General requirements for all conditional uses.
(1)

Adherence to approved plans, regulations. A conditional use shall be established, operated and maintained in
accordance with the plans, terms, conditions, and limitations contained in the permit approved by the city
council.
(2)

Duration. Conditional use permits may be granted for a de nite or an inde nite period of time.
(3)
324/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Revocation. The city council, after notice and public hearing, may revoke any conditional use permit for one or
more of the following reasons:
a.
A substantial violation of any of the plans, terms, conditions, and limitations applicable to the conditional use;
b.
A substantial violation of any applicable ordinance or regulation;
c.
Operation or maintenance of the conditional use in a manner that is detrimental to the public's health or safety,
or so as to constitute a nuisance; and/or
d.
Discontinuance of the use.
(4)

Lapse of Permit. A conditional use permit shall lapse if the use has not been commenced, or, in the case of
construction, if construction has not been commenced, within one year of the date the permit was issued.
(5)

Transfer. A conditional use permit is not transferable and shall cease upon transfer.
(6)

Professional and consulting fees and ling fees. Each applicant must pay all professional and consulting fees, if
any, and ling fees, if any.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 17, 2-21-2000; Ord. No. 2-19-04-1, § 17, 2-19-2004)

Sec. 102-153. - Certi cate of occupancy.
(a)
No vacant land shall be occupied or used, except for agricultural purposes, and no building erected,
reconstructed, altered, enlarged or vacated shall be occupied or used until a certi cate of occupancy shall have
been issued by the building o cial stating that the building, or proposed use of a building or premises, complies
with the building laws and provisions of this chapter.
(b)
Certi cates of occupancy shall be applied for coincident with the application for a building permit, and shall be
issued within ten days after the erection or structural alteration of such building shall have been completed in
conformity with the provisions of this chapter and any other city ordinance and approval of all required
inspections. Approval of the nal building inspection by the building inspection department shall serve as a
certi cate of occupancy for all one-family and two-family residential dwelling units.
(c)
Certi cates of occupancy shall be required for all legal nonconforming uses. Application for a certi cate of
occupancy for such nonconforming uses shall be led within 12 months from the e ective date of the ordinance
from which this section is derived, accompanied by a davits of proof that such nonconforming uses were not
established in violation of this chapter or any previous zoning ordinance.
(d)
325/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

A certi cate of occupancy shall state that the building, or proposed use of a building or land, complies with all
building and health laws and ordinances and the provisions of this chapter. A record of all certi cates of
occupancy shall be kept on le in the o ce of the building inspector, and copies shall be furnished, upon
request, to any person having a proprietary or tenancy interest in the building a ected. No fee shall be charged
for a certi cate of occupancy for a legal nonconforming use.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 22, 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-154—102-180. - Reserved.
DIVISION 5. - ENFORCEMENT
Sec. 102-181. - Administrator; right of entry.
The provisions of this chapter shall be administered by the city manager or his duly authorized
representative. The city manager or any duly authorized person shall have the right to enter upon
any premises at any reasonable time for the purpose of making inspections of buildings or
premises which are necessary to carry out the enforcement of this chapter.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 28, 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-182—102-210. - Reserved.
ARTICLE IV. - NONCONFORMING USES AND STRUCTURES
Sec. 102-211. - Nonconforming uses.
(a)

General policy. The general public, the city council and the commission are directed to take note that
nonconformities in the use and development of land and buildings are to be avoided, or eliminated where now
existing, whenever and wherever possible, except:
(1)
When necessary to preserve property rights established prior to the date these regulations become e ective as
to the property in question; and
(2)
When necessary to promote the general welfare and to protect the character of the surrounding property.
(b)

Nonconforming structures. Where a lawful structure exists on the e ective date of the adoption or amendment
of the city zoning ordinance, that could not be built under the terms the zoning ordinance or amendment
thereto, by reason of restrictions on permitted use, area, lot coverage, height, years, its locations on the lot, or
other requirements concerning the structure, such structure may be continued as long as it remains otherwise
lawful, subject to the following provisions:
326/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(1)
No such nonconforming structure may be enlarged or altered in a way which increases its structural
nonconformity, but any structure or portion thereof may be altered to decrease its structural nonconformity.
(2)
Should such nonconforming structure or nonconforming portions of a structure be damaged by any means to
an extent of more than 50 percent of its replacement cost at the time of destruction, it shall not be
reconstructed except in conformity with these regulations.
(3)
Should such structure be moved for any reason for any distance whatsoever, it shall thereafter conform to the
regulations of the district in which it is located after it is moved.
(c)

Nonconforming uses. A nonconforming use may be continued as long as it remains otherwise lawful, subject to
the following provisions:
(1)
No existing structure devoted to a nonconforming use shall be enlarged, extended, constructed or
reconstructed.
(2)
The use of the structure shall only be changed to a use permitted in the district in which it is located.
(3)
A nonconforming use that has been discontinued may be resumed only if there has been no other use of the
premises or structure since the nonconforming use was discontinued, and such use was not discontinued for a
period of 12 months or more.
(4)
Any nonconforming use may be extended throughout any parts of a building which were manifestly arranged or
designed for such use at the time of adoption or amendment of these regulations, but no such use shall be
extended to any land outside such building.
(5)
Removal or destruction of a structure containing a nonconforming use shall eliminate the nonconforming use
status. Destruction for the purpose of this subsection is de ned as damage equal to more than 50 percent of
the replacement cost of the structure.
(d)

Repairs and maintenance. On any nonconforming structure, or nonconforming portion of a structure,
containing a nonconforming use, repairs and maintenance shall be performed to maintain the structure in
compliance with the electrical, plumbing and building codes; provided that such repairs and maintenance shall
be subject to the following conditions and limitations:
(1)
If 50 percent or more of the nonconforming structure containing a nonconforming use becomes physically
unsafe or unlawful due to lack of repairs or maintenance, and is declared by a duly authorized o cial to be
unsafe or unlawful by reason of physical condition, it shall not thereafter be restored, repaired or rebuilt except
in conformity with the regulations of the district in which it is located.
327/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 6-11-07-1, § 2, 6-11-2007)

Secs. 102-212—102-250. - Reserved.

Sec. 102-251. - Districts and district boundaries.
(a)
In order to regulate and restrict the location of trades and industries and the location of buildings erected,
reconstructed, altered or enlarged for speci ed uses, to regulate and limit the height and bulk of buildings
hereafter erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged, to regulate and determine the area of yards and other
open spaces and to regulate and limit the density of population, the City of Dublin is hereby divided into 11

upon the map attached hereto and made a part of this article, said map being designated "Zoning Map of the
City of Dublin, Texas", and said map and all notations, references, and other information shown thereon shall be
a part of this article the same as if all such matters and information were fully described herein. Such uses as
listed but not shown on the zoning map are provided for future growth and use. The original of said map shall
bear the date with the passing of this article and shall be signed by the mayor and attested by the city secretary,
under the seal of the City of Dublin, Texas; said original map shall be kept in the o ce of the city secretary in the
Dublin City Hall, and a replica thereof shall be produced upon paper in such reduced scale as will permit its
being attached to the ordinance from which this article is derived.

It shall be the duty of the city secretary to keep the o cial maps and current copies up to date, by entering on
such maps any changes that the city council may from time to time order by amendments to the zoning
ordinance and map.

The distance from the property line to the nearest part of the building, structure or sign, measured
perpendicularly to the property line. See also "Building line". The nearest part of the building shall include
building projections such as eaves, awnings, window boxes, roof, and porch overhangs that extend from the
building or structure.

Sec. 102-252. - District boundaries.
The following rules shall apply where uncertainty exists with respect to the boundaries of the various
zoning districts as shown on the map accompanying and made a part of this chapter:
(1)
330/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Unless otherwise shown, the district boundaries are either streets, alleys, creeks, pipe lines, electric
transmission lines, railroads or other natural or manmade features not likely to change, and where the districts
designated on the map accompanying and made a part of this chapter are bounded approximately by street or
alley lines, such street or alley shall be construed to be the boundary of such district.
(2)
Where the district boundaries are not otherwise indicated, and where the property has been or may be divided
into blocks and lots, the district boundaries shall be construed to be lot lines, and where the districts designated
on the map accompanying and made a part of this chapter are bounded approximately by lot lines, such lot
lines shall be construed to be the boundaries of such districts, unless such boundaries are otherwise indicated
on the map.
(3)
In unsubdivided property, the district boundary lines on the map accompanying and made a part of this chapter
shall be determined by the use of the scale contained on such map, unless dimensions are shown.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 25, 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-253. - Amendments, supplements or changes.
(a)
The city council may from time to time amend, supplement or change, by ordinance, the boundaries of the
zoning districts or the regulations established in this chapter. Before taking action on any such proposed
amendment, supplement or change, the city council shall submit the proposed amendment, supplement or
change to the planning and zoning commission for its recommendation and report. A public hearing shall be
held by the city council before adopting any proposed amendment, supplement or change, notice of which
hearing shall be given by publication one time in the o cial paper of the city, stating the time and place of such
hearing, which shall not be earlier than 15 days from the date of such publication. Unless such proposed
amendment, supplement or change has been approved by the planning and zoning commission, or if a protest
against such amendment, supplement or change has been led with the city secretary, duly signed and
acknowledged by the owners of 20 percent or more either of the area of the lots included in such proposed
change or all property within 200 feet of all boundaries of the proposed change, such amendment, supplement
or change shall not become e ective, except by a favorable vote of three-fourths of all members of the city
council.
(b)
Written notice of all public hearings on proposed changes in district boundaries shall be sent not less than ten
days before such hearing is held to all owners of property located within 200 feet of any such reclassi cation or
the person rendering such property for city taxes. Such notice may be served by using the last known address of
such persons as listed on the city tax rolls and depositing the notice, postage paid, at the United States Post
O ce. This shall be the method of notice for all public hearings of the planning and zoning commission and
zoning board of adjustment.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 26, 2-21-2000)

331/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 102-254. - Newly annexed territory; permanent zoning.
All territory annexed into the city shall be classified as A agricultural district, until such territory is
permanently zoned by the city council. After annexation of any territory into the city, the planning and zoning
commission may institute proceedings on its own motion to give newly annexed territory a permanent zoning,
and the procedure to be followed shall be the same as provided by law for the adoption of original zoning
regulations.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 23, 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-255—102-280. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - A AGRICULTURAL DISTRICT
Sec. 102-281. - Purpose.
The purpose of the A agricultural district is for the general continuation of certain farm, ranch, residential
and nonurban uses of land, which is not anticipated to be put to an urban-developed use in the immediate
future. The A district classification is to be used only in the outlying areas of the city's urban development;
newly annexed areas; or on major tracts of land containing ten acres or more of land. Within the A district,
upon the subdivision of land for sale or an intended use other than as set forth in section 102-282, the
appropriate zoning district and classification for which the land subdivision is intended shall be required.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 6(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-282. - Use regulations.
In the A district, no building or land shall be used; no building shall be erected, reconstructed, altered or
enlarged; and no certificate of occupancy shall be issued, except for one or more of the following uses:
(1)

Permitted uses.
a.
Single-family dwelling.
b.
Farms, orchards, truck gardens and nurseries for the growing of plants and similar agrarian activities involving
the growing of plants, provided, that no operation shall be conducted which will be obnoxious or o ensive.
c.
Animal lots and ranches for the pasturing of horses, mules, cattle, sheep, goats, poultry, rabbits, or ratites
(emus, ostriches, etc.).
d.
Single-family dwellings clearly incidental to the operation of the activities listed in subsections (1)b. and c. of this
section, including dwellings on the same farm or ranch used exclusively for the housing of employees living on
332/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

the premises.
e.
Principal and accessory buildings and structures clearly incidental to the operations listed in subsections (1)b.
and c. of this section, including, but not limited to, private barns, private stables, equipment sheds, granaries,
pumphouses and water tanks.
f.
Installations owned and operated by the city, state or public utility companies, which are necessary for the
public safety, governmental services or furnishing of utility services to or through the A district.
g.
Antennae and towers not exceeding the maximum height allowed in the A district (see section 102-283(1));
antennae attached to existing structures and not increasing the overall height of the existing structure by more
than ten feet; and dish antennae not exceeding one meter in diameter. Except for satellite dish antennae, no
antennae or support structure shall be located within the required front, side or rear yard setback. To protect
tra c safety and community appearance, no satellite dish antennae or support structure shall be located within
the required front or second front yard setback, unless the zoning board of adjustment nds that such an
encroachment is necessary to prevent impairment of installation, maintenance or reception and that a tra c
sight restriction is not created.
h.
Parks, playgrounds, community buildings and other public recreational facilities owned and/or operated by the
city or other public agency.
i.
Public buildings, including libraries, museums, and police and re stations.
j.
Public elementary or high schools.
k.
Private schools, with curriculum equivalent to that of a public elementary or high school.
l.
Water supply reservoirs, pumping plants and towers.
m.
Accessory structures and uses customarily incidental to the uses set forth in subsections (1)a.—l. of this section
and located on the same lot with such uses, and not involving the conduct of any business or commercial
enterprise.
(2)

Conditional uses.
a.
Utility facilities.
b.
Antennae and towers exceeding the maximum height in the A district, and dish antennae exceeding only one
meter in diameter, in order to protect community appearance from the negative visual e ects of the
proliferation of large antennae. Such conditional use permits shall be acted upon within 90 days of receipt of the
333/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

application for such permit. Persons aggrieved by a decision on a satellite dish antenna application may appeal
to the Federal Communications Commission. Any new towers must also comply with the conditions of section
102-580.
c.
Commercial barn, stable or riding arenas, subject to the requirements of section 102-578.
d.
Churches.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 6(B), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-283. - Height and area regulations.
In the A district, the height of buildings and structures, and the minimum dimensions of yards, shall be as
follows:
(1)

Height. No building or structure erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged shall exceed 3½ stories, nor 45 feet.
(2)

Front yard. There shall be a front yard of not less than 25 feet, or the front yard indicated on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records, whichever is greater. Corner lots shall have a minimum side
yard of 15 feet on the second front yard (the yard generally parallel to the street with the greatest frontage),
unless reversed frontage is approved by the city manager. If a building line shown on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records is greater than 15 feet, then the platted building line shall be
required on the second front yard. Garage doors and gates meant for vehicle use shall not be located closer
than 20 feet from the right-of-way.
(3)

Rear yard. There shall be a rear yard having a depth of not less than 20 feet.
(4)

Side yard. Lots shall have a minimum side yard of 15 feet.
(5)

Maximum lot coverage. The maximum portion of the lot area which may be covered by the main building and all
accessory buildings shall not exceed 25 percent.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 6(C), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-284—102-300. - Reserved.
DIVISION 3. - RE RESIDENTIAL ESTATE DISTRICT
Sec. 102-301. - Purpose.

334/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

The RE residential estate district is for large lot residences with a capability of keeping and maintaining
limited numbers of livestock and other animals. The RE district classification should be applied in areas of
large lots and rural estate-type subdivision design and layout, and to conserve rural neighborhood character,
value and buildings.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 7(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-302. - Use regulations.
In the RE district, no building or land shall be used, and no building shall be erected, reconstructed,
altered or enlarged, unless otherwise provided in this chapter, except for one or more of the following uses:
(1)

Permitted uses.

Single-family dwellings.
b.
Private garages and accessory buildings not exceeding one story or 15 feet in overall height.
c.
Accessory storage buildings and greenhouses, when located behind the front setback; a minimum of ve feet
from other property lines; and not on any easement.
d.
Hobbies or crafts, as an accessory use.
e.
Temporary buildings to be used for construction purposes only, and which shall be removed upon completion
or abandonment of construction work or upon the request of the city manager. Permits shall be issued for such
temporary buildings for a period of six months only, with a renewal clause for a similar period of time.
f.
Family day care homes with 12 children or less.
g.
Farms, truck gardens, orchards or nurseries for the growing of plants, shrubs and trees, provided, no retail or
wholesale business sales o ces are maintained on the premises and, provided, that no obnoxious fertilizer is
stored upon the premises, and no obnoxious soil or fertilizer processing is conducted on the premises.
h.
Uses customarily incidental to any of the uses set forth in subsections (1)a.—g. of this section when situated in
the same dwelling, and when not involving the conduct of a business or industry, except for home occupations
as de ned in section 102-2, such as the o ce of a physician, surgeon, dentist or art gallery.

Real estate sales o ces for property located within the subdivision in which such o ces are located. Sales

sales o ce shall cease within 30 days of the sale of the last parcel within the subdivision. Field o ces for the

7/12/2019

sale or rental of real estate shall be removed upon the request of the building o cial. Sales o ce shall not be
