Any typically permitted secondary or accessory uses allowed in the district in the absence of the principal use if,
after consideration of the layout, con guration and relationship to existing subdivisions and neighborhoods, the
city manager determines that replatting of the principal and secondary lots into a single lot is not possible or
desirable.
k.
Utility facilities.
l.
Group homes, as provided under state and federal laws.
m.
Antennae and towers not exceeding the maximum height in the RE district (see section 102-303(2)), antennae
attached to existing structures and not increasing the overall height of the existing structure by more than ten
feet, and dish antennae not exceeding one meter in diameter. Except for satellite dish antennae, no antenna or
support structure shall be located within the required front, side or rear yard setback. To protect tra c safety
and community appearance, no satellite dish antennae or support structure shall be located within the required
front or second yard setback, unless the zoning board of adjustment nds that such an encroachment is
necessary to prevent impairment of installation, maintenance or reception, and that a tra c sight restriction is
not created.
n.
Parks, playgrounds,community buildings and other public recreational facilities, owned and/or operated by the
city or other public agency.
o.
Public buildings, including libraries, museums, and police and re stations.
p.
Public elementary or high schools.
q.
Private schools, with curriculum equivalent to that of a public elementary or high school.
r.
Water supply reservoirs, pumping plants and towers.
s.
Accessory structures and uses customarily incidental to the uses set forth in subsections (1)a.—r. of this section
and located on the same lot with such uses, and not involving the conduct of any business or commercial
enterprise.
(2)

Conditional uses.
a.
Antennae and towers exceeding the maximum height in the RD district, and dish antennae exceeding one meter
in diameter, in order to protect community appearance from the negative visual e ects of proliferation of large
336/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

antennae. Such conditional use permits shall be acted upon within 90 days of receipt of the application for such

Subsidiary dwelling.
c.
Churches.
(3)

Special exception uses. Special exception uses authorized by the zoning board of adjustment under the

(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 7(B), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-303. - Height and area regulations.
In the RE district, the height of buildings; minimum dimensions of lots and yards; minimum lot area; and
minimum floor space per family shall be as follows:
(1)

Floor space. The main residence shall contain a minimum of 1,500 square feet of livable oor space, exclusive of
garages, porches and breezeways, and incidental storage areas.
(2)

Height. No building erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged shall exceed 2½ stories, nor 35 feet.
(3)

Front yard. There shall be a front yard of not less than 30 feet, or the front yard indicated on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records, whichever is greater. Corner lots shall have a minimum side
yard of 15 feet on the second front yard (the yard generally parallel to the street with the greatest frontage),
unless reversed frontage is approved by the city manager. If a building line shown on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records is greater than 15 feet, then the platted building line shall be
required on the second front yard. Garage doors and gates meant for vehicle use shall not be located closer
than 20 feet from the right-of-way.
(4)

Rear yard. There shall be a rear yard having a depth of not less than 20 feet.
(5)

Side yard. Corner lots shall have a minimum side yard of ten feet on side yards adjacent to interior lots. Interior
lots shall have a minimum side yard dimension of ten feet.
(6)

Lot width. The width of a lot shall be a minimum of 100 feet at the building line.
(7)

Lot area. The minimum area of a lot shall be one acre or 43,560 square feet.
(8)
337/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Maximum lot coverage. The maximum portion of the lot area which may be covered by the main building and all
accessory buildings shall not exceed 30 percent.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 7(C), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-304—102-320. - Reserved.
DIVISION 4. - SF SINGLE-FAMILY DISTRICT
Sec. 102-321. - Purpose.
The SF single-family district zoning classification is the most restrictive of all residential zones and should
be applied in areas of larger lots; more contemporary subdivision design and layout; and areas that are
designed solely for residential uses. The SF zoning classification should be applied in areas of the city to
conserve neighborhood character, value and buildings. It is not intended that the SF district be the subject of
major alterations, except for a possible reclassification in minor areas for a less restrictive residential use for
reasonable adjustment necessary for orderly development of vacant lots or the gradual transition from other
districts.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 8(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-322. - Use regulations.
In the SF district, no building or land shall be used, and no building shall be erected, reconstructed, altered
or enlarged, unless otherwise provided in this chapter, except for one or more of the following uses:
(1)

Permitted uses.
a.
Single-family dwellings.
b.
Accessory structures and accessory uses customarily incident to the single family dwelling use permitted in the
district, that are located on the same lot with the primary residential structure, that are designed, constructed
and located for a use permitted in the single-family district, and that are in compliance with this chapter and all
other applicable city ordinances, are permitted in the district; provided the same do not involve the conduct of
any business or commercial enterprise and comply with each of the following requirements:
1.
A private garage may have a capacity for not more than three standard size automobiles, plus 100 square feet of
storage space for goods and materials. Where the residential structure is two stories or greater, the private
garage may have a second story containing an apartment or storage for use of the family constructed as an
integral part of the main building and shall be subject to the regulations a ecting the main building;
2.
All accessory structures larger than 100 square feet must:
338/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(i)
Have a roof line that is not greater in height than the roof line of the single family dwelling;
(ii)
Have walls that are of a height no greater than the average plate height of the primary structure;
(iii)
Not be constructed of scrap or salvage material;
(iv)
Be white in color or substantially the same color as the primary structure;
(v)
Meet the setback and yard requirements for the primary structure; and
(vi)
Not be incompatible by architectural design, appearance, materials or size with the single family dwelling or any
adjacent single family uses;
3.
Except for the single family dwelling, not more than one private garage, one carport, and one other accessory
structure may be constructed on a single family lot, subject to the maximum lot coverage restrictions;
4.
An accessory structure that is 120 square feet or smaller shall not have a wall height greater than eight feet.
c.
Greenhouses that meet the setback and yard requirements for the primary structure and are not located on any
easement.
d.
Hobbies or crafts, as an accessory use.
e.
Temporary buildings to be used for construction purposes only, and which shall be removed upon completion
or abandonment of construction work or upon the request of the city manager. Permits shall be issued for such
temporary buildings for a period of six months only, with a renewal clause for a similar period of time.
f.
Family day care homes with 12 children or less.
g.
Group homes as provided under state and federal laws.
h.
Antennae and towers not exceeding the maximum height in the SF district (see section 102-323(2)), antennae
attached to existing structures and not increasing the overall height of the existing structure by more than ten
feet, and dish antennae not exceeding one meter in diameter. Except for satellite dish antennae, no antenna or
support structure shall be located within the required front, side or rear yard setback. To protect tra c safety
and community appearance, no satellite dish antennae or support structure shall be located within the required
front or second yard setback, unless the zoning board of adjustment nds that such an encroachment is
necessary to prevent impairment of installation, maintenance or reception, and that a tra c sight restriction is
not created.
339/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

i.
Parks, playgrounds,community buildings and other public recreational facilities, owned and/or operated by the
city or other public agency.
j.
Public buildings, including libraries, museums, and police and re stations.
k.
Public elementary or high schools.
l.
Private schools, with curriculum equivalent to that of a public elementary or high school.
(2)

Conditional uses.
a.
Farms, truck gardens, orchards or nurseries for the growing of plants, shrubs and trees, provided, no retail or
wholesale business sales o ces are maintained on the premises and, provided, that no obnoxious fertilizer is
stored upon the premises, and no obnoxious soil or fertilizer processing is conducted on the premises.

de ned in section 102-2, such as the o ce of a physician, surgeon, dentist or art gallery.

Real estate sales o ces for property located within the subdivision in which such o ces are located. Sales
o ces shall be required to pay an annual permit fee, to be established by the city council. The use of such a
sales o ce shall cease within 30 days of the sale of the last parcel within the subdivision. Field o ces for the
sale or rental of real estate shall be removed upon the request of the building o cial. Sales o ce shall not be
used for the sale of property outside of the subdivision in which such o ces are located.
d.
Any typically permitted secondary or accessory uses allowed in the district in the absence of the principal use if,
after consideration of the layout, con guration and relationship to existing subdivisions and neighborhoods, the
city manager determines that replatting of the principal and secondary lots into a single lot is not possible or
desirable.
e.
Utility facilities.
f.
Subsidiary dwellings.
g.
Churches.
h.
Bed and breakfasts.
i.

Sec. 102-323. - Height and area regulations.
In the SF district, the height of buildings; minimum dimensions of lots and yards; minimum lot area; and
minimum floor space per family shall be as follows:
(1)

Floor space. The main residence shall contain a minimum of 1,000 square feet of livable oor space, exclusive of
garages, porches and breezeways, and incidental storage areas.
(2)

Height. No building erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged shall exceed 2½ stories, nor 35 feet. Accessory
buildings shall not exceed one story or 15 feet in height.
(3)

Front yard depth. There shall be a front yard having a depth of not less than 25 feet, or the front yard indicated
on a city-approved subdivision plat as led in the Erath County plat records, whichever is greater. Corner lots
shall have a side yard having a width of not less than 15 feet on the second front yard, the yard generally
parallel to the street with the greatest frontage, unless reversed frontage is approved by the city manager. If a
building line shown on a city-approved subdivision plat as led in the Erath County plat records is greater than
15 feet, then the platted building line shall be required on the second front yard. Garage doors and gates meant
for vehicle use shall be located no closer than 20 feet from the right-of-way.
(4)

Rear yard depth. There shall be a rear yard having a depth of not less than 20 feet. The building inspector may
authorize encroachments of up to 20 square feet for the replaces and/or bay windows that do not restrict
access for public safety and/or adjacent property.
(5)

Side yard. Corner lots shall have a side yard having a width of not less than eight feet on side yards adjacent to
interior lots. Interior lots shall have a side yard having a minimum width of eight feet.
(6)

Lot width. The width of a lot shall be a minimum of 70 feet at the building line, provided, that where a lot of
record and in separate ownership at the time of the passage of the ordinance from which this section is derived
has a width less than required in this subsection, this chapter shall not prohibit the erection of a single-family
dwelling.
(7)

Lot area. The minimum area of a lot shall be 7,000 square feet.
342/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(8)

Maximum lot coverage. The maximum portion of the lot area, which may be covered by the main building and
all accessory buildings shall not exceed 50 percent.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 8(C), 2-21-2000; Ord. No. 2-19-04-2, §§ 5, 6, 2-19-2004)

The D duplex residential district is the most restrictive of the multiple-family districts and is intended for
two-family and multiple-family use, and for zones of transition from the single-family zone to higher density
multiple-family or commercial zones.

buildings shall not exceed one story or 15 feet in height.

DIVISION 6. - MF MULTIPLE-FAMILY DISTRICT
Sec. 102-361. - Purpose.
The MF multiple-family district allows medium to high density multiple-family dwelling use of the land, and
is intended to comprise larger tracts of land designed to provide total residential amenities of open space,
recreation space and areas of protected off-street parking. The MF district is intended to be located near high
volume thoroughfares due to the traffic generating probability of medium to high density dwelling units within
347/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

the district. The MF district may be coupled with a planned development (PD) suffix to allow for site plan
development in the areas that would be appropriate for contemporary design of the structures and their
arrangement.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 10(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-362. - Use regulations.

altered or enlarged, unless otherwise provided in this chapter, except for one or more of the following uses:

feet, and dish antennae not exceeding one meter in diameter. Except for satellite dish antennae, no antenna or
support structure shall be located within the required front, side or rear yard setback. To protect tra c safety
and community appearance, no satellite dish antennae or support structure shall be located within the required
front or second yard setback, unless the zoning board of adjustment nds that such an encroachment is
necessary to prevent impairment of installation, maintenance or reception, and that a tra c sight restriction is
not created.

Public buildings, including libraries, museums, and police and re stations.

Single-family dwellings.

Sec. 102-363. - Height and area regulations.
In the MF district, the height of the buildings; minimum dimensions of lots and yards; minimum lot area;
and minimum floor space per family shall be as follows:
(1)

Floor space. The oor space requirements for two-family dwellings shall be the same as in district D. Every other
building, or portion thereof, erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged shall contain an average of 700 square
feet and a minimum of 550 square feet of total oor area, exclusive of garages, porches, breezeways and
exterior storage for each family to be housed in such building. Such minimum total oor area shall not apply to
hotels or apartment hotels where no provision is made for cooking in any individual room, suite or apartment;
nor to apartment complexes constructed and used exclusively for elderly retirees. Additionally, in apartment
complexes having 50 or more units, the computation of minimum and average square footage of total oor
area may include pro rata of separate recreational rooms or buildings up to ten percent of the required square
footage of livable area. Total oor area required in apartments constructed and used exclusively for elderly
citizens shall provide an average of 500 square feet. Dining rooms and recreational areas are included in
computing total oor space average.
(2)

Height. No building erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged shall exceed 2½ stories, nor 35 feet within 100
feet of a property line of a SF or D zoned property. Any building in excess of 100 feet from such property lines
shall not exceed 3½ stories or 45 feet. Accessory buildings shall not exceed one story or 15 feet in height.
(3)

Front yard. There shall be a front yard of not less than 25 feet, or the front yard indicated on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records, whichever is greater. Corner lots shall have a minimum side
yard of 15 feet on the second front yard (the yard generally parallel to the street with the greatest frontage),
unless reversed frontage is approved by the city manager. If a building line shown on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records is greater than 15 feet, then the platted building line shall be
required on the second front yard. Garage doors and gates meant for vehicle use shall not be located closer
than 20 feet from the right-of-way.
(4)

Rear yard. There shall be a rear yard having a depth of not less than 20 feet.
(5)

Side yard. On interior lots, there shall be a side yard of not less than ten feet on each side of each main building.
When more than one main building is erected on a platted lot, the distance between buildings shall be not less
than 20 feet. For buildings more than 2½ stories in height, each side yard shall be increased one foot in width
for each story above the second oor. No accessory building on a corner lot shall project beyond the front yard
line of the lots in the rear, nor shall accessory buildings be erected closer than ten feet to the line of the abutting
lot to the rear.
(6)
350/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Lot width. The width of a lot shall be a minimum of 75 feet at the building line, provided, that where a lot of
record and in separate ownership at the time of the passage of the ordinance from which this section is derived
has less width than required in this subsection, this chapter shall not prohibit the erection of a one-family
dwelling.
(7)

Lot area. The lot area for two-family dwellings shall be the same as in the D district. Every other building, or
portion thereof, erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged, shall provide a lot area of not less than 1,500
square feet per family. Such lot area requirement shall not apply to hotels, apartment hotels or elderly
retirement facilities, where no provision is made for cooking in any individual room, suite or apartment.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 10(C), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-364. - Usable open space.
(a)
All residential uses in the MF district shall provide and maintain a minimum of 200 square feet of usable open
space for each dwelling unit.
(b)
For the purpose of this section, the term "usable open space" means outdoor areas, excluding parking and
other service areas, which are utilized for livable and/or related amenity, such as outdoor living, associated
recreation and/or landscaping, and which is open and unobstructed from its lowest level to the sky, except for
roof overhangs and architectural projections. All usable open space, unless otherwise excepted in this chapter,
shall be accessible to, and usable by, all residents residing on the site. Private courtyards or balconies may
constitute usable open space for the purpose of calculating up to 30 percent of the total required usable open
space. Usable open space may include areas at the ground level and/or on roofs, decks or balconies designed
for common use, provided, that such areas meet other criteria as set forth in this chapter. The minimum
dimension for usable open space at the ground level shall be ten feet, and the minimum area shall be 100
square feet. The minimum dimensions for usable open space located on roofs or decks that are available for
common use shall be 20 feet by 20 feet, and the minimum area shall be 400 square feet. At least one-half of the
required open space shall be at the ground level.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 10(D), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-365. - Screening and landscaping.
Each complex within the MF district shall provide appropriate buffers and landscaping as determined by
the planning and zoning commission.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 10(E), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-366. - Site plan requirements.
(a)

351/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Any owner, builder or developer of a multiple-family condominium or townhouse dwelling complex within the
MF district shall submit the site and building plan for the proposed development to the planning and zoning
commission for review. The contents of the site plan shall contain drawings to scale to indicate the following, as
needed:
(1)

After conducting a public hearing, the planning and zoning commission shall approve an application for a
multiple-family dwelling complex if the proposed development meets all of the minimum standards established
in this chapter and other applicable ordinances, and if the planning and zoning commission nds that the
proposed development will not be detrimental to the health, safety or welfare of the surrounding neighborhood
or its occupants, or be substantially or permanently injurious to neighboring property. The planning and zoning
commission shall disapprove or conditionally approve any application which fails to meet the criteria set forth in
subsection (a) of this section or is in con ict with the comprehensive plan or the adopted growth policies of the
city.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 10(F), 2-21-2000)

DIVISION 7. - C COMMERCIAL DISTRICT
Sec. 102-391. - Purpose.
The C commercial district is a commercial category providing a uniform set of standards for retail
shopping facilities and general commercial activities. It is intended that the C district be served by major
thoroughfares and be of such a size that all parking and traffic maneuvering can take place on the commercial
site. It is expressly intended that no residential dwelling be erected in the C district and existing dwellings will
remain as legal nonconforming dwellings.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 11(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-392. - Use regulations.
In the C district, no buildings or land shall be used, and no buildings shall be erected, reconstructed,
altered or enlarged, unless otherwise provided in this chapter, except one or more of the following uses:

Permitted uses.

Antique shops.

may be a principal use on a property or an outdoor operation in conjunction with and subordinate to any
existing permitted permanent indoor retail establishment. Such temporary outdoor sales operations shall

Sec. 102-393. - Height and area regulations.
In the C district, the height of buildings; minimum dimensions of lots and yards; minimum lot area; and
minimum floor space per family shall be as follows:
(1)

Height. No building erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged shall exceed 2½ stories, nor 35 feet within 100
feet of a property line of a SF or D zoned property. Any building in excess of 100 feet from such property lines
shall not exceed 3½ stories or 45 feet.
(2)

Front yard. There shall be a front yard of not less than 25 feet, or the front yard indicated on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records, whichever is greater. Corner lots shall have a minimum side
yard of 15 feet on the second front yard (the yard generally parallel to the street with the greatest frontage),
unless reversed frontage is approved by the city manager. If a building line shown on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records is greater than 15 feet, then the platted building line shall be
360/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

required on the second front yard. Garage doors and gates meant for vehicle use shall not be located closer
than 20 feet from the right-of-way.
(3)

Rear yard. There shall be a rear yard having a depth of not less than 20 feet.
(4)

Side yard. There shall be a side yard of not less than ve feet. Where a lot abuts upon the side of a residentially
zoned lot, there shall be a side yard of not less than ten feet. In a uni ed commercial development, interior side
yard setbacks may be waived upon approval of the planning and zoning commission at the time of platting or
site plan approval.
(5)

Lot width. The width of a lot shall be a minimum of 70 feet at the building line, provided, that where a lot of
record and in separate ownership at the time of the passage of the ordinance from which this section is derived
has less width than required in this subsection, this chapter shall not prohibit its use for commercial purposes.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 11(C), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-394. - District restrictions.
(a)
Any lighting visible from outside a site in the C district shall be designed to re ect away from adjacent residential
districts and shall not interfere with tra c safety. No noise, odor or vibration shall be emitted so that it
constitutes a nuisance by substantially exceeding the general level of noise, odor or vibration emitted by uses
adjacent to or immediately surrounding the site. Such comparisons shall be made at the boundaries of the site.
(b)
Outdoor storage of trash receptacles shall be at the side or rear of the site, and shall be totally encircled or
screened by a fence, planting or other suitable visual barrier.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 11(D), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-395—102-420. - Reserved.
DIVISION 8. - CBD COMMERCIAL DISTRICT
Sec. 102-421. - Purpose.
The CBD commercial district is a special commercial zoning district reserved for downtown areas that
provides the greatest number and mix of retail and commercial uses. The CBD district is reserved for areas of
adequate size and location so that its broad range of high intensity land uses will not cause or create
nuisances to adjoining zoning districts. It is expressly intended that no residential dwelling be erected in the
CBD district, and existing dwellings will remain as legal nonconforming dwellings.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 12(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-422. - Use regulations.
361/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

In the CBD district, no buildings or land shall be used, and no buildings shall be erected, reconstructed,
altered or enlarged, unless otherwise provided in this chapter, except for one or more of the following uses:
(1)

Permitted uses.
a.
Any use permitted in the C district.
b.
Second story residences will be allowed in existing two-story buildings, provided, that the entrance to the
residence and parking for the residence shall be at the rear or side of the building.
(2)

Conditional uses.
a.
Utility facilities.
b.
Antennae and towers exceeding the maximum height in the CBD district, and dish antennae exceeding two
meters in diameter, in order to protect community appearance from the negative visual e ects of proliferation
of large antennae. Conditional use permits shall be acted upon within 90 days of receipt of an application for
such permit. Persons aggrieved by a decision on a satellite dish antenna application may appeal to the Federal
Communications Commission. Any new towers must also comply with the conditions of section 102-580.

Outdoor commercial amusement enterprises.

Special exception uses. Special exception uses, when authorized by the zoning board of adjustment under the
provision of article III, division 3 of this chapter.

DIVISION 9. - I INDUSTRIAL DISTRICT
Sec. 102-451. - Purpose.
The purpose of the I industrial district is to regulate the uses of the land that involve the manufacturing,
assembly, processing, storage and/or distribution, sale and repair of materials, goods, parts, products,
equipment, machinery and other such operations incidental to industrial uses. It is not the intent of the
363/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

regulations set forth in this division to allow the construction or development of residential uses within the I
district, and the residential uses existing at the time of the adoption of the ordinance from which this section is
derived and its zoning district map may continue, but shall be classified as nonconforming uses. All proposed
industrial uses shall be accompanied by a development site plan. Since the intended use may cause a
detrimental change to the environment or substantially affect the city operated utility or thoroughfare
systems, detailed descriptions of performance standards are included in the district regulations set forth in
this division, and are determined to be the maximum allowable within any single or combined industrial use or
district.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 13(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-452. - Use regulations.
In the I district, no buildings or land shall be used, and no buildings shall be erected, reconstructed,
altered or enlarged, unless otherwise provided in this chapter, except for one or more of the following uses:
(1)

Permitted uses.
a.
Any industrial and/or commercial use meeting the included development site plan requirements and
performance standards.
b.
Reserved.
c.
Antennae and towers not exceeding the maximum height allowed in the I district (see subsection 102-454(1)),
antennae attached to existing structures and not increasing the overall height of the existing structure by more
than ten feet, and dish antennae not exceeding two meters in diameter. Except for satellite dish antennae, no
antennae or support structure shall be located within the required front, side or rear yard setback. To protect
tra c safety and community appearance, no satellite dish antennae or support structure shall be located within
the required front or second front yard setback, unless the zoning board of adjustment nds that such an
encroachment is necessary to prevent impairment of installation, maintenance or reception and that a tra c
sight restriction is not created.
d.
Public buildings, including libraries, museums and police and re stations.
e.
Water supply reservoirs, pumping plants and towers.
f.
Accessory structures and uses customarily incidental to the uses set forth in subsections (1)a.—e. of this section
and located on the same lot with such uses.

Conditional uses.

Sec. 102-453. - Development site plan.
(a)
A development site plan shall be required for each building permit application within the I district, and shall be
submitted to the city manager for approval, and shall contain the following information:
(1)
A scale drawing showing the boundary of the tract and topography, with a contour interval of not less than twofoot intervals, and drainage information.
(2)
The location of each building and the minimum distance between buildings and between buildings and the
property lines, street lines and/or alley lines. The plan shall include all dimensions, easements, the legal
description and zoning of the subject property and all adjacent property.
(3)
A plan indicating the arrangement and provision of o -street parking, o -street loading, outside storage areas,
method and location of storage area screening and points of entry from adjoining thoroughfares.
(4)
A table showing net land area, ratio of building area and outside storage areas to net land area.
(5)
A table of performance standards of the characteristics of the industrial activities to be conducted on the site, if
required by the city manager.
(6)
365/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Scale, north arrow, and the names and addresses of owners and/or developers with the names and addresses
of the persons responsible for the preparation of the development plan.
(7)
For development projects in uenced by, or containing major drainageways or oodprone areas, by de nition of
the city engineer, a preliminary drainage plan shall become a part of the development site plan. Such
requirement may be waived only by the recommendation of the city engineer.
(8)
Existing and proposed re hydrants, sign information and provisions for external illumination and trash
collection.
(b)
The city manager shall review the development site plan for conformance with applicable ordinances,
regulations and codes. The city manager, in consultation with other city o cials, shall also review and evaluate
the site plans for re and safety concerns, tra c circulation, drainage, environmental constraints and impacts,
landscaping, amenities and adequacy of bu ers. The city manager shall approve the site plan if the proposed
site plan conforms to applicable requirements and, in the opinion of the city manager, provides adequate
design features to reasonably mitigate adverse e ects. An applicant may appeal a denial of site plan approval to
the planning and zoning commission for reconsideration at its next available agenda. Prior to such meeting, the
planning and zoning commission shall notify adjacent landowners potentially a ected by the appeal in writing of
the consideration.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 13(C), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-454. - Height and area regulations.
In the I district, the height of the buildings and the minimum dimension of yards shall be as follows:
(1)

Height. No building shall exceed 75 feet in height, unless the required yards are increased one foot for each foot
above such height limit. When a building is located adjacent to any residential district, it shall not exceed 40 feet
in height, unless the required yards are increased one foot for each one foot of additional height above 40 feet.
(2)

Front yard. There shall be a front yard of not less than 30 feet, or the front yard indicated on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records, whichever is greater. Corner lots shall have a minimum side
yard of 15 feet on the second front yard (the yard generally parallel tot he street with the greatest frontage),
unless reversed frontage is approved by the city manager. If a building line shown on a city-approved
subdivision plat as led in the county plat records is greater than 15 feet, then the platted building line shall be
required on the second front yard. Garage doors and gates meant for vehicle use shall not be located closer
than 20 feet from the right-of-way.
(3)

Side yard. There shall be a side yard of not less than ten feet, unless additional emergency access is required by
the re marshal.
(4)
366/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Rear yard. There shall be a rear yard of not less than 20 feet, unless additional emergency access is required by
the re marshal.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 13(D), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-455. - Performance standards.
The following are maximum accepted levels of noise, vibration and smoke, particulate matter and toxic
and noxious matter allowable for industrial uses in the I district. If the proposed use results in the discharge of
sanitary sewage effluent containing industrial wastes or other effluent into the city's sanitary sewage system, a
characterization of the effluent and a description of the proposed methods of pretreatment, if any, must
accompany the development site plan. The performance standards report may be waived by the city manager
if the proposed use is considered not to produce the listed effects.
(1)

Noise. The day-night average sound level at the property line shall not exceed 75 decibels, unless the property
line adjoins property zoned for residential uses where the maximum day-night average sound level shall not
exceed 65 decibels. The day-night average sound level (Ldn) is the 24-hour average sound level, in decibels,
obtained after the addition of ten decibels to sound levels in the night from 10:00 p.m. to 7:00 a.m.
(2)

Vibration. The sound pressure level or impact level of any operation or plant shall not exceed the decibel limits
for the octave bands designated in column I of the following table as measured at the point which has the
highest reading on the property line of the source property. If the point of measurement is located on a
property line which is also the boundary line of a residential district, the limits set forth in column II of the
following table shall apply.

Frequency

Column I

Column II*

(Cycles per second)

Displacement

Displacement

(inches)

(inches)

0—10

0.0022

0.0008

11—20

0.0016

0.0005

21—30

0.0010

0.0002

31 and over

0.0005

0.0001

367/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

* Steady state—Vibrations, for the purpose of this chapter, which are continuous or if in discrete
pulses, are more frequent than 60 per minute. Impact vibrations, that are discrete pulses, which
do not exceed 60 pulses per minute, shall not cause in excess of twice the displacement
stipulated.
(3)

Smoke, particulate matter and visible emissions. Smoke or visible emissions emitted from any vent, stack,
chimney, skylight or window shall not exceed an opacity of 20 percent, averaged over a ve-minute period. Any
emission of an air pollutant must be in accordance with the requirements of the state. Emissions shall not
exceed any of the following net ground level concentrations:
a.
One hundred micrograms per cubic meter of air sampled, averaged over any ve consecutive hours.
b.
Two hundred micrograms per cubic meter of air sampled, averaged over any three consecutive hours.
c.
Four hundred micrograms per cubic meter of air sampled, averaged over any one hour.
(4)

Toxic and noxious matter. The handling, processing, storage and disposal of hazardous, toxic or noxious
materials within the I district shall be in accordance with applicable state and federal laws and regulations. In
addition, the planning and zoning commission may establish additional performance standards, including
setbacks, berms and bu ers, for the siting of facilities which handle, treat, store or dispose of potentially
hazardous or dangerous materials.
(5)

Additional standards. The planning and zoning commission may establish additional performance standards to
protect neighboring areas and land uses from potential industrial hazards and nuisances.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 13(E), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-456—102-480. - Reserved.
DIVISION 10. - MH-1 MANUFACTURED HOME DISTRICT-1
Sec. 102-481. - Purpose.
The MH-1 manufactured home district-1 is established to provide adequate space and restrictions for the
placement of manufactured homes in the city where adequate streets and other community facilities are
available for present and future needs. The MH-1 district is established to provide housing densities
compatible with existing and proposed neighborhoods; promote the most desirable use of land and direction
of building development; promote stability of development; protect the character of the district; preserve the
value of the land and buildings; and protect the city's tax base.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 14(A), 2-21-2000)
368/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 102-482. - Use regulations.
Individual lots platted prior to the passage date of the ordinance from which this section is derived and
zoned MH-1 may be used and occupied by mobile and manufactured homes, provided, that no mobile home
shall be placed or installed on any lot, tract or parcel of land within the city. In the MH-1 district, no buildings
or land shall be used, and no buildings shall be erected, placed, reconstructed, altered or enlarged, unless
otherwise provided in this chapter, except for one or more of the following uses:
(1)

Permitted uses.
a.
Manufactured homes, with one single-family manufactured home per lot.
b.
Accessory structures and accessory uses customarily incident to the "MH-1" use permitted in the district, that
are located on the same lot with the primary manufactured home structure, that are designed, constructed and
located for a use permitted in the "MH-1" district, and that are in compliance with this chapter and all other
applicable city ordinances, are permitted in the district; provided the same do not involve the conduct of any
business or commercial enterprise and comply with each of the following requirements:
1.
A private garage may have a capacity for not more than three standard size automobiles, plus one hundred
square feet of storage space for goods and materials;
2.
All accessory structures larger than one hundred square feet must:
(i)
Have a roof line that is not greater in height than the roof line of the manufactured home dwelling;
(ii)
Have walls that are of a height no greater than the average plate height of the primary structure;
(iii)
Not be constructed of scrap or salvage material;
(iv)
Be white in color or substantially the same color as the primary structure;
(v)
Meet the setback and yard requirements for the primary structure;
(vi)
Not be incompatible by architectural design, appearance, materials or size with the manufactured home
dwelling or adjacent "MH-1" uses;
3.
Except for the manufactured home dwelling, not more than one private garage, one carport, and one other
accessory structure may be constructed on a manufactured home lot, subject to the maximum lot coverage
restrictions;
369/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

4.
An accessory structure that is 120 square feet or smaller shall not have a wall height greater than eight feet.
c.
Greenhouses that meet the setback and yard requirements for the primary structure and are not located on any
easement.
d.
Hobbies or crafts, as an accessory use.
e.
Temporary buildings to be used for construction purposes only, and which shall be removed upon completion
or abandonment of construction work or upon the request of the city manager. Permits shall be issued for such
temporary buildings for a period of six months only, with a renewal clause for similar periods.
f.
Antennae and towers not exceeding the maximum height allowed in the MH-1 district (see section 102-483(3)),
antennae attached to existing structures and not increasing the overall height of the existing structure by more
than ten feet, and dish antennae not exceeding one meter in diameter. Except for satellite dish antennae, no
antennae or support structure shall be located within the required front, side or rear yard setback. To protect
tra c safety and community appearance, no satellite dish antennae or support structure shall be located within
the required front or second front yard setback, unless the zoning board of adjustment nds that such an
encroachment is necessary to prevent impairment of installation, maintenance or reception, and that tra c
restriction is not created.
g.
Parks, playgrounds, community buildings and other public recreational facilities, owned and/or operated by the
city or other public agency.
h.
Public buildings, including libraries, museums, and police and re stations.
i.
Single-family dwellings.
j.
Public elementary or high schools.
k.
Private schools with curriculum equivalent to that of a public elementary or high school.
l.
Water supply reservoirs, pumping plants and towers.
(2)

Conditional uses.
a.
Farms, truck gardens, orchards or nurseries for the growing of plants, shrubs and trees, provided, no retail or
wholesale business sales o ces are maintained on the premises and, provided, that no obnoxious fertilizer is
stored upon the premises, and no obnoxious soil or fertilizer processing is conducted on such premises.
b.
370/428

7/12/2019

dwelling and not involving the conduct of a business or industry, except home occupations as de ned in section
102-2, such as the o ce of a physician, surgeon, dentist or art gallery.
c.
Real estate sales o ces for property located within the subdivision in which such o ce is located. Sales o ces
shall require payment of an annual permit fee, to be established by the city council. Use of a sales o ce shall
cease within 30 days of the sale of the last parcel within the subdivision. Field o ces for the sale or rental of real
estate shall be removed upon the request of the building o cial. Sales o ces shall not be used for the sale of
property outside of the subdivision in which it is located.
d.
Any typically permitted secondary or accessory uses allowed in the MH-1 district in the absence of the principal
use if, after consideration of the layout, con guration and relationship to existing subdivisions and
neighborhoods, the city manager determines that replatting the principal and secondary lots into a single lot is
not possible or desirable.
e.
Utility facilities.
f.
Antennae and towers exceeding the maximum height in the MH-1 district, and dish antennae exceeding one
meter in diameter, in order to protect community appearance from the negative visual e ects of proliferation of
large antennae. Conditional use permits shall be acted upon within 90 days of receipt of an application for such
permit. Persons aggrieved by a decision on a satellite dish antenna application may appeal to the Federal
Communications Commission. Any new towers must also comply with the conditions of section 102-580.

Churches.
h.

personal services that meet basic needs of the families residing in areas adjacent to such uses. Requirements

of the following uses is approved because the incidental retail trade and service uses located within it are
intended to become an integral part of the neighborhood or district and must operate with other residential,
educational, religious, and recreational land use activities.
1.
Antique shop that displays sales items inside the shop.

Sec. 102-483. - Height and area regulations.
In the MH-1 district, the following height and area requirements shall apply:
(1)

Floor space. Manufactured homes must have a minimum of 600 square feet of living area, exclusive of garages,
porches and breezeways, and incidental storage areas. No horizontal dimension shall be less than 14 feet,

372/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

except for original extensions or subsequent additions containing less than 50 percent of the total enclosed
oor area.
(2)

Density. Only one residential structure may be placed upon an approved lot.
(3)

Height. No building erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged shall exceed 2½ stories, nor 35 feet. Accessory
buildings shall not exceed one story or 15 feet in height.
(4)

Front yard depth. There shall be a front yard having a depth of not less than 25 feet, or the front yard indicated
on a city-approved subdivision plat as led in the Erath County plat records, whichever is greater. Corner lots
shall have a side yard having a width of not less than 15 feet on the second front yard, the yard generally
parallel to the street with the greatest frontage, unless reversed frontage is approved by the city manager. If a
building line shown on a city-approved subdivision plat as led in the Erath County plat records is greater than
15 feet, then the platted building line shall be required on the second front yard. Garage doors and gates meant
for vehicle use shall be located no closer than 20 feet from the right-of-way.
(5)

Rear yard depth. There shall be a rear yard having a depth of not less than 25 feet.
(6)

Side yard width. Corner lots shall have a side yard having a width of not less than eight feet on side yards
adjacent to interior lots. Interior lots shall have a side yard having a minimum width of eight feet.
(7)

Lot width. The width of a lot shall be a minimum of 60 feet at the building line, provided, that where a lot of
record and in separate ownership at the time of the passage of the ordinance from which this section is derived
has less width than required in this subsection, this chapter shall not prohibit the erection of a one-family
dwelling.
(8)

Lot area. The minimum area of a lot shall be 7,000 square feet, provided, that where a lot has less area than
required in this subsection, and was of record and in separate ownership at the time of passage of the
ordinance from which this section is derived, this chapter shall not prohibit the erection of a one-family
dwelling.
(9)

Maximum lot coverage. The maximum portion of the lot area, which may be covered by the main building and
all accessory buildings, shall not exceed 50 percent.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 14(C), 2-21-2000; Ord. No. 2-19-04-2, §§ 13, 14, 2-19-2004)

Sec. 102-484. - Required conditions.
Manufactured homes shall be installed in accordance with the following criteria:
(1)
373/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Anchorage and foundation of the manufactured home shall be by a person licensed by the state in compliance
with state law as outlined in the latest edition of Manufactured Housing Rules: Administrative Rules of the Texas
Department of Housing and Community A airs, 10 Tex. Admin. Code Ch. 60.
(2)
Each manufactured home shall be totally skirted within 30 days with metal, masonry, pressure-treated wood or
other nondegradable re-retardant material, which is compatible with the design and exterior materials of the
primary structure.
(3)
Exterior siding material, excluding skirting, shall be nonmetallic.
(4)
The structure shall be of adequate quality and a safe design, as certi ed by a label stating that the unit is
constructed in conformance with the federal manufactured home construction and safety standards in e ect on
the date of manufacture of the manufactured home, or other such applicable standards as required by state or
federal law.
(5)
The manufactured home shall be in a sound and safe structural condition. Any structure that shows signs of re
damage will not be acceptable. The building o cial and/or re marshal make the determination of the condition
of such manufactured home.
(6)
Electrical power shall be from a meter installed on the mobile home, or from a permanent meter pedestal.
(7)
Driveways and o -street parking shall be provided in accordance with the requirements for single-family
dwellings.
(8)
Garage and carport additions are permitted, provided, they meet the minimum building setback requirements,
and have roof and siding material compatible with the primary structure.
(9)
Patio and porch covers are permitted, provided, they cover an improved patio, deck or porch, and meet the
minimum building setback requirements.
(10)
Living area additions are permitted, provided, they meet the minimum building setback requirements; have roof
and siding material that is compatible with the primary structure; and comply with the same structural
standards as the primary structure.
(11)
All accessory structures and additions shall comply with all applicable city ordinances.
(12)
An adequate supply of potable water shall be supplied to each manufactured home through piping conforming
with the city's plumbing code (chapter 14, article VI of this Code), as amended, and an outdoor hydrant shall be
installed at each manufactured home at least four inches above the ground.
(13)
374/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Each manufactured home shall be provided with a sewer riser pipe of a minimum of four inches in diameter.
(14)
Gas piping systems shall be installed underground in accordance with the applicable codes and regulations, as
amended. Natural gas shall be used, except that a lique ed petroleum gas system may be installed if the
available natural gas supply is not available to the lot upon which the home is located.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 14(D), 2-21-2000)

(8)
Garage and carport additions are permitted, provided, they meet the minimum building setback requirements,
and have roof and siding material compatible with the primary structure.
(9)
Patio and porch covers are permitted, provided, they cover an improved patio, deck or porch, and meet the
minimum building setback requirements.
(10)
Living area additions are permitted, provided, they meet the minimum building setback requirements; have roof
and siding material that is compatible with the primary structure; and comply with the same structural
standards as the primary structure.
(11)
All accessory structures and additions shall comply with all applicable city ordinances.
(12)
An adequate supply of potable water shall be supplied to each manufactured home through piping conforming
with the city's plumbing code (chapter 14, article VI of this Code), as amended, and an outdoor hydrant shall be
installed at each manufactured home at least four inches above the ground.
(13)
Each manufactured home shall be provided with a sewer riser pipe of a minimum of four inches in diameter.
(14)
Gas piping systems shall be installed underground in accordance with the applicable codes and regulations, as
amended. Natural gas shall be used, except that a lique ed petroleum gas system may be installed if the
available natural gas supply is not available to the lot upon which the home is located.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 15(D), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-505—102-530. - Reserved.
DIVISION 12. - PD PLANNED DEVELOPMENT DISTRICT
Sec. 102-531. - De nitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:

Nonresidential planned development means developments which have:
(1)
Commercial or industrial uses grouped into clusters, allowing an appreciable amount of the land for open space
or joint use, such as parking and storage.
381/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(2)
Commercial or industrial projects with part of the land used for residential purposes.
(3)
Single purpose commercial or industrial uses of innovative land utilization.

Residential planned development means developments which have:
(1)
Dwelling units grouped into clusters, allowing an appreciable amount of land for open space.
(2)
Projects with much or all of the housing in townhouses or apartments, or both.
(3)
Part of the land uses for nonresidential purposes, such as shopping or employment centers.
(4)
Areas exhibiting environmentally sensitive natural features which should be considered for preservation and/or
enhancement.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(A), 2-21-2000)

Cross reference—Definitions generally, § 1-2.
Sec. 102-532. - Purpose.
The purpose of the PD planned development district, generally identified as a suffix to one of the other
zoning districts, is to permit flexibility and encourage a more creative, efficient and aesthetically desirable
design and placement of buildings, open spaces, circulation patterns and to best utilize special site features,
such as topography, size and shape. It is intended that the flexibility permitted by the PD district extends to
discretionary approval, through site plan review of items such as parking space requirements, building line
setbacks, square footage of buildings and structures, protective screening or sign placement and
specifications in order to achieve the purposes and objectives stated in conformance with good planning
practices. The PD district may also be used either alone or as a suffix to another district to accommodate
planned associations of uses developed as integral land use units, including mixed uses, which may be
planned, developed and operated either by a single owner or a combination of owners.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(A), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-533. - Development regulations.
(a)

Height regulations. The maximum height requirement for permissible uses in the PD district shall conform to
the maximum height requirements which would be applicable to such uses if the such uses were situated in the
most restrictive district in which such uses are permitted. However, the planning and zoning commission may
establish speci c heights after consideration of the building height on the surrounding and adjacent property.
(b)
382/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Area regulations. The minimum dimensions of lots and yards of any lot in the PD district shall conform to the
minimum lot and yard requirements which would be applicable to such uses if the uses were situated in the
most restrictive districts in which such uses are permitted. However, the planning and zoning commission may
establish speci c lot, yard and area requirements after consideration of density, building coverage, the
relationship of proposed buildings to surrounding and adjacent property. The area requirements for the
applicable zoning district to which the PD district is to be applied shall be in e ect in the regulations set forth in
this subdivision.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(B), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-534. - Parking regulations.
(a)
All parking and vehicle use areas in the PD district shall be paved with an all-weather surface.
(b)
O -street parking facilities shall be provided at locations designated on the approved development plan.
(c)
Minimum o -street parking requirements shall be established in the approved development plan. Any deviation
from such plan, less than the minimum requirements speci ed in article VI, division 2 of this chapter, shall
require speck approval from the planning and zoning commission.
(d)
Parking areas and numbers of spaces for the applicable district shall apply to the parking regulations.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(C), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-535. - Application and process procedures.
An application for a PD district may be made to the planning and zoning commission in the same manner
that an application for a zoning change is made. Application for approval of a PD district shall be processed
according to the procedure set forth in this section and a development site plan and related data shall be
submitted for approval in accordance with the following requirements:
(1)
An application for a PD district shall be accompanied by a development site plan meeting the requirements set
forth in section 102-536.
(2)
Upon receipt of an application for a PD district, the city manager shall make noti cation of a public hearing as
set forth in this chapter.
(3)
The city manager shall prepare a written report analyzing the development site plan, and such report shall be
given to the planning and zoning commission and the applicant at least three working days prior to the public
hearing.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(D), 2-21-2000)
383/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Sec. 102-536. - Required development site plan.
(a)
An application for a PD district shall be accompanied by a development site plan, which will become a part of
the amending ordinance and be referenced on the zoning district map. Changes in the development site plan
shall be considered the same as changes in the zoning district map, except that the planning and zoning
commission shall have the nal authority to grant, deny or require modi cations consistent with this chapter on
the proposed site plan. The proposed site plan shall be processed as required, except that minor changes which
do not alter the basic relationship of the proposed development to adjacent property and the uses permitted;
increase the density, oor area ratio, height or coverage of the site; decrease the o -street parking ratio; or
reduce the yards provided at the boundary of the site as indicated on the approved development site plan, may
be authorized by the city manager or referred to the planning and zoning commission.
(b)
The development site plan may, in some cases, be a two-phase document. The rst phase shall illustrate and
contain the applicant's request and suggestion for the use, con guration of buildings, parking, etc., and the
second phase shall illustrate the development plan showing the suggestions and recommendations of the
planning and zoning commission after review of phase one. In either case, the applicant shall provide as much
detail as possible, including, but not limited to:
(1)
A scale drawing shall be submitted, showing all proposed public or private streets and alleys; building sites or
building lots; any areas proposed for dedication or reserved as parks, parkways, playgrounds, utility and
garbage easements, school sites, street widening or street changes; the points of ingress and egress from
existing public streets on an accurate survey of the boundary of the tract, and existing and proposed nished
grades with contour intervals of not less than two feet, or spot grades where the relief is limited.
(2)
A land use plan delineating the speci c areas to be devoted to various uses shall be required where multiple
types of land uses are proposed.
(3)
A site plan showing the location of each building, and the distances between buildings, and buildings and the
property line, street line and/or alley line shall be submitted. For buildings more than one story in height, except
single-family and two-family residences, elevations and/or perspective drawings may be required in order that
the relationship of the buildings to adjacent property, open spaces and other features of the development plan
may be determined. Such drawings need only indicate the height, number of oors and exposures for access,
light and air.
(4)
A plan indicating the arrangement and provisions of o -street parking and o -street loading, where required,
shall be required. Such plan may be presented as a ratio of o -street parking and o -street loading area to
building area, when accompanied by a typical example indicating the feasibility of the arrangements proposed
and when the areas where the example would be applied are dimensioned on the drawing of the entire site.

384/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

Any special tra c regulation facilities proposed or required to assure the safe function of the circulation plan
shall also be shown. All streets shall be constructed to the adopted street design standards and section design.
(5)
A designation of the maximum building coverage of the site shall be indicated upon the site plan.
(6)
For development projects in uenced by, impacting on oodprone areas or containing major drainageways or
areas oodprone by de nition of the city engineer, preliminary drainage plans shall be a part of the
development site plan. Such requirement may be waived only by the recommendation of the city engineer.
(7)
The development site plan shall show north arrows, true scale, names and addresses of the developer, licensed
engineer or architect preparing the site plan, and a land description by reference to the name of the subdivision
and survey tract in which the subdivision is located.
(8)
A screening and landscaping plan shall be required where such treatment is essential to the proper
arrangement of the development in relation to adjacent property. When required, such plan shall include
screening walls, plantings, wooded areas to be retained and lawns, if such are determined to be necessary by
the planning and zoning commission.
(9)
The location of re hydrants shall be shown.
(10)
The location of all outside facilities for waste disposal; location and orientation for all external illumination
facilities; location, size, height and orientation of all signs shall be shown.
(11)
All pedestrian walks, malls and open areas for use by tenants or the public shall be shown, as well as the types
of surfacing, such as paving or tur ng, to be used at all locations on the site.
(12)
Any or all of the required features may be incorporated on a single drawing if such drawing is clear, and may be
evaluated by the city manager and an interpretation shall be made by the building o cial.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(E), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-537. - Development schedule.
(a)
A development schedule indicating the approximate date on which construction is expected to begin; the rate of
anticipated development; and the date of completion shall accompany an application for a PD district. The
development schedule, if adopted and approved by the city council, shall become part of the development site
plan, and shall be adhered to by the owner, developer and his successors in interest.
(b)
Annually, the building o cial shall con rm a report provided by the developer to the planning and zoning
commission of the actual development accomplished in the various PD districts as compared with development
385/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

schedules.
(c)
If the planning and zoning commission determines that the owners of property are failing, or have failed, to
meet the approved schedule, the planning and zoning commission may initiate proceedings to amend the
zoning district map or the PD district by removing all, or part of, the PD district from the zoning district map and
placing the area involved in another appropriate zoning district. Upon the recommendation of the planning and
zoning commission, and for good cause shown by the owner and developer, the city council may also extend the
development schedule or adopt such new development schedule as may be indicated by the facts and
conditions of the case.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(F), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-538. - Special conditions.
(a)
The permanent character of common space lands shall be insured by private reservation for the use and bene t
of residents or dedication to public use, or a combination thereof. Common open spaces not dedicated to public
use shall be maintained by the owner thereof. Land required for common open space shall not include the
following:
(1)
Areas reserved for the exclusive use and bene t of an individual tenant or owner.
(2)
Dedicated streets, alleys or other public rights-of-way.
(3)
Vehicular driveways, private streets or parking, loading or storage areas.
(b)
When homeowners associations are to be established for the purpose of ownership and/or management of
common open spaces, all such homeowners associations shall meet the recommended guidelines as
established by the department of housing and urban development (HUD).
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(G), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-539. - Approval.
Every PD district approved under the provisions of this chapter shall be considered as an amendment to
this chapter as applicable to the property involved. In carrying out the development of a PD district, the
development conditions and development schedule shall be complied with, and such conditions as are
specified for the development of a PD district shall not be construed as conditions precedent to the approval
of the zoning amendment, but shall be construed as conditions precedent to the granting of a certificate of
occupancy and compliance.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 16(H), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-540—102-570. - Reserved.
386/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

ARTICLE VI. - SUPPLEMENTARY DISTRICT REGULATIONS
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 102-571. - In general.
(a)
No building shall be erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged, nor shall any building or land be used for any
purpose other than as permitted in the district in which such building or land is located.
(b)
No building shall be erected, reconstructed, altered or enlarged to exceed the height or bulk limit established in
this chapter for the district in which such building is located, nor shall any building be erected, reconstructed or
altered so as to provide a oor space smaller than the minimum prescribed by this chapter.
(c)
No lot area shall be reduced or diminished so that the yards or other open spaces shall be smaller than
prescribed by this chapter, nor shall the density of population be increased in any manner, except in conformity
with the area regulations established in this chapter.
(d)
Every building erected shall be located on a lot as de ned in section 102-2, and in no case shall there be more
than one building on one lot, except as provided in this chapter.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(A)—(D), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-572. - Visibility at intersections.
On a corner lot in any district, nothing shall be erected, placed, planted or allowed to grow in such a
manner as to materially impede vision between a height of 2½ feet and ten feet above the centerline grades of
the intersecting streets in the area bounded by the street lines of such corner lots and a line joining points
along such street lines 35 feet from the point of intersection.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(E), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-573. - Accessory buildings.
No accessory building shall be erected in any required yard or setback, and no separate accessory building
shall be erected within five feet of any other building on the lot, tract, or property.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(F), 2-21-2000; Ord. No. 2-19-04-2, § 19, 2-19-2004)

Sec. 102-574. - Erection of more than one principal structure on a lot.
More than one structure housing a permitted or permissible principal use may be erected on a single lot
in any district, provided, that the yard and other requirements of this chapter shall be met for each structure
as though such structure were on an individual lot.
387/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(G), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-575. - Exceptions to height regulations.
The height limitations contained in article V of this chapter do not apply to spires, belfries, cupolas,
receiving antennas (excluding dish antennas), water tanks, ventilators, chimneys or other appurtenances
usually required to be placed above the roof level and not intended for human occupancy.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(H), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-576. - Buildings to have access.
Every building erected or moved shall be on a lot adjacent to a public street or with access to an approved
private street, and all structures shall be located on lots so as to provide safe and convenient access for
servicing, fire protection and required off-street parking.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(I), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-577. - Residential lots.
Any residentially zoned lot having less area and/or width than required in this chapter, and which was
platted of record and in separate ownership at the time of the passage of the ordinance from which this
section is derived may be occupied by not more than a one family structure. Nothing in this chapter shall
prevent the residential use of any lot platted of record prior to the effective date of this chapter [3-1-2000],
provided that all front yards, side yards, rear yards, floor areas, parking and provisions other than lot area
and/or lot width are met or exceeded.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(J), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-578. - Living quarters for resident managers, etc.
In C, CBD and I districts, not intended for residential use and where residential use is not a permitted use,
living quarters may be provided for resident managers, resident security and maintenance personnel, etc.,
provided, that:
(1)
The living quarters are clearly subordinate to the permitted use such districts.
(2)
The living quarters are only occupied by a manager, security, maintenance or other individual with full-time
duties employed on the site on which the living quarters are located. This is not intended to preclude the
additional occupancy of the living quarters by family members of the full-time individual employed on the site.
(3)
The living quarters are incorporated into the design of the permitted use in such a manner that the living
quarters are not perceptible as living quarters.
388/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(4)
Two o -street parking spaces are provided per living quarter in addition to the required parking for the
permitted use.
(5)
Not more than one such living quarter shall be authorized per platted lot without prior speci c approval of the
planning
and zoning commission as a conditional use following procedures established in section 102152.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(K), 2-21-2000)

Sec. 102-579. - Reserved.
Editor's note—Ord. No. 06-13-05-3, § 6, adopted June 13, 2005, repealed § 102-579, which pertained to
location of sexually-oriented businesses and derived from Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(L), adopted Feb. 21, 2000.
See art. VII for similar provisions.
Sec. 102-580. - Standards for telecommunications towers and antennae.
The city has a goal of minimizing the number of new telecommunications towers and antennae, while
balancing the needs of telecommunication providers to establish a reasonable network to provide quality
service.
(1)
Before a conditional use permit is granted for a new telecommunications tower, the applicant must
demonstrate a good faith e ort to locate on an existing tower or other structure. Such e ort shall be
demonstrated by providing evidence that all potential existing structures were contacted and determined
unavailable, or engineering data showing that there were no acceptable existing structures that met the grid
requirements. Any new telecommunications towers shall be designed to accommodate at least one additional
antenna.
(2)
Any telecommunications antenna or tower that is not operated for a continuous period of 12 months shall be
considered abandoned, and the owner of such antenna or tower shall remove it within 90 days of receipt of
notice from the city notifying the owner of such abandonment. If such antenna or tower is not removed within
such 90 days, the city may remove the antenna or tower at the owner's expense. If there are two or more users
of a single tower, this subsection shall not become e ective until all users cease using the tower.
(Ord. No. 2-21-00-7, § 18(M), 2-21-2000)

Secs. 102-581—102-600. - Reserved.

Sec. 102-603. - Stack space requirements.
All business uses containing an automobile drive-in type ordering or service facility, whether manned or
unmanned, shall provide automobile stack space in conjunction with the drive-in facility. Stack spaces shall be
nine feet wide by 18 feet long, and shall be located in a sequential arrangement oriented to the drive-in
ordering or service area. The space occupied by an automobile placing an order or being served shall not be
considered as a stack space. Required stack spaces shall not be on any street right-of-way or alley; any
necessary maneuvering area for parking spaces within the general traffic circulation pattern of a parking lot;
or a designated fire lane. Stack spaces may be situated in a straight alignment or curved pattern with
functional radii. All stack space requirements shall be in addition to all parking
space and loading requirements specified in sections 102-601 and 102-602. Such stack spaces
shall be provided as follows:

(1)

Sec. 102-604. - General requirements.
(a)
Parking requirements in all SF, B, BR, CR and C districts shall be provided behind the required front yard and
second front yard setback.
(b)
For the purpose of this section, an o -street parking space shall be a minimum of nine feet in width and 18 feet
in length, plus o -street maneuvering space.
(c)
For a single row of 90-degree head-in parking, the minimum width for a parking space, plus the aisle, shall be 38
feet. For two rows of 90-degree head-in parking using the same aisle, the minimum width for parking spaces,
plus the aisle, shall be 56 feet. (See gure 4.)
(d)
For a single row of 60-degree head-in parking, the minimum width for parking space, plus the aisle, shall be 34
feet. For two rows of 60-degree head-in parking using the same aisle, the minimum width for parking spaces,
plus the aisle, shall be 52 feet. (See gure 4.)
(e)

410/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

For a single row of 45-degree head-in parking, the minimum width for parking space, plus the aisle, shall be 30
feet. For two rows of 45-degree head-in parking using the same aisle, the minimum width for parking spaces,
plus the aisle, shall be 48 feet. (See gure 4.)
(f)
A single line of parking spaces may be provided parallel to an aisle, provided, they are at least 22 feet in length
and nine feet in width, with 22 feet of maneuvering space in front of and diagonal to the front most parallel
parking space. (See gure 5.)

(g)
When driveways are less than 20 feet in width, marked separate entrances and exits shall be provided so that
tra c shall ow in one direction only. Entrances and exits to an alley may be provided if prior approval is
obtained in writing from the city.
(h)
When more than one aisle is provided, adequate internal circulation shall be provided between the aisles to
allow movement between the aisles without using public rights-of-way.
(i)
No parking shall be allowed within an area measuring 18 feet square with one side of the square along a
property line and a second side of the square along the width limit of a drive approach in any district. The 18foot square area of no parking shall be behind the property line and adjacent to the throat of a driveway.
Attached to this section is gure 6, which is incorporated in and made a part of this chapter.
(j)
Maneuvering space shall be completely o the right-of-way of a public street, place or court. Drives and parking
areas, including one-family and two-family dwellings, shall be asphalt, concrete or other approved hard, allweather surface, free of litter, debris, weeds, grass or other objectionable material or objects. All parking
requirements applying to a stated unit of measurement shall be understood to include a parking space for each
unit, or fraction thereof.
(k)
Parking areas which would require the use of public rights-of-way for maneuvering shall not be acceptable,
other than for one-family and two-family dwellings. Parking parallel to the curb on a public street shall not be
substituted for o -street parking requirements.
(l)
Nothing in this division shall require the furnishing of additional parking spaces for existing buildings to meet
the requirements of this division for the existing use.
(m)
When the occupancy of any building is changed to another use, parking shall be provided to meet the
requirements of this division for the new use.
411/428

7/12/2019

Dublin, TX Code of Ordinances

(n)
For existing buildings which are enlarged, parking spaces shall be required for the overall building.
(o)
When permanent seating is not provided in any public assembly area, the occupant load shall be computed in
accordance with current re code regulations of the city, without requiring an amendment to this chapter. The
applicable parking requirement will then be calculated as if each occupant had a permanent seat.
(p)
The location of ingress and egress driveways shall be subject to the approval of the city manager under curb cut
or laid down curb authorization procedures.
(q)
Auxiliary parking may be used if su cient parking is not available on the premises. A private parking lot may be
provided within 500 feet, either on property zoned for such purpose or as approved by the planning and zoning
commission under the following restrictions:
(1)
The parking must be subject to the front yard setback requirements of the district in which it is located.
(2)
The parking area must be hard-surfaced and dust-free.
(3)
A minimum ve-foot high screen type fence or planting must be provided on all sides for the protection of the
adjacent properties zoned for residential use.
(4)
Area lights must be directed away from adjacent properties and roadways.
(r)
In each parking facility in districts CF, MF, C, CBD and I, a portion of the total parking spaces available shall be
speci cally designed, located and reserved for vehicles licensed by the state for use by the handicapped. Such
spaces shall be provided according to the following:
